\section{Reference-PDE Finite Extraction on the Explicit Seed Profile}

\section{Goal}

We keep the reference reduced PDE fixed as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c,
}
\label{eq:ref_goal_dict_now}
\end{equation}
and perform the next nonredundant step:
insert the explicit seed profile
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\sech(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
f_+(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{\kappa}{2}}\,\sech(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
f_-(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{3\kappa}{2}}\,\tanh(\kappa\xi)\sech(\kappa\xi),
}
\label{eq:ref_explicit_seed_profiles}
\end{equation}
into the overlap integrals
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_3=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
I_c=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:ref_I3Ic_defs_now}
\end{equation}

\section{Explicit background data}

Write
\begin{equation}
s(\xi):=\sech(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
t(\xi):=\tanh(\kappa\xi).
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0 s(\xi),
\qquad
\theta'(\xi)=-\theta_0\kappa\,s(\xi)t(\xi),
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)
=
\sqrt{\frac{\kappa}{2}}\sqrt{\frac{3\kappa}{2}}\,t(\xi)s(\xi)^2
=
\frac{\sqrt3\,\kappa}{2}\,t(\xi)s(\xi)^2.
\end{equation}

\section{Exact evaluation of \texorpdfstring{$I_3$}{I3}}

Substituting the explicit profiles gives
\begin{align}
I_3
&=
\int d\xi\,
\frac{\sqrt3\,\kappa}{2}\,t s^2
\left(-\theta_0\kappa\,s t\right)^3
\\
&=
-\frac{\sqrt3}{2}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^4
\int d\xi\, t^4 s^5.
\end{align}
Now set
\begin{equation}
u=\tanh(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
du=\kappa s^2\,d\xi,
\qquad
s=\sqrt{1-u^2}.
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{align}
I_3
&=
-\frac{\sqrt3}{2}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3
\int_{-1}^{1} u^4(1-u^2)^{3/2}\,du.
\end{align}
The remaining integral is elementary:
\begin{equation}
\int_{-1}^{1} u^4(1-u^2)^{3/2}\,du=\frac{3\pi}{128}.
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_3
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:ref_I3_exact}
\end{equation}

Hence the longitudinal reduced coefficient becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:ref_lambda_parallel_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{Immediate exact longitudinal matching}

The canonical mixed odd-active target sheet requires
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:ref_target_long_sheet}
\end{equation}
Comparing \eqref{eq:ref_lambda_parallel_explicit} with \eqref{eq:ref_target_long_sheet} yields
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c=\alpha_XL_*.
}
\label{eq:ref_lambda_c_match_exact}
\end{equation}

So on the explicit seed profile the longitudinal matching is exact.

\section{Exact finite representation of \texorpdfstring{$I_c$}{Ic}}

Now evaluate
\begin{align}
I_c
&=
\int d\xi\,
\frac{\sqrt3\,\kappa}{2}\,t s^2
\left(-\theta_0\kappa\,s t\right)\cos(\theta_0 s)
\\
&=
-\frac{\sqrt3\,\theta_0\kappa^2}{2}
\int d\xi\, t^2 s^3 \cos(\theta_0 s).
\end{align}
Using again \(u=\tanh(\kappa\xi)\), one obtains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_c
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\,\theta_0\kappa}{2}
\int_{-1}^{1}
u^2\sqrt{1-u^2}\,
\cos\!\bigl(\theta_0\sqrt{1-u^2}\bigr)\,du.
}
\label{eq:ref_Ic_exact_integral}
\end{equation}

This is an exact finite one-dimensional representation of the transverse overlap.

\section{Small-\texorpdfstring{$\theta_0$}{theta0} expansion of \texorpdfstring{$I_c$}{Ic}}

Using
\begin{equation}
\cos\theta
=
1-\frac{\theta^2}{2}+O(\theta^4),
\end{equation}
we get
\begin{equation}
I_c
=
I_\theta-\frac12 I_{\theta^3}+O(\theta_0^5\kappa),
\label{eq:ref_Ic_expand_start}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
I_\theta:=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta',
\qquad
I_{\theta^3}:=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'\theta^2.
\end{equation}

The already known explicit value is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:ref_Itheta_known}
\end{equation}

Now compute \(I_{\theta^3}\):
\begin{align}
I_{\theta^3}
&=
\int d\xi\,
\frac{\sqrt3\,\kappa}{2}\,t s^2
\left(-\theta_0\kappa s t\right)
\left(\theta_0^2 s^2\right)
\\
&=
-\frac{\sqrt3\,\theta_0^3\kappa^2}{2}
\int d\xi\, t^2 s^5
\\
&=
-\frac{\sqrt3\,\theta_0^3\kappa}{2}
\int_{-1}^{1}u^2(1-u^2)^{3/2}\,du.
\end{align}
Since
\begin{equation}
\int_{-1}^{1}u^2(1-u^2)^{3/2}\,du=\frac{\pi}{16},
\end{equation}
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta^3}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\,\theta_0^3\kappa.
}
\label{eq:ref_Itheta3_exact}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{align}
I_c
&=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa
+\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{64}\,\theta_0^3\kappa
+O(\theta_0^5\kappa)
\\
&=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa
\left(
1-\frac{\theta_0^2}{4}+O(\theta_0^4)
\right).
\label{eq:ref_Ic_smalltheta}
\end{align}

\section{Transverse matching}

The target mixed odd-active transverse sheet is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:ref_target_trans_sheet}
\end{equation}
From the reference route,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c.
}
\label{eq:ref_trans_reference}
\end{equation}
Hence the exact matching condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}
=
\frac{\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa}{I_c}.
}
\label{eq:ref_gamma_perp_exact_match}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:ref_Ic_smalltheta},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}
=
-\,\frac{1}{1-\theta_0^2/4+O(\theta_0^4)}
=
-\left(
1+\frac{\theta_0^2}{4}+O(\theta_0^4)
\right).
}
\label{eq:ref_gamma_perp_smalltheta}
\end{equation}

So at leading order,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\gamma_\perp \approx -M_X^2.
}
\label{eq:ref_gamma_perp_leading}
\end{equation}

\section{Resulting explicit reference coefficient sheet}

The reference branch therefore becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c,
\qquad
I_c
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\,\theta_0\kappa}{2}
\int_{-1}^{1}
u^2\sqrt{1-u^2}\,
\cos\!\bigl(\theta_0\sqrt{1-u^2}\bigr)\,du.
}
\end{equation}

In the small-defect regime this simplifies to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa).
}
\label{eq:ref_coeffsheet_smalltheta_final}
\end{equation}

\section{Honest status}

At the level of the explicit seed profile:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the longitudinal overlap is fully closed and yields the exact match
\[
\boxed{\lambda_c=\alpha_XL_*};
\]

\item the transverse overlap is reduced to the exact finite integral \eqref{eq:ref_Ic_exact_integral};

\item in the small-defect regime, the transverse matching gives
\[
\boxed{\gamma_\perp/M_X^2=-1+O(\theta_0^2)};
\]

\item therefore the reference route is now analytically bridged to the canonical mixed odd-active target, up to the remaining finite audits on the target branch itself.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

On the explicit seed profile
\[
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\sech(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
f_+(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{\kappa}{2}}\,\sech(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
f_-(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{3\kappa}{2}}\,\tanh(\kappa\xi)\sech(\kappa\xi),
\]
the overlap integrals satisfy
\[
\boxed{
I_3=-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
I_c
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\,\theta_0\kappa}{2}
\int_{-1}^{1}
u^2\sqrt{1-u^2}\,
\cos\!\bigl(\theta_0\sqrt{1-u^2}\bigr)\,du.
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c.
}
\]

Matching to the canonical mixed odd-active target gives the exact longitudinal identity
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c=\alpha_XL_*.
}
\]

For small \(\theta_0\),
\[
I_c
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa
\left(1-\frac{\theta_0^2}{4}+O(\theta_0^4)\right),
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
\frac{\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}
=
-\left(1+\frac{\theta_0^2}{4}+O(\theta_0^4)\right),
}
\]
and in particular
\[
\boxed{
\gamma_\perp\approx -M_X^2
}
\]
at leading order.

Therefore the reference PDE is now analytically matched to the target mixed branch as far as the explicit seed profile allows; the genuinely remaining open items are the two target-branch finite audits (Audit A and Audit B) and the actual microscopic insertion of the remaining same-shell/mixed-block constants.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exact Meaning of ``Audit-Free'' and Immediate Closure of Audit A}

\section{Goal}

The phrase ``audit-free'' should be understood sharply and operationally.

At the present stage, the canonical mixed odd-active branch is already structurally fixed by
\[
T_E=T_O=1,
\qquad
R_\perp=\sqrt2,
\qquad
\Delta_{00}=\frac1{\sqrt2},
\]
and its reduced branch-level coefficient sheet is already
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa.
\]
What is still missing is not a structural theorem, but the insertion of the two remaining finite microscopic audits. Therefore the next nonredundant step is to convert Audit A into a completely explicit linear package.

\section{1. Exact operational meaning of audit-free}

A branch is \emph{audit-free} if there remains no unresolved finite PASS/FAIL slot of the following kind:

\begin{enumerate}
\item an uninserted support inequality;
\item an uncomputed finite overlap package;
\item an unresolved cancellation/comparison correction;
\item a coefficient sheet that still depends on placeholders such as
\[
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{(\pi/4)},
\quad
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)},
\quad
\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}},
\quad
\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Equivalently, the branch is audit-free iff the final microscopic coefficient point
\[
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
\]
is fully populated with no remaining conditional insertion.

Thus the present mixed odd-active branch is \emph{not} yet audit-free, because exactly two finite microscopic audits remain:
\[
\text{Audit A: mixed same-shell support insertion},
\qquad
\text{Audit B: mixed-block transverse cancellation audit}.
\]

\section{2. Exact statement of Audit A}

The branch-consistent sufficient support condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{(\pi/4)}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}.
}
\label{eq:AuditA_support_main}
\end{equation}

The previously isolated unresolved same-shell package consists of seven constants:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT},
\qquad
L_+^{TT},\ L_-^{TT},\ L_0^{TT},
\qquad
C_+^{TT},\ C_-^{TT},\ C_m^{TT}.
}
\label{eq:AuditA_7const}
\end{equation}

The point of the present step is that these are not seven independent new mysteries.
On the mixed branch they are exact linear combinations of the already available \(EE\), \(OO\), and \(EO\) Taylor packages.

\section{3. Exact mixed same-shell overlap family}

The exact branch-consistent mixed same-shell overlap family is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{ab}^{TT}(p;\varphi)
=
\cos^2\varphi\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
+
\sin^2\varphi\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{OO}(p)
+
2\sin\varphi\cos\varphi\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}(p),
}
\label{eq:AuditA_STT_general}
\end{equation}
for \(a,b\in\{+,-\}\).

On the canonical mixed branch,
\[
\varphi=\frac{\pi}{4},
\qquad
\cos^2\varphi=\sin^2\varphi=\frac12,
\qquad
2\sin\varphi\cos\varphi=1.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{ab}^{TT}(p;\pi/4)
=
\frac12\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
+
\frac12\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{OO}(p)
+
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}(p).
}
\label{eq:AuditA_STT_pi4}
\end{equation}

This is the key exact reduction formula.

\section{4. Taylor expansion and the seven-constant package}

Expand each block near \(p=0\) in the already used same-shell Taylor form:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal S_{ab}^{XY}(p)
=
\mathcal S_{ab}^{XY}(0)
+
L_{ab}^{XY}\cdot p
+
Q_{ab}^{XY}(p),
\qquad
Q_{ab}^{XY}(p)=O(|p|^2),
\end{equation}
where \(XY\in\{EE,OO,EO\}\).

Then by linearity of \eqref{eq:AuditA_STT_pi4}, every Taylor coefficient of \(TT\) is the same linear combination of the corresponding \(EE\), \(OO\), and \(EO\) coefficients.

In particular, the diagonal zero-momentum term is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{(\pi/4)}
=
\frac12\,\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\frac12\,\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{OO}
+
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EO}.
}
\label{eq:AuditA_Sdiag_pi4}
\end{equation}

Likewise the linear Taylor data become
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_+^{TT}
=
\frac12L_+^{EE}
+
\frac12L_+^{OO}
+
L_+^{EO},
}
\label{eq:AuditA_Lplus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_-^{TT}
=
\frac12L_-^{EE}
+
\frac12L_-^{OO}
+
L_-^{EO},
}
\label{eq:AuditA_Lminus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_0^{TT}
=
\frac12L_0^{EE}
+
\frac12L_0^{OO}
+
L_0^{EO}.
}
\label{eq:AuditA_Lzero}
\end{equation}

And the quadratic drift constants become
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_+^{TT}
=
\frac12C_+^{EE}
+
\frac12C_+^{OO}
+
C_+^{EO},
}
\label{eq:AuditA_Cplus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_-^{TT}
=
\frac12C_-^{EE}
+
\frac12C_-^{OO}
+
C_-^{EO},
}
\label{eq:AuditA_Cminus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_m^{TT}
=
\frac12C_m^{EE}
+
\frac12C_m^{OO}
+
C_m^{EO}.
}
\label{eq:AuditA_Cm}
\end{equation}

Therefore the seven unresolved Audit-A constants are exactly reducible to the \(EE/OO/EO\) Taylor package.

\section{5. Explicit drift bound in mixed form}

The small-\(p\) drift term entering Audit A has the same form as in the pure branch, but now with the mixed \(TT\) constants:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}
\le
\Bigl[
(\rho A_+^{TT}+C_+^{TT}\rho^2)^2
+
(\rho A_-^{TT}+C_-^{TT}\rho^2)^2
+
2(\rho B^{TT}+C_m^{TT}\rho^2)^2
\Bigr]^{1/2},
}
\label{eq:AuditA_eps_bound}
\end{equation}
where the linear budgets \(A_\pm^{TT},B^{TT}\) are extracted from \(L_\pm^{TT},L_0^{TT}\) in the same way as in the already established same-shell drift estimate.

So after \eqref{eq:AuditA_Lplus}--\eqref{eq:AuditA_Cm}, the only remaining work in Audit A is literal insertion.

\section{6. Audit A is now reduced to a table-fill problem}

Substituting \eqref{eq:AuditA_Sdiag_pi4}--\eqref{eq:AuditA_Cm} into \eqref{eq:AuditA_support_main} gives the exact mixed-branch same-shell support condition:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}
\left(
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{OO}
+
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EO}
\right)
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)},
}
\label{eq:AuditA_support_explicit}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}
\]
itself determined by the linear combinations
\eqref{eq:AuditA_Lplus}--\eqref{eq:AuditA_Cm}.

Hence Audit A is no longer conceptually open.
It is reduced exactly to the insertion of the already defined \(EE\), \(OO\), and \(EO\) Taylor tables.

\section{7. Sharp execution order for Audit B}

Once Audit A is reduced as above, the next step is not to reopen any structural discussion.
It is to execute Audit B in the minimal order:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(i) compute }e_{0;K}^{(1)},\ o_{0;K}^{(1)},
\qquad
\text{(ii) compute }\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}},\ \Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}},
}
\end{equation}
from the mixed blocks
\[
TD,\ DT,\ OD,\ DO,\ DD.
\]

The actual transverse pair is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}},
\qquad
\Lambda_O=o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}.
}
\label{eq:AditB_actual_pair}
\end{equation}

For mere survival, a strong sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}|<|e_{0;K}^{(1)}|,
\qquad
|\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}|<|o_{0;K}^{(1)}|.
}
\label{eq:AuditB_survival_recall}
\end{equation}

For the canonical symmetric mixed target, one needs in addition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=\Lambda_O,
}
\label{eq:AuditB_equal_target}
\end{equation}
that is,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}-\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}
=
e_{0;K}^{(1)}-o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:AuditB_equal_difference}
\end{equation}

So Audit B naturally splits into two independent checks:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{non-cancellation check:} \((\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq(0,0)\);
\item \textbf{symmetric-target check:} \(\Lambda_E=\Lambda_O\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{8. Honest status after the present step}

After the exact reduction \eqref{eq:AuditA_STT_pi4}--\eqref{eq:AuditA_Cm}, Audit A is no longer a conceptual audit.
It is a finite table-fill audit.

Therefore the only genuinely uncomputed object left after Audit A is Audit B:
the mixed-block transverse correction pair
\[
(\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}},\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}).
\]

So the sharp current statement is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{not audit-free yet,}
\quad
\text{but Audit A has now been algebraically closed.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

Audit-free means:
\[
\boxed{
\text{no remaining unresolved finite PASS/FAIL insertion slot.}
}
\]
Equivalently, the final microscopic coefficient point
\[
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
\]
must be fully populated with no placeholder constants or pending cancellation checks.

At the present stage, the mixed odd-active branch is still \emph{not} audit-free because exactly two finite audits remain:
\[
\text{Audit A: mixed same-shell support insertion},
\qquad
\text{Audit B: mixed-block transverse cancellation audit}.
\]

However, Audit A is now algebraically closed.

On the canonical mixed branch \(\varphi=\pi/4\),
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{ab}^{TT}(p)
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{OO}(p)
+
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}(p).
}
\]
Therefore the full seven-constant same-shell package is exactly
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{(\pi/4)}
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{OO}
+
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EO},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
L_\pm^{TT}
=
\frac12L_\pm^{EE}
+
\frac12L_\pm^{OO}
+
L_\pm^{EO},
\qquad
L_0^{TT}
=
\frac12L_0^{EE}
+
\frac12L_0^{OO}
+
L_0^{EO},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
C_\pm^{TT}
=
\frac12C_\pm^{EE}
+
\frac12C_\pm^{OO}
+
C_\pm^{EO},
\qquad
C_m^{TT}
=
\frac12C_m^{EE}
+
\frac12C_m^{OO}
+
C_m^{EO}.
}
\]

Thus Audit A is no longer structurally open.
It is reduced to literal insertion of the \(EE/OO/EO\) Taylor table into the support inequality.

The only genuinely remaining unresolved object after that is Audit B:
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}},
\qquad
\Lambda_O=o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}.
}
\]

For the canonical symmetric target one must check both
\[
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq(0,0)
\]
and
\[
\Lambda_E=\Lambda_O.
\]

So the project is not audit-free yet, but one of the two final audits has now been reduced to a direct table-fill computation.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Audit B: Exact Reduction to Principal Pair plus Residual Correction}

\section{Goal}

The remaining mixed-block transverse audit is to determine whether the actual transverse coefficient pair
\[
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)
\]
survives after the mixed completion channels are inserted, and whether it matches the canonical symmetric mixed target
\[
\Lambda_E=\Lambda_O\neq 0.
\]

The exact conservative branch-level form is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}},
\qquad
\Lambda_O=o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}.
}
\label{eq:AuditB_start}
\end{equation}

\section{1. Exact blockwise decomposition}

For each candidate mixed block
\[
AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\},
\]
define the leading even/odd transverse coefficients by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr\!\left[\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M^{\rm inv}_{AB,\mu}\right],
}
\label{eq:AuditB_eAB}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr\!\left[\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M^{\rm inv}_{AB,\mu}\right].
}
\label{eq:AuditB_oAB}
\end{equation}

Then the full leading transverse coefficient point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} o_{0;AB}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:AuditB_fullsum}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Principal pair and residual correction vector}

Define the principal pair
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\rm pr}:=e_{0;TD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DT}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\rm pr}:=o_{0;TD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DT}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:AuditB_principal_pair}
\end{equation}

Define the residual correction vector
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\rm rem}
:=
\left(
r_E,\ r_O
\right),
}
\qquad
r_E:=e_{0;OD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DO}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD}^{(1)}+\cdots,
\qquad
r_O:=o_{0;OD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DO}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD}^{(1)}+\cdots.
\label{eq:AuditB_rrem}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=\Lambda_E^{\rm pr}+r_E,
\qquad
\Lambda_O=\Lambda_O^{\rm pr}+r_O.
}
\label{eq:AuditB_pr_plus_rem}
\end{equation}

At the current conservative bookkeeping level one may identify
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;K}^{(1)}\equiv \Lambda_E^{\rm pr},
\qquad
o_{0;K}^{(1)}\equiv \Lambda_O^{\rm pr},
\qquad
\Delta e_{\rm mix}\equiv r_E,
\qquad
\Delta o_{\rm mix}\equiv r_O.
}
\label{eq:AuditB_K_identification}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Leading minimal truncation}

At the minimal mixed-block truncation,
\[
OD=DO=DD=0,
\]
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=\Lambda_E^{\rm pr},
\qquad
\Lambda_O=\Lambda_O^{\rm pr}.
}
\end{equation}

If the branch-summary invariant form is written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{TD}
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[A_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a+A_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a\Bigr],
\qquad
V^\mu_{DT}
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[B_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a+B_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a\Bigr],
}
\label{eq:AuditB_AEBO}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\rm pr}=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\rm pr}=\frac12(A_O+B_O).
}
\label{eq:AuditB_principal_AEBO}
\end{equation}

Hence in the minimal truncation the reduced coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa\,(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa\,(A_O+B_O).
}
\label{eq:AuditB_alpha_beta_minimal}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Survival condition}

The exact no-cancellation survival condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\rm mix}\neq -e_{0;K}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\rm mix}\neq -o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:AuditB_nocancel}
\end{equation}

A stronger sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta e_{\rm mix}|<|e_{0;K}^{(1)}|,
\qquad
|\Delta o_{\rm mix}|<|o_{0;K}^{(1)}|.
}
\label{eq:AuditB_strong_survival}
\end{equation}

Under \eqref{eq:AuditB_strong_survival}, the signs of \(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O\) are inherited from the principal \(K\)-sector pair.

\section{5. Symmetric-target reduction}

For the canonical mixed odd-active target, one needs
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:AuditB_equal_target}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:AuditB_start}, this is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta o_{\rm mix}-\Delta e_{\rm mix}
=
e_{0;K}^{(1)}-o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:AuditB_difference_condition}
\end{equation}

This is the sharp exact equality test.

Thus the symmetric-target audit is not a two-dimensional comparison problem anymore.
It is a single scalar difference equation.

\section{6. Sum/difference normal form}

Define
\begin{equation}
s_K:=\frac12\Bigl(e_{0;K}^{(1)}+o_{0;K}^{(1)}\Bigr),
\qquad
d_K:=\frac12\Bigl(e_{0;K}^{(1)}-o_{0;K}^{(1)}\Bigr),
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
s_{\rm mix}:=\frac12\Bigl(\Delta e_{\rm mix}+\Delta o_{\rm mix}\Bigr),
\qquad
d_{\rm mix}:=\frac12\Bigl(\Delta e_{\rm mix}-\Delta o_{\rm mix}\Bigr).
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=(s_K+s_{\rm mix})+(d_K+d_{\rm mix}),
\qquad
\Lambda_O=(s_K+s_{\rm mix})-(d_K+d_{\rm mix}).
}
\label{eq:AuditB_sumdiff}
\end{equation}

Therefore:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{symmetric target}
\[
\Lambda_E=\Lambda_O
\iff
d_K+d_{\rm mix}=0;
\]

\item \textbf{nonzero survival on the symmetric target}
\[
\Lambda_E=\Lambda_O\neq0
\iff
d_K+d_{\rm mix}=0
\quad\text{and}\quad
s_K+s_{\rm mix}\neq0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_{\rm mix}=-d_K,
\qquad
s_{\rm mix}\neq -s_K.
}
\label{eq:AuditB_sumdiff_target}
\end{equation}

This is the cleanest normal form of Audit B.

\section{7. Final populated coefficient sheet after Audit B}

Once Audit B is inserted, the mixed odd-active branch coefficient point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
}
\label{eq:AuditB_lambda_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\rm mix}\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:AuditB_alpha_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\rm mix}\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:AuditB_beta_final}
\end{equation}

For the canonical symmetric mixed target one further imposes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\rm mix}
=
o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\rm mix}
\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:AuditB_canonical_target}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Honest status}

Audit B is now reduced to two finite microscopic objects:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the principal pair
\[
\bigl(\Lambda_E^{\rm pr},\Lambda_O^{\rm pr}\bigr)
=
\bigl(e_{0;TD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DT}^{(1)},\ 
o_{0;TD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DT}^{(1)}\bigr);
\]

\item the residual correction vector
\[
r_{\rm rem}
=
(r_E,r_O)
=
\left(
\sum_{AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}}e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\ 
\sum_{AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}}o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
\right).
\]
\end{enumerate}

So the actual remaining work is no longer conceptual.
It is the literal evaluation of
\[
r_{\rm rem}.
\]

Once \(r_{\rm rem}\) is known, both survival and the symmetric-target condition are decided immediately by
\eqref{eq:AuditB_nocancel} and \eqref{eq:AuditB_difference_condition}.

\section{Final Summary}

The mixed-block transverse audit is exactly reducible to

\[
\boxed{
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)
=
(\Lambda_E^{\rm pr},\Lambda_O^{\rm pr})+r_{\rm rem},
}
\]
where
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\rm pr}=e_{0;TD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DT}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\rm pr}=o_{0;TD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DT}^{(1)},
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
r_{\rm rem}
=
\left(
\sum_{AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}}e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\ 
\sum_{AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}}o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
\right).
}
\]

The exact survival condition is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\rm mix}\neq -e_{0;K}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\rm mix}\neq -o_{0;K}^{(1)},
}
\]
and a strong sufficient condition is
\[
\boxed{
|\Delta e_{\rm mix}|<|e_{0;K}^{(1)}|,
\qquad
|\Delta o_{\rm mix}|<|o_{0;K}^{(1)}|.
}
\]

For the canonical mixed odd-active target, the equality condition is reduced to the single scalar test
\[
\boxed{
\Delta o_{\rm mix}-\Delta e_{\rm mix}
=
e_{0;K}^{(1)}-o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
}
\]

In sum/difference variables
\[
s_K=\frac{e_{0;K}^{(1)}+o_{0;K}^{(1)}}{2},
\quad
d_K=\frac{e_{0;K}^{(1)}-o_{0;K}^{(1)}}{2},
\quad
s_{\rm mix}=\frac{\Delta e_{\rm mix}+\Delta o_{\rm mix}}{2},
\quad
d_{\rm mix}=\frac{\Delta e_{\rm mix}-\Delta o_{\rm mix}}{2},
\]
the canonical target condition becomes
\[
\boxed{
d_{\rm mix}=-d_K,
\qquad
s_{\rm mix}\neq -s_K.
}
\]

Therefore Audit B is no longer conceptually open.
It is reduced completely to the finite evaluation of the residual correction vector
\[
r_{\rm rem}=
\left(
\sum_{AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}}e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\ 
\sum_{AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}}o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
\right).
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Audit B Reduced to Two Explicit Residual Projector Computations}

\section{Goal}

The exact residual mixed-block audit has already been reduced to the blocks
\[
OD,\qquad DO,\qquad DD.
\]
The next nonredundant step is to reduce this further by the two available structural simplifications:

\begin{enumerate}
\item reflection parity under \(\xi\mapsto-\xi\);
\item \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry.
\end{enumerate}

This yields the sharpest executable form of Audit B.

\section{1. Exact residual vector}

For each residual block \(AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}\), define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim \mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{AB}^{\rm inv}],
\qquad
o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim \mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{AB}^{\rm inv}].
}
\label{eq:RB_eo_defs}
\end{equation}
Then the exact residual correction vector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\rm rem}
=
\bigl(\Delta e_{\rm rem},\Delta o_{\rm rem}\bigr)
=
\sum_{AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}}
\bigl(e_{0;AB}^{(1)},o_{0;AB}^{(1)}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:RB_rrem_full}
\end{equation}

The full transverse coefficient point is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)=r_{\rm pr}+r_{\rm rem},
}
\label{eq:RB_full_split}
\end{equation}
with \(r_{\rm pr}\) the already isolated principal \(TD+DT\) source.

\section{2. Parity elimination rule}

For a given residual block \(AB\), the exact next test is the reflection parity of
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\rm inv}(\xi)
\]
under
\[
\xi\mapsto-\xi.
\]

The sharp rule is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\rm inv}(-\xi)=+\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\rm inv}(\xi)
\Longrightarrow
\bigl(e_{0;AB}^{(1)},o_{0;AB}^{(1)}\bigr)=(0,0),
}
\label{eq:RB_even_zero}
\end{equation}
while
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\rm inv}(-\xi)=-\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\rm inv}(\xi)
\Longrightarrow
\text{the block is parity-allowed and must be computed.}
}
\label{eq:RB_odd_keep}
\end{equation}

Hence the true residual vector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\rm rem}
=
\sum_{\substack{AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}\\ \mathcal M_{AB}\ \text{odd}}}
\bigl(e_{0;AB}^{(1)},o_{0;AB}^{(1)}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:RB_rrem_parity}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exchange reduction}

If the projected mixed sector preserves the \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry, then
\(DO\) is not independent of \(OD\), and one may reduce at the symmetry-reduced level to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;DO}^{(1)}=e_{0;OD}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_{0;DO}^{(1)}=o_{0;OD}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:RB_DOeqOD}
\end{equation}

Therefore the residual vector becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\rm rem}
=
2\bigl(e_{0;OD}^{(1)},o_{0;OD}^{(1)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(e_{0;DD}^{(1)},o_{0;DD}^{(1)}\bigr),
}
\label{eq:RB_exchange_reduced}
\end{equation}
again with the understanding that any even-parity block drops out exactly.

Thus the practical audit is reduced from three raw projector computations to:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute only the parity-allowed part of }OD\text{ and }DD,
}
\label{eq:RB_practical_reduction}
\end{equation}
provided exchange symmetry holds.

\section{4. Canonical symmetric mixed-target condition}

The conservative coefficient sheet is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\rm rem}\bigr),
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\rm rem}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:RB_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}

For the canonical mixed odd-active target one needs
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=\Lambda_O\neq0.
}
\label{eq:RB_target_eq}
\end{equation}

Using the exchange-reduced form
\[
\Delta e_{\rm rem}=2e_{0;OD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\rm rem}=2o_{0;OD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD}^{(1)},
\]
the equality condition becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2\Bigl(o_{0;OD}^{(1)}-e_{0;OD}^{(1)}\Bigr)
+
\Bigl(o_{0;DD}^{(1)}-e_{0;DD}^{(1)}\Bigr)
=
e_{0;K}^{(1)}-o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:RB_final_difference}
\end{equation}

This is the sharp final scalar condition for the symmetric target.

\section{5. Survival inequalities}

The strong componentwise sufficient survival condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta e_{\rm rem}|<|\Lambda_E^{\rm pr}|,
\qquad
|\Delta o_{\rm rem}|<|\Lambda_O^{\rm pr}|.
}
\label{eq:RB_component_survival}
\end{equation}

A weaker Euclidean sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|r_{\rm rem}\|_2<\|r_{\rm pr}\|_2.
}
\label{eq:RB_euclidean_survival}
\end{equation}

Under exchange reduction, these become
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|2e_{0;OD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD}^{(1)}\right|<|\Lambda_E^{\rm pr}|,
\qquad
\left|2o_{0;OD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD}^{(1)}\right|<|\Lambda_O^{\rm pr}|,
}
\label{eq:RB_component_survival_reduced}
\end{equation}
or, more coarsely,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left\|
2\bigl(e_{0;OD}^{(1)},o_{0;OD}^{(1)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(e_{0;DD}^{(1)},o_{0;DD}^{(1)}\bigr)
\right\|_2
<
\|r_{\rm pr}\|_2.
}
\label{eq:RB_euclidean_survival_reduced}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Final executable decision tree}

Thus the residual transverse audit is now exactly:

\begin{enumerate}
\item test the parity of \(\mathcal M^\mu_{OD,\rm inv}\) and \(\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\rm inv}\);
\item discard whichever block is reflection-even;
\item compute the projector traces only for the parity-allowed blocks;
\item insert the result into \eqref{eq:RB_component_survival_reduced} and \eqref{eq:RB_final_difference}.
\end{enumerate}

If both \(OD\) and \(DD\) are even, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\rm rem}=0,
}
\end{equation}
and the canonical target reduces immediately to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;K}^{(1)}=o_{0;K}^{(1)}\neq0.
}
\end{equation}

If exactly one of them is odd, only that one must be computed.

If both are odd, then both must be computed and inserted through
\eqref{eq:RB_final_difference}.

\section{Final Summary}

The residual transverse correction is no longer a three-block open problem in practice.

Its exact starting form is
\[
r_{\rm rem}
=
\sum_{AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}}
\bigl(e_{0;AB}^{(1)},o_{0;AB}^{(1)}\bigr).
\]

Using reflection parity, only the \(\xi\mapsto-\xi\) odd kernels survive:
\[
r_{\rm rem}
=
\sum_{\substack{AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}\\ \mathcal M_{AB}\ \text{odd}}}
\bigl(e_{0;AB}^{(1)},o_{0;AB}^{(1)}\bigr).
\]

Using \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry, one gets
\[
e_{0;DO}^{(1)}=e_{0;OD}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_{0;DO}^{(1)}=o_{0;OD}^{(1)},
\]
so the residual vector reduces to
\[
\boxed{
r_{\rm rem}
=
2\bigl(e_{0;OD}^{(1)},o_{0;OD}^{(1)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(e_{0;DD}^{(1)},o_{0;DD}^{(1)}\bigr),
}
\]
with any even-parity block removed exactly.

Therefore the practical Audit B is reduced to two literal residual projector computations:
\[
OD,\qquad DD.
\]

The canonical symmetric mixed-target condition
\[
\Lambda_E=\Lambda_O
\]
becomes the single scalar equation
\[
\boxed{
2\Bigl(o_{0;OD}^{(1)}-e_{0;OD}^{(1)}\Bigr)
+
\Bigl(o_{0;DD}^{(1)}-e_{0;DD}^{(1)}\Bigr)
=
e_{0;K}^{(1)}-o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
}
\]

The strong sufficient survival inequalities become
\[
\boxed{
\left|2e_{0;OD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD}^{(1)}\right|<|\Lambda_E^{\rm pr}|,
\qquad
\left|2o_{0;OD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD}^{(1)}\right|<|\Lambda_O^{\rm pr}|.
}
\]

So the project is now at the sharpest possible finite stage:

\[
\boxed{
\text{compute the parity-allowed part of }OD\text{ and }DD,
\text{ then insert them once.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Residual Audit B Reduced to the Odd Parts of \(OD\) and \(DD\)}

\section{Goal}

The next sharp step is not to re-open the block list
\[
OD,\qquad DO,\qquad DD,
\]
but to split each residual block into its reflection-even and reflection-odd pieces, and keep only the odd pieces that can survive the graded projection.

\section{1. General parity decomposition}

For any residual block \(AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}\), write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}(\xi)
=
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{even}}(\xi)
+
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{odd}}(\xi),
}
\label{eq:RB_split_general}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{even}}(-\xi)=+\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{even}}(\xi),
\qquad
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{odd}}(-\xi)=-\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{odd}}(\xi).
\label{eq:RB_evenodd_def}
\end{equation}

For the reflection-symmetric defect background, the graded low modes satisfy
\[
u_a^+(-\xi)=+u_a^+(\xi),
\qquad
u_b^-(-\xi)=-u_b^-(\xi).
\]
Hence the projected mixed matrix element
\[
(M^\mu_{AB})_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,
(u_a^+)^\dagger\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}u_b^-
\]
receives no contribution from the even part:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\int d\xi\,(u_a^+)^\dagger\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{even}}u_b^-=0.
}
\label{eq:RB_even_killed}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim \mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{odd}}],
\qquad
o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim \mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{odd}}].
}
\label{eq:RB_only_odd_survives}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Sharp \(OD\)-classification}

The \(OD\)-block is not a direct \(J^{(1)}/K^{(1)}\) odd transport source.
Instead it is generated from the mixed quartic interaction
\[
\lambda_{OD}\rho_O\rho_D
\]
on the background
\[
\bar\Phi_{\min}=(0,\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)).
\]
Its background-generated cubic vertices are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\sim
\lambda_{OD}\,\bar\chi_B(\xi),
\qquad
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\zeta\zeta}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\sim
\lambda_{OD}\,\bar n_B(\xi).
}
\label{eq:RB_OD_vertices}
\end{equation}

Therefore the \(OD\)-kernel is not theorem-level odd by itself.
Its honest decomposition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{OD,\mathrm{inv}}
=
\mathcal M^\mu_{OD,\mathrm{pot/even}}
+
\mathcal M^\mu_{OD,\mathrm{trans/odd}}.
}
\label{eq:RB_OD_split}
\end{equation}

Here:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\mathcal M^\mu_{OD,\mathrm{pot/even}}\) denotes the part built only from background amplitudes and non-gradient projector contractions; it is reflection-even and vanishes after graded projection;

\item \(\mathcal M^\mu_{OD,\mathrm{trans/odd}}\) denotes the part that acquires one transverse background-gradient insertion through the projected kernel extraction, derivative-anisotropy response, or background-to-worldvolume transport conversion; this is the parity-allowed piece.
\end{enumerate}

Thus the exact projector-visible \(OD\)-coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;OD}^{(1)}
=
\lim\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M^\mu_{OD,\mathrm{trans/odd}}],
\qquad
o_{0;OD}^{(1)}
=
\lim\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M^\mu_{OD,\mathrm{trans/odd}}].
}
\label{eq:RB_OD_coeffs}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Sharp \(DD\)-classification}

The \(DD\)-sector contains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{DD}
=
-Z_{D,k}\partial^2
+
\mathcal M_{DD}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
+
Y_k\mathcal K_{DD}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(\xi,\partial)
+
\mathcal T_{DD}(\xi,\partial_y).
}
\label{eq:RB_DD_full}
\end{equation}

Hence its first-order projected kernel also splits naturally:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}
=
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{pot/even}}
+
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\nabla\mathrm{ani}/\mathrm{odd}}
+
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{trans}/\mathrm{odd}}.
}
\label{eq:RB_DD_split}
\end{equation}

The honest status is therefore:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the defect-background-dependent potential tensor contributes an even piece, killed by the graded projection;

\item derivative-anisotropy terms may generate an odd piece once one transverse background-gradient insertion is present;

\item the explicit transport block \(\mathcal T_{DD}\) is the most natural source of a parity-allowed odd contribution.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;DD}^{(1)}
=
\lim\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{odd}}],
\qquad
o_{0;DD}^{(1)}
=
\lim\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{odd}}],
}
\label{eq:RB_DD_coeffs}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{odd}}
:=
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\nabla\mathrm{ani}/\mathrm{odd}}
+
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{trans}/\mathrm{odd}}.
\]

\section{4. Universal monomial normal form of every surviving odd residual piece}

The full principal transport kernel is already classified by the monomial families
\[
\theta'X_A\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\qquad
\theta'^3X_A\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\qquad
\theta'X_A\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad
\theta'X_A\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\]
where \(X_A\) are parity-even local defect invariants.

Therefore any residual contribution that survives the parity filter and contributes to the transverse pair must necessarily reduce to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{odd}}
=
\theta'(\xi)\,
\Bigl[
X^{(AB)}_{E}(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
X^{(AB)}_{O}(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr],
\qquad
AB\in\{OD,DD\},
}
\label{eq:RB_odd_normal_form}
\end{equation}
with
\[
X_E^{(AB)}(-\xi)=X_E^{(AB)}(\xi),
\qquad
X_O^{(AB)}(-\xi)=X_O^{(AB)}(\xi).
\]

Thus the parity-allowed residual sector is not arbitrary:
every surviving transverse correction must contain exactly one odd defect-gradient factor \(\theta'(\xi)\), multiplied by parity-even local invariants.

\section{5. Exchange reduction}

If the background and projected regulator preserve the \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry to leading order, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;DO}^{(1)}=e_{0;OD}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_{0;DO}^{(1)}=o_{0;OD}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:RB_exchange_reduction}
\end{equation}

So the residual correction vector becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\rm rem}
=
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\rm rem}
=
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:RB_final_residual_pair}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Final scalar condition for the canonical symmetric target}

The canonical mixed odd-active target requires
\[
\Lambda_E=\Lambda_O\neq 0.
\]
Using
\[
\Lambda_E=e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\rm rem},
\qquad
\Lambda_O=o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\rm rem},
\]
together with \eqref{eq:RB_final_residual_pair}, the exact equality condition becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2\Bigl(
o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr)
+
\Bigl(
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr)
=
e_{0;K}^{(1)}-o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:RB_scalar_final}
\end{equation}

The strong sufficient survival conditions become
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\right|
<
|e_{0;K}^{(1)}|,
}
\label{eq:RB_survival_E}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\right|
<
|o_{0;K}^{(1)}|.
}
\label{eq:RB_survival_O}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Honest closure status}

At the present stage the sharpest closed statement is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
OD \text{ and } DD \text{ are not theorem-level zero,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{their even parts are killed exactly, and only their odd }\theta'X_A\text{-type parts remain load-bearing.}
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the final residual work is no longer
``compute the full \(OD\) and \(DD\) blocks''.
It is only:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{extract the coefficients of the odd normal forms }
\theta'X_AE^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a,
\qquad
\theta'X_AJ^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\text{ in }OD\text{ and }DD.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The residual blocks \(OD\) and \(DD\) do not vanish automatically.

However, each one splits as
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}
=
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{even}}
+
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{odd}},
\qquad
AB\in\{OD,DD\},
\]
and the reflection-even part is killed exactly by the graded projection:
\[
e_{0;AB}^{(1)}=o_{0;AB}^{(1)}=0
\quad\text{for }\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{even}}.
\]

The \(OD\)-block is generated from the mixed quartic interaction
\[
\lambda_{OD}\rho_O\rho_D
\]
through the cubic vertices
\[
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta}\sim \lambda_{OD}\bar\chi_B,
\qquad
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\zeta\zeta}\sim \lambda_{OD}\bar n_B.
\]
Therefore it is not theorem-level odd by itself; only its transport-producing odd part survives.

The \(DD\)-block contains
\[
\mathcal M_{DD}^{\mathrm{pot}},
\qquad
\mathcal K_{DD}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}},
\qquad
\mathcal T_{DD},
\]
so its potential part is even, while its derivative-anisotropy and explicit transport parts can carry an odd contribution.

Every surviving residual transverse contribution must reduce to the universal odd normal form
\[
\boxed{
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
X_E(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
X_O(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr],
}
\]
with \(X_E,X_O\) parity-even local defect invariants.

Under \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry,
\[
\Delta e_{\rm rem}
=
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\rm rem}
=
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}.
\]

Therefore the canonical symmetric mixed-target condition is reduced to the single scalar equation
\[
\boxed{
2\Bigl(
o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr)
+
\Bigl(
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr)
=
e_{0;K}^{(1)}-o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
}
\]

So the remaining microscopic work is now maximally sharp:
\[
\boxed{
\text{extract only the odd } \theta'X_A\text{-type coefficients in }OD\text{ and }DD.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exact Extraction Formulas for the Residual Odd Coefficients}

\section{Goal}

The transverse coefficient point is already split as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)=v_{\mathrm{pr}}+r_{\mathrm{rem}},
}
\label{eq:goal_split_residual}
\end{equation}
where
\[
v_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\Bigl(
e_{0;TD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DT}^{(1)},
\;
o_{0;TD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DT}^{(1)}
\Bigr),
\]
and the residual correction is carried by
\[
OD,\qquad DO,\qquad DD.
\]

The next nonredundant step is to write the exact executable formulas for the parity-allowed residual coefficients
\[
e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\quad
o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\quad
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\quad
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}.
\]

\section{1. Universal projector extraction rule}

For any block \(AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}\), define the tangent-projected first-order kernel
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB}(\xi):=\Pi_Q\,\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}(\xi)\,\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:universal_MAB}
\end{equation}
Its parity-odd part is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
:=
\frac12\Bigl(
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB}(\xi)-\mathcal M^\mu_{AB}(-\xi)
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:universal_oddpart}
\end{equation}
Then the surviving transverse coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;AB,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\,\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M_{AB,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}\bigr),
}
\label{eq:universal_eodd}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
o_{0;AB,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\,\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M_{AB,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:universal_oodd}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact \(OD\)-odd extraction}

On the minimal admissible background
\[
\bar\Phi_{\min}=(0,\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)),
\]
the mixed quartic interaction
\[
\lambda_{OD}\rho_O\rho_D
\]
generates the cubic vertices
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\sim
\lambda_{OD}\,\bar\chi_B(\xi),
\qquad
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\zeta\zeta}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\sim
\lambda_{OD}\,\bar n_B(\xi).
\label{eq:OD_cubic_vertices_exec}
\end{equation}

Let
\[
\mathcal H_{OO}u_m=E_m^O u_m,
\qquad
\mathcal H_{DD}v_n=E_n^D v_n,
\]
with projected regulated propagators
\[
G_O^{(m)}(q),
\qquad
G_D^{(n)}(q).
\]
The projected \(OD\)-self-energy kernel on the \(O\)-sector is
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
-
\int\!\frac{d^d q}{(2\pi)^d}
\sum_{m,n}
\mathcal V^{(OD)}_{O;mn}(p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(q)\,
\mathcal V^{(OD)}_{O;nm}(-p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(p+q)\,
\partial_tR_k(q),
\label{eq:SigmaO_OD_exec}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\mathcal V^{(OD)}_{O;mn}(p,q)
=
\braket{u_m|\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta}(p,q;\bar\Phi_{\min})|v_n}.
\label{eq:VOD_exec}
\end{equation}

The parity-allowed first-order transport kernel extracted from this loop is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{OD,\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
:=
\frac12
\left[
\Pi_Q
\left(
\frac{\partial}{\partial p_\mu}\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p;\xi)
\right)_{p=0}
\Pi_Q
-
\Pi_Q
\left(
\frac{\partial}{\partial p_\mu}\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p;-\xi)
\right)_{p=0}
\Pi_Q
\right].
}
\label{eq:MOD_odd_from_Sigma}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact executable formulas are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\,
\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(
\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M_{OD,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}
\bigr),
}
\label{eq:eOD_exec}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\,
\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(
\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M_{OD,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:oOD_exec}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, inserting \eqref{eq:SigmaO_OD_exec},
\begin{align}
e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
&=
-\frac14 E^\mu{}_a
\int\!\frac{d^dq}{(2\pi)^d}\sum_{m,n}
\Tr_{Q_B}
\Bigl[
\Sigma_a\,
\partial_{p_\mu}
\Bigl(
\mathcal V^{(OD)}_{O;mn}(p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(q)\,
\mathcal V^{(OD)}_{O;nm}(-p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(p+q)
\Bigr)_{p=0}^{\mathrm{odd}}
\Bigr]
\,\partial_tR_k(q),
\label{eq:eOD_integral}
\\
o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
&=
-\frac14 J^\mu{}_a
\int\!\frac{d^dq}{(2\pi)^d}\sum_{m,n}
\Tr_{Q_B}
\Bigl[
\Sigma_a\,
\partial_{p_\mu}
\Bigl(
\mathcal V^{(OD)}_{O;mn}(p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(q)\,
\mathcal V^{(OD)}_{O;nm}(-p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(p+q)
\Bigr)_{p=0}^{\mathrm{odd}}
\Bigr]
\,\partial_tR_k(q).
\label{eq:oOD_integral}
\end{align}

Thus the only actual work in the \(OD\)-sector is the \(p\)-derivative at \(p=0\) followed by odd parity projection.

\section{3. Exact \(DD\)-odd extraction}

The projected \(DD\)-kernel already has the invariant decomposition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_{\parallel;DD}(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3
+
a_{E;DD}(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
a_{O;DD}(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a.
}
\label{eq:MDD_invariant}
\end{equation}

Define the odd parts
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
:=
\frac12\Bigl(a_{E;DD}(\xi)-a_{E;DD}(-\xi)\Bigr),
\qquad
a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
:=
\frac12\Bigl(a_{O;DD}(\xi)-a_{O;DD}(-\xi)\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:DD_odd_coeffs}
\end{equation}

Then the transverse residual coefficients from \(DD\) are directly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}},
\qquad
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}.
}
\label{eq:eDD_oDD_exec}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_{DD,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}\bigr),
\qquad
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_{DD,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}\bigr),
}
\label{eq:DD_projector_equiv}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{odd}}
=
a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a.
\]

\section{4. Exchange-reduced residual pair}

If the background and projected regulator preserve \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry to leading order, then
\[
e_{0;DO,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}=e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_{0;DO,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}=o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}.
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\mathrm{rem}}
=
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\mathrm{rem}}
=
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:residual_pair_final}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Final transverse coefficients}

The final reduced coefficients are therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:alpha_final_exec}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,
\Bigl(
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:beta_final_exec}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Canonical symmetric mixed-target condition}

For the canonical mixed odd-active target one needs
\[
\Lambda_E=\Lambda_O\neq0.
\]
Thus the exact scalar equality condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2\Bigl(
o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr)
+
\Bigl(
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr)
=
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}-\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}.
}
\label{eq:symmetric_target_scalar}
\end{equation}

A strong sufficient survival condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\right|
<
|\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}|,
}
\label{eq:survival_E}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\right|
<
|\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}|.
}
\label{eq:survival_O}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Honest status}

At this point nothing conceptual remains in the residual transverse audit.

The actual remaining work is exactly:

\begin{enumerate}
\item evaluate the \(p\)-derivative of the projected \(OD\)-self-energy kernel at \(p=0\);
\item take its odd part in \(\xi\);
\item read off \(e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}\) and \(o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}\) using \eqref{eq:eOD_exec}--\eqref{eq:oOD_exec};
\item split \(a_{E;DD},a_{O;DD}\) into odd/even parts and keep only \eqref{eq:DD_odd_coeffs};
\item insert the result into \eqref{eq:alpha_final_exec}, \eqref{eq:beta_final_exec}, and \eqref{eq:symmetric_target_scalar}.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

The residual transverse audit is now fully reduced to four explicit numbers:
\[
e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\quad
o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\quad
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\quad
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}.
\]

They are extracted by the universal projector rule
\[
e_{0;AB,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_{AB,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}),
\qquad
o_{0;AB,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_{AB,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}),
\]
with \(AB\in\{OD,DD\}\).

For \(OD\), the odd kernel is obtained from the projected self-energy by
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{OD,\mathrm{odd}}
=
\frac12\left[
\Pi_Q\left(\partial_{p_\mu}\Sigma_O^{(OD)}\right)_{p=0,\xi}\Pi_Q
-
\Pi_Q\left(\partial_{p_\mu}\Sigma_O^{(OD)}\right)_{p=0,-\xi}\Pi_Q
\right].
\]

For \(DD\), the invariant decomposition is already
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_{\parallel;DD}n^\mu\Sigma_3
+
a_{E;DD}E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
a_{O;DD}J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a,
\]
so only
\[
a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}
=
\frac12(a_{E;DD}(\xi)-a_{E;DD}(-\xi)),
\qquad
a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}
=
\frac12(a_{O;DD}(\xi)-a_{O;DD}(-\xi))
\]
matter.

Under leading \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry,
\[
\Delta e_{\mathrm{rem}}
=
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\mathrm{rem}}
=
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}.
\]

Therefore the final reduced coefficients are
\[
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr),
\]
\[
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
\]

The canonical symmetric mixed-target condition is reduced to the single scalar equation
\[
2\Bigl(
o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr)
+
\Bigl(
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr)
=
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}-\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}.
\]

So the remaining microscopic task is no longer structural:
it is the literal evaluation of those four odd residual coefficients.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Combined Residual Insertion from \(OD+DO+DD\)}

\section{Goal}

The principal transverse pair has already been isolated from the mixed shell--defect blocks:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\mathrm{inv}}],
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\mathrm{inv}}].
}
\label{eq:ODDD_principal_pair}
\end{equation}

Hence the full residual completion problem is now exactly:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)
=
(\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}},\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}})
+
r_{OD/DO}
+
r_{DD}.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_full_split}
\end{equation}

\section{1. Universal residual projector rule}

For any candidate residual block \(AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}\), define the tangent-projected first-order kernel
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB}(\xi):=\Pi_Q\,\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}(\xi)\,\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_MAB}
\end{equation}
Its reflection-odd part is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\frac12
\Bigl(
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB}(\xi)-\mathcal M^\mu_{AB}(-\xi)
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:ODDD_MAB_odd}
\end{equation}
The projector-visible transverse coefficients are then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;AB,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M_{AB,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}\bigr),
}
\label{eq:ODDD_eAB}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
o_{0;AB,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M_{AB,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:ODDD_oAB}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact \(OD\)-sector insertion}

On the minimal admissible background
\[
\bar\Phi_{\min}=(0,\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)),
\]
the mixed quartic interaction
\[
\lambda_{OD}\rho_O\rho_D
\]
generates the background-induced cubic vertices
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\sim
\lambda_{OD}\,\bar\chi_B(\xi),
\qquad
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\zeta\zeta}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\sim
\lambda_{OD}\,\bar n_B(\xi).
\label{eq:ODDD_cubic_vertices}
\end{equation}

Choose orthonormal projected mode bases
\[
\mathcal H_{OO}u_m=E_m^O u_m,
\qquad
\mathcal H_{DD}v_n=E_n^D v_n,
\]
and define the regulated projected propagators
\begin{equation}
G_O(q)
=
\Bigl(
P_O[\mathcal H_{OO}+R_{O,k}]P_O
\Bigr)^{-1},
\qquad
G_D(q)
=
\Bigl(
P_D[\mathcal H_{DD}+R_{D,k}]P_D
\Bigr)^{-1}.
\label{eq:ODDD_projected_props}
\end{equation}

The explicit projected mixed self-energies are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p)
=
-\lambda_{OD}^2
\int_q
\sum_{m,n}
\mathcal B^\chi_{mn}\,
\mathcal P_O(p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(q)\,
\mathcal B^\chi_{nm}\,
\mathcal P_O(-p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(p+q)\,
\partial_tR_k(q),
}
\label{eq:ODDD_SigmaO}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p)
=
-\lambda_{OD}^2
\int_q
\sum_{m,n}
\mathcal B^n_{nm}\,
\mathcal P_D(p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(q)\,
\mathcal B^n_{mn}\,
\mathcal P_D(-p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(p+q)\,
\partial_tR_k(q).
}
\label{eq:ODDD_SigmaD}
\end{equation}

The correct residual transport kernel is the first momentum derivative of the \emph{projected} mixed self-energy:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{OD/DO,\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
:=
\frac12
\Pi_Q
\left[
\partial_{p_\mu}\Bigl(\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p;\xi)+\Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p;\xi)\Bigr)_{p=0}
-
\partial_{p_\mu}\Bigl(\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p;-\xi)+\Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p;-\xi)\Bigr)_{p=0}
\right]
\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_MODDO_odd}
\end{equation}

Hence the exchange-type residual coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;OD/DO,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(
\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M_{OD/DO,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}
\bigr),
}
\label{eq:ODDD_eODDO}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
o_{0;OD/DO,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(
\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M_{OD/DO,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:ODDD_oODDO}
\end{equation}

If \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry is valid at the projected level, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;DO,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}=e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_{0;DO,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}=o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
}
\label{eq:ODDD_exchange}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{OD/DO}
=
\Bigl(
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\;
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:ODDD_rODDO}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exact \(DD\)-sector insertion}

The \(DD\)-block already has the explicit invariant decomposition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_{\parallel;DD}(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3
+
a_{E;DD}(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
a_{O;DD}(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_MDD}
\end{equation}

Define the reflection-odd parts
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\frac12\Bigl(a_{E;DD}(\xi)-a_{E;DD}(-\xi)\Bigr),
\qquad
a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\frac12\Bigl(a_{O;DD}(\xi)-a_{O;DD}(-\xi)\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:ODDD_DDoddparts}
\end{equation}

Then the direct \(DD\)-residual coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}},
\qquad
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_eDDoDD}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M_{DD,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}\bigr),
\qquad
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M_{DD,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:ODDD_DDprojectors}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{DD}
=
\Bigl(
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\;
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:ODDD_rDD}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Final combined residual vector}

Combining \eqref{eq:ODDD_rODDO} and \eqref{eq:ODDD_rDD}, the full residual correction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\mathrm{rem}}
=
\Bigl(
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\;
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:ODDD_rrem_final}
\end{equation}

Therefore the complete transverse coefficient point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
}
\label{eq:ODDD_LambdaE_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_O
=
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_LambdaO_final}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Final \texorpdfstring{$\alpha,\beta$}{alpha,beta} coefficients}

Using the already fixed branch dictionary
\[
\alpha=I_\theta\,\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\,\Lambda_O,
\]
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
I_\theta
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:ODDD_alpha_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
I_\theta
\Bigl(
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:ODDD_beta_final}
\end{equation}

If the explicit seed profile is used, one may further substitute
\[
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa.
\]

\section{6. Canonical symmetric mixed-target condition}

The canonical mixed odd-active target requires
\[
\Lambda_E=\Lambda_O\neq0.
\]
Hence the exact scalar equality condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2\Bigl(
o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr)
+
\Bigl(
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr)
=
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}-\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_symmetry_condition}
\end{equation}

The strong sufficient survival conditions are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\right|
<
|\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}|,
}
\label{eq:ODDD_survivalE}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\right|
<
|\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}|.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_survivalO}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Honest closure status}

At the present stage, the combined \(OD+DD\) problem is fully reduced to the four explicit odd residual numbers
\[
e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\quad
o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\quad
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\quad
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}.
\]
No further structural reduction is needed.

What remains open is not the formula, but the actual evaluation/sign of these four quantities.

\section{Final Summary}

The full residual transverse completion beyond the principal \(TD+DT\) pair is
\[
\boxed{
r_{\mathrm{rem}}
=
r_{OD/DO}
+
r_{DD}.
}
\]

The exchange-type \(OD/DO\) correction is obtained from the projected mixed self-energies
\[
\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p),
\qquad
\Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p),
\]
through the first momentum derivative at \(p=0\), followed by reflection-odd extraction and transverse projection:
\[
\boxed{
e_{0;OD/DO,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_{OD/DO,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}),
\qquad
o_{0;OD/DO,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_{OD/DO,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}).
}
\]

The intrinsic \(DD\)-residual is directly obtained from
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_{\parallel;DD}n^\mu\Sigma_3
+
a_{E;DD}E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
a_{O;DD}J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\]
by taking only the reflection-odd parts of \(a_{E;DD}\) and \(a_{O;DD}\):
\[
\boxed{
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}},
\qquad
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}.
}
\]

Under leading \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry,
\[
\boxed{
r_{\mathrm{rem}}
=
\Bigl(
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\;
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
}
\]

Therefore the final transverse coefficient point is
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_O
=
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}.
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\]

For the canonical symmetric mixed odd-active target, the exact scalar condition is
\[
\boxed{
2\bigl(o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}\bigr)
=
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}-\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}.
}
\]

So the combined \(OD+DD\) problem is now fully reduced to four odd residual coefficients and their insertion into the final \((\alpha,\beta)\) sheet.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Combined \(OD+DD\) Residual Completion of the Transverse Coefficient Point}

\section{Goal}

The leading transverse pair is already isolated in the principal mixed blocks
\[
TD+DT.
\]
Therefore the only remaining transverse completion problem is to insert the residual exchange-type sector \(OD/DO\) together with the intrinsic defect-tangent sector \(DD\).

The exact transverse coefficient point must therefore be written in the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)
=
(\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}},\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}})
+
r_{OD/DO}
+
r_{DD}.
}
\label{eq:combined_goal}
\end{equation}

\section{1. Principal pair}

The already isolated principal pair is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
=
e_{0;TD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DT}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
=
o_{0;TD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DT}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:combined_principal}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, at the conservative working level,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}\approx e_{0;K}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}\approx o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:combined_Kpair}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Universal odd projector rule}

For any residual block \(AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}\), define the tangent-projected first-order kernel
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB}(\xi):=\Pi_Q\,\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}(\xi)\,\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:combined_MAB}
\end{equation}
Its reflection-odd part is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\frac12
\Bigl(
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB}(\xi)-\mathcal M^\mu_{AB}(-\xi)
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:combined_odd}
\end{equation}

Then the transverse residual coefficients are extracted by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;AB,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M_{AB,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}\bigr),
}
\label{eq:combined_eproj}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
o_{0;AB,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M_{AB,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:combined_oproj}
\end{equation}

So only the odd parts of \(OD,DO,DD\) matter.

\section{3. Exact \(OD\)-sector insertion}

Choose projected mode bases
\[
\mathcal H_{OO}u_m=E_m^O u_m,
\qquad
\mathcal H_{DD}v_n=E_n^D v_n,
\]
with projectors
\[
P_O=\sum_m|u_m\rangle\langle u_m|,
\qquad
P_D=\sum_n|v_n\rangle\langle v_n|.
\]

The projected propagators are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_O(q;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
\Bigl(P_O[\mathcal H_{OO}+R_{O,k}]P_O\Bigr)^{-1},
\qquad
G_D(q;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
\Bigl(P_D[\mathcal H_{DD}+R_{D,k}]P_D\Bigr)^{-1}.
}
\label{eq:combined_props}
\end{equation}

The projected mixed self-energy on the \(O\)-sector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
-
\int\!\frac{d^d q}{(2\pi)^d}
\sum_{m,n}
\mathcal V^{(OD)}_{O;mn}(p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(q)\,
\mathcal V^{(OD)}_{O;nm}(-p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(p+q)\,
\partial_t R_k(q),
}
\label{eq:combined_SigmaO}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal V^{(OD)}_{O;mn}(p,q)
=
\left\langle
u_m
\middle|
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta}(p,q;\bar\Phi_{\min})
\middle|
v_n
\right\rangle
=
\lambda_{OD}\,\mathcal B_{mn}^{\chi}(\xi)\,\mathcal P_O(p,q),
}
\label{eq:combined_VO}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\mathcal B_{mn}^{\chi}(\xi)\sim\langle u_m,\bar\chi_B(\xi)v_n\rangle.
\]

Likewise the \(D\)-sector companion mixed self-energy is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p;\bar\Phi_{\min})
=
-
\int\!\frac{d^d q}{(2\pi)^d}
\sum_{m,n}
\widetilde{\mathcal V}^{(OD)}_{D;nm}(p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(q)\,
\widetilde{\mathcal V}^{(OD)}_{D;mn}(-p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(p+q)\,
\partial_t R_k(q),
}
\label{eq:combined_SigmaD}
\end{equation}
with schematic factorization
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal V}^{(OD)}_{D;nm}(p,q)
=
\lambda_{OD}\,\mathcal B_{nm}^{n}(\xi)\,\mathcal P_D(p,q),
}
\label{eq:combined_VD}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\mathcal B_{nm}^{n}(\xi)\sim \langle v_n,\bar n_B(\xi)u_m\rangle.
\]

The exact odd transport kernel from the exchange-type sector is then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{OD/DO,\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\frac12\Pi_Q
\left[
\partial_{p_\mu}\Bigl(\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p;\xi)+\Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p;\xi)\Bigr)_{p=0}
-
\partial_{p_\mu}\Bigl(\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p;-\xi)+\Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p;-\xi)\Bigr)_{p=0}
\right]
\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:combined_MODDO}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;OD/DO,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a
\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M_{OD/DO,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}\bigr),
}
\label{eq:combined_eODDO}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
o_{0;OD/DO,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a
\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M_{OD/DO,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:combined_oODDO}
\end{equation}

If the projected background and regulator preserve \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;DO,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}=e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_{0;DO,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}=o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:combined_exchange}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{OD/DO}
=
\Bigl(
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\;
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:combined_rODDO}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Exact \(DD\)-sector insertion}

The projected \(DD\)-kernel already has the explicit invariant decomposition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_{\parallel;DD}(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3
+
a_{E;DD}(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
a_{O;DD}(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a.
}
\label{eq:combined_MDD}
\end{equation}

Define the reflection-odd transverse coefficients
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\frac12\Bigl(a_{E;DD}(\xi)-a_{E;DD}(-\xi)\Bigr),
\qquad
a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\frac12\Bigl(a_{O;DD}(\xi)-a_{O;DD}(-\xi)\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:combined_aEodd_aOodd}
\end{equation}

Then the \(DD\)-residual contribution is directly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}},
\qquad
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}.
}
\label{eq:combined_eDD_oDD}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M_{DD,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}\bigr),
\qquad
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M_{DD,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:combined_projector_DD}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{DD}
=
\Bigl(
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\;
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:combined_rDD}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Final combined residual vector}

Combining \eqref{eq:combined_rODDO} and \eqref{eq:combined_rDD}, the exact residual correction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\mathrm{rem}}
=
\Bigl(
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\;
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:combined_rrem}
\end{equation}

Hence the full transverse coefficient point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
}
\label{eq:combined_LambdaE}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_O
=
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:combined_LambdaO}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Final \texorpdfstring{$\alpha,\beta$}{alpha,beta} insertion}

Using the exact overlap dictionary
\[
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O,
\]
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
I_\theta
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:combined_alpha}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
I_\theta
\Bigl(
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:combined_beta}
\end{equation}

For the explicit defect profile one may insert
\[
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\]
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:combined_alpha_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:combined_beta_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Canonical symmetric mixed-target condition}

The canonical mixed odd-active target requires
\[
\Lambda_E=\Lambda_O\neq 0.
\]
Thus the exact scalar equality condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2\Bigl(
o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr)
+
\Bigl(
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr)
=
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}-\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}.
}
\label{eq:combined_symmetry_condition}
\end{equation}

A strong sufficient survival condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\right|
<
|\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}|,
}
\label{eq:combined_survivalE}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\right|
<
|\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}|.
}
\label{eq:combined_survivalO}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Honest status}

At this point the combined \(OD+DD\) problem is reduced completely to four explicit odd residual quantities:
\[
e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\qquad
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}.
\]

No further structural theorem is needed.
What remains open is only their actual evaluation/sign.

\section{Final Summary}

The full residual transverse completion beyond the principal \(TD+DT\) source is
\[
\boxed{
r_{\mathrm{rem}}=r_{OD/DO}+r_{DD}.
}
\]

The \(OD/DO\) part is obtained from the projected mixed self-energies
\[
\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p),\qquad \Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p)
\]
by taking the first momentum derivative at \(p=0\), then the reflection-odd part, and finally the transverse projectors:
\[
\boxed{
e_{0;OD/DO,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_{OD/DO,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}),
\qquad
o_{0;OD/DO,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_{OD/DO,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}).
}
\]

The \(DD\) part is directly read from the invariant decomposition
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_{\parallel;DD}n^\mu\Sigma_3
+
a_{E;DD}E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
a_{O;DD}J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\]
by keeping only the odd parts of \(a_{E;DD}\) and \(a_{O;DD}\):
\[
\boxed{
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}=a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}},
\qquad
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}=a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}.
}
\]

Under leading \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry,
\[
\boxed{
r_{\mathrm{rem}}
=
\Bigl(
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\;
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
}
\]

Hence the final transverse coefficients are
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_O
=
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}.
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O,
}
\]
and with the explicit profile,
\[
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa.
\]

The canonical symmetric mixed-target condition is reduced to the single scalar equation
\[
\boxed{
2\bigl(o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}\bigr)
=
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}-\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}.
}
\]

So the combined \(OD+DD\) problem is now fully reduced to four explicit odd residual coefficients and their literal insertion into the final \((\alpha,\beta)\) sheet.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Combined \(OD+DD\) Residual Bounds and a Usable Sufficient Survival Criterion}

\section{Goal}

At this stage, the residual transverse completion is no longer a structural question.
The exact remaining quantities are
\[
e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},\quad
o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},\quad
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},\quad
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}.
\]
What we now do is reduce these to a finite executable bound package.

\section{1. Principal-plus-residual split}

The exact transverse coefficient point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)=v_{\mathrm{pr}}+r_{\mathrm{rem}},
}
\label{eq:ODDD_bound_split}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
(\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}},\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}})
=
\left(
\frac12(A_E+B_E),\,
\frac12(A_O+B_O)
\right),
}
\label{eq:ODDD_bound_principal}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\mathrm{rem}}
=
\Bigl(
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\;
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:ODDD_bound_residual}
\end{equation}
assuming the leading \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange reduction.

\section{2. Exact overlap packages for the \(OD\)-sector}

The background overlap matrices are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal B^\chi_{mn}:=\langle u_m,\bar\chi_B v_n\rangle,
\qquad
\mathcal B^n_{nm}:=\langle v_n,\bar n_B u_m\rangle.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_BchiBn}
\end{equation}
Define the Hilbert--Schmidt overlap budgets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak B_\chi:=\|P_O\bar\chi_B P_D\|_{\mathrm{HS}},
\qquad
\mathfrak B_n:=\|P_D\bar n_B P_O\|_{\mathrm{HS}}.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_HSbudgets}
\end{equation}
These satisfy the basis identities
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak B_\chi^2
=
\sum_{m,n}|\mathcal B^\chi_{mn}|^2,
\qquad
\mathfrak B_n^2
=
\sum_{m,n}|\mathcal B^n_{nm}|^2.
\label{eq:ODDD_HSbasis}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Propagator and projector derivative budgets}

Let
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_O:=\sup_q\|G_O(q)\|,
\qquad
\mathfrak G_D:=\sup_q\|G_D(q)\|.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_Gbudgets}
\end{equation}
Let the momentum/projector budgets be
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_O^{(0)}:=\sup_q|\mathcal P_O(0,q)|,
\qquad
\mathfrak P_D^{(0)}:=\sup_q|\mathcal P_D(0,q)|,
}
\label{eq:ODDD_P0}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_O^{(1)}:=\sup_q\left|\partial_{p_\mu}\mathcal P_O(p,q)\big|_{p=0}\right|,
\qquad
\mathfrak P_D^{(1)}:=\sup_q\left|\partial_{p_\mu}\mathcal P_D(p,q)\big|_{p=0}\right|.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_P1}
\end{equation}
Likewise define the propagator momentum-derivative budgets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak K_O^{(1)}:=\sup_q\left\|\partial_{p_\mu}G_O(p+q)\big|_{p=0}\right\|,
\qquad
\mathfrak K_D^{(1)}:=\sup_q\left\|\partial_{p_\mu}G_D(p+q)\big|_{p=0}\right\|.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_K1}
\end{equation}

These are the exact finite derivative packages needed by the product rule on the projected loop kernel.

\section{4. Bound for the \(OD\)-odd coefficients}
