The projected \(OD\)-self-energies have the factorized form
\begin{align}
\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p)
&=
-\lambda_{OD}^2
\int_q
\sum_{m,n}
\mathcal B^\chi_{mn}\,
\mathcal P_O(p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(q)\,
\mathcal B^\chi_{nm}\,
\mathcal P_O(-p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(p+q)\,
\partial_tR_k(q),
\label{eq:ODDD_SigmaO_bound_start}
\\
\Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p)
&=
-\lambda_{OD}^2
\int_q
\sum_{m,n}
\mathcal B^n_{nm}\,
\mathcal P_D(p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(q)\,
\mathcal B^n_{mn}\,
\mathcal P_D(-p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(p+q)\,
\partial_tR_k(q).
\label{eq:ODDD_SigmaD_bound_start}
\end{align}

Applying the product rule at \(p=0\), the \(O\)-side derivative contributes two projector-derivative terms and one propagator-derivative term.
Hence define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak L_O
:=
\int_q
\Bigl[
2\mathfrak P_O^{(0)}\mathfrak P_O^{(1)}\mathfrak G_D\mathfrak G_O
+
(\mathfrak P_O^{(0)})^2\mathfrak G_D\mathfrak K_O^{(1)}
\Bigr]
\,|\partial_tR_k(q)|.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_LO}
\end{equation}
Similarly define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak L_D
:=
\int_q
\Bigl[
2\mathfrak P_D^{(0)}\mathfrak P_D^{(1)}\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak G_D
+
(\mathfrak P_D^{(0)})^2\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak K_D^{(1)}
\Bigr]
\,|\partial_tR_k(q)|.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_LD}
\end{equation}

Then the odd projected transport norm from the exchange-type residual obeys
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|\mathcal M_{OD/DO,\mathrm{odd}}\|
\le
\lambda_{OD}^2
\Bigl(
\mathfrak B_\chi^2\,\mathfrak L_O
+
\mathfrak B_n^2\,\mathfrak L_D
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:ODDD_MODDO_bound}
\end{equation}

Since for any \(2\times2\) tangent endomorphism \(M\),
\[
\left|\frac14\Tr(\Sigma_a M)\right|
\le
\frac12\|M\|_{\mathrm{op}},
\]
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|e_{0;OD/DO,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}|,
\ |o_{0;OD/DO,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}|
\le
\frac12\lambda_{OD}^2
\Bigl(
\mathfrak B_\chi^2\,\mathfrak L_O
+
\mathfrak B_n^2\,\mathfrak L_D
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:ODDD_eoOD_bound}
\end{equation}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{OD}
:=
\frac12\lambda_{OD}^2
\Bigl(
\mathfrak B_\chi^2\,\mathfrak L_O
+
\mathfrak B_n^2\,\mathfrak L_D
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:ODDD_rhoOD}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}|,\ |o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}|
\le
\rho_{OD}.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_OD_finalbound}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Exact and bounded \(DD\)-sector coefficients}

The \(DD\)-kernel has the invariant decomposition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_{\parallel;DD}n^\mu\Sigma_3
+
a_{E;DD}E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
a_{O;DD}J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_DD_decomp}
\end{equation}
Define the odd parts
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\frac12\bigl(a_{E;DD}(\xi)-a_{E;DD}(-\xi)\bigr),
\qquad
a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\frac12\bigl(a_{O;DD}(\xi)-a_{O;DD}(-\xi)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:ODDD_DDodd}
\end{equation}
Then exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}},
\qquad
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_DD_exact}
\end{equation}

Introduce the direct \(DD\)-budgets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{DD,E}:=
\sup_\xi |a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)|,
\qquad
\rho_{DD,O}:=
\sup_\xi |a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)|,
\qquad
\rho_{DD}:=\max\{\rho_{DD,E},\rho_{DD,O}\}.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_rhoDD}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}|\le \rho_{DD,E},
\qquad
|o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}|\le \rho_{DD,O},
\qquad
\max\{|e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}|,|o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}|\}\le \rho_{DD}.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_DDbound}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Combined residual bound}

Under the leading exchange reduction,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\mathrm{rem}}
=
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\mathrm{rem}}
=
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_Delta_rem}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta e_{\mathrm{rem}}|
\le
2\rho_{OD}+\rho_{DD,E},
\qquad
|\Delta o_{\mathrm{rem}}|
\le
2\rho_{OD}+\rho_{DD,O}.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_Delta_bound_comp}
\end{equation}
In particular,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|r_{\mathrm{rem}}\|_2
\le
\sqrt{2}\,(2\rho_{OD}+\rho_{DD}).
}
\label{eq:ODDD_rrem_norm}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Strong sufficient survival criterion}

The exact transverse coefficient point is
\[
\Lambda_E=\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{rem}},
\qquad
\Lambda_O=\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{rem}}.
\]
Hence a strong sufficient survival condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2\rho_{OD}+\rho_{DD,E}<|\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}|,
\qquad
2\rho_{OD}+\rho_{DD,O}<|\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}|.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_strong_survival_final}
\end{equation}
A weaker Euclidean sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sqrt{2}\,(2\rho_{OD}+\rho_{DD})
<
\sqrt{(\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}})^2+(\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}})^2}.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_euclid_survival_final}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Final \texorpdfstring{$\alpha,\beta$}{alpha,beta} bound sheet}

Using
\[
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O,
\]
we obtain the exact insertion formulas
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
I_\theta
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:ODDD_alpha_boundsheet}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
I_\theta
\Bigl(
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:ODDD_beta_boundsheet}
\end{equation}
For the explicit defect profile,
\[
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa.
\]

\section{9. Symmetric-target sufficient condition}

The canonical mixed odd-active target requires
\[
\Lambda_E=\Lambda_O\neq0.
\]
An exact equality test still needs the signed residual coefficients.
However, a clear sufficient symmetry-preserving condition is the following:
if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}=\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}},
\qquad
e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}=o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\qquad
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}=o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
}
\label{eq:ODDD_symmetry_preserving}
\end{equation}
then automatically
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_auto_equal}
\end{equation}

Thus the signed mismatch that must vanish in general is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{\mathrm{sym}}
:=
2\bigl(o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}\bigr)
-
\bigl(\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}-\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:ODDD_delta_sym}
\end{equation}
The exact symmetric target is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{\mathrm{sym}}=0.
}
\label{eq:ODDD_delta_sym_zero}
\end{equation}

\section{Honest status}

At this point the combined \(OD+DD\) residual problem is reduced to a finite executable bound package:
\[
\mathfrak B_\chi,\ \mathfrak B_n,\ 
\mathfrak G_O,\ \mathfrak G_D,\ 
\mathfrak P_O^{(0)},\ \mathfrak P_D^{(0)},\
\mathfrak P_O^{(1)},\ \mathfrak P_D^{(1)},\
\mathfrak K_O^{(1)},\ \mathfrak K_D^{(1)},\
\rho_{DD,E},\ \rho_{DD,O}.
\]
No additional conceptual reduction is needed.
What remains is only the literal evaluation of these finite quantities on the intended branch.

\section{Final Summary}

The exchange-type residual \(OD/DO\) can be bounded entirely by the finite packages
\[
\mathfrak B_\chi=\|P_O\bar\chi_B P_D\|_{\mathrm{HS}},
\qquad
\mathfrak B_n=\|P_D\bar n_B P_O\|_{\mathrm{HS}},
\]
together with projected propagator and momentum/projector derivative budgets
\[
\mathfrak G_O,\ \mathfrak G_D,\ 
\mathfrak P_O^{(0)},\ \mathfrak P_D^{(0)},\
\mathfrak P_O^{(1)},\ \mathfrak P_D^{(1)},\
\mathfrak K_O^{(1)},\ \mathfrak K_D^{(1)}.
\]

Its sharp finite bound is
\[
\boxed{
\rho_{OD}
=
\frac12\lambda_{OD}^2
\Bigl(
\mathfrak B_\chi^2\,\mathfrak L_O
+
\mathfrak B_n^2\,\mathfrak L_D
\Bigr),
}
\]
with
\[
\mathfrak L_O
=
\int_q
\Bigl[
2\mathfrak P_O^{(0)}\mathfrak P_O^{(1)}\mathfrak G_D\mathfrak G_O
+
(\mathfrak P_O^{(0)})^2\mathfrak G_D\mathfrak K_O^{(1)}
\Bigr]
|\partial_tR_k(q)|,
\]
\[
\mathfrak L_D
=
\int_q
\Bigl[
2\mathfrak P_D^{(0)}\mathfrak P_D^{(1)}\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak G_D
+
(\mathfrak P_D^{(0)})^2\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak K_D^{(1)}
\Bigr]
|\partial_tR_k(q)|.
\]

The intrinsic defect-tangent residual \(DD\) is directly controlled by the odd parts of its projector-visible transverse coefficients:
\[
\boxed{
\rho_{DD,E}:=\sup_\xi |a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)|,
\qquad
\rho_{DD,O}:=\sup_\xi |a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)|,
\qquad
\rho_{DD}:=\max\{\rho_{DD,E},\rho_{DD,O}\}.
}
\]

Thus the combined residual correction obeys
\[
\boxed{
|\Delta e_{\mathrm{rem}}|
\le
2\rho_{OD}+\rho_{DD,E},
\qquad
|\Delta o_{\mathrm{rem}}|
\le
2\rho_{OD}+\rho_{DD,O},
}
\]
and hence
\[
\boxed{
\|r_{\mathrm{rem}}\|_2
\le
\sqrt2\,(2\rho_{OD}+\rho_{DD}).
}
\]

A strong sufficient survival criterion is
\[
\boxed{
2\rho_{OD}+\rho_{DD,E}<|\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}|,
\qquad
2\rho_{OD}+\rho_{DD,O}<|\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}|.
}
\]

The full transverse coefficient point is therefore
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_O
=
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
}
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\]

Finally, the canonical symmetric mixed-target condition is exactly
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{\mathrm{sym}}
=
2\bigl(o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}\bigr)
-
\bigl(\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}-\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}\bigr)
=0.
}
\]

So the \(OD+DD\) problem is no longer structural.
It is reduced to a finite executable budget test plus, if one wants exact symmetry, one final signed residual equality test.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Optimized-Regulator Reduction of the \(OD\)-Residual Budget}

\section{Goal}

The remaining exchange-type residual budget was
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{OD}
=
\frac12\lambda_{OD}^2
\Bigl(
\mathfrak B_\chi^2\,\mathfrak L_O
+
\mathfrak B_n^2\,\mathfrak L_D
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:rhoOD_old}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\mathfrak L_O,\qquad \mathfrak L_D
\]
still written in terms of abstract propagator/projector derivative packages.

The next nonredundant step is to insert the explicit working regulator choice already fixed in the notes and reduce these packages further.

\section{1. Explicit optimized regulator choice}

The background-adapted sectoral regulator is taken as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_k[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
\mathrm{diag}\bigl(R_{T,k},R_{O,k},R_{D,k}\bigr),
}
\label{eq:reg_diag}
\end{equation}
with the explicit optimized profile
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_{I,k}
=
Z_{I,k}\bigl(k^2-\mathcal H_{II}^{(0)}\bigr)
\Theta\!\bigl(k^2-\mathcal H_{II}^{(0)}\bigr),
\qquad
I\in\{T,O,D\}.
}
\label{eq:reg_opt_operator}
\end{equation}
In momentum representation this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_{I,k}(q)=Z_{I,k}(k^2-q^2)\Theta(k^2-q^2).
}
\label{eq:reg_opt_momentum}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Explicit regulator-derivative bound}

For the optimized momentum profile,
\[
R_{I,k}(q)=Z_{I,k}(k^2-q^2)\Theta(k^2-q^2),
\]
we compute
\begin{align}
\partial_t R_{I,k}(q)
&=
(\partial_t Z_{I,k})(k^2-q^2)\Theta(k^2-q^2)
+
Z_{I,k}\,\partial_t\!\Bigl[(k^2-q^2)\Theta(k^2-q^2)\Bigr].
\end{align}
Since \(t=\ln(k/\Lambda)\), one has \(\partial_t=k\partial_k\), and
\[
\partial_t\!\Bigl[(k^2-q^2)\Theta(k^2-q^2)\Bigr]
=
2k^2\Theta(k^2-q^2),
\]
because the distributional boundary term is multiplied by \(k^2-q^2\) and vanishes.

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_t R_{I,k}(q)
=
\Bigl[
(\partial_t Z_{I,k})(k^2-q^2)
+
2Z_{I,k}k^2
\Bigr]\Theta(k^2-q^2).
}
\label{eq:dR_opt_exact}
\end{equation}
Hence the sharp uniform bound is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak R_{I,k}
:=
\sup_q |\partial_t R_{I,k}(q)|
\le
k^2\bigl(|\partial_t Z_{I,k}|+2|Z_{I,k}|\bigr).
}
\label{eq:Rbudget_opt}
\end{equation}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak R_{OD}
:=
\max\{\mathfrak R_{O,k},\mathfrak R_{D,k}\}
\le
k^2
\max\{
|\partial_t Z_{O,k}|+2|Z_{O,k}|,
\;
|\partial_t Z_{D,k}|+2|Z_{D,k}|
\}.
}
\label{eq:Rbudget_OD}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Propagator bounds}

The notes already reduce the projected propagator part to the explicit projected spectral gaps:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_O\le \Delta_O^{-1},
\qquad
\mathfrak G_D\le \Delta_D^{-1}.
}
\label{eq:G_budget_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Propagator momentum-derivative bounds}

Let
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak V_O
:=
\sup_q
\left\|
\partial_{p_\mu}\mathcal H_{OO}^{\mathrm{eff}}(p+q)\big|_{p=0}
\right\|,
\qquad
\mathfrak V_D
:=
\sup_q
\left\|
\partial_{p_\mu}\mathcal H_{DD}^{\mathrm{eff}}(p+q)\big|_{p=0}
\right\|.
}
\label{eq:V_budgets}
\end{equation}
Since
\[
G_I=(P_I[\mathcal H_{II}+R_{I,k}]P_I)^{-1},
\]
the resolvent identity gives
\[
\partial_{p_\mu}G_I
=
-
G_I
\bigl(\partial_{p_\mu}\mathcal H_{II}^{\mathrm{eff}}\bigr)
G_I.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak K_O^{(1)}
\le
\mathfrak G_O^2\,\mathfrak V_O
\le
\Delta_O^{-2}\mathfrak V_O,
\qquad
\mathfrak K_D^{(1)}
\le
\mathfrak G_D^2\,\mathfrak V_D
\le
\Delta_D^{-2}\mathfrak V_D.
}
\label{eq:K1_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Regulator-support momentum volume}

For the optimized cutoff, the support of \(\partial_tR_{I,k}\) is contained in
\[
q^2\le k^2.
\]
Define the support volume
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak Q_k
:=
\int_{q^2\le k^2}\frac{d^d q}{(2\pi)^d}
=
\frac{S_{d-1}}{d(2\pi)^d}k^d,
}
\label{eq:Qk_def}
\end{equation}
where \(S_{d-1}\) is the area of the unit \((d-1)\)-sphere.

\section{6. Explicit \texorpdfstring{$\mathfrak L_O,\mathfrak L_D$}{LO,LD} bounds}

Recall
\begin{align}
\mathfrak L_O
&=
\int_q
\Bigl[
2\mathfrak P_O^{(0)}\mathfrak P_O^{(1)}\mathfrak G_D\mathfrak G_O
+
(\mathfrak P_O^{(0)})^2\mathfrak G_D\mathfrak K_O^{(1)}
\Bigr]
\,|\partial_tR_k(q)|,
\\
\mathfrak L_D
&=
\int_q
\Bigl[
2\mathfrak P_D^{(0)}\mathfrak P_D^{(1)}\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak G_D
+
(\mathfrak P_D^{(0)})^2\mathfrak G_O\mathfrak K_D^{(1)}
\Bigr]
\,|\partial_tR_k(q)|.
\end{align}
Using \eqref{eq:Rbudget_OD}, \eqref{eq:G_budget_explicit}, \eqref{eq:K1_explicit}, and \eqref{eq:Qk_def}, we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak L_O
\le
\mathfrak Q_k\,\mathfrak R_{OD}
\left[
2\mathfrak P_O^{(0)}\mathfrak P_O^{(1)}\Delta_D^{-1}\Delta_O^{-1}
+
(\mathfrak P_O^{(0)})^2\Delta_D^{-1}\Delta_O^{-2}\mathfrak V_O
\right],
}
\label{eq:LO_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak L_D
\le
\mathfrak Q_k\,\mathfrak R_{OD}
\left[
2\mathfrak P_D^{(0)}\mathfrak P_D^{(1)}\Delta_O^{-1}\Delta_D^{-1}
+
(\mathfrak P_D^{(0)})^2\Delta_O^{-1}\Delta_D^{-2}\mathfrak V_D
\right].
}
\label{eq:LD_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Fully explicit \(OD\)-residual budget}

Substituting \eqref{eq:LO_explicit} and \eqref{eq:LD_explicit} into \eqref{eq:rhoOD_old} yields
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{OD}
\le
\frac12\lambda_{OD}^2\,\mathfrak Q_k\,\mathfrak R_{OD}
\Biggl\{
\mathfrak B_\chi^2
\left[
2\mathfrak P_O^{(0)}\mathfrak P_O^{(1)}\Delta_D^{-1}\Delta_O^{-1}
+
(\mathfrak P_O^{(0)})^2\Delta_D^{-1}\Delta_O^{-2}\mathfrak V_O
\right]
+
\mathfrak B_n^2
\left[
2\mathfrak P_D^{(0)}\mathfrak P_D^{(1)}\Delta_O^{-1}\Delta_D^{-1}
+
(\mathfrak P_D^{(0)})^2\Delta_O^{-1}\Delta_D^{-2}\mathfrak V_D
\right]
\Biggr\}.
}
\label{eq:rhoOD_fully_explicit}
\end{equation}

This is the sharpest explicit working-branch bound currently licensed by the uploaded notes.

\section{8. Combined \(OD+DD\) survival criterion}

The \(DD\)-sector remains directly controlled by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{DD,E}:=\sup_\xi |a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)|,
\qquad
\rho_{DD,O}:=\sup_\xi |a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)|,
\qquad
\rho_{DD}:=\max\{\rho_{DD,E},\rho_{DD,O}\}.
}
\label{eq:DD_budget_repeat}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta e_{\mathrm{rem}}|
\le
2\rho_{OD}+\rho_{DD,E},
\qquad
|\Delta o_{\mathrm{rem}}|
\le
2\rho_{OD}+\rho_{DD,O}.
}
\label{eq:Delta_rem_explicit}
\end{equation}

Therefore the strong sufficient survival condition becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2\rho_{OD}+\rho_{DD,E}<|\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}|,
\qquad
2\rho_{OD}+\rho_{DD,O}<|\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}|.
}
\label{eq:survival_explicit_final}
\end{equation}

A Euclidean sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sqrt2\,(2\rho_{OD}+\rho_{DD})
<
\sqrt{(\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}})^2+(\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}})^2}.
}
\label{eq:survival_euclid_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{9. Final coefficient sheet}

The full transverse coefficient point is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O
=
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:Lambda_final_explicit}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=I_\theta\,\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\,\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:alpha_beta_final_explicit}
\end{equation}
For the explicit defect profile,
\[
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa.
\]

\section{10. Honest status}

The remaining \(OD+DD\) completion is no longer a structural problem.

It is reduced to the finite executable package
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak B_\chi,\ \mathfrak B_n,\ 
\Delta_O,\ \Delta_D,\ 
Z_{O,k},\ Z_{D,k},\ 
\partial_t Z_{O,k},\ \partial_t Z_{D,k},\
\mathfrak P_O^{(0)},\ \mathfrak P_D^{(0)},\
\mathfrak P_O^{(1)},\ \mathfrak P_D^{(1)},\
\mathfrak V_O,\ \mathfrak V_D,\
\rho_{DD,E},\ \rho_{DD,O}.
}
\]
Once these are evaluated on the intended branch, the residual transverse audit is decided.

\section{Final Summary}

Using the explicit optimized regulator
\[
R_{I,k}(q)=Z_{I,k}(k^2-q^2)\Theta(k^2-q^2),
\]
the regulator derivative factor is no longer abstract:
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak R_{I,k}
\le
k^2\bigl(|\partial_t Z_{I,k}|+2|Z_{I,k}|\bigr).
}
\]

The projected propagators are bounded by the explicit projected gaps:
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_O\le \Delta_O^{-1},
\qquad
\mathfrak G_D\le \Delta_D^{-1}.
}
\]

The propagator momentum-derivative budgets satisfy
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak K_O^{(1)}\le \Delta_O^{-2}\mathfrak V_O,
\qquad
\mathfrak K_D^{(1)}\le \Delta_D^{-2}\mathfrak V_D.
}
\]

Therefore the exchange-type residual budget becomes
\[
\boxed{
\rho_{OD}
\le
\frac12\lambda_{OD}^2\,\mathfrak Q_k\,\mathfrak R_{OD}
\Biggl\{
\mathfrak B_\chi^2
\left[
2\mathfrak P_O^{(0)}\mathfrak P_O^{(1)}\Delta_D^{-1}\Delta_O^{-1}
+
(\mathfrak P_O^{(0)})^2\Delta_D^{-1}\Delta_O^{-2}\mathfrak V_O
\right]
+
\mathfrak B_n^2
\left[
2\mathfrak P_D^{(0)}\mathfrak P_D^{(1)}\Delta_O^{-1}\Delta_D^{-1}
+
(\mathfrak P_D^{(0)})^2\Delta_O^{-1}\Delta_D^{-2}\mathfrak V_D
\right]
\Biggr\}.
}
\]

The \(DD\)-sector is controlled directly by
\[
\boxed{
\rho_{DD,E}=\sup_\xi|a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)|,
\qquad
\rho_{DD,O}=\sup_\xi|a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)|.
}
\]

Hence the strong sufficient combined survival criterion is
\[
\boxed{
2\rho_{OD}+\rho_{DD,E}<|\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}|,
\qquad
2\rho_{OD}+\rho_{DD,O}<|\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}|.
}
\]

So the \(OD+DD\) residual problem is now reduced to a finite explicit budget test on the intended branch.

\section{Actual Working PDE with the Full \(OD+DO+DD\) Residual Insertion}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

We now stop rewriting the residual sector as abstract budgets only.
Instead, we insert the \(OD\)- and \(DD\)-residuals directly into the transverse coefficient point and write the actual working PDE in the current reference frame.

At the theorem level currently licensed by the uploaded notes, this is the furthest honest forward form:
the residuals are not yet numerically populated, but their exact insertion structure is now complete.

\section{1. Principal transverse pair}

The leading transverse pair is already isolated as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
=
e_{0;TD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DT}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
=
o_{0;TD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DT}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:actual_pr_pair}
\end{equation}

In the current reference frame, the reduced coefficients satisfy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:actual_alpha_beta_dict}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exchange-type \(OD/DO\) residual}

The mixed quartic interaction
\[
\lambda_{OD}\rho_O\rho_D
\]
generates the background-induced cubic vertices
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\nu\zeta}\sim \lambda_{OD}\bar\chi_B(\xi),
\qquad
\Gamma^{(3)}_{\nu\zeta\zeta}\sim \lambda_{OD}\bar n_B(\xi).
}
\label{eq:actual_OD_vertices}
\end{equation}

The corresponding projected mixed self-energies are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p)
=
-\int_q\sum_{m,n}
\mathcal V^{(OD)}_{O;mn}(p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(q)\,
\mathcal V^{(OD)}_{O;nm}(-p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(p+q)\,
\partial_tR_k(q),
}
\label{eq:actual_SigmaO}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal V^{(OD)}_{O;mn}(p,q)
=
\lambda_{OD}\,\mathcal B^\chi_{mn}(\xi)\,\mathcal P_O(p,q),
\qquad
\mathcal B^\chi_{mn}=\langle u_m,\bar\chi_B v_n\rangle,
}
\label{eq:actual_VO}
\end{equation}
and similarly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p)
=
-\int_q\sum_{m,n}
\widetilde{\mathcal V}^{(OD)}_{D;nm}(p,q)\,
G_O^{(m)}(q)\,
\widetilde{\mathcal V}^{(OD)}_{D;mn}(-p,q)\,
G_D^{(n)}(p+q)\,
\partial_tR_k(q),
}
\label{eq:actual_SigmaD}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal V}^{(OD)}_{D;nm}(p,q)
=
\lambda_{OD}\,\mathcal B^n_{nm}(\xi)\,\mathcal P_D(p,q),
\qquad
\mathcal B^n_{nm}=\langle v_n,\bar n_B u_m\rangle.
}
\label{eq:actual_VD}
\end{equation}

The reflection-odd projected transport kernel is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{OD/DO,\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\frac12\Pi_Q
\left[
\partial_{p_\mu}\bigl(\Sigma_O^{(OD)}+\Sigma_D^{(OD)}\bigr)_{p=0,\xi}
-
\partial_{p_\mu}\bigl(\Sigma_O^{(OD)}+\Sigma_D^{(OD)}\bigr)_{p=0,-\xi}
\right]
\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:actual_MODDO}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;OD/DO,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_{OD/DO,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}\bigr),
}
\label{eq:actual_eODDO}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
o_{0;OD/DO,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_{OD/DO,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:actual_oODDO}
\end{equation}

If the projected mixed sector preserves \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;DO,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}=e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_{0;DO,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}=o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:actual_exchange}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{OD/DO}
=
\Bigl(
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\;
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:actual_rODDO}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Intrinsic \(DD\) residual}

The projected \(DD\)-kernel is already of the explicit transverse form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_{\parallel;DD}(\theta)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
a_{E;DD}(\theta)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
a_{O;DD}(\theta)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
}
\label{eq:actual_MDD}
\end{equation}

Define the odd parts
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\frac12\bigl(a_{E;DD}(\xi)-a_{E;DD}(-\xi)\bigr),
\qquad
a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\frac12\bigl(a_{O;DD}(\xi)-a_{O;DD}(-\xi)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:actual_DDodd}
\end{equation}

Then the direct \(DD\)-residual coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}},
\qquad
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}.
}
\label{eq:actual_eDDoDD}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_{DD,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}\bigr),
\qquad
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\frac14J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_{DD,\mu,\mathrm{odd}}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:actual_DDprojector}
\end{equation}

So
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{DD}
=
\Bigl(
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\;
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:actual_rDD}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Final combined residual transverse pair}

Combining \eqref{eq:actual_rODDO} and \eqref{eq:actual_rDD},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\mathrm{rem}}
=
\Bigl(
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\;
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:actual_rrem}
\end{equation}

Therefore the full transverse coefficient point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
}
\label{eq:actual_LambdaE}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_O
=
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:actual_LambdaO}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Final inserted \texorpdfstring{$\alpha,\beta$}{alpha,beta} sheet}

Using \eqref{eq:actual_alpha_beta_dict},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
I_\theta
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:actual_alpha}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
I_\theta
\Bigl(
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:actual_beta}
\end{equation}

For the explicit defect profile,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:actual_Itheta}
\end{equation}
So the actual inserted transverse coefficients become
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:actual_alpha_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:actual_beta_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Actual working PDE}

The current actual working PDE in the reference frame is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
\alpha\Bigl(
\sigma_1(-i\partial_{q_1})
\Bigr)
-
\beta\Bigl(
\sigma_2(-i\partial_{q_2})
\Bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0,
}
\label{eq:actual_working_PDE_raw}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\]
and \(\alpha,\beta\) given by \eqref{eq:actual_alpha_explicit}--\eqref{eq:actual_beta_explicit}.

Equivalently, in the symmetric canonical target basis where one wants \(\alpha=\beta\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_\perp^{(1)}\sigma_1(-i\partial_{q_1})
-
v_\perp^{(2)}\sigma_2(-i\partial_{q_2})
\Bigr]\chi=0,
}
\label{eq:actual_working_PDE_can}
\end{equation}
where
\[
v_\perp^{(1)}=\alpha,
\qquad
v_\perp^{(2)}=\beta.
\]

\section{7. Symmetric mixed-target condition}

The canonical mixed odd-active target requires
\[
\alpha=\beta
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\Lambda_E=\Lambda_O.
\]
Thus the exact scalar condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2\Bigl(
o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr)
+
\Bigl(
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr)
=
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}-\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}.
}
\label{eq:actual_sym_target}
\end{equation}

If this holds, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:actual_alpha_equal_beta}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Strong sufficient survival condition}

A strong sufficient condition for the transverse carrier to survive is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\right|
<
|\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}|,
}
\label{eq:actual_survival_E}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\right|
<
|\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}|.
}
\label{eq:actual_survival_O}
\end{equation}

\section{9. Honest status}

At this point the \(OD+DD\) sector is not conceptually open any more.

The exact remaining unknowns are only the four odd residual numbers
\[
e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\quad
o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\quad
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\quad
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}.
\]

Everything else is already inserted into the actual working PDE.

\section{Final Summary}

The full residual transverse completion has now been inserted explicitly.

The exchange-type residual is generated by the projected mixed self-energies
\[
\Sigma_O^{(OD)}(p),\qquad \Sigma_D^{(OD)}(p),
\]
with factorized projected vertices
\[
\mathcal V^{(OD)}_{O;mn}=\lambda_{OD}\mathcal B^\chi_{mn}\mathcal P_O,
\qquad
\widetilde{\mathcal V}^{(OD)}_{D;nm}=\lambda_{OD}\mathcal B^n_{nm}\mathcal P_D.
\]

The intrinsic \(DD\)-residual is directly projector-visible through
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_{\parallel;DD}n^\mu\sigma_3
+
a_{E;DD}E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
a_{O;DD}J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\]

Under leading \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry, the full residual vector is
\[
\boxed{
r_{\mathrm{rem}}
=
\Bigl(
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
\;
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
}
\]

Therefore the full transverse coefficient point is
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_O
=
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}.
}
\]

Hence the actual inserted transverse coefficients are
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
\Bigr).
}
\]

The canonical symmetric mixed-target condition is the single scalar equation
\[
\boxed{
2\bigl(o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(o_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}-e_{0;DD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}\bigr)
=
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}-\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}.
}
\]

So the actual working PDE is already fully populated except for those four odd residual numbers.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Actual Forward Form of the Transverse Coefficient Sheet Including \(OD+DD\)}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

We now stop leaving the residual sector as an abstract correction vector only.

Instead, we use the already-closed local invariant algebra to write the \(DD\)-sector explicitly at leading and first subleading odd order, and we absorb the \(OD\)-sector into the same local odd expansion class.

This produces an actual corrected coefficient sheet for \((\alpha,\beta)\), not just a residual placeholder.

\section{1. General local odd expansion for every transverse contribution}

The complete shell-compatible local transport kernel has the invariant form
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)
=
h_\parallel(\xi)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
h_E(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
h_O(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
V^\mu_{\mathrm{irr}}(\xi),
\label{eq:AF_hkernel}
\end{equation}
and parity implies that every principal transport density must carry one explicit odd factor.
Hence the most general local odd expansions are
\begin{equation}
h_E(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal E_1(\mathcal X(\xi))
+
\theta'(\xi)^3\,\mathcal E_3(\mathcal X(\xi))
+
O_{\mathrm{odd},\ge 5},
\label{eq:AF_hE_general}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
h_O(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal O_1(\mathcal X(\xi))
+
\theta'(\xi)^3\,\mathcal O_3(\mathcal X(\xi))
+
O_{\mathrm{odd},\ge 5},
\label{eq:AF_hO_general}
\end{equation}
where the local invariant list is parity-even:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal X(\xi)=\bigl(X_0(\xi),X_1(\xi),X_2(\xi),\dots\bigr),
\qquad
X_0=\theta^2,
\quad
X_1=\theta'^2,
\quad
X_2=\theta\theta'',
\ \dots
\label{eq:AF_Xlist}
\end{equation}

Therefore every surviving \(DD\)- or \(OD\)-residual contribution must belong to this same odd local class.

\section{2. Leading local expansion of the \(DD\)-sector}

The projected \(DD\)-kernel already has the explicit transverse decomposition
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_{\parallel;DD}(\xi)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
a_{E;DD}(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
a_{O;DD}(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:AF_MDD}
\end{equation}

Because only the odd part survives after graded projection, the transverse coefficients must have the local form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)
\left[
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
+
\sum_A \Lambda_{E;DD,A}^{(2)}X_A(\xi)
\right]
+
O_{\mathrm{odd},\ge 5},
}
\label{eq:AF_aEDD_expand}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)
\left[
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
+
\sum_A \Lambda_{O;DD,A}^{(2)}X_A(\xi)
\right]
+
O_{\mathrm{odd},\ge 5}.
}
\label{eq:AF_aODD_expand}
\end{equation}

At the first nontrivial level it is enough to keep
\[
X_0=\theta^2,
\qquad
X_1=\theta'^2.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl[
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
+
\Lambda_{E;DD,0}^{(2)}\theta(\xi)^2
+
\Lambda_{E;DD,1}^{(2)}\theta'(\xi)^2
\Bigr]
+
O_{\mathrm{odd},\ge 5},
}
\label{eq:AF_aEDD_trunc}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl[
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
+
\Lambda_{O;DD,0}^{(2)}\theta(\xi)^2
+
\Lambda_{O;DD,1}^{(2)}\theta'(\xi)^2
\Bigr]
+
O_{\mathrm{odd},\ge 5}.
}
\label{eq:AF_aODD_trunc}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Projection of the \(DD\)-sector}

The reduced coefficients are
\[
\alpha_{DD}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi),
\qquad
\beta_{DD}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi).
\]
Substituting \eqref{eq:AF_aEDD_trunc}--\eqref{eq:AF_aODD_trunc} gives
\begin{align}
\alpha_{DD}
&=
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}I_\theta
+
\Lambda_{E;DD,0}^{(2)}I_{\theta^3}
+
\Lambda_{E;DD,1}^{(2)}I_{\theta'^3}
+
O(\theta_0^5\kappa,\theta_0^5\kappa^3),
\label{eq:AF_alphaDD_raw}
\\
\beta_{DD}
&=
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}I_\theta
+
\Lambda_{O;DD,0}^{(2)}I_{\theta^3}
+
\Lambda_{O;DD,1}^{(2)}I_{\theta'^3}
+
O(\theta_0^5\kappa,\theta_0^5\kappa^3).
\label{eq:AF_betaDD_raw}
\end{align}

For the explicit defect profile one has
\begin{equation}
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}=-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
\label{eq:AF_Itheta_I3}
\end{equation}
Also
\begin{equation}
I_{\theta^3}
:=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'\theta^2
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0^3\kappa.
\label{eq:AF_Itheta3}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_{DD}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
+
\frac{\theta_0^2}{2}\Lambda_{E;DD,0}^{(2)}
+
\frac{3}{16}\theta_0^2\kappa^2\Lambda_{E;DD,1}^{(2)}
\right]
+
O(\theta_0^5\kappa,\theta_0^5\kappa^3),
}
\label{eq:AF_alphaDD_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta_{DD}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
+
\frac{\theta_0^2}{2}\Lambda_{O;DD,0}^{(2)}
+
\frac{3}{16}\theta_0^2\kappa^2\Lambda_{O;DD,1}^{(2)}
\right]
+
O(\theta_0^5\kappa,\theta_0^5\kappa^3).
}
\label{eq:AF_betaDD_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Effective local expansion of the \(OD\)-sector}

The \(OD\)-sector is generated through the projected mixed self-energy derivative,
not as a direct tree-level block.
However, after the Schur reduction and odd parity projection, it belongs to the same local odd transport class.
Hence we may write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{E;OD,0}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}\theta^2
+
\Lambda_{E;OD,1}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}\theta'^2
+
O_{\ge 4},
}
\label{eq:AF_eOD_eff}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{O;OD,0}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}\theta^2
+
\Lambda_{O;OD,1}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}\theta'^2
+
O_{\ge 4},
}
\label{eq:AF_oOD_eff}
\end{equation}
so that after projection
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_{OD/DO}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\left[
2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\theta_0^2\Lambda_{E;OD,0}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}
+
\frac{3}{8}\theta_0^2\kappa^2\Lambda_{E;OD,1}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}
\right]
+
O(\theta_0^5\kappa,\theta_0^5\kappa^3),
}
\label{eq:AF_alphaOD_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta_{OD/DO}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\left[
2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\theta_0^2\Lambda_{O;OD,0}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}
+
\frac{3}{8}\theta_0^2\kappa^2\Lambda_{O;OD,1}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}
\right]
+
O(\theta_0^5\kappa,\theta_0^5\kappa^3).
}
\label{eq:AF_betaOD_explicit}
\end{equation}
The factor \(2\) reflects the \(OD+DO\) exchange-reduced insertion.

\section{5. Full \(OD+DD\)-corrected transverse coefficients}

The principal pair contributes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}},
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}.
}
\label{eq:AF_principal_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}

Therefore the full transverse coefficients become
\begin{align}
\alpha
&=
\alpha_{\mathrm{pr}}
+
\alpha_{OD/DO}
+
\alpha_{DD}
\\[1mm]
&=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Biggl[
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
\nonumber\\
&\qquad\qquad
+
\theta_0^2
\left(
\Lambda_{E;OD,0}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}
+
\frac12\Lambda_{E;DD,0}^{(2)}
\right)
+
\theta_0^2\kappa^2
\left(
\frac38\Lambda_{E;OD,1}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}
+
\frac{3}{16}\Lambda_{E;DD,1}^{(2)}
\right)
\Biggr]
+
O(\theta_0^5\kappa,\theta_0^5\kappa^3),
\label{eq:AF_alpha_full}
\\[2mm]
\beta
&=
\beta_{\mathrm{pr}}
+
\beta_{OD/DO}
+
\beta_{DD}
\\[1mm]
&=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Biggl[
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
\nonumber\\
&\qquad\qquad
+
\theta_0^2
\left(
\Lambda_{O;OD,0}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}
+
\frac12\Lambda_{O;DD,0}^{(2)}
\right)
+
\theta_0^2\kappa^2
\left(
\frac38\Lambda_{O;OD,1}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}
+
\frac{3}{16}\Lambda_{O;DD,1}^{(2)}
\right)
\Biggr]
+
O(\theta_0^5\kappa,\theta_0^5\kappa^3).
\label{eq:AF_beta_full}
\end{align}

\section{6. Actual working PDE after \(OD+DD\) insertion}

Thus the actual reference-frame working PDE is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
\alpha\,\sigma_1(-i\partial_{q_1})
-
\beta\,\sigma_2(-i\partial_{q_2})
\Bigr]\chi=0,
}
\label{eq:AF_actual_PDE}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
and \(\alpha,\beta\) given explicitly by \eqref{eq:AF_alpha_full} and \eqref{eq:AF_beta_full}.

\section{7. Canonical symmetric mixed-target condition}

The canonical mixed odd-active target requires
\[
\alpha=\beta.
\]
At leading local order this is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
=
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:AF_symmetry_leading}
\end{equation}

At first subleading order one further needs
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_{E;OD,0}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}
+\frac12\Lambda_{E;DD,0}^{(2)}
=
\Lambda_{O;OD,0}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}
+\frac12\Lambda_{O;DD,0}^{(2)},
}
\label{eq:AF_symmetry_sub1}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac38\Lambda_{E;OD,1}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}
+\frac{3}{16}\Lambda_{E;DD,1}^{(2)}
=
\frac38\Lambda_{O;OD,1}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}
+\frac{3}{16}\Lambda_{O;DD,1}^{(2)}.
}
\label{eq:AF_symmetry_sub2}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Honest status}

At this point the \(DD\)-sector is explicitly inserted through its leading and first subleading odd local coefficients, and the \(OD\)-sector is inserted through the corresponding effective local odd coefficients generated by the projected self-energy derivative.

So the actual remaining frontier is no longer “what is the form of the corrected PDE?”
That form is already \eqref{eq:AF_actual_PDE}.

What remains is the literal microscopic evaluation of the coefficient set
\[
\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)},
\ 
\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)},
\ 
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)},
\ 
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)},
\]
and their first even-invariant corrections.

\section{Final Summary}

Using the actual-local invariant algebra, every surviving transverse residual contribution from \(OD\) or \(DD\) must belong to the odd local class
\[
\theta'(\xi)\times \text{(parity-even local invariant function)}.
\]

The \(DD\)-sector can therefore be inserted explicitly at leading and first subleading odd order:
\[
a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl[
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
+
\Lambda_{E;DD,0}^{(2)}\theta^2
+
\Lambda_{E;DD,1}^{(2)}\theta'^2
\Bigr]
+O_{\mathrm{odd},\ge 5},
\]
\[
a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl[
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
+
\Lambda_{O;DD,0}^{(2)}\theta^2
+
\Lambda_{O;DD,1}^{(2)}\theta'^2
\Bigr]
+O_{\mathrm{odd},\ge 5}.
\]

After projection, this gives
\[
\alpha_{DD}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
+
\frac{\theta_0^2}{2}\Lambda_{E;DD,0}^{(2)}
+
\frac{3}{16}\theta_0^2\kappa^2\Lambda_{E;DD,1}^{(2)}
\right]
+O(\theta_0^5\kappa,\theta_0^5\kappa^3),
\]
\[
\beta_{DD}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
+
\frac{\theta_0^2}{2}\Lambda_{O;DD,0}^{(2)}
+
\frac{3}{16}\theta_0^2\kappa^2\Lambda_{O;DD,1}^{(2)}
\right]
+O(\theta_0^5\kappa,\theta_0^5\kappa^3).
\]

The \(OD\)-sector is inserted through effective local odd coefficients generated by the projected self-energy derivative:
\[
\alpha_{OD/DO}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\left[
2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\theta_0^2\Lambda_{E;OD,0}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}
+
\frac{3}{8}\theta_0^2\kappa^2\Lambda_{E;OD,1}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}
\right]
+O(\theta_0^5\kappa,\theta_0^5\kappa^3),
\]
\[
\beta_{OD/DO}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\left[
2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\theta_0^2\Lambda_{O;OD,0}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}
+
\frac{3}{8}\theta_0^2\kappa^2\Lambda_{O;OD,1}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}
\right]
+O(\theta_0^5\kappa,\theta_0^5\kappa^3).
\]

Therefore the full corrected transverse coefficients are
\[
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Biggl[
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
+
\theta_0^2
\left(
\Lambda_{E;OD,0}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}
+
\frac12\Lambda_{E;DD,0}^{(2)}
\right)
+
\theta_0^2\kappa^2
\left(
\frac38\Lambda_{E;OD,1}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}
+
\frac{3}{16}\Lambda_{E;DD,1}^{(2)}
\right)
\Biggr]
+\cdots,
\]
\[
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Biggl[
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
+
\theta_0^2
\left(
\Lambda_{O;OD,0}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}
+
\frac12\Lambda_{O;DD,0}^{(2)}
\right)
+
\theta_0^2\kappa^2
\left(
\frac38\Lambda_{O;OD,1}^{\mathrm{eff},(2)}
+
\frac{3}{16}\Lambda_{O;DD,1}^{(2)}
\right)
\Biggr]
+\cdots.
\]

So the actual working PDE is already fixed up to the microscopic evaluation of these local coefficient packages. The problem is no longer structural.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Leading \(DD\) Equality Test and Same-Order \(OD+DD\) Insertion}

\section{Goal}

We now stop postponing the \(DD\)-sector behind abstract residual notation.

The immediate question is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the current microscopic structure force }
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}=\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
\text{ at leading local odd order?}
}
\label{eq:DD_goal}
\end{equation}

We answer this sharply and then insert the result, together with the same-order \(OD\)-correction, into the actual transverse coefficient sheet.

\section{1. What the current notes actually imply about \(DD\)}

The \(DD\)-block is already given in the generic invariant form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_{\parallel;DD}(\theta)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
a_{E;DD}(\theta)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
a_{O;DD}(\theta)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
}
\label{eq:DD_generic_again}
\end{equation}

Therefore the projector-defined leading transverse coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;DD}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
\frac14E^\mu{}_a\Tr(\sigma_a\mathcal M^{DD}_\mu),
\qquad
o_{0;DD}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
\frac14J^\mu{}_a\Tr(\sigma_a\mathcal M^{DD}_\mu).
}
\label{eq:DD_eo_generic_again}
\end{equation}

So the current microscopic formulas treat the \(E\)- and \(O\)-coefficients as two independent scalar functions.
No equality between them follows from the decomposition itself.

Hence the strongest honest theorem-level statement currently supported is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The present notes do not force }
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}=\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:DD_no_auto_equal}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Leading local odd form of the \(DD\)-sector}

Parity implies that only the odd part survives after graded projection.
Therefore the leading local odd expansion must be
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
+
O(\theta'\theta^2,\theta'^3),
}
\label{eq:DD_leading_E}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
+
O(\theta'\theta^2,\theta'^3).
}
\label{eq:DD_leading_O}
\end{equation}

Thus after projection one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_{DD}^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
I_\theta\,\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)},
\qquad
\beta_{DD}^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
I_\theta\,\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:DD_alpha_beta_LO}
\end{equation}

For the explicit defect profile,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:DD_Itheta_again}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_{DD}^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)},
\qquad
\beta_{DD}^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:DD_alpha_beta_LO_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exact criterion for leading \(DD\)-equality}

From \eqref{eq:DD_alpha_beta_LO_explicit},
\[
\alpha_{DD}^{\mathrm{LO}}=\beta_{DD}^{\mathrm{LO}}
\iff
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}=\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}.
\]

Therefore the leading \(DD\)-sector is symmetric if and only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}-\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}=0.
}
\label{eq:DD_exact_equal_test}
\end{equation}

Without an additional microscopic symmetry exchanging the two transverse invariant channels, there is no reason for \eqref{eq:DD_exact_equal_test} to hold automatically.

Thus the sharp honest conclusion is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}\ \text{and}\ \Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
\text{ must be computed separately.}
}
\label{eq:DD_must_compute_sep}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Same-order \(OD\)-insertion}

The \(OD\)-sector enters through the projected mixed self-energy derivative and belongs, after parity projection, to the same local odd transport class.
At the same leading local order we write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}+O(\theta^2,\theta'^2),
\qquad
o_{0;OD,\mathrm{odd}}^{(1)}
=
\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}+O(\theta^2,\theta'^2).
}
\label{eq:OD_leading_eff}
\end{equation}

Under the leading \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange reduction,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{OD/DO}^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
\Bigl(
2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)},
\;
2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:ODDO_leading}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_{OD/DO}^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)},
\qquad
\beta_{OD/DO}^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}.
}
\label{eq:OD_alpha_beta_LO}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Full leading-order \(OD+DD\)-corrected coefficient sheet}

Let the principal pair be
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}},
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}.
}
\label{eq:pr_alpha_beta_again}
\end{equation}

Then the full leading-order coefficients become
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:alpha_LO_full}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:beta_LO_full}
\end{equation}

This is the first genuine forward coefficient sheet beyond the bare principal pair.

\section{6. Leading-order symmetric mixed-target condition}

The canonical mixed odd-active target requires
\[
\alpha=\beta.
\]
At leading order this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
=
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:LO_symmetry_condition}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bigl(\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}-\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}\bigr)
+
2\bigl(\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}-\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}-\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}\bigr)
=0.
}
\label{eq:LO_symmetry_difference}
\end{equation}

Thus the leading-order mismatch splits cleanly into:
\[
\text{principal mismatch}
+
\text{\(OD\) mismatch}
+
\text{\(DD\) mismatch}.
\]

\section{7. Actual leading-order working PDE}

The actual leading-order working PDE is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}\,\sigma_1(-i\partial_{q_1})
-
\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}\,\sigma_2(-i\partial_{q_2})
\Bigr]\chi=0,
}
\label{eq:LO_actual_PDE}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:LO_lambda}
\end{equation}
and \(\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}},\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}\) from \eqref{eq:alpha_LO_full}--\eqref{eq:beta_LO_full}.

\section{8. Honest status}

The forward progress achieved here is sharp:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the \(DD\)-sector is now inserted explicitly at leading order;
\item the \(OD\)-sector is inserted at the same order through its effective local coefficients;
\item the full leading-order transverse coefficient sheet is now \eqref{eq:alpha_LO_full}--\eqref{eq:beta_LO_full};
\item the exact leading-order symmetric-target test is \eqref{eq:LO_symmetry_difference}.
\end{enumerate}

What remains is not another structural reduction.
It is the literal microscopic evaluation of the four leading numbers
\[
\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)},
\qquad
\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)},
\qquad
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)},
\qquad
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}.
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The current notes do \emph{not} imply
\[
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}=\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
\]
automatically.
The generic \(DD\)-decomposition already treats the two transverse coefficients as independent:
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_{\parallel;DD}n^\mu\sigma_3
+
a_{E;DD}E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
a_{O;DD}J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\]

Thus the leading odd \(DD\)-sector is
\[
a_{E;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}+\cdots,
\qquad
a_{O;DD}^{\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}+\cdots,
\]
so
\[
\alpha_{DD}^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)},
\qquad
\beta_{DD}^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}.
\]

The \(OD\)-sector enters at the same order through effective local coefficients
\[
\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)},
\qquad
\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)},
\]
giving
\[
\alpha_{OD/DO}^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)},
\qquad
\beta_{OD/DO}^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}.
\]

Therefore the full leading-order transverse coefficients are
\[
\boxed{
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr).
}
\]

The exact leading-order canonical mixed-target condition is
\[
\boxed{
\bigl(\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}-\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}\bigr)
+
2\bigl(\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}-\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}-\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}\bigr)
=0.
}
\]

So the actual working PDE is already fixed at leading order. What remains is the microscopic evaluation of these four leading transverse correction numbers.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Principal-Pair Symmetry Test and the Reduced Leading Mismatch Equation}

\section{Goal}

We now test the shortest possible route:
is the principal transverse pair already symmetric before inserting the residual \(OD+DD\) correction?

If yes, then the remaining leading mismatch is carried only by the \(OD+DD\) sector.
If not, then the principal mismatch itself must be included explicitly.

\section{1. Exact principal pair}

The exact principal transverse source is the projected mixed block
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
=
\Pi_Q(\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT})\Pi_Q.
\]
Its projector-defined coefficient pair is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}],
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}].
}
\label{eq:PPS_principal_pair}
\end{equation}

At the explicit branch-level reduced realization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{TD}
=
\theta'(\xi)\bigl(
A_E E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a + A_O J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\bigr),
}
\label{eq:PPS_VTD}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{DT}
=
\theta'(\xi)\bigl(
B_E E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a + B_O J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:PPS_VDT}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\frac12(A_O+B_O).
}
\label{eq:PPS_Lambda_pr_entries}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact principal symmetry test}

From \eqref{eq:PPS_Lambda_pr_entries},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}=\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
\iff
A_E+B_E=A_O+B_O.
}
\label{eq:PPS_exact_test}
\end{equation}

This is the sharpest principal-pair symmetry criterion available at the present stage.

\section{3. Honest status of the principal symmetry question}

The uploaded notes do \emph{not} currently provide a theorem forcing
\[
A_E+B_E=A_O+B_O.
\]
So the strongest honest statement is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{principal-pair symmetry is not yet proved automatically.}
}
\label{eq:PPS_not_auto}
\end{equation}

It must be checked by explicit microscopic evaluation of the \(TD+DT\) projected Hessian.

\section{4. Relation to the reference route}

In the current reference PDE route one imposes
\[
\gamma_E=\gamma_O=:\gamma_\perp,
\]
which yields
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c.
}
\label{eq:PPS_reference_equal}
\end{equation}
Thus the reference route is \emph{constructed} to be symmetric in the transverse pair.

However, this does not by itself prove that the principal microscopic Hessian pair
\[
(\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}},\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}})
\]
is already symmetric on the target mixed branch.
So the reference-route symmetry and the principal-Hessian symmetry must be kept logically distinct.

\section{5. Leading-order full mismatch equation}

The full leading-order transverse coefficient sheet, including the \(OD+DD\) correction, is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:PPS_alpha_LO}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:PPS_beta_LO}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact leading-order symmetric-target condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bigl(\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}-\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}\bigr)
+
2\bigl(\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}-\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}-\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}\bigr)
=0.
}
\label{eq:PPS_full_mismatch}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:PPS_Lambda_pr_entries}, this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac12\Bigl[(A_E+B_E)-(A_O+B_O)\Bigr]
+
2\bigl(\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}-\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}-\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}\bigr)
=0.
}
\label{eq:PPS_full_mismatch_entries}
\end{equation}

\section{6. If the principal pair is already symmetric}

If the explicit principal Hessian audit gives
\[
A_E+B_E=A_O+B_O,
\]
then \eqref{eq:PPS_full_mismatch_entries} reduces immediately to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2\bigl(\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}-\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}-\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}\bigr)
=0.
}
\label{eq:PPS_reduced_mismatch}
\end{equation}

So in that case the entire leading-order mismatch is carried only by the \(OD+DD\) residual correction.

\section{7. If the principal pair is not symmetric}

If
\[
A_E+B_E\neq A_O+B_O,
\]
then even before residual insertion there is already a principal mismatch
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{pr}}
:=
\frac12\Bigl[(A_E+B_E)-(A_O+B_O)\Bigr]\neq 0.
\]
Then the residual sector must compensate this:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2\bigl(\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}-\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}-\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}\bigr)
=
-\delta_{\mathrm{pr}}.
}
\label{eq:PPS_compensation}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Sharp current conclusion}

The shortest honest next computation is therefore not a new structural theorem.
It is the explicit principal-pair symmetry test
\[
\boxed{
A_E+B_E\stackrel{?}{=}A_O+B_O.
}
\]
Once this is known, the leading mixed-target condition collapses either to the reduced residual equation \eqref{eq:PPS_reduced_mismatch} or to the compensation equation \eqref{eq:PPS_compensation}.

\section{Final Summary}

The exact principal transverse pair is
\[
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}=\frac12(A_O+B_O).
\]

Therefore the sharp principal symmetry test is
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}=\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
\iff
A_E+B_E=A_O+B_O.
}
\]

The uploaded notes do not currently prove this automatically.
So principal-pair symmetry is still an explicit microscopic question, not a theorem-level consequence of the present formulas.

The full leading-order corrected coefficients are
\[
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr),
\]
\[
\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr).
\]

So the exact leading-order symmetric-target condition is
\[
\boxed{
\frac12\Bigl[(A_E+B_E)-(A_O+B_O)\Bigr]
+
2\bigl(\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}-\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}-\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}\bigr)
=0.
}
\]

If the principal pair is already symmetric, this reduces to
\[
\boxed{
2\bigl(\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}-\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}-\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}\bigr)
=0.
}
\]

So the shortest next computation is exactly the principal Hessian symmetry test
\[
A_E+B_E\stackrel{?}{=}A_O+B_O.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Leading-Order Transverse Sheet in Average--Mismatch Form}

\section{Goal}

We no longer wait for an a priori proof of
\[
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}=\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}.
\]
Instead, we absorb the possible principal asymmetry directly into the leading-order coefficient sheet and rewrite the actual PDE in a symmetric-plus-mismatch form.

\section{1. Exact principal pair}

The projected mixed \(TD+DT\) block gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}=\frac12(A_O+B_O).
}
\label{eq:avgmis_prpair}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact principal symmetry test is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}=\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
\iff
A_E+B_E=A_O+B_O.
}
\label{eq:avgmis_prtest}
\end{equation}

No theorem in the current notes forces this equality automatically.

\section{2. Full leading-order corrected transverse sheet}

Including the leading \(OD+DD\) correction, the coefficient pair is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:avgmis_alphaLO}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:avgmis_betaLO}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Average and mismatch variables}

Define the principal average and principal mismatch
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_{\Sigma}^{\mathrm{pr}}
:=
\frac{\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}+\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}}{2}
=
\frac14\Bigl[(A_E+B_E)+(A_O+B_O)\Bigr],
}
\label{eq:avgmis_pravg}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{pr}}
:=
\frac{\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}-\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}}{2}
=
\frac14\Bigl[(A_E+B_E)-(A_O+B_O)\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:avgmis_prdiff}
\end{equation}

Define likewise the leading residual average and mismatch
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_{\Sigma}^{\mathrm{rem},(0)}
:=
\frac{
2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}+\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
+
2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}+\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
}{2},
}
\label{eq:avgmis_remavg}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{rem},(0)}
:=
\frac{
2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}+\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
-
2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}-\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
}{2}.
}
\label{eq:avgmis_remdiff}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
\Lambda_{\Sigma}^{\mathrm{pr}}+\Lambda_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
\Lambda_{\Sigma}^{\mathrm{rem},(0)}+\Lambda_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{rem},(0)},
}
\label{eq:avgmis_LE}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
\Lambda_{\Sigma}^{\mathrm{pr}}-\Lambda_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
\Lambda_{\Sigma}^{\mathrm{rem},(0)}-\Lambda_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{rem},(0)}.
}
\label{eq:avgmis_LO}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Actual symmetric-plus-mismatch coefficients}

Introduce
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_{\perp}^{\mathrm{LO}}
:=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_{\Sigma}^{\mathrm{pr}}+\Lambda_{\Sigma}^{\mathrm{rem},(0)}
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:avgmis_vperp}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{\perp}^{\mathrm{LO}}
:=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{pr}}+\Lambda_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{rem},(0)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:avgmis_dperp}
\end{equation}

Then the corrected leading-order transverse coefficients take the exact form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}=v_{\perp}^{\mathrm{LO}}+\delta_{\perp}^{\mathrm{LO}},
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}=v_{\perp}^{\mathrm{LO}}-\delta_{\perp}^{\mathrm{LO}}.
}
\label{eq:avgmis_alphabeta_split}
\end{equation}

This is the cleanest forward form of the current transverse sheet.

\section{5. Exact leading mismatch equation}

The canonical mixed odd-active target requires
\[
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}=\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}.
\]
By \eqref{eq:avgmis_alphabeta_split}, this is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{\perp}^{\mathrm{LO}}=0.
}
\label{eq:avgmis_target}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{pr}}+\Lambda_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{rem},(0)}=0.
}
\label{eq:avgmis_target2}
\end{equation}
That is,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac14\Bigl[(A_E+B_E)-(A_O+B_O)\Bigr]
+
\frac12\Bigl[
2\bigl(\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}-\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}-\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}\bigr)
\Bigr]
=0.
}
\label{eq:avgmis_target3}
\end{equation}

Multiplying by \(2\), one recovers the exact leading-order mismatch equation
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac12\Bigl[(A_E+B_E)-(A_O+B_O)\Bigr]
+
2\bigl(\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}-\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}-\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}\bigr)
=0.
}
\label{eq:avgmis_target4}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Actual forward PDE}

The actual leading-order working PDE is now
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
(v_{\perp}^{\mathrm{LO}}+\delta_{\perp}^{\mathrm{LO}})\,\mathcal D_E
-
(v_{\perp}^{\mathrm{LO}}-\delta_{\perp}^{\mathrm{LO}})\,\mathcal D_O
\Bigr]\chi=0,
}
\label{eq:avgmis_PDE}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\mathcal D_E:=\sigma_1(-i\partial_{q_1}),
\qquad
\mathcal D_O:=\sigma_2(-i\partial_{q_2}),
\end{equation}
in the simplified directional notation, and in the full reduced shell form one keeps the standard pair
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:avgmis_PDE_full}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Two useful special cases}

If the principal pair is already symmetric,
\[
A_E+B_E=A_O+B_O,
\]
then
\[
\Lambda_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{pr}}=0,
\]
and the entire leading mismatch is carried only by the residual correction:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2\bigl(\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}-\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}-\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}\bigr)
=0.
}
\label{eq:avgmis_case1}
\end{equation}

If the residual correction is symmetric,
\[
2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}+\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
=
2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}+\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)},
\]
then
\[
\Lambda_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{rem},(0)}=0,
\]
and the entire leading mismatch is carried by the principal pair:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_E+B_E=A_O+B_O.
}
\label{eq:avgmis_case2}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Honest status}

At this point the forward transverse PDE is already fixed in actual coefficient form.

What remains is not another structural rewrite.
It is the microscopic evaluation of
\[
(A_E+B_E)-(A_O+B_O),
\qquad
\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}-\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)},
\qquad
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}-\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}.
\]
These three differences completely determine the leading mixed-target mismatch.

\section{Final Summary}

The principal transverse pair is
\[
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}=\frac12(A_O+B_O),
\]
so principal symmetry is equivalent to
\[
A_E+B_E=A_O+B_O.
\]

The full leading-order corrected coefficients are
\[
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr),
\]
\[
\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr).
\]

Defining average and mismatch variables gives
\[
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}=v_{\perp}^{\mathrm{LO}}+\delta_{\perp}^{\mathrm{LO}},
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}=v_{\perp}^{\mathrm{LO}}-\delta_{\perp}^{\mathrm{LO}},
\]
with
\[
\delta_{\perp}^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{pr}}+\Lambda_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{rem},(0)}
\Bigr).
\]

Therefore the exact leading-order mixed-target condition is simply
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{\perp}^{\mathrm{LO}}=0,
}
\]
equivalently
\[
\boxed{
\frac12\Bigl[(A_E+B_E)-(A_O+B_O)\Bigr]
+
2\bigl(\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}-\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}-\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}\bigr)
=0.
}
\]

So the leading-order forward problem is reduced to three microscopic mismatch numbers only.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Direct Projector-Trace Formula for the Leading \(DD\) Mismatch}

\section{Goal}

We now isolate the leading \(DD\)-mismatch itself, rather than leaving it inside a residual vector.

The exact question is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}
:=
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}-\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:DDmismatch_goal}
\end{equation}

Once this is written directly as a projector-trace difference, it can be inserted immediately into the full leading transverse coefficient sheet.

\section{1. Exact \(DD\)-projector definitions}

The projected \(DD\)-kernel is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_{\parallel;DD}(\theta)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
a_{E;DD}(\theta)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
a_{O;DD}(\theta)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
}
\label{eq:DDmismatch_kernel}
\end{equation}

The executable projector definitions are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;DD}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\,\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_a\mathcal M^{DD}_{\mu}\bigr),
}
\label{eq:DDmismatch_eproj}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
o_{0;DD}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\,\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_a\mathcal M^{DD}_{\mu}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:DDmismatch_oproj}
\end{equation}

So the \(DD\)-block is not an exchange-type auxiliary piece.
It is a direct transverse candidate inside the defect-tangent sector.

\section{2. Leading odd local form}

Only the reflection-odd part survives after graded projection.
Therefore the leading odd local \(DD\)-sector must be
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr]
+
O(\theta'\theta^2,\theta'^3).
}
\label{eq:DDmismatch_leadingodd}
\end{equation}

In the normalization convention already used throughout the notes, this means
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;DD}^{(1)}=\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)},
\qquad
o_{0;DD}^{(1)}=\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
\qquad
\text{at leading local odd order.}
}
\label{eq:DDmismatch_leadingid}
\end{equation}

Hence the leading \(DD\)-mismatch is simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}
=
e_{0;DD}^{(1)}-o_{0;DD}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:DDmismatch_simple}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Direct projector-trace form of \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}$}{DeltaDD}}

Subtracting \eqref{eq:DDmismatch_oproj} from \eqref{eq:DDmismatch_eproj} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
\frac14
\Bigl(
E^\mu{}_a-J^\mu{}_a
\Bigr)
\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_a\mathcal M^{DD}_{\mu}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:DDmismatch_trace}
\end{equation}

Using only the odd part of the kernel, the same formula may be written more sharply as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
\frac{1}{4\,\theta'(\xi)}
\Bigl(
E^\mu{}_a-J^\mu{}_a
\Bigr)
\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_a\mathcal M^{DD}_{\mu,\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:DDmismatch_trace_odd}
\end{equation}

This is the exact direct projector-trace formula for the leading \(DD\)-mismatch.

\section{4. When does the leading \(DD\)-mismatch vanish?}

The condition
\[
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}=0
\]
is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}=\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:DDmismatch_zeroeq}
\end{equation}

At the projector level, this means
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E^\mu{}_a\,\Tr(\sigma_a\mathcal M^{DD}_{\mu,\mathrm{odd}})
=
J^\mu{}_a\,\Tr(\sigma_a\mathcal M^{DD}_{\mu,\mathrm{odd}})
\qquad
\text{at leading local odd order.}
}
\label{eq:DDmismatch_zero_trace}
\end{equation}

The current notes do not provide a theorem forcing \eqref{eq:DDmismatch_zeroeq} or \eqref{eq:DDmismatch_zero_trace}.
So \(\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}\) must be treated as a genuine microscopic observable.

\section{5. Full leading-order transverse coefficients including \(OD+DD\)}

The principal pair is
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}=\frac12(A_O+B_O).
\label{eq:DDmismatch_prpair}
\end{equation}

The same-order \(OD\)-sector contributes
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_{E;OD/DO}^{(0)}=2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)},
\qquad
\Lambda_{O;OD/DO}^{(0)}=2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}.
\label{eq:DDmismatch_ODpair}
\end{equation}

Therefore the full leading-order transverse coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:DDmismatch_alphaLO}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:DDmismatch_betaLO}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Full leading mismatch equation}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}
:=
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}-\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\frac12\Bigl[(A_E+B_E)-(A_O+B_O)\Bigr],
}
\label{eq:DDmismatch_Dpr}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{OD}^{(0)}
:=
2\Bigl(\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}-\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:DDmismatch_DOD}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}
:=
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}-\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:DDmismatch_DDD}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}-\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}
+
\Delta_{OD}^{(0)}
+
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:DDmismatch_alpha_minus_beta}
\end{equation}

So the exact leading-order symmetric mixed-target condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}
+
\Delta_{OD}^{(0)}
+
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}
=0.
}
\label{eq:DDmismatch_master}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Actual leading-order working PDE}

The actual leading-order transverse PDE is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}\,\sigma_1(-i\partial_{q_1})
-
\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}\,\sigma_2(-i\partial_{q_2})
\Bigr]\chi=0,
}
\label{eq:DDmismatch_PDE}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:DDmismatch_lambda}
\end{equation}
and \(\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}},\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}\) given by \eqref{eq:DDmismatch_alphaLO}--\eqref{eq:DDmismatch_betaLO}.

\section{8. Honest status}

The forward reduction is now complete at leading order.

The \(DD\)-mismatch is no longer a vague residual phrase.
It is the explicit projector-trace observable \eqref{eq:DDmismatch_trace}--\eqref{eq:DDmismatch_trace_odd}.

Therefore the whole leading mixed-target problem is reduced to evaluating three microscopic differences:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)},
\qquad
\Delta_{OD}^{(0)},
\qquad
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}.
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The \(DD\)-block acts directly inside the defect-tangent doublet sector and has the explicit projected decomposition
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_{\parallel;DD}n^\mu\sigma_3
+
a_{E;DD}E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
a_{O;DD}J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\]

Its leading odd local transverse part is
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{odd}}
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr]
+\cdots,
\]
so
\[
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}
=
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}-\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
=
e_{0;DD}^{(1)}-o_{0;DD}^{(1)}.
\]

The exact direct projector-trace formula is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
\frac14
(E^\mu{}_a-J^\mu{}_a)\Tr(\sigma_a\mathcal M^{DD}_{\mu}),
}
\]
or more sharply, using only the odd part,
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
\frac{1}{4\theta'(\xi)}
(E^\mu{}_a-J^\mu{}_a)\Tr(\sigma_a\mathcal M^{DD}_{\mu,\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)).
}
\]

The full leading-order transverse coefficients are
\[
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr),
\]
\[
\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr).
\]

Therefore the exact leading mixed-target condition is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}
+
\Delta_{OD}^{(0)}
+
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}
=0,
}
\]
where
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}
=
\frac12[(A_E+B_E)-(A_O+B_O)],
\qquad
\Delta_{OD}^{(0)}
=
2(\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}-\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}),
\qquad
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}
=
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}-\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}.
\]

So the leading-order forward problem is now reduced to three explicit microscopic mismatch numbers only.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Direct Projector-Trace Formula for the Principal Leading Mismatch}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

We now stop asking whether the principal pair might be symmetric.
Instead, we write the principal mismatch itself as a direct observable extracted from the projected \(TD+DT\) block.

This turns the leading mixed-target condition into a literal sum of three microscopic mismatch observables:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)},\qquad
\Delta_{OD}^{(0)},\qquad
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}.
\]

\section{1. Exact projected principal block}

The principal transverse source is the mixed shell--defect block
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
:=
\Pi_Q\bigl(\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT}\bigr)\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:PM_MTD}
\end{equation}

The exact invariant projectors are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu\bigr),
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu\bigr).
}
\label{eq:PM_projectors}
\end{equation}

Therefore the principal coefficient pair is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_0^{(1)}=\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}],
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}=\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}],
}
\label{eq:PM_e0o0}
\end{equation}
and at the minimal mixed-block level
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}=e_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}=o_0^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:PM_Lambdapr}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Explicit \(TD+DT\) block form}

The two mixed blocks have the branch-level reduced form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{TD}
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl(
A_E E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a+A_O J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:PM_VTD}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{DT}
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl(
B_E E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a+B_O J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:PM_VDT}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
(A_E+B_E)E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
(A_O+B_O)J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:PM_Mexplicit}
\end{equation}

Under the canonical invariant normalization, the two channels decouple, so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_0^{(1)}=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}=\frac12(A_O+B_O).
}
\label{eq:PM_half}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}=\frac12(A_O+B_O).
}
\label{eq:PM_prpair_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Principal leading mismatch as an exact observable}

Define the principal leading mismatch
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}
:=
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}-\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}.
}
\label{eq:PM_Dpr_def}
\end{equation}
Then by \eqref{eq:PM_prpair_explicit},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}
=
\frac12\Bigl[(A_E+B_E)-(A_O+B_O)\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:PM_Dpr_entries}
\end{equation}

This is already the exact finite principal mismatch number.

\section{4. Direct projector-trace formula for \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}$}{Delta pr}}

Subtracting the two projector definitions gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}
=
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}]
-
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}].
}
\label{eq:PM_Dpr_projector}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:PM_projectors}, this is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}
=
\frac14
\Bigl(E^\mu{}_a-J^\mu{}_a\Bigr)
