\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M^{TD+DT}_\mu\bigr).
}
\label{eq:PM_Dpr_trace}
\end{equation}

Since \(\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}\) contains one explicit factor of \(\theta'(\xi)\), one may also write the normalized odd-coefficient form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
\frac{1}{4\,\theta'(\xi)}
\Bigl(E^\mu{}_a-J^\mu{}_a\Bigr)
\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M^{TD+DT}_\mu(\xi)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:PM_Dpr_trace_odd}
\end{equation}

Thus the principal mismatch is not a vague branch label.
It is a direct projector-trace observable.

\section{5. Full leading mismatch equation}

The \(OD\)- and \(DD\)-sector leading mismatches are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{OD}^{(0)}
=
2\Bigl(
\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
-
\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:PM_DOD}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}
=
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
-
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:PM_DDD}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact leading mixed-target condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}
+
\Delta_{OD}^{(0)}
+
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}
=0.
}
\label{eq:PM_master}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:PM_Dpr_entries} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac12\Bigl[(A_E+B_E)-(A_O+B_O)\Bigr]
+
2\Bigl(
\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
-
\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
\Bigr)
+
\Bigl(
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
-
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr)
=0.
}
\label{eq:PM_master_entries}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Leading-order transverse coefficient sheet}

With
\[
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O,
\qquad
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\]
the principal pair alone gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa(A_O+B_O).
}
\label{eq:PM_alpha_beta_pr}
\end{equation}

Including the same-order \(OD+DD\) correction,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:PM_alpha_LO}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:PM_beta_LO}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}-\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}
+
\Delta_{OD}^{(0)}
+
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:PM_alpha_minus_beta}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Actual leading-order working PDE}

The actual leading-order working PDE is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}\,\sigma_1(-i\partial_{q_1})
-
\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}\,\sigma_2(-i\partial_{q_2})
\Bigr]\chi=0,
}
\label{eq:PM_PDE}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:PM_lambda}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Honest status}

The principal mismatch is now fully reduced to the direct observable
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}
=
\frac14(E^\mu{}_a-J^\mu{}_a)\Tr(\Sigma_a\mathcal M^{TD+DT}_\mu),
\]
equivalently
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}
=
\frac12\Bigl[(A_E+B_E)-(A_O+B_O)\Bigr].
\]

So the whole leading-order mixed-target problem is reduced to three explicit microscopic mismatch observables:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)},
\qquad
\Delta_{OD}^{(0)},
\qquad
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}.
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The principal \(TD+DT\) pair is already an exact finite observable:
\[
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}=\frac12(A_O+B_O).
\]

Therefore the principal leading mismatch is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}
=
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}-\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\frac12\Bigl[(A_E+B_E)-(A_O+B_O)\Bigr].
}
\]

It is also given directly by the projector-trace formula
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}
=
\frac14
(E^\mu{}_a-J^\mu{}_a)\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M^{TD+DT}_\mu\bigr).
}
\]

The full leading mixed-target condition is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}
+
\Delta_{OD}^{(0)}
+
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}
=0,
}
\]
where
\[
\Delta_{OD}^{(0)}
=
2(\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}-\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}),
\qquad
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}
=
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}-\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}.
\]

Hence
\[
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}-\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}
+
\Delta_{OD}^{(0)}
+
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr).
\]

So the leading-order problem is now reduced exactly to three microscopic mismatch observables only.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Principal Leading Mismatch as a Direct Observable}

\section{Goal}

We now freeze the principal \(TD+DT\) contribution itself as an explicit observable, rather than leaving it as a qualitative symmetry question.

\section{1. Exact projected principal block}

The principal mixed shell--defect transverse carrier is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
:=
\Pi_Q\bigl(\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT}\bigr)\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:PLM_MTD}
\end{equation}

The exact invariant projector functionals are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu\bigr),
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu\bigr).
}
\label{eq:PLM_projectors}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}],
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}].
}
\label{eq:PLM_Lambdas}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Explicit branch-level form}

At the current branch-level reduced realization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{TD}
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl(
A_EE^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a+A_OJ^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:PLM_VTD}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{DT}
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl(
B_EE^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a+B_OJ^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:PLM_VDT}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
(A_E+B_E)E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
(A_O+B_O)J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:PLM_Mexplicit}
\end{equation}

By canonical invariant normalization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}=\frac12(A_O+B_O).
}
\label{eq:PLM_half}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Principal mismatch}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}
:=
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}-\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}.
}
\label{eq:PLM_Dpr_def}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}
=
\frac12\Bigl[(A_E+B_E)-(A_O+B_O)\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:PLM_Dpr_entries}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, directly at the projector level,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}
=
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}]
-
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}]
=
\frac14
\bigl(E^\mu{}_a-J^\mu{}_a\bigr)
\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M^{TD+DT}_\mu\bigr).
}
\label{eq:PLM_Dpr_trace}
\end{equation}

So the principal transverse mismatch is already a direct finite observable.

\section{4. Principal contribution to the reduced PDE coefficients}

The reduced shell dictionary is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O,
\qquad
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:PLM_dict}
\end{equation}

Therefore the principal pair contributes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa\,(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa\,(A_O+B_O).
}
\label{eq:PLM_alpha_beta_pr}
\end{equation}
and hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_{\mathrm{pr}}-\beta_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:PLM_pr_diff}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Full leading-order mismatch equation}

The same-order residual mismatches are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{OD}^{(0)}
=
2\Bigl(
\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}-\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:PLM_DOD}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}
=
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}-\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:PLM_DDD}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact leading mixed-target condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}+\Delta_{OD}^{(0)}+\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}=0.
}
\label{eq:PLM_master}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac12\Bigl[(A_E+B_E)-(A_O+B_O)\Bigr]
+
2\Bigl(
\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}-\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
\Bigr)
+
\Bigl(
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}-\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr)
=0.
}
\label{eq:PLM_master_expanded}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Actual leading-order working PDE}

The leading-order transverse coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{E;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{E;DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:PLM_alphaLO}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
+
2\Lambda_{O;OD}^{\mathrm{eff},(0)}
+
\Lambda_{O;DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:PLM_betaLO}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}-\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}+\Delta_{OD}^{(0)}+\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:PLM_alpha_minus_beta}
\end{equation}

This is the actual leading-order mismatch equation inside the reduced PDE.

\section{Final Summary}

The principal \(TD+DT\) audit is already reduced to the exact finite pair
\[
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}=\frac12(A_O+B_O).
\]

Therefore the principal leading mismatch is the direct observable
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}
=
\frac12\Bigl[(A_E+B_E)-(A_O+B_O)\Bigr]
=
\frac14(E^\mu{}_a-J^\mu{}_a)\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_a\mathcal M^{TD+DT}_\mu).
}
\]

The full leading mixed-target condition is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}+\Delta_{OD}^{(0)}+\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}=0.
}
\]

Hence
\[
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}-\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}+\Delta_{OD}^{(0)}+\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}
\Bigr).
\]

So the entire leading-order transverse problem is now reduced exactly to three microscopic mismatch observables:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)},
\qquad
\Delta_{OD}^{(0)},
\qquad
\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Forward Reorganization: From the Target-Audit Decomposition Back to the Reference PDE}

\section{Goal}

We now stop further decomposing the target-branch audits and reorganize the program according to the latest fixed master contents:

\[
\boxed{
\text{current forward route}=\text{explicit odd extra-carrier reference PDE},
}
\]
\qquad
\[
\boxed{
\text{current target route}=\text{canonical mixed odd-active branch}.
}
\]

The honest next step is therefore not another audit decomposition, but:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{populate the reference PDE coefficients explicitly and use them as the bridge to the target branch.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{1. Reference-route coefficient dictionary}

The explicit odd-route reduced coefficient dictionary is already fixed:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:FR_ref_dict}
\end{equation}

The overlap integrals are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_3=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
I_c=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:FR_I3Ic}
\end{equation}

At one-mediator level,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(1)}
= -\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2},
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}
= -\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}.
}
\label{eq:FR_tildeLambda}
\end{equation}

Under the fixed reference choice
\[
\gamma_E=\gamma_O=:\gamma_\perp,
\]
this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c.
}
\label{eq:FR_ref_sheet}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Current reference PDE}

The current reference reduced PDE is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c\,
\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c\,
\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:FR_ref_PDE}
\end{equation}

Introducing the rotated coordinates
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
q_1:=\frac{p_1-p_2}{\sqrt2},
\qquad
q_2:=\frac{p_1+p_2}{\sqrt2},
}
\end{equation}
the same PDE becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_\perp^{\mathrm{ref}}
\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_{q_1})+\sigma_2(-i\partial_{q_2})\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0,
}
\label{eq:FR_ref_PDE_rot}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\perp^{\mathrm{ref}}
=
-\sqrt2\,\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c.
}
\label{eq:FR_vperp_ref}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Target branch as a coefficient-matching problem}

The canonical mixed odd-active target is already structurally fixed as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:FR_target_sheet}
\end{equation}

Therefore the reference route matches the target iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:FR_match_long}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:FR_match_trans}
\end{equation}

Thus the whole target problem is now reduced to:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{explicitly evaluate }I_3,\ I_c,\ \lambda_c,\ \gamma_\perp
\text{ and choose their signs compatibly.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{4. What happens to the target-branch mismatch analysis?}

The target-branch leading-order mismatch analysis is still valid:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}+\Delta_{OD}^{(0)}+\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}=0.
}
\label{eq:FR_target_mismatch}
\end{equation}

But after the latest master update, this should be interpreted as a \emph{secondary diagnostic} for the target branch, not as the primary forward route.

The primary forward route is the explicit reference PDE \eqref{eq:FR_ref_PDE_rot} and the matching conditions \eqref{eq:FR_match_long}--\eqref{eq:FR_match_trans}.

\section{5. Explicit status sentence}

So the correct current status is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{reference PDE fixed, target branch structurally closed, remaining work = finite coefficient insertion and matching.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Actual next computation}

The shortest nonredundant next computation is therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute }I_3\text{ exactly on the explicit seed, compute }I_c\text{ to the same order, and solve for }\lambda_c,\gamma_\perp.
}
\end{equation}

Once that is done, the reference route either lands exactly on the target branch or produces a controlled mismatch that can then be compared against the target-audit diagnostics.

\section{Final Summary}

The latest fixed master contents imply that the active forward route is no longer the direct target-branch audit chain, but the explicit odd extra-carrier reference PDE.

Its exact coefficient dictionary is
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_O,
\]
and under the fixed symmetric reference choice
\[
\gamma_E=\gamma_O=:\gamma_\perp,
\]
this becomes
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c.
\]

The current reference PDE is therefore
\[
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_\perp^{\mathrm{ref}}
\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_{q_1})+\sigma_2(-i\partial_{q_2})\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0,
\]
with
\[
v_\perp^{\mathrm{ref}}
=
-\sqrt2\,\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c.
\]

The target mixed odd-active branch remains
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa.
\]

So the exact bridge conditions are
\[
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\frac{\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa.
\]

The target-branch mismatch equation
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{pr}}^{(0)}+\Delta_{OD}^{(0)}+\Delta_{DD}^{(0)}=0
\]
remains correct, but it is now secondary. The primary forward problem is simply the finite extraction of
\[
I_3,\ I_c,\ \lambda_c,\ \gamma_\perp.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Actual Nonlinear PDE Branch Construction}

\section{Goal}

The true bottleneck is no longer the reduced projector algebra.
It is the construction of an actual nonlinear stationary branch
\[
\Psi_{\mathrm{actual}}(x)
\]
solving the microscopic Euler--Lagrange equation
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal E'[\Psi]=0.
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_goal}
\end{equation}

The correct next step is therefore to formulate the nonlinear branch problem in a way that is simultaneously:

\begin{enumerate}
\item variationally well-defined,
\item numerically solvable,
\item compatible with the intended BCC shell structure,
\item directly usable for later Bloch linearization.
\end{enumerate}

\section{1. Minimal stationary microscopic equation}

We use the current strongest working microscopic stationary equation in the generic form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-\mu^2 \Psi
+Z\nabla^2\Psi
-Y\nabla^4\Psi
-\lambda(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi
+\mathcal N_{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P,X,\sigma]
=0,
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_stationary}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal N_{\mathrm{ref}}\) denotes the remaining refined microscopic nonlinear terms already admitted by the working branch.

For the actual nonlinear branch construction, the correct viewpoint is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{first solve the full stationary branch problem,}
\quad
\text{then linearize around that solution.}
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_order}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Energy functional formulation}

Assume the stationary equation is the Euler--Lagrange equation of an energy functional
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal E[\Psi]
=
\int d^3x\;
\Bigl[
-\mu^2\,\Psi^\dagger\Psi
+Z\,\partial_i\Psi^\dagger\partial_i\Psi
+Y\,(\nabla^2\Psi)^\dagger(\nabla^2\Psi)
+\frac{\lambda}{2}(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)^2
+\mathcal E_{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P,X,\sigma]
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_energy}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\delta \mathcal E}{\delta \Psi^\dagger}=0
\iff
\mathcal E'[\Psi]=0.
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_variational}
\end{equation}

So the actual branch problem is equivalent to finding a nontrivial critical point of \(\mathcal E\).

\section{3. Intended branch ansatz}

To avoid drifting into irrelevant solution sectors, we restrict the nonlinear search to the intended BCC-shell branch.

Write the field as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi(x)
=
\sum_{A\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}}
\phi_A(x)\,e^{iG_A\cdot x}\,z_A(x),
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_BCC_ansatz}
\end{equation}
where

\begin{itemize}
\item \(S_{\mathrm{BCC}}\) is the chosen BCC reciprocal shell,
\item \(G_A\) are the shell wavevectors,
\item \(\phi_A(x)\) are slowly varying complex amplitudes,
\item \(z_A(x)\) are internal orientation vectors.
\end{itemize}

For the first actual branch construction, we impose the minimal locked branch reduction
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\phi_A(x)=\phi(x)\,\eta_A,
\qquad
z_A(x)=z(x),
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_locked_reduction}
\end{equation}
with fixed shell weights \(\eta_A\) specifying the intended BCC sector.

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi(x)=\phi(x)\,z(x)\sum_{A\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}}\eta_A e^{iG_A\cdot x}.
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_locked_field}
\end{equation}

This is the first nontrivial nonlinear search manifold.

\section{4. Defect-compatible decomposition}

Because the intended branch must later support the carrier construction, we further resolve
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z(x)=z_B(\xi)+\delta z(x),
\qquad
\phi(x)=\phi_B(\xi)+\delta\phi(x),
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_defect_split}
\end{equation}
where \(\xi\) is the transverse defect coordinate and \(z_B,\phi_B\) are the defect-profile background fields.

At the first construction level, the actual branch search is reduced to solving for
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\phi_B(\xi),\qquad z_B(\xi),
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_profile_unknowns}
\end{equation}
subject to asymptotic and regularity conditions.

\section{5. Reduced one-dimensional stationary problem}

Under the defect-compatible locked reduction, the stationary problem collapses to an effective one-dimensional variational problem
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal E_{\mathrm{red}}[\phi_B,z_B]
=
\int d\xi\;
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{red}}
\bigl(
\phi_B,\phi_B',\phi_B'',
z_B,z_B',z_B'',\dots
\bigr),
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_Ered}
\end{equation}
with Euler--Lagrange equations
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\delta \mathcal E_{\mathrm{red}}}{\delta \phi_B^\dagger}=0,
\qquad
\frac{\delta \mathcal E_{\mathrm{red}}}{\delta z_B^\dagger}=0,
\qquad
z_B^\dagger z_B=1.
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_redEL}
\end{equation}

This is the first actual nonlinear branch equation we must solve.

\section{6. Residual map for the actual branch solver}

Introduce the nonlinear residual map
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal R[\phi_B,z_B]
:=
\begin{pmatrix}
R_\phi[\phi_B,z_B]\\
R_z[\phi_B,z_B]\\
z_B^\dagger z_B-1
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_residual_map}
\end{equation}
where \(R_\phi\) and \(R_z\) are the reduced Euler--Lagrange residuals.

The actual nonlinear branch problem is then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal R[\phi_B,z_B]=0.
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_residual_zero}
\end{equation}

This is the correct object for Newton, gradient flow, or continuation methods.

\section{7. Newton--Kantorovich step}

Given an approximate branch \((\phi_B^{(n)},z_B^{(n)})\), define the linearized Hessian/Jacobian operator
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal J^{(n)}
:=
D\mathcal R[\phi_B^{(n)},z_B^{(n)}].
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_Jacobian}
\end{equation}

Then the Newton step is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal J^{(n)}
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta\phi_B^{(n)}\\
\delta z_B^{(n)}\\
\delta\lambda^{(n)}
\end{pmatrix}
=
-
\mathcal R[\phi_B^{(n)},z_B^{(n)}],
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_Newton}
\end{equation}
where \(\delta\lambda^{(n)}\) enforces the normalization constraint on \(z_B\).

The update is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\phi_B^{(n+1)}=\phi_B^{(n)}+\delta\phi_B^{(n)},
\qquad
z_B^{(n+1)}=\frac{z_B^{(n)}+\delta z_B^{(n)}}{\|z_B^{(n)}+\delta z_B^{(n)}\|}.
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_update}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Gradient-flow alternative}

If the Newton step is numerically stiff, use the relaxation flow
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_s\phi_B
=
-\,\frac{\delta \mathcal E_{\mathrm{red}}}{\delta \phi_B^\dagger},
\qquad
\partial_s z_B
=
-\,\Pi_{z_B^\perp}
\frac{\delta \mathcal E_{\mathrm{red}}}{\delta z_B^\dagger},
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_flow}
\end{equation}
where \(\Pi_{z_B^\perp}\) projects orthogonally to preserve \(z_B^\dagger z_B=1\).

A stationary branch is then a fixed point:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_s\phi_B=0,
\qquad
\partial_s z_B=0.
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_flow_fixed}
\end{equation}

\section{9. Acceptance criteria for \texorpdfstring{$\Psi_{\mathrm{actual}}$}{Psi actual}}

A candidate branch \(\Psi_{\mathrm{actual}}\) is accepted only if all of the following hold:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|\mathcal R[\phi_B,z_B]\|<\varepsilon_{\mathrm{NL}},
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_accept1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{grid refinement changes observables by }<\varepsilon_{\mathrm{grid}},
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_accept2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{flow/Newton convergence is stable under initialization perturbations,}
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_accept3}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the shell content is BCC-dominant,}
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_accept4}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the Hessian around the branch has no forbidden unstable mode.}
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_accept5}
\end{equation}

Only after these pass do we call the result
\[
\Psi_{\mathrm{actual}}(x).
\]

\section{10. Why this ends the repetition}

All later objects are then derived from the same branch:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi_{\mathrm{actual}}(x)
\;\Longrightarrow\;
L_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)
\;\Longrightarrow\;
K_i=\partial_{k_i}L|_{k_*}
\;\Longrightarrow\;
P_*K_iP_*
\;\Longrightarrow\;
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\label{eq:ANPDE_unified_chain}
\end{equation}

Thus the carrier coefficients, CKM-type reduced quantities, and all branch audits are no longer computed from different fronts.
They all come from one common nonlinear branch.

\section{11. Immediate next task}

The immediate next task is not another decomposition of reduced coefficients.
It is to write the first explicit reduced residual map
\[
R_\phi[\phi_B,z_B],\qquad R_z[\phi_B,z_B]
\]
for the locked BCC defect ansatz and to choose the first numerical scheme.

That is the first real construction step toward
\[
\Psi_{\mathrm{actual}}(x).
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The actual bottleneck is the construction of the nonlinear stationary branch
\[
\Psi_{\mathrm{actual}}(x),
\]
not further decomposition of reduced audit quantities.

The correct formulation is:

\[
\mathcal E'[\Psi]=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\Psi_{\mathrm{actual}}(x),
\]
with the intended BCC locked defect ansatz
\[
\Psi(x)=\phi(x)\,z(x)\sum_{A\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}}\eta_A e^{iG_A\cdot x},
\]
further reduced to the defect-profile unknowns
\[
\phi_B(\xi),\qquad z_B(\xi).
\]

This gives the reduced nonlinear residual map
\[
\mathcal R[\phi_B,z_B]=0,
\]
which can be solved either by Newton--Kantorovich iteration or by constrained gradient flow.

A candidate branch is accepted only if:

\[
\|\mathcal R\|<\varepsilon_{\mathrm{NL}},
\]
the branch is grid-converged,
the convergence is stable,
the shell content is BCC-dominant,
and the Hessian has no forbidden unstable mode.

Once \(\Psi_{\mathrm{actual}}(x)\) is obtained, all later quantities follow from the same chain:
\[
\Psi_{\mathrm{actual}}(x)
\to
L_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)
\to
K_i
\to
P_*K_iP_*
\to
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

So from here on, there is one route only:
construct the actual nonlinear branch first, then derive everything else from it.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit Class II Callback and Phase-I Actual Branch Search}

\section{Goal}

After reviewing the accumulated materials, the most forward nonredundant step is clear:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{freeze the explicit solver-ready Class II callback } \mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi]
\text{ and run the first accepted actual-BCC branch search.}
}
\end{equation}

The point is not to further decompose reduced audits.
It is to construct a stationary nonlinear branch
\[
\Psi_{\mathrm{actual}}(x)
\]
of the strongest currently explicit working microscopic PDE.

\section{1. Frozen stationary working PDE}

We take the Phase-I stationary microscopic PDE in the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-\mu^2\Psi
+Z\nabla^2\Psi
-Y\nabla^4\Psi
-\lambda |\Psi|^2\Psi
-\gamma |\Psi|^4\Psi
+\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi]
=
0.
}
\label{eq:phase1_stationary_final}
\end{equation}

The pseudo-time relaxation flow is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_\tau \Psi
=
\mu^2\Psi
-Z\nabla^2\Psi
+Y\nabla^4\Psi
+\lambda |\Psi|^2\Psi
+\gamma |\Psi|^4\Psi
-\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi].
}
\label{eq:phase1_relax_final}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Explicit working Class II branch}

The strongest explicit working microscopic branch is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^a J_i^a[P,\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^a K_i^a[P,\Psi].
}
\label{eq:phase1_working_branch}
\end{equation}

The working \(\Psi\)-only promotion used by the solver is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_\varepsilon:=\Psi^\dagger\Psi+\varepsilon,
\qquad
m^a:=\Psi^\dagger T^a\Psi,
\qquad
n^a:=\frac{m^a}{\rho_\varepsilon}.
}
\label{eq:phase1_rho_m_n}
\end{equation}

Then the current sector is realized as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_i^a=\partial_i m^a,
\qquad
K_i^a=\rho_\varepsilon\,\partial_i n^a
=
\partial_i m^a-n^a\partial_i\rho_\varepsilon.
}
\label{eq:phase1_JK_working}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Heavy-mediator elimination}

The algebraic heavy-field equation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
X_i^a
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\bigl(
\alpha_X J_i^a+\beta_X K_i^a
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:phase1_X_elim}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:phase1_JK_working} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
X_i^a
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\Bigl[
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)\partial_i m^a
-\beta_X n^a\partial_i\rho_\varepsilon
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:phase1_X_explicit}
\end{equation}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
F_i^a
:=
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)\partial_i m^a
-\beta_X n^a\partial_i\rho_\varepsilon.
}
\label{eq:phase1_Fi}
\end{equation}

Then the induced energy correction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta\mathcal E_{II}
=
-\frac{1}{2M_X^2}\sum_{i,a}F_i^aF_i^a.
}
\label{eq:phase1_deltaE}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Explicit solver-ready callback}

Define the auxiliary fields
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A^a
=
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)T^a\Psi-\beta_X n^a\Psi,
}
\label{eq:phase1_Aa}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_i^a
=
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)T^a(\partial_i\Psi)
-\beta_X n^a(\partial_i\Psi)
-\beta_X\frac{(T^a-n^a\mathbf 1)\Psi}{\rho_\varepsilon}\,\partial_i\rho_\varepsilon.
}
\label{eq:phase1_Bia}
\end{equation}

The explicit solver-ready working callback is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi]
=
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\sum_{i,a}
\Bigl[
\partial_i(F_i^aA^a)-F_i^aB_i^a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:phase1_callback}
\end{equation}

This is the actual model-specific ingredient that the solver was missing.

\section{5. Semi-implicit Fourier step}

Split the flow into
\[
L=\mu^2-Z\nabla^2+Y\nabla^4,
\qquad
N(\Psi)=\lambda|\Psi|^2\Psi+\gamma|\Psi|^4\Psi-\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi].
\]
Then one semi-implicit step is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(1-\Delta\tau\,L)\Psi^{n+1}
=
\Psi^n+\Delta\tau\,N(\Psi^n).
}
\label{eq:phase1_semiimplicit_final}
\end{equation}

In Fourier space,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat\Psi^{\,n+1}(k)
=
\frac{
\widehat\Psi^{\,n}(k)+\Delta\tau\,\widehat{N(\Psi^n)}(k)
}{
1+\Delta\tau\bigl(\mu^2-Z(-|k|^2)+Y|k|^4\bigr)
}.
}
\label{eq:phase1_fourier_final}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Commensurate BCC branch setup}

To remove box-induced shell ambiguity, freeze the first commensurate BCC setup
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L=4\pi m,
\qquad
q_0=q_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2},
\qquad
m\in\mathbb Z_{>0}.
}
\label{eq:phase1_commensurate}
\end{equation}

Initialize from the equal-amplitude 12-mode BCC shell seed
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\phi_0(x)
=
A_{\mathrm{BCC}}
\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}e^{iQ\cdot x},
}
\label{eq:phase1_BCC_seed}
\end{equation}
plus a small defect-seeded perturbation.

\section{7. Orbit-symmetric stabilization layer}

Because the actual observed bottleneck is orbit-level instability inside the retained BCC shell, add the weak orbit-balancing map after each PDE step:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat\Psi_\alpha
\longmapsto
\widehat\Psi_\alpha
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{bal}}
\bigl(
\overline{\widehat\Psi}-\widehat\Psi_\alpha
\bigr),
\qquad
\overline{\widehat\Psi}
=
\frac1{12}\sum_{\beta=1}^{12}\widehat\Psi_\beta.
}
\label{eq:phase1_orbit_balance}
\end{equation}
At the current working level one may take
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{bal}}=0.08
}
\label{eq:phase1_epsbal}
\end{equation}
as the first test value.

This is not yet promoted to a constitutive physical term.
It is a numerical stabilization layer used only to test whether an orbit-symmetric BCC stationary branch exists nearby.

\section{8. Residual map and acceptance criteria}

Define the nonlinear PDE residual
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_{\mathrm{PDE}}[\Psi]
:=
-\mu^2\Psi
+Z\nabla^2\Psi
-Y\nabla^4\Psi
-\lambda |\Psi|^2\Psi
-\gamma |\Psi|^4\Psi
+\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi].
}
\label{eq:phase1_residual}
\end{equation}

The branch is accepted only if:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{rel\_residual}
:=
\frac{\|R_{\mathrm{PDE}}[\Psi]\|}{\|\Psi\|}
<\varepsilon_{\mathrm{res}},
}
\label{eq:phase1_accept1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{shell\_fraction}
=
\frac{\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}|\widehat\Psi(Q)|^2}
{\sum_k |\widehat\Psi(k)|^2}
>\varepsilon_{\mathrm{shell}},
}
\label{eq:phase1_accept2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{orbit\_balance}
=
\frac{\min_{\alpha\in\mathcal S_{12}}P_\alpha}
{\max_{\alpha\in\mathcal S_{12}}P_\alpha}
>\varepsilon_{\mathrm{orb}},
}
\label{eq:phase1_accept3}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{no-one-patch-collapse indicator passes,}
}
\label{eq:phase1_accept4}
\end{equation}
and finally
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the accepted branch is stable under grid refinement and seed perturbation.}
}
\label{eq:phase1_accept5}
\end{equation}

\section{9. Output map}

Once an accepted branch \(\Psi_{\mathrm{actual}}\) is found, all later extractions come from that same branch:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi_{\mathrm{actual}}
\to
L_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)
\to
K_i
\to
P_*K_iP_*
\to
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta),
}
\label{eq:phase1_output1}
\end{equation}
and in parallel
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi_{\mathrm{actual}}
\to
\text{carrier gates},
\quad
\text{CKM finite tables},
\quad
(W_2,m_*,g_{\mathrm{eff}},Z_{\mathrm{cub}}).
}
\label{eq:phase1_output2}
\end{equation}

\section{10. Immediate next calculation}

Therefore the actual next calculation is not another reduced audit.

It is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{run the Phase-I relaxation with }
\eqref{eq:phase1_callback}
+
\eqref{eq:phase1_commensurate}
+
\eqref{eq:phase1_orbit_balance},
\text{ and test acceptance.}
}
\label{eq:phase1_next}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

After reviewing the accumulated materials carefully, the most forward nonredundant move is now unambiguous:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{freeze the explicit working Class II callback }\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi]
\text{ and run the first accepted actual-BCC branch search.}
}
\end{equation}

The correct stationary PDE is
\[
-\mu^2\Psi
+Z\nabla^2\Psi
-Y\nabla^4\Psi
-\lambda |\Psi|^2\Psi
-\gamma |\Psi|^4\Psi
+\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi]
=0,
\]
with pseudo-time relaxation
\[
\partial_\tau\Psi
=
\mu^2\Psi
-Z\nabla^2\Psi
+Y\nabla^4\Psi
+\lambda |\Psi|^2\Psi
+\gamma |\Psi|^4\Psi
-\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi].
\]

The explicit working callback is
\[
\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi]
=
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\sum_{i,a}
\left[
\partial_i(F_i^aA^a)-F_i^aB_i^a
\right],
\]
with
\[
\rho_\varepsilon=\Psi^\dagger\Psi+\varepsilon,
\qquad
m^a=\Psi^\dagger T^a\Psi,
\qquad
n^a=\frac{m^a}{\rho_\varepsilon},
\]
\[
F_i^a
=
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)\partial_i m^a
-\beta_X n^a\partial_i\rho_\varepsilon,
\]
\[
A^a
=
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)T^a\Psi-\beta_X n^a\Psi,
\]
\[
B_i^a
=
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)T^a(\partial_i\Psi)
-\beta_X n^a(\partial_i\Psi)
-\beta_X\frac{(T^a-n^a\mathbf1)\Psi}{\rho_\varepsilon}\partial_i\rho_\varepsilon.
\]

The branch-preserving numerical setup is:

\[
L=4\pi m,
\qquad
q_0=q_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2},
\]
equal-amplitude 12-mode BCC initial data, and the weak orbit-balancing step
\[
\widehat\Psi_\alpha
\mapsto
\widehat\Psi_\alpha+\varepsilon_{\rm bal}(\overline{\widehat\Psi}-\widehat\Psi_\alpha),
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm bal}=0.08.
\]

A branch is accepted only if the PDE residual is small, the shell fraction remains high, the orbit balance remains high, no one-patch collapse occurs, and the result is stable under grid/seed perturbations.

So the project has now been reduced to one executable next step:
\[
\boxed{
\text{run the Phase-I actual nonlinear branch search with the frozen callback and stabilization protocol.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Phase-I Actual Branch Execution Protocol}

\section{Goal}

The solver infrastructure is already frozen.
The true remaining issue is not another reduction of audits, but the execution protocol for the actual nonlinear branch search.

We therefore fix one concrete Phase-I protocol:
\[
\boxed{
\text{same solver backbone, same commensurate BCC box, same working callback, fixed acceptance ladder.}
}
\]

\section{1. Frozen branch geometry and solver backbone}

Keep the commensurate BCC setup fixed:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L=4\pi,
\qquad
q_0=q_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}.
}
\label{eq:EP_geom}
\end{equation}

Keep the same explicit working Class II callback
\[
\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi]
\]
and the same semi-implicit pseudo-time relaxation scheme already fixed in the solver backbone.

Keep the orbit-balancing map
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat\Psi_\alpha
\mapsto
\widehat\Psi_\alpha
+
\varepsilon_{\rm bal}
\bigl(\overline{\widehat\Psi}-\widehat\Psi_\alpha\bigr),
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm bal}=0.08,
}
\label{eq:EP_bal}
\end{equation}
as the default stabilization layer for the first accepted-branch search.

\section{2. Grid ladder and time-step ladder}

Use the following fixed refinement ladder:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
N\in\{32,\,48,\,64\},
\qquad
\Delta\tau\in\{5\times10^{-3},\,2.5\times10^{-3},\,1.25\times10^{-3}\}.
}
\label{eq:EP_grid_dt}
\end{equation}

The branch search always proceeds in this order:
\[
(N,\Delta\tau)=(32,5\times10^{-3})
\to
(48,2.5\times10^{-3})
\to
(64,1.25\times10^{-3}).
\]

No new seed family is introduced after this point.
Only the same intended BCC seed is refined.

\section{3. Measured diagnostics}

At every checkpoint, record exactly the four solver diagnostics already implemented:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{rel\_step}
=
\frac{\|\Psi^{n+1}-\Psi^n\|_{L^2}}{\|\Psi^n\|_{L^2}},
}
\label{eq:EP_relstep}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{rel\_residual}
=
\frac{\|R[\Psi]\|_{L^2}}{\|\Psi\|_{L^2}},
}
\label{eq:EP_relres}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
f_{\rm shell}
=
\frac{\sum_{||k|-q_0|\le \delta}|\widehat\Psi(k)|^2}
{\sum_k|\widehat\Psi(k)|^2},
}
\label{eq:EP_shell}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_{\rm orb}
=
\frac{\min_{\alpha\in\mathcal S_{12}}P_\alpha}
{\max_{\alpha\in\mathcal S_{12}}P_\alpha}.
}
\label{eq:EP_orb}
\end{equation}

These are the only primary phase-I diagnostics.

\section{4. Three-level acceptance ladder}

Because recent runs show that shell/orbit geometry can already become excellent while the residual stays large, we separate the protocol into three levels.

\subsection{Level 1: geometric pre-acceptance}

A run passes the geometric gate if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
f_{\rm shell}>0.90,
\qquad
b_{\rm orb}>0.95.
}
\label{eq:EP_geo}
\end{equation}

This is chosen because one recent run already achieved
\[
f_{\rm shell}\approx 0.9184,
\qquad
b_{\rm orb}\approx 0.9963,
\]
while still failing stationarity.
So \eqref{eq:EP_geo} is demanding but already known to be reachable.

\subsection{Level 2: stationary candidate}

A run is called a stationary candidate if, in addition to \eqref{eq:EP_geo},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{rel\_step}<10^{-3},
\qquad
\mathrm{rel\_residual}<10^{-1}.
}
\label{eq:EP_candidate}
\end{equation}

This is not the final acceptance level.
It is only the first point at which it is meaningful to perform refinement and stability checks.

\subsection{Level 3: accepted actual branch}

A run is accepted as \(\Psi_{\rm actual}\) only if, after refinement,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{rel\_step}<10^{-4},
\qquad
\mathrm{rel\_residual}<10^{-2},
\qquad
f_{\rm shell}>0.90,
\qquad
b_{\rm orb}>0.95.
}
\label{eq:EP_accept}
\end{equation}

In addition, the extracted observables must satisfy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{|O_{64,1.25\times10^{-3}}-O_{48,2.5\times10^{-3}}|}{|O_{64,1.25\times10^{-3}}|}<10^{-2}
}
\label{eq:EP_gridconv}
\end{equation}
for every monitored observable \(O\) in the set
\[
\{f_{\rm shell},\,b_{\rm orb},\,W_0,\,W_2,\,\|\Psi\|_{L^2}\}.
\]

\section{5. Early rejection and bottleneck diagnosis}

To prevent further repetition, impose the following hard decision rules.

\subsection{Rule A: shell-loss rejection}

If after \(100\) pseudo-time steps,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
f_{\rm shell}<0.80,
}
\label{eq:EP_reject_shell}
\end{equation}
reject the run as leaving the intended BCC sector.

\subsection{Rule B: orbit-collapse rejection}

If after \(100\) pseudo-time steps,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_{\rm orb}<0.20,
}
\label{eq:EP_reject_orb}
\end{equation}
reject the run as orbit-collapsed.

\subsection{Rule C: callback-mismatch diagnosis}

If a run satisfies the geometric gate \eqref{eq:EP_geo} but, over three successive halvings of \(\Delta\tau\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{rel\_residual}>10^{-1}
\quad\text{and}\quad
\mathrm{rel\_residual}\ \text{does not decrease by at least a factor }2,
}
\label{eq:EP_callback_diag}
\end{equation}
then diagnose the failure as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{constitutive/callback mismatch, not geometric branch failure.}
}
\label{eq:EP_callback_conclusion}
\end{equation}

This rule is directly motivated by the already observed pattern:
geometry can be nearly perfect while the residual remains \(O(10^{-1}\text{--}10^0)\).

\section{6. Phase-I stop condition}

The phase-I search stops immediately when either:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{an accepted actual branch satisfying \eqref{eq:EP_accept}--\eqref{eq:EP_gridconv} is found,}
}
\label{eq:EP_stop_accept}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the callback-mismatch diagnosis \eqref{eq:EP_callback_diag}--\eqref{eq:EP_callback_conclusion} is triggered.}
}
\label{eq:EP_stop_callback}
\end{equation}

In the second case, the correct next step is not a new seed or a new box.
It is a revision of the constitutive callback \(\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi]\).

\section{7. What this protocol accomplishes}

This protocol prevents the project from drifting.

It cleanly distinguishes:

\begin{enumerate}
\item geometric failure of the intended BCC branch,
\item orbit-collapse failure,
\item and constitutive mismatch of the working callback.
\end{enumerate}

So Phase I now has an exact executable outcome map:
\[
\boxed{
\text{accept branch}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\text{reject geometry}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\text{diagnose callback mismatch.}
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The actual nonlinear branch search is now fixed by one execution protocol.

The frozen setup is:
\[
L=4\pi,\qquad q_0=\frac{1}{\sqrt2},\qquad \varepsilon_{\rm bal}=0.08,
\]
with refinement ladder
\[
N\in\{32,48,64\},
\qquad
\Delta\tau\in\{5\times10^{-3},\,2.5\times10^{-3},\,1.25\times10^{-3}\}.
\]

The only primary diagnostics are:
\[
\mathrm{rel\_step},\qquad
\mathrm{rel\_residual},\qquad
f_{\rm shell},\qquad
b_{\rm orb}.
\]

The three-level acceptance ladder is:

\[
f_{\rm shell}>0.90,\quad b_{\rm orb}>0.95
\qquad
\text{(geometric pre-acceptance)},
\]

\[
\mathrm{rel\_step}<10^{-3},\quad \mathrm{rel\_residual}<10^{-1}
\qquad
\text{(stationary candidate)},
\]

\[
\mathrm{rel\_step}<10^{-4},\quad
\mathrm{rel\_residual}<10^{-2},\quad
f_{\rm shell}>0.90,\quad
b_{\rm orb}>0.95,
\]
plus \(<1\%\) grid/time refinement stability
\[
\qquad\text{(accepted actual branch)}.
\]

The hard early decisions are:

\[
f_{\rm shell}<0.80
\Rightarrow
\text{reject as shell-loss},
\]
\[
b_{\rm orb}<0.20
\Rightarrow
\text{reject as orbit-collapse},
\]
and if geometry is good but the residual stays \(>10^{-1}\) without a factor-2 decrease across three halvings of \(\Delta\tau\),
\[
\text{diagnose callback mismatch, not branch failure.}
\]

So Phase I is no longer vague.
It now has one exact executable outcome map:
\[
\boxed{
\text{accept branch}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\text{reject geometry}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\text{diagnose constitutive mismatch.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Stage IA: Orientation-Frozen Actual Nonlinear Branch}

\section{Goal}

The first real construction step of the actual nonlinear branch is not the full coupled \((\phi_B,z_B)\) problem yet.

Instead, we first freeze the internal orientation and solve the scalar amplitude branch:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi(x)=\Phi(x)\,z_0,
\qquad
z_0^\dagger z_0=1,
\qquad
z_0=\text{fixed}.
}
\label{eq:IA_ansatz}
\end{equation}

This produces the first actual nonlinear stationary branch candidate.
Only after that do we release the tangent orientation sector.

\section{1. Frozen-orientation reduction of the Class II dictionary}

Let
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_\varepsilon=\Psi^\dagger\Psi+\varepsilon,
\qquad
m^a=\Psi^\dagger T^a\Psi,
\qquad
n^a=\frac{m^a}{\rho_\varepsilon}.
}
\label{eq:IA_rho_m_n}
\end{equation}

For the frozen ansatz \(\Psi=\Phi z_0\), define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
n_0^a:=z_0^\dagger T^a z_0.
}
\label{eq:IA_n0}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m^a = |\Phi|^2 n_0^a,
\qquad
n^a=n_0^a
\quad
(\text{constant in }x).
}
\label{eq:IA_mn_const}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_i^a=\partial_i m^a=n_0^a\,\partial_i|\Phi|^2,
}
\label{eq:IA_J}
\end{equation}
while
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^a
=
\partial_i m^a-n^a\partial_i\rho_\varepsilon
=
0
}
\label{eq:IA_K_zero}
\end{equation}
at this frozen-orientation level.

Therefore the heavy-field elimination simplifies to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
F_i^a
=
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)\partial_i m^a-\beta_X n^a\partial_i\rho_\varepsilon
=
\alpha_X n_0^a\,\partial_i|\Phi|^2.
}
\label{eq:IA_F}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Scalar projection of the working callback}

The solver-ready callback is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi]
=
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\sum_{i,a}
\Bigl[
\partial_i(F_i^aA^a)-F_i^aB_i^a
\Bigr].
\label{eq:IA_callback_start}
\end{equation}

Projecting along \(z_0\), only the \(z_0\)-parallel component matters for the Stage-IA scalar branch.
Using
\[
z_0^\dagger T^a z_0=n_0^a,
\qquad
z_0^\dagger(T^a-n_0^a\mathbf 1)z_0=0,
\]
one obtains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_0^\dagger A^a = \alpha_X n_0^a\,\Phi,
\qquad
z_0^\dagger B_i^a = \alpha_X n_0^a\,\partial_i\Phi.
}
\label{eq:IA_projAB}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:IA_F} and \eqref{eq:IA_projAB} into \eqref{eq:IA_callback_start},
\begin{align}
z_0^\dagger\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Phi z_0]
&=
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\sum_{i,a}
\Bigl[
\partial_i\bigl(\alpha_X n_0^a\partial_i|\Phi|^2 \cdot \alpha_X n_0^a\Phi\bigr)
-
\alpha_X n_0^a\partial_i|\Phi|^2\cdot \alpha_X n_0^a\partial_i\Phi
\Bigr]
\\
&=
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
\sum_a (n_0^a)^2
\Bigl[
\partial_i\bigl((\partial_i|\Phi|^2)\Phi\bigr)-(\partial_i|\Phi|^2)(\partial_i\Phi)
\Bigr]
\\
&=
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
\sum_a (n_0^a)^2
\bigl[\nabla^2(|\Phi|^2)\bigr]\Phi.
\end{align}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\nu_0:=\sum_a (n_0^a)^2,
\qquad
\chi_{II}:=\frac{\alpha_X^2\nu_0}{M_X^2}.
}
\label{eq:IA_nu0_chi}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_0^\dagger\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Phi z_0]
=
\chi_{II}\,\nabla^2(|\Phi|^2)\,\Phi.
}
\label{eq:IA_scalar_callback}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Stage-IA scalar stationary PDE}

Projecting the full stationary microscopic PDE along \(z_0\), the frozen-orientation branch satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-\mu^2\Phi
+Z\nabla^2\Phi
-Y\nabla^4\Phi
-\lambda |\Phi|^2\Phi
-\gamma |\Phi|^4\Phi
+\chi_{II}\,\nabla^2(|\Phi|^2)\,\Phi
=
0.
}
\label{eq:IA_scalar_PDE}
\end{equation}

This is the first actual nonlinear PDE we must solve.

\section{4. Stage-IA pseudo-time relaxation}

The corresponding relaxation flow is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_\tau \Phi
=
\mu^2\Phi
-Z\nabla^2\Phi
+Y\nabla^4\Phi
+\lambda |\Phi|^2\Phi
+\gamma |\Phi|^4\Phi
-\chi_{II}\,\nabla^2(|\Phi|^2)\,\Phi.
}
\label{eq:IA_scalar_flow}
\end{equation}

A semi-implicit step may be written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(1-\Delta\tau\,L)\Phi^{n+1}
=
\Phi^n
+
\Delta\tau\,N_{\rm IA}(\Phi^n),
}
\label{eq:IA_step}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
L=\mu^2-Z\nabla^2+Y\nabla^4,
\qquad
N_{\rm IA}(\Phi)=\lambda |\Phi|^2\Phi+\gamma |\Phi|^4\Phi-\chi_{II}\nabla^2(|\Phi|^2)\Phi.
\label{eq:IA_LN}
\end{equation}

\section{5. BCC-locked amplitude reduction}

Now impose the commensurate BCC locked ansatz
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Phi(x)=\phi(\xi)\,S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x),
\qquad
S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x):=\sum_{A\in\mathcal S_{12}}\eta_A e^{iG_A\cdot x}.
}
\label{eq:IA_BCC}
\end{equation}

Define the cell averages
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_2:=\langle |S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^2\rangle_{\rm cell},
\qquad
C_4:=\langle |S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^4\rangle_{\rm cell},
\qquad
C_6:=\langle |S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^6\rangle_{\rm cell}.
}
\label{eq:IA_C246}
\end{equation}

Then the first shell-averaged reduced residual is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_\phi[\phi]
=
-\mu^2 C_2\,\phi
+Z\,\mathcal L_2[\phi]
-Y\,\mathcal L_4[\phi]
-\lambda C_4\,|\phi|^2\phi
-\gamma C_6\,|\phi|^4\phi
+\chi_{II}\,\mathcal C_{II}[\phi],
}
\label{eq:IA_Rphi}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_2[\phi]
:=
\bigl\langle \overline{S_{\mathrm{BCC}}}\,\nabla^2(\phi S_{\mathrm{BCC}})\bigr\rangle_{\rm cell},
}
\label{eq:IA_L2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_4[\phi]
:=
\bigl\langle \overline{S_{\mathrm{BCC}}}\,\nabla^4(\phi S_{\mathrm{BCC}})\bigr\rangle_{\rm cell},
}
\label{eq:IA_L4}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{II}[\phi]
:=
\bigl\langle \overline{S_{\mathrm{BCC}}}\,\nabla^2(|\phi S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^2)\,S_{\mathrm{BCC}}\bigr\rangle_{\rm cell}\,\phi.
}
\label{eq:IA_CII}
\end{equation}

Thus the first actual branch search is reduced to the scalar one-dimensional residual equation
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_\phi[\phi]=0.
}
\label{eq:IA_Rphi_zero}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Tangent consistency residual}

The frozen-orientation branch is acceptable only if the orthogonal tangent forcing is small.

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_\perp[\Phi;z_0]
:=
\Pi_{z_0^\perp}\,\mathcal E'[\Phi z_0].
}
\label{eq:IA_Rperp_def}
\end{equation}

At leading Class II order, a sufficient consistency condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_{z_0^\perp}(n_0^a T^a z_0)=0.
}
\label{eq:IA_consistency_suff}
\end{equation}

More generally, Stage IA is accepted only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\|R_\perp[\Phi;z_0]\|}{\|\Phi\|}<\varepsilon_\perp,
}
\label{eq:IA_consistency_tol}
\end{equation}
with \(\varepsilon_\perp\) chosen smaller than the PDE residual tolerance.

If \eqref{eq:IA_consistency_tol} fails, the Stage-IA branch is still useful as the seed for Stage IB, where \(z(\xi)\) is released dynamically.

\section{7. What this accomplishes}

Stage IA already removes the biggest ambiguity.

The actual nonlinear branch construction is no longer a vague search over the full \(\Psi\)-space.
It is first reduced to:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a scalar fourth-order nonlinear PDE \eqref{eq:IA_scalar_PDE},
\item then a shell-averaged defect-amplitude residual equation \eqref{eq:IA_Rphi_zero},
\item together with the tangent consistency check \eqref{eq:IA_Rperp_def}.
\end{enumerate}

So the immediate next executable problem is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{solve }R_\phi[\phi]=0\text{ on the commensurate BCC box, then test }R_\perp.
}
\label{eq:IA_next}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The first real forward step of the actual nonlinear branch construction is the orientation-frozen Stage-IA ansatz
\[
\Psi(x)=\Phi(x)\,z_0.
\]

In this sector,
\[
m^a=|\Phi|^2 n_0^a,
\qquad
n^a=n_0^a,
\qquad
J_i^a=n_0^a\partial_i|\Phi|^2,
\qquad
K_i^a=0,
\]
so the heavy-mediator Class II callback simplifies drastically.

Projecting along \(z_0\), one gets the exact scalar callback
\[
\boxed{
z_0^\dagger\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Phi z_0]
=
\chi_{II}\,\nabla^2(|\Phi|^2)\,\Phi,
\qquad
\chi_{II}=\frac{\alpha_X^2\nu_0}{M_X^2},
\qquad
\nu_0=\sum_a(n_0^a)^2.
}
\]

Therefore the Stage-IA stationary PDE is
\[
\boxed{
-\mu^2\Phi
+Z\nabla^2\Phi
-Y\nabla^4\Phi
-\lambda |\Phi|^2\Phi
-\gamma |\Phi|^4\Phi
+\chi_{II}\,\nabla^2(|\Phi|^2)\,\Phi
=
0.
}
\]

With the locked BCC shell ansatz
\[
\Phi(x)=\phi(\xi)S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x),
\]
this reduces to the scalar residual equation
\[
\boxed{
R_\phi[\phi]
=
-\mu^2 C_2\,\phi
+Z\,\mathcal L_2[\phi]
-Y\,\mathcal L_4[\phi]
-\lambda C_4\,|\phi|^2\phi
-\gamma C_6\,|\phi|^4\phi
+\chi_{II}\,\mathcal C_{II}[\phi]
=0.
}
\]

The frozen-orientation branch is accepted only if the tangent consistency residual
\[
R_\perp[\Phi;z_0]=\Pi_{z_0^\perp}\mathcal E'[\Phi z_0]
\]
is also sufficiently small.

So the immediate next executable problem is no longer vague:
\[
\boxed{
\text{solve }R_\phi[\phi]=0\text{ first, then test }R_\perp.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Stage IA: BCC Cell-Averaged Scalar Amplitude ODE}

\section{Goal}

Starting from the Stage-IA scalar stationary PDE
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-\mu^2\Phi
+Z\nabla^2\Phi
-Y\nabla^4\Phi
-\lambda |\Phi|^2\Phi
-\gamma |\Phi|^4\Phi
+\chi_{II}\,\nabla^2(|\Phi|^2)\Phi
=
0,
}
\label{eq:SIA_scalar_PDE}
\end{equation}
we now insert the commensurate locked BCC ansatz
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Phi(x)=\phi(\xi)\,S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x),
\qquad
\xi=\hat n\cdot x,
}
\label{eq:SIA_BCC_ansatz}
\end{equation}
and reduce the PDE to a one-dimensional amplitude equation for \(\phi(\xi)\).

\section{1. Basic shell identities}

Let
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x)=\sum_{A\in\mathcal S_{12}}\eta_A e^{iG_A\cdot x},
\qquad
|G_A|=q_*.
}
\label{eq:SIA_shell}
\end{equation}

Define the cell averages
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_2:=\langle |S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^2\rangle_{\rm cell},
\qquad
C_4:=\langle |S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^4\rangle_{\rm cell},
\qquad
C_6:=\langle |S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^6\rangle_{\rm cell}.
}
\label{eq:SIA_C246}
\end{equation}

We also define the fourth-order shell-gradient constant
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_{\Delta}:=
\left\langle
|S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^2\,\nabla^2|S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^2
\right\rangle_{\rm cell}.
}
\label{eq:SIA_CDelta}
\end{equation}

For the orbit-symmetric BCC shell,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left\langle
\overline{S_{\mathrm{BCC}}}\,\partial_\xi S_{\mathrm{BCC}}
\right\rangle_{\rm cell}=0,
\qquad
\left\langle
(\hat n\cdot G_A)^2
\right\rangle_{\mathcal S_{12}}
=
\frac{q_*^2}{3}.
}
\label{eq:SIA_shell_sym}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Quadratic operator reduction}

We define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_2[\phi]
:=
\left\langle
\overline{S_{\mathrm{BCC}}}\,\nabla^2(\phi S_{\mathrm{BCC}})
\right\rangle_{\rm cell}.
}
\label{eq:SIA_L2_def}
\end{equation}

Now
\begin{equation}
\nabla^2(\phi e^{iG_A\cdot x})
=
\bigl(
\phi''+2i(\hat n\cdot G_A)\phi'-q_*^2\phi
\bigr)e^{iG_A\cdot x}.
\end{equation}
Summing over the shell and averaging over the cell, the odd term cancels by symmetry, hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_2[\phi]
=
C_2(\phi''-q_*^2\phi).
}
\label{eq:SIA_L2_final}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Quartic derivative operator reduction}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_4[\phi]
:=
\left\langle
\overline{S_{\mathrm{BCC}}}\,\nabla^4(\phi S_{\mathrm{BCC}})
\right\rangle_{\rm cell}.
}
\label{eq:SIA_L4_def}
\end{equation}

For each mode, with \(g_A:=\hat n\cdot G_A\),
\begin{equation}
\nabla^2(\phi e^{iG_A\cdot x})
=
\bigl(D^2+2ig_A D-q_*^2\bigr)\phi\,e^{iG_A\cdot x},
\qquad
D:=\frac{d}{d\xi}.
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\nabla^4(\phi e^{iG_A\cdot x})
=
\bigl(D^2+2ig_A D-q_*^2\bigr)^2\phi\,e^{iG_A\cdot x},
\end{equation}
that is,
\begin{equation}
\bigl(D^2+2ig_A D-q_*^2\bigr)^2
=
D^4+4ig_A D^3-(4g_A^2+2q_*^2)D^2-4ig_Aq_*^2D+q_*^4.
\end{equation}

After shell averaging, the odd \(D^3\) and \(D\) terms vanish, while
\[
\langle g_A^2\rangle=q_*^2/3.
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_4[\phi]
=
C_2\left(
\phi''''-\frac{10}{3}q_*^2\phi''+q_*^4\phi
\right).
}
\label{eq:SIA_L4_final}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Class-II nonlinear callback reduction}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{II}[\phi]
:=
\left\langle
\overline{S_{\mathrm{BCC}}}\,
\nabla^2\bigl(|\phi S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^2\bigr)\,
S_{\mathrm{BCC}}
\right\rangle_{\rm cell}\,\phi.
}
\label{eq:SIA_CII_def}
\end{equation}

Since
\[
|\phi S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^2
=
|\phi|^2|S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^2,
\]
we have
\begin{align}
\nabla^2\bigl(|\phi S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^2\bigr)
&=
(|\phi|^2)''|S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^2
+
2(|\phi|^2)' \partial_\xi |S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^2
+
|\phi|^2\nabla^2|S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^2.
\end{align}
Multiplying by \(\overline{S_{\mathrm{BCC}}}S_{\mathrm{BCC}}=|S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^2\) and averaging over the cell, the odd middle term vanishes by symmetry:
\begin{equation}
\left\langle
|S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^2\,\partial_\xi |S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^2
\right\rangle_{\rm cell}=0.
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{II}[\phi]
=
C_4 (|\phi|^2)''\,\phi
+
C_{\Delta}|\phi|^2\phi.
}
\label{eq:SIA_CII_final_complex}
\end{equation}

For the real branch \(\phi\in\mathbb R\),
\[
(|\phi|^2)''=(\phi^2)''=2(\phi')^2+2\phi\phi'',
\]
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{II}[\phi]
=
2C_4\phi^2\phi''
+
2C_4\phi(\phi')^2
+
C_{\Delta}\phi^3.
}
\label{eq:SIA_CII_final_real}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Reduced scalar amplitude residual}

The shell-averaged scalar residual is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_\phi[\phi]
=
-\mu^2C_2\phi
+Z\mathcal L_2[\phi]
-Y\mathcal L_4[\phi]
-\lambda C_4 |\phi|^2\phi
-\gamma C_6 |\phi|^4\phi
+\chi_{II}\mathcal C_{II}[\phi].
}
\label{eq:SIA_Rphi_def}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:SIA_L2_final}, \eqref{eq:SIA_L4_final}, and \eqref{eq:SIA_CII_final_real} yields the explicit real scalar ODE
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-YC_2\,\phi''''
+
C_2\left(
Z+\frac{10}{3}Yq_*^2
\right)\phi''
-
C_2\left(
\mu^2+Zq_*^2+Yq_*^4
\right)\phi
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,\phi^2\phi''
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,\phi(\phi')^2
+
(\chi_{II}C_{\Delta}-\lambda C_4)\phi^3
-
\gamma C_6\phi^5
=
0.
}
\label{eq:SIA_scalar_ODE}
\end{equation}

This is the first actual one-dimensional nonlinear branch equation.

\section{6. Effective coefficient interpretation}

Equation \eqref{eq:SIA_scalar_ODE} shows that the frozen-orientation actual branch has the following effective structure:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{effective linear mass}
=
C_2(\mu^2+Zq_*^2+Yq_*^4),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{effective second-derivative stiffness}
=
C_2\left(Z+\frac{10}{3}Yq_*^2\right),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{effective cubic coefficient}
=
\chi_{II}C_\Delta-\lambda C_4,
}
\end{equation}
and two genuinely new derivative-cubic terms
\[
2\chi_{II}C_4\phi^2\phi'',
\qquad
2\chi_{II}C_4\phi(\phi')^2.
\]

So the Class-II callback survives the scalar reduction as a derivative-cubic nonlinear stiffness correction.

\section{7. Boundary conditions}

For the defect branch search, impose the standard localized/heteroclinic conditions
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\phi'(\xi)\to 0,
\qquad
\phi'''(\xi)\to 0,
\qquad
\phi(\xi)\to \phi_\infty
\quad
\text{as }|\xi|\to\infty,
}
\label{eq:SIA_bc_inf}
\end{equation}
together with center symmetry
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\phi' (0)=0,
\qquad
\phi'''(0)=0,
}
\label{eq:SIA_bc_center}
\end{equation}
for the even branch.

If a node-type branch is desired, replace \eqref{eq:SIA_bc_center} by the appropriate odd conditions.

\section{8. Immediate next step}

The actual next calculation is now completely concrete:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{solve the scalar fourth-order ODE }
\eqref{eq:SIA_scalar_ODE}
\text{ with }
\eqref{eq:SIA_bc_inf}\text{--}\eqref{eq:SIA_bc_center},
\text{ then evaluate }R_\perp.
}
\label{eq:SIA_next_actual}
\end{equation}

Only after that do we release the internal orientation and move to Stage IB.

\section{Final Summary}

Under the locked BCC ansatz
\[
\Phi(x)=\phi(\xi)S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x),
\]
the shell-averaged operators reduce to

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal L_2[\phi]=C_2(\phi''-q_*^2\phi),
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal L_4[\phi]
=
C_2\left(
\phi''''-\frac{10}{3}q_*^2\phi''+q_*^4\phi
\right),
}
\]

and the Class-II nonlinear callback becomes

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{II}[\phi]
=
2C_4\phi^2\phi''
+
2C_4\phi(\phi')^2
+
C_{\Delta}\phi^3
}
\]
for the real branch.

Therefore the Stage-IA actual scalar amplitude equation is

\[
-YC_2\,\phi''''
+
C_2\left(
Z+\frac{10}{3}Yq_*^2
\right)\phi''
-
C_2\left(
\mu^2+Zq_*^2+Yq_*^4
\right)\phi
\]
\[
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,\phi^2\phi''
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,\phi(\phi')^2
+
(\chi_{II}C_{\Delta}-\lambda C_4)\phi^3
-
\gamma C_6\phi^5
=
0.
\]

This is the first real one-dimensional nonlinear branch equation for the actual branch search.

So the project is now past abstract solver scaffolding.
The immediate next problem is simply:
\[
\boxed{
\text{solve this fourth-order scalar ODE, then test the tangent residual }R_\perp.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Stage IA Solver-Ready Form: Two Second-Order Equations and a First-Order System}

\section{Starting point}

From the BCC cell-averaged Stage-IA reduction, the real scalar amplitude equation is
\[
-YC_2\,\phi''''
+
C_2\left(
Z+\frac{10}{3}Yq_*^2
\right)\phi''
-
C_2\left(
\mu^2+Zq_*^2+Yq_*^4
\right)\phi
\]
\[
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,\phi^2\phi''
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,\phi(\phi')^2
+
(\chi_{II}C_{\Delta}-\lambda C_4)\phi^3
-
\gamma C_6\phi^5
=
0.
\label{eq:SR_start_ODE}
\]

For compactness, define the frozen coefficients
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_2:=C_2\left(Z+\frac{10}{3}Yq_*^2\right),
\qquad
M_2:=C_2\left(\mu^2+Zq_*^2+Yq_*^4\right),
\qquad
U_3:=\chi_{II}C_\Delta-\lambda C_4.
}
\label{eq:SR_A2M2U3}
\end{equation}

Then \eqref{eq:SR_start_ODE} becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-YC_2\,\phi''''
+
A_2\,\phi''
-
M_2\,\phi
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,\phi^2\phi''
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,\phi(\phi')^2
+
U_3\,\phi^3
-
\gamma C_6\,\phi^5
=
0.
}
\label{eq:SR_compact_ODE}
\end{equation}

\section{1. Reduction to two second-order equations}

Introduce
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u(\xi):=\phi(\xi),
\qquad
w(\xi):=\phi''(\xi).
}
\label{eq:SR_uw_def}
\end{equation}

Then the first relation is simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u''-w=0.
}
\label{eq:SR_eq1}
\end{equation}

Since \(\phi''''=w''\), the second equation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-YC_2\,w''
+
A_2\,w
-
M_2\,u
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u^2 w
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u(u')^2
+
U_3\,u^3
-
\gamma C_6\,u^5
=
0.
}
\label{eq:SR_eq2}
\end{equation}

Therefore the Stage-IA branch equation is exactly equivalent to the coupled two-field second-order system
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u''=w,
}
\label{eq:SR_system1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
w''
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
A_2\,w
-
M_2\,u
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u^2 w
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u(u')^2
+
U_3\,u^3
-
\gamma C_6\,u^5
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:SR_system2}
\end{equation}

This is the first solver-ready BVP form.

\section{2. First-order system form}

For shooting or general ODE integrators, introduce
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
y_1:=u,
\qquad
y_2:=u',
\qquad
y_3:=w,
\qquad
y_4:=w'.
}
\label{eq:SR_ydef}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
y_1'=y_2,
}
\label{eq:SR_y1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
y_2'=y_3,
}
\label{eq:SR_y2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
y_3'=y_4,
}
\label{eq:SR_y3}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
y_4'
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
A_2\,y_3
-
M_2\,y_1
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,y_1^2 y_3
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,y_1 y_2^2
+
U_3\,y_1^3
-
\gamma C_6\,y_1^5
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:SR_y4}
\end{equation}

So the scalar actual branch search is now reduced to a four-dimensional first-order autonomous system.

\section{3. Boundary conditions for the even localized branch}

For the even branch centered at \(\xi=0\), the symmetry conditions are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u'(0)=0,
\qquad
w'(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:SR_centerBC}
\end{equation}

At infinity, a stationary defect branch must approach a constant vacuum:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u(\xi)\to u_\infty,
\qquad
u'(\xi)\to 0,
\qquad
w(\xi)\to 0,
\qquad
w'(\xi)\to 0
\quad
(\xi\to\infty).
}
\label{eq:SR_infBC}
\end{equation}

Thus on a finite computational interval \([0,L_\xi]\), the practical BVP conditions are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u'(0)=0,
\qquad
w'(0)=0,
\qquad
u(L_\xi)=u_\infty,
\qquad
w(L_\xi)=0.
}
\label{eq:SR_finiteBC}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Asymptotic vacuum equation}

The asymptotic constant \(u_\infty\) is not free.
Setting
\[
u'=u''=u'''=u''''=0
\]
in \eqref{eq:SR_compact_ODE} gives the vacuum equation
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-M_2\,u_\infty
+
U_3\,u_\infty^3
-
\gamma C_6\,u_\infty^5
=
0.
}
\label{eq:SR_vacuum_eq}
\end{equation}

Therefore either
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\infty=0,
}
\label{eq:SR_vacuum_zero}
\end{equation}
or, for a nontrivial asymptotic branch, \(s:=u_\infty^2\) must satisfy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\gamma C_6\,s^2-U_3\,s+M_2=0.
}
\label{eq:SR_vacuum_quad}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\infty^2
=
\frac{
U_3\pm\sqrt{U_3^2-4\gamma C_6 M_2}
}{
2\gamma C_6
},
}
\label{eq:SR_vacuum_sol}
\end{equation}
provided the discriminant is nonnegative and the selected root is positive.

\section{5. Residual operator for Newton/collocation}

For a two-field BVP solver, define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_1[u,w]:=u''-w,
}
\label{eq:SR_R1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_2[u,w]
:=
-YC_2\,w''
+
A_2\,w
-
M_2\,u
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u^2 w
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u(u')^2
+
U_3\,u^3
-
\gamma C_6\,u^5.
}
\label{eq:SR_R2}
\end{equation}

Then the Stage-IA BVP is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_1[u,w]=0,
\qquad
R_2[u,w]=0,
}
\label{eq:SR_BVP}
\end{equation}
with boundary data \eqref{eq:SR_finiteBC}.

\section{6. Linearization for Newton--Kantorovich}

Let
\[
u\mapsto u+\delta u,
\qquad
w\mapsto w+\delta w.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta R_1=(\delta u)''-\delta w.
}
\label{eq:SR_dR1}
\end{equation}

For \(R_2\), one gets
\begin{align}
\delta R_2
&=
-YC_2\,(\delta w)''
+
\bigl(A_2+2\chi_{II}C_4\,u^2\bigr)\delta w
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+
\Bigl[
-M_2
+
4\chi_{II}C_4\,u w
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,(u')^2
+
3U_3\,u^2
-
5\gamma C_6\,u^4
\Bigr]\delta u
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+
4\chi_{II}C_4\,u u'(\delta u)'.
\label{eq:SR_dR2}
\end{align}

So the Newton step solves
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta R_1= -R_1,
\qquad
\delta R_2= -R_2
}
\label{eq:SR_Newton}
\end{equation}
with linearized boundary conditions.

\section{7. Relaxation flow form}

If one wants a geometry-preserving residual flow rather than direct Newton, use
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_s u = -R_1[u,w],
\qquad
\partial_s w = -R_2[u,w].
}
\label{eq:SR_relax}
\end{equation}

Explicitly,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_s u = -(u''-w),
}
\label{eq:SR_relax_u}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_s w
=
YC_2\,w''
-
A_2\,w
+
M_2\,u
-
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u^2 w
-
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u(u')^2
-
U_3\,u^3
+
\gamma C_6\,u^5.
}
\label{eq:SR_relax_w}
\end{equation}

A stationary point of this \(s\)-flow is exactly a solution of the Stage-IA branch equation.

\section{8. Acceptance observables at the scalar level}

At Stage IA, before tangent release, the scalar branch is accepted only if

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|R_1\|_{L^2}+\|R_2\|_{L^2}<\varepsilon_{\rm IA},
}
\label{eq:SR_accept1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u(\xi)\ \text{remains in the intended BCC-shell basin through }S_{\rm BCC},
}
\label{eq:SR_accept2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\|R_\perp[\Phi;z_0]\|}{\|\Phi\|}<\varepsilon_\perp.
}
\label{eq:SR_accept3}
\end{equation}

Only then is the result promoted to the Stage-IA actual branch candidate.

\section{9. Immediate next step}

The actual next step is therefore no longer conceptual.
It is exactly:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{solve the BVP }(R_1,R_2)=0\text{ with }\eqref{eq:SR_finiteBC},
\text{ using either } \eqref{eq:SR_Newton}\text{ or }\eqref{eq:SR_relax}.
}
\label{eq:SR_next}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The Stage-IA scalar amplitude equation has now been reduced from one fourth-order ODE to two coupled second-order equations:

\[
u''=w,
\]
\[
w''
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
A_2\,w
-
M_2\,u
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u^2 w
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u(u')^2
+
U_3\,u^3
-
\gamma C_6\,u^5
\Bigr].
\]

Equivalently, in first-order form:
\[
y_1'=y_2,\qquad
y_2'=y_3,\qquad
y_3'=y_4,
\]
\[
y_4'
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
A_2\,y_3
-
M_2\,y_1
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,y_1^2 y_3
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,y_1 y_2^2
+
U_3\,y_1^3
-
\gamma C_6\,y_1^5
\Bigr].
\]

The finite-interval even-branch boundary conditions are:
\[
u'(0)=0,\qquad
w'(0)=0,\qquad
u(L_\xi)=u_\infty,\qquad
w(L_\xi)=0,
\]
where \(u_\infty\) is determined by
\[
-M_2 u_\infty + U_3 u_\infty^3 - \gamma C_6 u_\infty^5=0.
\]

The Newton residual system is
\[
R_1[u,w]=u''-w,
\]
\[
R_2[u,w]
=
-YC_2\,w''
+
A_2\,w
-
M_2\,u
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u^2 w
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u(u')^2
+
U_3\,u^3
-
\gamma C_6\,u^5.
\]

So the project has now advanced from abstract branch construction to a concrete solver-ready Stage-IA BVP.
The next step is simply to solve \((R_1,R_2)=0\) and then test the tangent residual \(R_\perp\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Stage IA Numerical Realization: Tail, Seed, and Chebyshev--Newton Collocation}

\section{Goal}

The Stage-IA scalar branch has already been reduced to the two-field second-order system
\begin{equation}
u''=w,
\label{eq:NR_sys1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
w''
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
A_2\,w
-
M_2\,u
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u^2w
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u(u')^2
+
U_3\,u^3
-
\gamma C_6\,u^5
\Bigr].
\label{eq:NR_sys2}
\end{equation}

We now convert this into a concrete numerical boundary-value problem.

\section{1. Vacuum selection}

The asymptotic vacuum \(u_\infty\) is determined by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-M_2u_\infty+U_3u_\infty^3-\gamma C_6u_\infty^5=0.
}
\label{eq:NR_vacuum}
\end{equation}

Hence either
\[
u_\infty=0,
\]
or \(s=u_\infty^2\) satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\gamma C_6\,s^2-U_3\,s+M_2=0.
}
\label{eq:NR_vacuum_quad}
\end{equation}

For the nontrivial branch we choose the positive root
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\infty^2
=
\frac{U_3+\sqrt{U_3^2-4\gamma C_6M_2}}{2\gamma C_6},
}
\label{eq:NR_uinf}
\end{equation}
provided the discriminant is nonnegative and the result is positive.
If both roots are positive, the larger one is the default first probe for the stable large-amplitude vacuum.

\section{2. Tail linearization and decay scale}

Write
\[
u(\xi)=u_\infty+\delta(\xi),
\qquad
|\delta|\ll 1.
\]
Since \(u'_\infty=w_\infty=0\), linearization of \eqref{eq:NR_sys1}--\eqref{eq:NR_sys2} yields
\begin{equation}
\delta''=\omega,
\label{eq:NR_lin1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
-YC_2\,\omega''
+
\bigl(A_2+2\chi_{II}C_4u_\infty^2\bigr)\omega
+
V_\infty\,\delta
=0,
\label{eq:NR_lin2}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_\infty:=
-M_2+3U_3u_\infty^2-5\gamma C_6u_\infty^4.
}
\label{eq:NR_Vinf}
\end{equation}

Eliminating \(\omega=\delta''\), the tail satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-YC_2\,\delta''''
+
\bigl(A_2+2\chi_{II}C_4u_\infty^2\bigr)\delta''
+
V_\infty\,\delta
=0.
}
\label{eq:NR_tailODE}
\end{equation}

Using \(\delta(\xi)\sim e^{-m\xi}\), we obtain the characteristic equation
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-YC_2\,m^4
+
\bigl(A_2+2\chi_{II}C_4u_\infty^2\bigr)m^2
+
V_\infty
=0.
}
\label{eq:NR_char}
\end{equation}

Setting \(s=m^2\), this is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
YC_2\,s^2
-
\bigl(A_2+2\chi_{II}C_4u_\infty^2\bigr)s
-
V_\infty
=0.
}
\label{eq:NR_char_s}
\end{equation}

The admissible tail branch requires at least one positive root \(s_*>0\), giving decay rate
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_*=\sqrt{s_*}>0.
}
\label{eq:NR_mstar}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Finite-interval truncation}

Choose the computational interval \([0,L_\xi]\) by requiring
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e^{-m_*L_\xi}\le \varepsilon_{\rm tail}.
}
\label{eq:NR_tail_tol}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_\xi\ge \frac{|\log \varepsilon_{\rm tail}|}{m_*}.
}
\label{eq:NR_Lxi}
\end{equation}

For the first run, take
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\rm tail}=10^{-8},
\qquad
L_\xi=\frac{18}{m_*}
}
\label{eq:NR_tail_default}
\end{equation}
as the default practical choice.

\section{4. Even-branch seed profile}

For the even localized branch around \(u_\infty\), use the first seed
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u^{(0)}(\xi)=u_\infty-a_0\,\sech^2\!\left(\frac{\xi}{\ell_0}\right),
}
\label{eq:NR_seed_u}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
w^{(0)}(\xi)=\bigl(u^{(0)}\bigr)''(\xi).
}
\label{eq:NR_seed_w}
\end{equation}

A practical initial amplitude is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0=\frac{u_\infty}{2},
}
\label{eq:NR_a0}
\end{equation}
and the initial width is chosen from the tail rate:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_0=\frac{1}{m_*}.
}
\label{eq:NR_l0}
\end{equation}

This seed matches the correct asymptotic scale and preserves the even symmetry:
\[
u'(0)=0,\qquad w'(0)=0.
\]

\section{5. Chebyshev--Lobatto grid}

Map the finite interval \([0,L_\xi]\) to \(x\in[-1,1]\) by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\xi=\frac{L_\xi}{2}(1+x).
}
\label{eq:NR_map}
\end{equation}

Take the Chebyshev--Lobatto nodes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
x_j=\cos\frac{\pi j}{N},
\qquad
j=0,\dots,N.
}
\label{eq:NR_nodes}
\end{equation}

Let \(D^{(1)}\) and \(D^{(2)}\) be the usual first and second Chebyshev differentiation matrices on \([-1,1]\). Then on \([0,L_\xi]\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_\xi=\frac{2}{L_\xi}D^{(1)},
\qquad
\partial_\xi^2=\frac{4}{L_\xi^2}D^{(2)}.
}
\label{eq:NR_Dmat}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Discrete residual vector}

Let
\[
u_j\approx u(\xi_j),
\qquad
w_j\approx w(\xi_j).
\]
Define the discrete derivative vectors
\[
u_\xi:=\frac{2}{L_\xi}D^{(1)}u,
\qquad
u_{\xi\xi}:=\frac{4}{L_\xi^2}D^{(2)}u,
\qquad
w_{\xi\xi}:=\frac{4}{L_\xi^2}D^{(2)}w.
\]

For the interior nodes \(j=1,\dots,N-1\), define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(R_1)_j=(u_{\xi\xi})_j-w_j,
}
\label{eq:NR_R1disc}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(R_2)_j
=
-YC_2\,(w_{\xi\xi})_j
+
A_2\,w_j
-
M_2\,u_j
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u_j^2w_j
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u_j(u_\xi)_j^2
+
U_3\,u_j^3
-
\gamma C_6\,u_j^5.
}
\label{eq:NR_R2disc}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Boundary residuals}

The even-branch boundary conditions are imposed by replacing four rows of the residual vector with:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_1=(u_\xi)_0,
\qquad
B_2=(w_\xi)_0,
}
\label{eq:NR_Bcenter}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_3=u_N-u_\infty,
\qquad
B_4=w_N.
}
\label{eq:NR_Binf}
\end{equation}

Thus the full discrete nonlinear system is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{\rm disc}(u,w)
=
\bigl(
B_1,\ B_2,\ (R_1)_1,\dots,(R_1)_{N-1},\ (R_2)_1,\dots,(R_2)_{N-1},\ B_3,\ B_4
\bigr)=0.
}
\label{eq:NR_Rdisc}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Newton step}

Let
\[
U:=(u_0,\dots,u_N,w_0,\dots,w_N)^T.
\]
Then the Newton update is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{\rm disc}(U^{(n)})\,\delta U^{(n)}
=
-\mathcal R_{\rm disc}(U^{(n)}),
}
\label{eq:NR_Newtondisc}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U^{(n+1)}=U^{(n)}+\delta U^{(n)}.
}
\label{eq:NR_update}
\end{equation}

Because the continuous Jacobian was already computed,
\begin{align}
\delta R_1&=(\delta u)''-\delta w,
\\
\delta R_2
&=
-YC_2(\delta w)''
+
\bigl(A_2+2\chi_{II}C_4u^2\bigr)\delta w
+
\Bigl[
-M_2+4\chi_{II}C_4uw+2\chi_{II}C_4(u')^2+3U_3u^2-5\gamma C_6u^4
\Bigr]\delta u
+
4\chi_{II}C_4uu'(\delta u)',
\end{align}
the discrete Jacobian is obtained by direct matrix substitution:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\delta u)' \;\mapsto\; \frac{2}{L_\xi}D^{(1)}\delta u,
\qquad
(\delta u)'' \;\mapsto\; \frac{4}{L_\xi^2}D^{(2)}\delta u,
\qquad
(\delta w)'' \;\mapsto\; \frac{4}{L_\xi^2}D^{(2)}\delta w.
}
\label{eq:NR_Jdisc_rule}
\end{equation}

\section{9. Damped Newton and continuation}

Because the branch can be stiff, use a damping parameter \(\eta_n\in(0,1]\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U^{(n+1)}=U^{(n)}+\eta_n\,\delta U^{(n)}.
}
\label{eq:NR_damped}
\end{equation}

Start with \(\eta_n=1\).
If
\[
\|\mathcal R_{\rm disc}(U^{(n+1)})\|>\|\mathcal R_{\rm disc}(U^{(n)})\|,
\]
halve \(\eta_n\) until descent occurs.

The preferred continuation order is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi_{II}=0
\;\to\;
\text{solve the simpler branch}
\;\to\;
\chi_{II}>0
\text{ continuation.}
}
\label{eq:NR_continuation}
\end{equation}

That is the cheapest robust route.

\section{10. Stage IA acceptance test}

The scalar branch is accepted when
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|\mathcal R_{\rm disc}\|_2<\varepsilon_{\rm IA},
}
\label{eq:NR_acc1}
\end{equation}
with default
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\rm IA}=10^{-8},
}
\label{eq:NR_acc_eps}
\end{equation}
and, in addition,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\|R_\perp[\Phi;z_0]\|}{\|\Phi\|}<\varepsilon_\perp,
\qquad
\varepsilon_\perp=10^{-9}.
}
\label{eq:NR_acc2}
\end{equation}

Finally, repeat at
\[
N,\ 2N
\]
and accept only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\|u_{2N}-u_N\|}{\|u_{2N}\|}<10^{-4}.
}
\label{eq:NR_grid}
\end{equation}

\section{11. Immediate next computation}

The next actual computation is therefore fully explicit:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{construct }u_\infty,\ m_*,\ L_\xi,\ u^{(0)},\ w^{(0)},
\text{ assemble }\mathcal R_{\rm disc},
\text{ and run damped Newton with continuation in }\chi_{II}.
}
\label{eq:NR_next}
\end{equation}

Once this converges, Stage IA is done.
Then we test the tangent residual and release \(z(\xi)\) in Stage IB.

\section{Final Summary}

The Stage-IA scalar actual branch is now a fully explicit numerical BVP.

First, choose the asymptotic vacuum \(u_\infty\) from
\[
-M_2u_\infty+U_3u_\infty^3-\gamma C_6u_\infty^5=0.
\]

Next, linearize around \(u_\infty\) and solve the tail characteristic equation
\[
YC_2\,s^2-(A_2+2\chi_{II}C_4u_\infty^2)s-V_\infty=0,
\qquad s=m^2,
\]
to get the decay scale \(m_*\), then choose
\[
L_\xi=\frac{18}{m_*},
\qquad
u^{(0)}(\xi)=u_\infty-\frac{u_\infty}{2}\sech^2(m_*\xi),
\qquad
w^{(0)}=(u^{(0)})''.
\]

Then solve the discrete collocation system
\[
(R_1)_j=(u_{\xi\xi})_j-w_j=0,
\]
\[
(R_2)_j
=
-YC_2(w_{\xi\xi})_j
+
A_2w_j
-
M_2u_j
+
2\chi_{II}C_4u_j^2w_j
+
2\chi_{II}C_4u_j(u_\xi)_j^2
+
U_3u_j^3
-
\gamma C_6u_j^5
=0,
\]
with boundary data
\[
(u_\xi)_0=0,\qquad
(w_\xi)_0=0,\qquad
u_N=u_\infty,\qquad
w_N=0.
\]

Use damped Newton and continuation from \(\chi_{II}=0\) to the desired \(\chi_{II}>0\).

So the project is now beyond structural setup:
the next step is literally to run this Stage-IA collocation/Newton solve.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Stage IA Base Branch at \texorpdfstring{$\chi_{II}=0$}{chiII=0}: Vacuum, Tail, First Integral, and Analytic Seed}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

We now freeze the continuation base point by turning off the Class-II derivative-cubic callback:
\[
\chi_{II}=0.
\]
This does not yet solve the full actual branch problem, but it gives the cleanest base equation for continuation.

At this base level we can do four things exactly:

\begin{enumerate}
\item determine the asymptotic vacuum \(u_\infty\),
\item determine the tail decay rate \(m_*\),
\item derive an exact first integral,
\item construct a closed-form analytic seed family consistent with the vacuum and the tail.
\end{enumerate}

\section{1. Base ODE at \texorpdfstring{$\chi_{II}=0$}{chiII=0}}

The Stage-IA scalar ODE was
\[
-YC_2\,u''''
+
A_2\,u''
-
M_2\,u
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u^2u''
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u(u')^2
+
U_3\,u^3
-
\gamma C_6\,u^5
=
0,
\]
with
\[
A_2=C_2\left(Z+\frac{10}{3}Yq_*^2\right),
\qquad
M_2=C_2\left(\mu^2+Zq_*^2+Yq_*^4\right),
\qquad
U_3=\chi_{II}C_\Delta-\lambda C_4.
\]

At \(\chi_{II}=0\), this reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-YC_2\,u''''
+
A_2\,u''
-
M_2\,u
-
\lambda C_4\,u^3
-
\gamma C_6\,u^5
=
0.
}
\label{eq:baseODE}
\end{equation}

This is the clean continuation base equation.

\section{2. Exact asymptotic vacuum}

A constant vacuum \(u_\infty\) satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-M_2u_\infty-\lambda C_4u_\infty^3-\gamma C_6u_\infty^5=0.
}
\label{eq:vac_eq0}
\end{equation}

Thus either
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\infty=0,
}
\label{eq:vac_zero0}
\end{equation}
or \(s=u_\infty^2\) solves
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\gamma C_6\,s^2+\lambda C_4\,s+M_2=0.
}
\label{eq:vac_quad0}
\end{equation}

Hence the nontrivial vacuum branches are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\infty^2
=
\frac{-\lambda C_4\pm\sqrt{\lambda^2C_4^2-4\gamma C_6M_2}}{2\gamma C_6}.
}
\label{eq:vac_sol0}
\end{equation}

A real nonzero vacuum exists iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda^2C_4^2-4\gamma C_6M_2\ge 0
}
\label{eq:vac_disc0}
\end{equation}
and at least one root in \eqref{eq:vac_sol0} is positive.

\section{3. Tail linearization and exact decay rate}

Linearize around the selected vacuum:
\[
u(\xi)=u_\infty+\delta(\xi),
\qquad
|\delta|\ll 1.
\]
The linearized equation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-YC_2\,\delta''''
+
A_2\,\delta''
+
V_\infty^{(0)}\,\delta
=
0,
}
\label{eq:tail_lin0}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_\infty^{(0)}
=
