-M_2-3\lambda C_4u_\infty^2-5\gamma C_6u_\infty^4.
}
\label{eq:Vinf0}
\end{equation}

Using the vacuum equation \eqref{eq:vac_eq0}, this simplifies to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_\infty^{(0)}
=
-2\lambda C_4u_\infty^2-4\gamma C_6u_\infty^4
=
-2u_\infty^2(\lambda C_4+2\gamma C_6u_\infty^2).
}
\label{eq:Vinf0_simplified}
\end{equation}

With the tail ansatz
\[
\delta(\xi)\sim e^{-m\xi},
\]
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-YC_2\,m^4+A_2\,m^2+V_\infty^{(0)}=0.
}
\label{eq:tail_char0}
\end{equation}

Setting \(s=m^2\), the admissible tail root satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
YC_2\,s^2-A_2\,s-V_\infty^{(0)}=0.
}
\label{eq:tail_quad0}
\end{equation}

Thus the positive decay rate is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_*^2
=
\frac{A_2+\sqrt{A_2^2+4YC_2V_\infty^{(0)}}}{2YC_2},
}
\label{eq:mstar0}
\end{equation}
provided the numerator is positive and the discriminant is nonnegative.

\section{4. Exact first integral}

Multiply \eqref{eq:baseODE} by \(u'\).
Then
\[
-YC_2\,u''''u'
=
\frac{d}{d\xi}
\left(
-YC_2\,u'''u'+\frac{YC_2}{2}(u'')^2
\right),
\]
and
\[
A_2u''u'
=
\frac{d}{d\xi}\left(\frac{A_2}{2}(u')^2\right).
\]
Therefore the ODE has the exact first integral
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-YC_2\,u'''u'
+\frac{YC_2}{2}(u'')^2
+\frac{A_2}{2}(u')^2
-\frac{M_2}{2}u^2
-\frac{\lambda C_4}{4}u^4
-\frac{\gamma C_6}{6}u^6
=
\mathcal C_0.
}
\label{eq:first_integral0}
\end{equation}

For a localized defect branch with
\[
u\to u_\infty,\qquad
u'\to 0,\qquad
u''\to 0,\qquad
u'''\to 0
\quad
(|\xi|\to\infty),
\]
the constant is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_0
=
-\frac{M_2}{2}u_\infty^2
-\frac{\lambda C_4}{4}u_\infty^4
-\frac{\gamma C_6}{6}u_\infty^6.
}
\label{eq:C0}
\end{equation}

This first integral is exact and should be used as a solver diagnostic:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I[u](\xi)
:=
-YC_2\,u'''u'
+\frac{YC_2}{2}(u'')^2
+\frac{A_2}{2}(u')^2
-\frac{M_2}{2}u^2
-\frac{\lambda C_4}{4}u^4
-\frac{\gamma C_6}{6}u^6
-\mathcal C_0
\equiv 0.
}
\label{eq:first_integral_residual}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Closed-form analytic seed family}

A generic exact elementary solution of \eqref{eq:baseODE} is not available for generic parameters.
So the correct base strategy is not an exact closed-form solution, but an exact vacuum/tail matched analytic seed family.

The default even localized dip seed is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u^{(0)}(\xi)
=
u_\infty-a\,\sech^2(b\xi),
}
\label{eq:seed_sech2}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u^{(0)\prime}(0)=0,
\qquad
u^{(0)\prime\prime\prime}(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:seed_even}
\end{equation}

Its derivatives at the center are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u^{(0)}(0)=u_\infty-a,
\qquad
u^{(0)\prime\prime}(0)=2ab^2,
\qquad
u^{(0)\prime\prime\prime\prime}(0)=-16ab^4.
}
\label{eq:seed_center_vals}
\end{equation}

To match the exact tail, choose
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b=m_*.
}
\label{eq:seed_b}
\end{equation}

Then the center-amplitude parameter \(a\) can be fixed by the center equation
\eqref{eq:baseODE} evaluated at \(\xi=0\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
16YC_2\,a m_*^4
+
2A_2\,a m_*^2
-
M_2(u_\infty-a)
-
\lambda C_4(u_\infty-a)^3
-
\gamma C_6(u_\infty-a)^5
=
0.
}
\label{eq:seed_center_eq}
\end{equation}

This is the natural algebraic amplitude-fixing condition for the base seed.

\section{6. Two practical seed choices}

There are two especially useful seed subclasses.

\subsection{Dark-defect seed}

Impose a core dip to zero:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u^{(0)}(0)=0
\iff
a=u_\infty.
}
\label{eq:dark_seed}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u^{(0)}_{\rm dark}(\xi)
=
u_\infty\bigl(1-\sech^2(m_*\xi)\bigr)
=
u_\infty\tanh^2(m_*\xi).
}
\label{eq:dark_seed_profile}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Algebraically matched shallow-dip seed}

Solve \eqref{eq:seed_center_eq} for \(a\) with \(b=m_*\).
This gives the most faithful one-parameter analytic seed near the actual branch.

\section{7. Newton continuation order}

The actual continuation order is now fixed:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi_{II}=0
\text{ base branch}
\;\to\;
\text{solve } \eqref{eq:baseODE}
\;\to\;
\text{obtain }u_0(\xi)
\;\to\;
\chi_{II}>0
\text{ continuation}.
}
\label{eq:cont_order0}
\end{equation}

At the \(\chi_{II}=0\) stage, the solver should monitor simultaneously:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|R_1\|+\|R_2\|,
\qquad
\|\mathcal I[u]\|,
\qquad
\text{grid refinement error}.
}
\label{eq:monitor0}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Honest status}

At \(\chi_{II}=0\), we do \emph{not} have a generic exact closed-form branch.
But we now have:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the exact vacuum equation,
\item the exact tail equation,
\item the exact first integral,
\item and an exact vacuum/tail matched analytic seed family.
\end{enumerate}

That is sufficient to fix a robust Newton/continuation starting point for the actual nonlinear branch search.

\section{Final Summary}

The \(\chi_{II}=0\) Stage-IA base equation is
\[
-YC_2\,u''''
+
A_2\,u''
-
M_2\,u
-
\lambda C_4\,u^3
-
\gamma C_6\,u^5
=
0.
\]

Its nontrivial vacuum is determined exactly by
\[
\gamma C_6\,u_\infty^4+\lambda C_4\,u_\infty^2+M_2=0,
\]
so
\[
u_\infty^2
=
\frac{-\lambda C_4\pm\sqrt{\lambda^2C_4^2-4\gamma C_6M_2}}{2\gamma C_6}.
\]

Its exact tail decay rate is determined by
\[
-YC_2\,m^4+A_2\,m^2+V_\infty^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
V_\infty^{(0)}
=
-2\lambda C_4u_\infty^2-4\gamma C_6u_\infty^4,
\]
so
\[
m_*^2
=
\frac{A_2+\sqrt{A_2^2+4YC_2V_\infty^{(0)}}}{2YC_2}.
\]

The equation also has the exact first integral
\[
-YC_2\,u'''u'
+\frac{YC_2}{2}(u'')^2
+\frac{A_2}{2}(u')^2
-\frac{M_2}{2}u^2
-\frac{\lambda C_4}{4}u^4
-\frac{\gamma C_6}{6}u^6
=
\mathcal C_0.
\]

A robust analytic continuation seed is
\[
u^{(0)}(\xi)=u_\infty-a\,\sech^2(m_*\xi),
\]
with either the dark-defect choice \(a=u_\infty\), or \(a\) fixed by the center equation
\[
16YC_2\,a m_*^4
+
2A_2\,a m_*^2
-
M_2(u_\infty-a)
-
\lambda C_4(u_\infty-a)^3
-
\gamma C_6(u_\infty-a)^5
=
0.
\]

So the \(\chi_{II}=0\) base branch is now fixed strongly enough to serve as the continuation start for the full \(\chi_{II}>0\) actual branch search.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Stage IA Newton Start: Initial Unknown Vector and Block Jacobian}

\section{Goal}

We now freeze the actual Newton input for the Stage-IA scalar branch.
The purpose is to make the \(\chi_{II}=0\) base branch the explicit starting point for continuation to \(\chi_{II}>0\).

\section{1. Base branch equation}

At \(\chi_{II}=0\), the scalar amplitude equation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-YC_2\,u''''
+
A_2\,u''
-
M_2\,u
-
\lambda C_4\,u^3
-
\gamma C_6\,u^5
=
0,
}
\label{eq:NS_baseODE}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_2=C_2\left(Z+\frac{10}{3}Yq_*^2\right),
\qquad
M_2=C_2\left(\mu^2+Zq_*^2+Yq_*^4\right).
}
\label{eq:NS_A2M2}
\end{equation}

Introduce
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u(\xi):=\phi(\xi),
\qquad
w(\xi):=u''(\xi).
}
\label{eq:NS_uw}
\end{equation}
Then the coupled second-order system is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u''-w=0,
}
\label{eq:NS_R1eq}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-YC_2\,w''
+
A_2\,w
-
M_2\,u
-
\lambda C_4\,u^3
-
\gamma C_6\,u^5
=
0.
}
\label{eq:NS_R2eq}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Chebyshev grid and discrete unknown vector}

On \([0,L_\xi]\), map from \(x\in[-1,1]\) by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\xi=\frac{L_\xi}{2}(1+x).
}
\label{eq:NS_map}
\end{equation}

Take the Chebyshev--Lobatto nodes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
x_j=\cos\frac{\pi j}{N},
\qquad
j=0,\dots,N.
}
\label{eq:NS_nodes}
\end{equation}

Let
\[
D^{(1)},\qquad D^{(2)}
\]
be the standard Chebyshev differentiation matrices on \([-1,1]\).
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D_\xi^{(1)}:=\frac{2}{L_\xi}D^{(1)},
\qquad
D_\xi^{(2)}:=\frac{4}{L_\xi^2}D^{(2)}.
}
\label{eq:NS_Dxi}
\end{equation}

The Newton unknown vector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U:=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_0\\
\vdots\\
u_N\\
w_0\\
\vdots\\
w_N
\end{pmatrix}
\in\mathbb R^{2N+2}.
}
\label{eq:NS_U}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Analytic initial seed}

Choose the asymptotic vacuum \(u_\infty\) from
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-M_2u_\infty-\lambda C_4u_\infty^3-\gamma C_6u_\infty^5=0.
}
\label{eq:NS_vacuum}
\end{equation}

Let the admissible tail decay be \(m_*>0\).
Then the default even seed is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u^{(0)}(\xi)=u_\infty-a\,\sech^2(m_*\xi),
}
\label{eq:NS_seedu}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
w^{(0)}(\xi)=u^{(0)\prime\prime}(\xi)
=
2am_*^2\Bigl(3\sech^4(m_*\xi)-2\sech^2(m_*\xi)\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:NS_seedw}
\end{equation}

Hence the initial Newton vector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U^{(0)}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u^{(0)}(\xi_0)\\
\vdots\\
u^{(0)}(\xi_N)\\
w^{(0)}(\xi_0)\\
\vdots\\
w^{(0)}(\xi_N)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:NS_U0}
\end{equation}

For the dark-defect seed one sets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a=u_\infty.
}
\label{eq:NS_dark}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Discrete residual vector}

Define the derivative vectors
\[
u_\xi=D_\xi^{(1)}u,
\qquad
u_{\xi\xi}=D_\xi^{(2)}u,
\qquad
w_\xi=D_\xi^{(1)}w,
\qquad
w_{\xi\xi}=D_\xi^{(2)}w.
\]

For the interior nodes \(j=1,\dots,N-1\), set
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(R_1)_j=(u_{\xi\xi})_j-w_j,
}
\label{eq:NS_R1j}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(R_2)_j
=
-YC_2(w_{\xi\xi})_j
+
A_2w_j
-
M_2u_j
-
\lambda C_4u_j^3
-
\gamma C_6u_j^5.
}
\label{eq:NS_R2j}
\end{equation}

The boundary rows are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_1=(u_\xi)_0,
\qquad
B_2=(w_\xi)_0,
\qquad
B_3=u_N-u_\infty,
\qquad
B_4=w_N.
}
\label{eq:NS_BCs}
\end{equation}

Thus the full discrete nonlinear system is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{\rm disc}(U)
=
\bigl(
B_1,\ B_2,\ (R_1)_1,\dots,(R_1)_{N-1},\ (R_2)_1,\dots,(R_2)_{N-1},\ B_3,\ B_4
\bigr)^T=0.
}
\label{eq:NS_Rdisc}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Block Jacobian structure}

Write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{\rm disc}(U)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
J_{uu} & J_{uw}\\
J_{wu} & J_{ww}
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:NS_Jblock}
\end{equation}
where each block is \((N+1)\times(N+1)\).

For the interior rows corresponding to \(R_1\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{uu}^{(R_1)}=D_\xi^{(2)},
\qquad
J_{uw}^{(R_1)}=-I.
}
\label{eq:NS_JR1}
\end{equation}

For the interior rows corresponding to \(R_2\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{wu}^{(R_2)}
=
\operatorname{diag}\!\Bigl(
-M_2-3\lambda C_4u^2-5\gamma C_6u^4
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:NS_JR2u}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{ww}^{(R_2)}
=
-YC_2\,D_\xi^{(2)}+A_2 I.
}
\label{eq:NS_JR2w}
\end{equation}

So for \(\chi_{II}=0\), the Newton Jacobian is especially simple:
there are no derivative-cubic mixed terms yet.

\section{6. Boundary rows of the Jacobian}

The boundary rows are inserted by replacing the corresponding rows of the block matrix with:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_1=(u_\xi)_0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{row}(B_1)=\bigl((D_\xi^{(1)})_{0,:}\ \big|\ 0\bigr),
}
\label{eq:NS_JB1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_2=(w_\xi)_0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{row}(B_2)=\bigl(0\ \big|\ (D_\xi^{(1)})_{0,:}\bigr),
}
\label{eq:NS_JB2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_3=u_N-u_\infty
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{row}(B_3)=\bigl(e_N^T\ \big|\ 0\bigr),
}
\label{eq:NS_JB3}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_4=w_N
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{row}(B_4)=\bigl(0\ \big|\ e_N^T\bigr),
}
\label{eq:NS_JB4}
\end{equation}
where \(e_N\) is the standard basis vector selecting the last node.

\section{7. Newton step}

The damped Newton step is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{\rm disc}(U^{(n)})\,\delta U^{(n)}
=
-\mathcal R_{\rm disc}(U^{(n)}),
}
\label{eq:NS_Newton}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U^{(n+1)}=U^{(n)}+\eta_n\,\delta U^{(n)},
\qquad
0<\eta_n\le 1.
}
\label{eq:NS_update}
\end{equation}

Use the backtracking rule:
start with \(\eta_n=1\), and halve until
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|\mathcal R_{\rm disc}(U^{(n+1)})\|_2
<
\|\mathcal R_{\rm disc}(U^{(n)})\|_2.
}
\label{eq:NS_backtracking}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Continuation in \texorpdfstring{$\chi_{II}$}{chiII}}

Once the \(\chi_{II}=0\) base branch converges, continue in small increments
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi_{II}^{(k+1)}=\chi_{II}^{(k)}+\Delta\chi,
}
\label{eq:NS_cont}
\end{equation}
using the converged solution at \(\chi_{II}^{(k)}\) as the initial vector for \(\chi_{II}^{(k+1)}\).

At \(\chi_{II}>0\), the second residual becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(R_2)_j
=
-YC_2(w_{\xi\xi})_j
+
A_2w_j
-
M_2u_j
+
2\chi_{II}C_4u_j^2w_j
+
2\chi_{II}C_4u_j(u_\xi)_j^2
+
U_3u_j^3
-
\gamma C_6u_j^5,
}
\label{eq:NS_R2chi}
\end{equation}
and the Jacobian picks up the extra terms
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta J_{wu}
=
\operatorname{diag}\!\Bigl(
4\chi_{II}C_4uw+2\chi_{II}C_4(u_\xi)^2+3\chi_{II}C_\Delta u^2
\Bigr)
+
\operatorname{diag}\!\bigl(4\chi_{II}C_4u\,u_\xi\bigr)D_\xi^{(1)},
}
\label{eq:NS_deltaJ_u}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta J_{ww}
=
\operatorname{diag}\!\bigl(2\chi_{II}C_4u^2\bigr).
}
\label{eq:NS_deltaJ_w}
\end{equation}

Thus the \(\chi_{II}=0\) Jacobian is the clean exact base block, and the full \(\chi_{II}>0\) Jacobian is obtained by explicit low-order corrections.

\section{9. Immediate execution order}

The exact next execution order is now:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(i) build }U^{(0)}\text{ from }\eqref{eq:NS_seedu}\text{--}\eqref{eq:NS_seedw},
}
\label{eq:NS_exec1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(ii) solve }\mathcal R_{\rm disc}(U)=0\text{ at }\chi_{II}=0,
}
\label{eq:NS_exec2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(iii) continue in }\chi_{II}>0,
}
\label{eq:NS_exec3}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(iv) test }R_\perp[\Phi;z_0].
}
\label{eq:NS_exec4}
\end{equation}

At this point the actual nonlinear branch problem is fully solver-ready.

\section{Final Summary}

The Stage-IA \(\chi_{II}=0\) base branch is now in fully explicit Newton form.

The discrete unknown vector is
\[
U=(u_0,\dots,u_N,w_0,\dots,w_N)^T,
\]
with analytic initial seed
\[
u^{(0)}(\xi)=u_\infty-a\,\sech^2(m_*\xi),
\qquad
w^{(0)}(\xi)=2am_*^2\bigl(3\sech^4(m_*\xi)-2\sech^2(m_*\xi)\bigr).
\]

The residual system is
\[
(R_1)_j=(u_{\xi\xi})_j-w_j,
\]
\[
(R_2)_j
=
-YC_2(w_{\xi\xi})_j
+
A_2w_j
-
M_2u_j
-
\lambda C_4u_j^3
-
\gamma C_6u_j^5,
\]
with boundary rows
\[
(u_\xi)_0=0,\qquad
(w_\xi)_0=0,\qquad
u_N=u_\infty,\qquad
w_N=0.
\]

The \(\chi_{II}=0\) Jacobian block structure is
\[
J_{\rm disc}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
D_\xi^{(2)} & -I\\
\operatorname{diag}(-M_2-3\lambda C_4u^2-5\gamma C_6u^4) & -YC_2D_\xi^{(2)}+A_2I
\end{pmatrix},
\]
with the appropriate boundary-row replacements.

Once this base branch converges, continuation to \(\chi_{II}>0\) is performed by reusing the converged solution as the next initial seed and adding the explicit derivative-cubic Jacobian corrections.

So the problem is now fully in executable Newton/continuation form.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Stage IA Tangent Consistency Residual}

\section{Goal}

After solving the scalar frozen-orientation branch
\[
\Psi(x)=\Phi(x)\,z_0,
\qquad
z_0^\dagger z_0=1,
\]
the next nonredundant question is whether this branch is also stationary in the internal tangent directions.

Therefore we must compute the exact tangent residual
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_\perp[\Phi;z_0]
:=
\Pi_{z_0^\perp}\,\mathcal E'[\Phi z_0].
}
\label{eq:TR_goal}
\end{equation}

If \(R_\perp=0\), Stage IA is already an exact actual branch inside the current working microscopic theory.
If \(R_\perp\neq0\), it is only a scalar precursor and we must release the orientation in Stage IB.

\section{1. Frozen-orientation identities}

Recall
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_\varepsilon=\Psi^\dagger\Psi+\varepsilon,
\qquad
m^a=\Psi^\dagger T^a\Psi,
\qquad
n^a=\frac{m^a}{\rho_\varepsilon}.
}
\label{eq:TR_rho}
\end{equation}

For
\[
\Psi=\Phi z_0,
\qquad
n_0^a:=z_0^\dagger T^a z_0,
\]
we have
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m^a=|\Phi|^2 n_0^a,
\qquad
n^a=n_0^a,
\qquad
\rho_\varepsilon=|\Phi|^2+\varepsilon.
}
\label{eq:TR_frozen_id}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_i^a=\partial_i m^a=n_0^a\,\partial_i|\Phi|^2,
\qquad
K_i^a=0,
}
\label{eq:TR_JK}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
F_i^a
=
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)\partial_i m^a-\beta_X n^a\partial_i\rho_\varepsilon
=
\alpha_X n_0^a\,\partial_i|\Phi|^2.
}
\label{eq:TR_F}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact perpendicular projection of \(A^a\) and \(B_i^a\)}

The explicit working callback was
\[
\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi]
=
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\sum_{i,a}
\Bigl[
\partial_i(F_i^aA^a)-F_i^aB_i^a
\Bigr],
\]
with
\begin{equation}
A^a
=
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)T^a\Psi-\beta_X n^a\Psi,
\label{eq:TR_A}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
B_i^a
=
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)T^a(\partial_i\Psi)
-\beta_X n^a(\partial_i\Psi)
-\beta_X\frac{(T^a-n^a\mathbf1)\Psi}{\rho_\varepsilon}\,\partial_i\rho_\varepsilon.
\label{eq:TR_B}
\end{equation}

Define the tangent vectors
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q^a:=\Pi_{z_0^\perp}(T^a z_0).
}
\label{eq:TR_Qa}
\end{equation}

Since
\[
\Pi_{z_0^\perp}(n_0^a z_0)=0,
\qquad
\Psi=\Phi z_0,
\qquad
\partial_i\Psi=(\partial_i\Phi)z_0,
\]
we get
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_{z_0^\perp}A^a
=
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)\Phi\,Q^a,
}
\label{eq:TR_Aperp}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{align}
\Pi_{z_0^\perp}B_i^a
&=
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)(\partial_i\Phi)\,Q^a
-\beta_X\,\frac{\Phi}{|\Phi|^2+\varepsilon}\,\partial_i|\Phi|^2\,Q^a.
\label{eq:TR_Bperp}
\end{align}

\section{3. Exact tangent residual formula}

Projecting the callback orthogonally to \(z_0\), we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_\perp[\Phi;z_0]
=
\Pi_{z_0^\perp}\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Phi z_0]
=
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\sum_{i,a}
\Bigl[
\partial_i\!\bigl(F_i^a\Pi_{z_0^\perp}A^a\bigr)
-
F_i^a\Pi_{z_0^\perp}B_i^a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:TR_Rperp_start}
\end{equation}

Insert \eqref{eq:TR_F}, \eqref{eq:TR_Aperp}, \eqref{eq:TR_Bperp}. Since \(Q^a\) is constant in space,
\begin{align}
\partial_i\!\bigl(F_i^a\Pi_{z_0^\perp}A^a\bigr)
&=
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)\,\partial_i(F_i^a\Phi)\,Q^a,
\\
F_i^a\Pi_{z_0^\perp}B_i^a
&=
F_i^a
\left[
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)(\partial_i\Phi)
-\beta_X\frac{\Phi}{|\Phi|^2+\varepsilon}\partial_i|\Phi|^2
\right]Q^a.
\end{align}

Therefore
\begin{align}
R_\perp[\Phi;z_0]
&=
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\sum_{i,a}
\Bigl[
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)\,\partial_i(F_i^a\Phi)
-
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)F_i^a\partial_i\Phi
+
\beta_XF_i^a\Phi\frac{\partial_i|\Phi|^2}{|\Phi|^2+\varepsilon}
\Bigr]Q^a
\\
&=
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\sum_{i,a}
\Bigl[
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)(\partial_iF_i^a)\Phi
+
\beta_XF_i^a\Phi\frac{\partial_i|\Phi|^2}{|\Phi|^2+\varepsilon}
\Bigr]Q^a.
\end{align}

Now use
\[
F_i^a=\alpha_X n_0^a\partial_i|\Phi|^2,
\qquad
\partial_iF_i^a=\alpha_X n_0^a\nabla^2|\Phi|^2.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_\perp[\Phi;z_0]
=
\frac{\alpha_X}{M_X^2}
\left[
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)\,\Phi\,\nabla^2|\Phi|^2
+
\beta_X\,\Phi\,\frac{|\nabla|\Phi|^2|^2}{|\Phi|^2+\varepsilon}
\right]
\sum_a n_0^a Q^a.
}
\label{eq:TR_Rperp_exact}
\end{equation}

Define the internal tangent mismatch vector
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_0
:=
\sum_a n_0^a Q^a
=
\Pi_{z_0^\perp}\left(\sum_a n_0^aT^a\right)z_0.
}
\label{eq:TR_Xi0}
\end{equation}
Then the tangent residual takes the compact exact form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_\perp[\Phi;z_0]
=
\frac{\alpha_X}{M_X^2}\,
\Xi_0\,
\left[
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)\,\Phi\,\nabla^2|\Phi|^2
+
\beta_X\,\Phi\,\frac{|\nabla|\Phi|^2|^2}{|\Phi|^2+\varepsilon}
\right].
}
\label{eq:TR_Rperp_compact}
\end{equation}

This is the exact Stage-IA tangent consistency residual.

\section{4. Exact vanishing criterion}

From \eqref{eq:TR_Rperp_compact}, the strongest exact sufficient condition for perfect tangent consistency is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_0=0.
}
\label{eq:TR_Xi0_zero}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_{z_0^\perp}\left(\sum_a n_0^aT^a\right)z_0=0.
}
\label{eq:TR_eigen_condition}
\end{equation}

Thus Stage IA is exactly tangent-consistent if \(z_0\) is an eigenvector of the effective internal operator
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_0:=\sum_a n_0^aT^a.
}
\label{eq:TR_H0}
\end{equation}

So the frozen orientation is not arbitrary:
the natural exact Stage-IA orientations are precisely the eigenvectors of \(H_0\).

\section{5. Quantitative tangent-consistency bound}

Even when \(\Xi_0\neq0\), \eqref{eq:TR_Rperp_compact} gives a direct bound.
Using any consistent \(L^2\)-based norm,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\|R_\perp[\Phi;z_0]\|}{\|\Phi\|}
\le
\frac{|\alpha_X|\,\|\Xi_0\|}{M_X^2}
\left[
|\alpha_X+\beta_X|\,\|\nabla^2|\Phi|^2\|_\infty
+
|\beta_X|\left\|\frac{|\nabla|\Phi|^2|^2}{|\Phi|^2+\varepsilon}\right\|_\infty
\right].
}
\label{eq:TR_bound}
\end{equation}

This is the exact diagnostic inequality to decide whether Stage IA is good enough as an actual branch or only as a seed for Stage IB.

\section{6. Simplification on the scalar Stage-IA branch}

For the locked BCC ansatz
\[
\Phi(x)=\phi(\xi)S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x),
\]
the leading scalar branch is already concentrated on one defect coordinate \(\xi\).
At this level,
\[
|\nabla|\Phi|^2|^2
\sim
\bigl((|\phi|^2)' \bigr)^2 \cdot \text{(cell factor)},
\qquad
\nabla^2|\Phi|^2
\sim
(|\phi|^2)''\cdot \text{(cell factor)}.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_\perp[\phi;z_0]
\propto
\Xi_0
\left[
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)\,\phi\,(|\phi|^2)''
+
\beta_X\,\phi\,\frac{((|\phi|^2)')^2}{|\phi|^2+\varepsilon}
\right]
}
\label{eq:TR_scalar_reduction}
\end{equation}
up to frozen BCC cell factors.

So the tangent failure is completely controlled by two things only:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the internal mismatch vector \(\Xi_0\),
\item the scalar branch curvature/gradient profile.
\end{enumerate}

\section{7. Acceptance rule for Stage IA}

The Stage-IA scalar branch is promoted to an actual branch if, in addition to the scalar residual acceptance,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\|R_\perp[\Phi;z_0]\|}{\|\Phi\|}
<
\varepsilon_\perp.
}
\label{eq:TR_accept}
\end{equation}

If \eqref{eq:TR_accept} fails but the scalar branch residual is already small, then the correct next move is not to discard the branch.
Instead, use it as the initial data for Stage IB, where the internal orientation \(z(\xi)\) is released dynamically.

\section{8. Immediate next step}

The actual next step is now completely concrete:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{solve the Stage-IA scalar BVP for }\phi,
\quad
\text{compute }\Xi_0,
\quad
\text{evaluate }R_\perp[\phi;z_0].
}
\label{eq:TR_next}
\end{equation}

If \(\Xi_0=0\), Stage IA is already tangent-consistent.
If not, Stage IA is the exact continuation seed for Stage IB.

\section{Final Summary}

For the frozen-orientation branch
\[
\Psi(x)=\Phi(x)\,z_0,
\]
the Stage-IA tangent consistency residual can be computed exactly.

One has
\[
m^a=|\Phi|^2 n_0^a,
\qquad
n^a=n_0^a,
\qquad
J_i^a=n_0^a\partial_i|\Phi|^2,
\qquad
K_i^a=0,
\]
so
\[
F_i^a=\alpha_X n_0^a\partial_i|\Phi|^2.
\]

Projecting the Class II callback orthogonally to \(z_0\) gives the exact formula
\[
\boxed{
R_\perp[\Phi;z_0]
=
\frac{\alpha_X}{M_X^2}\,
\Xi_0\,
\left[
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)\,\Phi\,\nabla^2|\Phi|^2
+
\beta_X\,\Phi\,\frac{|\nabla|\Phi|^2|^2}{|\Phi|^2+\varepsilon}
\right],
}
\]
where
\[
\boxed{
\Xi_0
=
\Pi_{z_0^\perp}\left(\sum_a n_0^aT^a\right)z_0.
}
\]

Therefore the strongest exact sufficient condition for perfect Stage-IA tangent consistency is
\[
\boxed{
\Xi_0=0.
}
\]

Equivalently, \(z_0\) must be an eigenvector of
\[
H_0=\sum_a n_0^aT^a.
\]

More generally, the tangent residual satisfies the explicit bound
\[
\boxed{
\frac{\|R_\perp[\Phi;z_0]\|}{\|\Phi\|}
\le
\frac{|\alpha_X|\,\|\Xi_0\|}{M_X^2}
\left[
|\alpha_X+\beta_X|\,\|\nabla^2|\Phi|^2\|_\infty
+
|\beta_X|
\left\|
\frac{|\nabla|\Phi|^2|^2}{|\Phi|^2+\varepsilon}
\right\|_\infty
\right].
}
\]

So the Stage-IA branch is now fully split into two exact checks:

\[
\text{scalar BVP }R_\phi[\phi]=0,
\qquad
\text{tangent consistency }R_\perp[\phi;z_0].
\]

If \(R_\perp\) is small enough, Stage IA is already an actual branch.
If not, it becomes the exact initial seed for Stage IB.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Canonical Internal Choice for Exact Stage-IA Tangent Consistency}

\section{Goal}

We now choose the internal locked direction \(z_0\) so that the Stage-IA tangent residual vanishes exactly at the current working Class II level.

The exact condition derived previously was
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_0
:=
\Pi_{z_0^\perp}\left(\sum_a n_0^aT^a\right)z_0
=0,
\qquad
n_0^a:=z_0^\dagger T^a z_0.
}
\label{eq:CI_goal}
\end{equation}

\section{1. Canonical locked basis}

Use the canonical locked basis already fixed in the notes:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_0=e_1=
\begin{pmatrix}
1\\0\\0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
u_1=e_2=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\1\\0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
u_2=e_3=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\0\\1
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:CI_basis}
\end{equation}

The tangent space is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_{z_0}=\operatorname{span}_{\mathbb C}\{u_1,u_2\}.
}
\label{eq:CI_Q}
\end{equation}

Let
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T^a=\frac{\lambda^a}{2}
}
\label{eq:CI_Ta}
\end{equation}
be the standard Hermitian \(SU(3)\) generators.

\section{2. Exact values of \texorpdfstring{$n_0^a$}{n0a}}

Since \(z_0=e_1\),
\[
n_0^a=e_1^\dagger T^a e_1=(T^a)_{11}.
\]
For the standard Gell-Mann basis,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
n_0^3=\frac12,
\qquad
n_0^8=\frac{1}{2\sqrt3},
\qquad
n_0^a=0
\quad
(a\neq 3,8).
}
\label{eq:CI_n0}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exact effective internal operator}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_0:=\sum_a n_0^a T^a.
}
\label{eq:CI_H0}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:CI_n0},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_0
=
\frac12\,T^3+\frac{1}{2\sqrt3}\,T^8.
}
\label{eq:CI_H0_38}
\end{equation}

Now
\[
T^3=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
1&0&0\\
0&-1&0\\
0&0&0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
T^8=\frac{1}{2\sqrt3}
\begin{pmatrix}
1&0&0\\
0&1&0\\
0&0&-2
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_0
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\frac13&0&0\\
0&-\frac16&0\\
0&0&-\frac16
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:CI_H0_diag}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_0 z_0=\frac13 z_0.
}
\label{eq:CI_eigen}
\end{equation}

So \(z_0=e_1\) is an exact eigenvector of \(H_0\).

\section{4. Exact vanishing of the tangent mismatch vector}

By definition,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_0
=
\Pi_{z_0^\perp}H_0 z_0.
}
\label{eq:CI_Xi_def}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:CI_eigen},
\[
H_0 z_0=\frac13 z_0
\]
is purely longitudinal.
Therefore its orthogonal projection to \(Q_{z_0}\) vanishes:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_0=0.
}
\label{eq:CI_Xi_zero}
\end{equation}

This is the exact canonical solution of the Stage-IA tangent-consistency condition.

\section{5. Consequence for the Stage-IA tangent residual}

The exact tangent residual formula derived previously was
\begin{equation}
R_\perp[\Phi;z_0]
=
\frac{\alpha_X}{M_X^2}\,
\Xi_0\,
\left[
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)\,\Phi\,\nabla^2|\Phi|^2
+
\beta_X\,\Phi\,\frac{|\nabla|\Phi|^2|^2}{|\Phi|^2+\varepsilon}
\right].
\label{eq:CI_Rperp_prev}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:CI_Xi_zero} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_\perp[\Phi;z_0]=0
}
\label{eq:CI_Rperp_zero}
\end{equation}
identically, for every scalar Stage-IA profile \(\Phi\), at the current working Class II level.

\section{6. Sharp consequence}

Therefore the canonical internal choice
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_0=e_1
}
\label{eq:CI_z0_final}
\end{equation}
does not merely simplify the scalar branch.
It makes the frozen-orientation Stage-IA branch exactly tangent-consistent inside the current working microscopic model.

Hence the actual nonlinear branch construction is now reduced to:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{solve the Stage-IA scalar BVP only.}
}
\label{eq:CI_reduction}
\end{equation}

There is no Stage-IA obstruction from internal tangent forcing in this canonical choice.

\section{7. Honest status}

This does \emph{not} yet prove full unconditional closure of the complete microscopic TECT action.

But at the current explicit working Class II level, it proves the stronger practical statement:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the canonical frozen-orientation Stage-IA branch is internally self-consistent.}
}
\label{eq:CI_status}
\end{equation}

So Stage IB is no longer required as an immediate next step.
The shortest path is now to solve the scalar Stage-IA BVP and extract the accepted branch.

\section{Final Summary}

Using the canonical locked basis
\[
z_0=e_1,\qquad u_1=e_2,\qquad u_2=e_3,
\]
with standard \(SU(3)\) generators \(T^a=\lambda^a/2\), one gets
\[
n_0^3=\frac12,\qquad
n_0^8=\frac{1}{2\sqrt3},
\qquad
n_0^a=0\ \ (a\neq 3,8).
\]

Therefore
\[
H_0=\sum_a n_0^aT^a=\frac12T^3+\frac{1}{2\sqrt3}T^8
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\frac13&0&0\\
0&-\frac16&0\\
0&0&-\frac16
\end{pmatrix},
\]
so
\[
H_0 z_0=\frac13 z_0.
\]

Hence
\[
\Xi_0=\Pi_{z_0^\perp}H_0 z_0=0.
\]

Since the exact Stage-IA tangent residual is
\[
R_\perp[\Phi;z_0]
=
\frac{\alpha_X}{M_X^2}\,
\Xi_0\,
\left[
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)\,\Phi\,\nabla^2|\Phi|^2
+
\beta_X\,\Phi\,\frac{|\nabla|\Phi|^2|^2}{|\Phi|^2+\varepsilon}
\right],
\]
it follows that
\[
\boxed{
R_\perp[\Phi;z_0]=0
}
\]
identically for the canonical choice \(z_0=e_1\), at the current working Class II level.

So Stage IA is already tangent-consistent.
The immediate next problem is now only:
\[
\boxed{
\text{solve the scalar Stage-IA BVP.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Stage IA Actual Solve Protocol}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

Because the canonical frozen orientation \(z_0=e_1\) makes
\[
R_\perp[\Phi;z_0]=0
\]
at the current working Class II level, the immediate actual branch problem is reduced exactly to the scalar Stage-IA BVP.

So the right next step is no longer structural decomposition.
It is the actual numerical solve of the scalar branch, first at \(\chi_{II}=0\), then by continuation to \(\chi_{II}>0\).

\section{1. Final Stage-IA BVP}

The scalar Stage-IA system is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u''=w,
}
\label{eq:SAP_sys1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-YC_2\,w''
+
A_2\,w
-
M_2\,u
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u^2w
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u(u')^2
+
U_3\,u^3
-
\gamma C_6\,u^5
=
0,
}
\label{eq:SAP_sys2}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_2=C_2\left(Z+\frac{10}{3}Yq_*^2\right),
\qquad
M_2=C_2\left(\mu^2+Zq_*^2+Yq_*^4\right),
\qquad
U_3=\chi_{II}C_\Delta-\lambda C_4.
}
\label{eq:SAP_coeffs}
\end{equation}

The finite-interval even-branch boundary conditions are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u'(0)=0,
\qquad
w'(0)=0,
\qquad
u(L_\xi)=u_\infty,
\qquad
w(L_\xi)=0.
}
\label{eq:SAP_BC}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Execution order}

The exact execution order is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Step A: solve the base branch at }\chi_{II}=0,
}
\label{eq:SAP_stepA}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Step B: continue the converged branch in }\chi_{II}>0,
}
\label{eq:SAP_stepB}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Step C: refine }N\text{ and }L_\xi\text{ until the branch is grid-stable.}
}
\label{eq:SAP_stepC}
\end{equation}

Because \(R_\perp=0\) already holds for the canonical choice, there is no immediate need to release the internal orientation.

\section{3. Base branch at \texorpdfstring{$\chi_{II}=0$}{chiII=0}}

At the base point,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-YC_2\,u''''
+
A_2\,u''
-
M_2\,u
-
\lambda C_4\,u^3
-
\gamma C_6\,u^5
=
0.
}
\label{eq:SAP_baseODE}
\end{equation}

The nontrivial vacuum is determined by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-M_2u_\infty-\lambda C_4u_\infty^3-\gamma C_6u_\infty^5=0,
}
\label{eq:SAP_vac}
\end{equation}
equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\gamma C_6\,u_\infty^4+\lambda C_4\,u_\infty^2+M_2=0.
}
\label{eq:SAP_vac_quad}
\end{equation}

The admissible tail rate \(m_*\) is determined from
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-YC_2\,m^4+A_2m^2+V_\infty^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
V_\infty^{(0)}=-2\lambda C_4u_\infty^2-4\gamma C_6u_\infty^4.
}
\label{eq:SAP_tail}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Practical first seed}

Use the analytic vacuum/tail-matched seed
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u^{(0)}(\xi)=u_\infty-a\,\sech^2(m_*\xi),
}
\label{eq:SAP_seedu}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
w^{(0)}(\xi)=u^{(0)\prime\prime}(\xi).
}
\label{eq:SAP_seedw}
\end{equation}

Default first choice:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a=u_\infty
}
\label{eq:SAP_dark}
\end{equation}
(dark-defect seed), unless the center equation indicates a shallower defect.

\section{5. Domain and collocation defaults}

Choose the computational interval by the tail rule
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_\xi=\frac{18}{m_*}.
}
\label{eq:SAP_L}
\end{equation}

Use the Chebyshev--Lobatto grid
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
x_j=\cos\frac{\pi j}{N},
\qquad
\xi_j=\frac{L_\xi}{2}(1+x_j),
\qquad
j=0,\dots,N.
}
\label{eq:SAP_grid}
\end{equation}

Recommended refinement ladder:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
N\in\{64,\ 96,\ 128\}.
}
\label{eq:SAP_Nladder}
\end{equation}

Start with \(N=64\), converge the branch, then push to \(96\), then \(128\).

\section{6. Discrete residual system}

Let
\[
U=(u_0,\dots,u_N,w_0,\dots,w_N)^T.
\]
Then the interior residuals are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(R_1)_j=(u_{\xi\xi})_j-w_j,
}
\label{eq:SAP_R1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(R_2)_j
=
-YC_2(w_{\xi\xi})_j
+
A_2w_j
-
M_2u_j
+
2\chi_{II}C_4u_j^2w_j
+
2\chi_{II}C_4u_j(u_\xi)_j^2
+
U_3u_j^3
-
\gamma C_6u_j^5.
}
\label{eq:SAP_R2}
\end{equation}

The boundary rows are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(u_\xi)_0=0,
\qquad
(w_\xi)_0=0,
\qquad
u_N-u_\infty=0,
\qquad
w_N=0.
}
\label{eq:SAP_boundary}
\end{equation}

Thus the nonlinear system is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{\rm disc}(U)=0.
}
\label{eq:SAP_disc}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Newton solve and damping}

At fixed \(\chi_{II}\), solve
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{\rm disc}(U^{(n)})\,\delta U^{(n)}
=
-\mathcal R_{\rm disc}(U^{(n)}),
}
\label{eq:SAP_Newton}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U^{(n+1)}=U^{(n)}+\eta_n\,\delta U^{(n)},
\qquad
0<\eta_n\le 1.
}
\label{eq:SAP_damped}
\end{equation}

Use backtracking:
start with \(\eta_n=1\), and halve until
\[
\|\mathcal R_{\rm disc}(U^{(n+1)})\|_2
<
\|\mathcal R_{\rm disc}(U^{(n)})\|_2.
\]

\section{8. Continuation in \texorpdfstring{$\chi_{II}$}{chiII}}

Once the \(\chi_{II}=0\) base branch converges, continue in small increments:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi_{II}^{(k+1)}=\chi_{II}^{(k)}+\Delta\chi.
}
\label{eq:SAP_chicont}
\end{equation}

A safe first ladder is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta\chi
=
0.05\,\chi_{II}^{\rm target},
}
\label{eq:SAP_dchi}
\end{equation}
for \(20\) steps, or smaller if Newton loses monotonicity.

At each continuation step, reuse the previously converged solution as the new initial guess.

\section{9. Stage-IA acceptance criteria}

The Stage-IA scalar branch is accepted if

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|\mathcal R_{\rm disc}\|_2<10^{-8},
}
\label{eq:SAP_acc1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\|u_{2N}-u_N\|_2}{\|u_{2N}\|_2}<10^{-4},
}
\label{eq:SAP_acc2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left\|
-YC_2\,u'''u'
+\frac{YC_2}{2}(u'')^2
+\frac{A_2}{2}(u')^2
-\frac{M_2}{2}u^2
-\frac{\lambda C_4}{4}u^4
-\frac{\gamma C_6}{6}u^6
-\mathcal C_0
\right\|_\infty
<10^{-7},
}
\label{eq:SAP_acc3}
\end{equation}
and, because \(z_0=e_1\) gives \(\Xi_0=0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_\perp[\Phi;z_0]=0
}
\label{eq:SAP_acc4}
\end{equation}
at the current working Class II level.

\section{10. Output of Stage IA}

When the Stage-IA branch is accepted, denote it
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_{\rm IA}(\xi),
\qquad
\Phi_{\rm IA}(x)=u_{\rm IA}(\xi)\,S_{\rm BCC}(x),
\qquad
\Psi_{\rm IA}(x)=\Phi_{\rm IA}(x)\,e_1.
}
\label{eq:SAP_output}
\end{equation}

This is the first actual nonlinear branch candidate.

Only after this is obtained do we proceed to Bloch linearization
\[
L_{\rm Bloch}(k)\to K_i\to P_*K_iP_*
\]
and extract \((\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)\).

\section{11. Immediate next move}

Thus the immediate next move is not another reduction.
It is exactly:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{run the Stage-IA Newton/collocation solve at }\chi_{II}=0,
\text{ then continue to }\chi_{II}>0.
}
\label{eq:SAP_next}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

Because the canonical internal choice \(z_0=e_1\) makes
\[
R_\perp[\Phi;z_0]=0
\]
at the current working Class II level, the actual nonlinear branch problem is immediately reduced to the scalar Stage-IA BVP.

The practical execution protocol is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item solve the \(\chi_{II}=0\) base branch first,
\item use the vacuum/tail-matched seed
\[
u^{(0)}(\xi)=u_\infty-a\,\sech^2(m_*\xi),
\qquad
a=u_\infty,
\]
\item take
\[
L_\xi=\frac{18}{m_*},
\qquad
N=64\to 96\to 128,
\]
\item solve the Chebyshev collocation Newton system
\[
\mathcal R_{\rm disc}(U)=0,
\]
\item continue in small steps from \(\chi_{II}=0\) to \(\chi_{II}>0\),
\item accept only when the residual, grid convergence, and first-integral defect all pass.
\end{enumerate}

At that point the resulting branch
\[
\Psi_{\rm IA}(x)=u_{\rm IA}(\xi)\,S_{\rm BCC}(x)\,e_1
\]
is the first actual nonlinear branch candidate, and the next stage is Bloch linearization and coefficient extraction.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Stage IA as a Two-Parameter Shooting Problem}

\section{Goal}

The Stage-IA scalar branch has already been reduced to the solver-ready system
\begin{equation}
u''=w,
\label{eq:SH_sys1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
w''
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
A_2\,w
-
M_2\,u
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u^2 w
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u(u')^2
+
U_3\,u^3
-
\gamma C_6\,u^5
\Bigr].
\label{eq:SH_sys2}
\end{equation}

We now reduce the even branch to a two-parameter shooting problem.

\section{1. Even-branch center data}

For the even branch centered at \(\xi=0\), the symmetry conditions are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u'(0)=0,
\qquad
w'(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:SH_even}
\end{equation}

Therefore the only free center data are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_c:=u(0),
\qquad
w_c:=w(0).
}
\label{eq:SH_centerdata}
\end{equation}

Since \(w=u''\), this means the entire local branch is determined by
\[
u(0),\quad u''(0),
\]
with odd derivatives fixed to zero by symmetry.

\section{2. Exact center acceleration}

Evaluating \eqref{eq:SH_sys2} at \(\xi=0\), and using \(u'(0)=0\), we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
w''(0)
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
A_2\,w_c
-
M_2\,u_c
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u_c^2 w_c
+
U_3\,u_c^3
-
\gamma C_6\,u_c^5
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:SH_w2c}
\end{equation}

Since \(u''=w\), we also have
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u''(0)=w_c,
\qquad
u''''(0)=w''(0).
}
\label{eq:SH_u4c}
\end{equation}

Thus the full local Taylor data are fixed by \((u_c,w_c)\).

\section{3. Center Taylor expansion}

The even branch therefore has the local expansions
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u(\xi)
=
u_c
+
\frac{w_c}{2}\xi^2
+
\frac{w''(0)}{24}\xi^4
+
O(\xi^6),
}
\label{eq:SH_uTaylor}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
w(\xi)
=
w_c
+
\frac{w''(0)}{2}\xi^2
+
O(\xi^4).
}
\label{eq:SH_wTaylor}
\end{equation}

This is the correct regular seed for outward integration from the center.

\section{4. First-order shooting system}

Introduce
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
y_1:=u,
\qquad
y_2:=u',
\qquad
y_3:=w,
\qquad
y_4:=w'.
}
\label{eq:SH_y}
\end{equation}
Then the autonomous first-order system is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
y_1'=y_2,
\qquad
y_2'=y_3,
\qquad
y_3'=y_4,
}
\label{eq:SH_y123}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
y_4'
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
A_2\,y_3
-
M_2\,y_1
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,y_1^2y_3
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,y_1y_2^2
+
U_3\,y_1^3
-
\gamma C_6\,y_1^5
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:SH_y4}
\end{equation}

The center initial data are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
y_1(0)=u_c,
\qquad
y_2(0)=0,
\qquad
y_3(0)=w_c,
\qquad
y_4(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:SH_init}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Shooting target map}

Fix the finite truncation length \(L_\xi\), determined from the tail scale as before.
The desired asymptotic boundary conditions are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u(L_\xi)=u_\infty,
\qquad
w(L_\xi)=0.
}
\label{eq:SH_targetBC}
\end{equation}

Therefore define the two-component shooting map
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S(u_c,w_c)
:=
\begin{pmatrix}
u(L_\xi;u_c,w_c)-u_\infty\\[1mm]
w(L_\xi;u_c,w_c)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:SH_map}
\end{equation}

The Stage-IA branch problem is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S(u_c,w_c)=0.
}
\label{eq:SH_root}
\end{equation}

Thus the full scalar BVP has now been reduced to a two-dimensional root-finding problem.

\section{6. Variational equations for the shooting Jacobian}

To apply Newton in \((u_c,w_c)\), define the two variational solutions
\[
\delta^{(u)}y:=\frac{\partial y}{\partial u_c},
\qquad
\delta^{(w)}y:=\frac{\partial y}{\partial w_c}.
\]

Linearizing \eqref{eq:SH_y123}--\eqref{eq:SH_y4}, one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta y_1'=\delta y_2,
\qquad
\delta y_2'=\delta y_3,
\qquad
\delta y_3'=\delta y_4,
}
\label{eq:SH_var123}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{align}
\delta y_4'
&=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
\bigl(
-M_2
+
4\chi_{II}C_4y_1y_3
+
2\chi_{II}C_4y_2^2
+
3U_3y_1^2
-
5\gamma C_6y_1^4
\bigr)\delta y_1
\nonumber\\
&\qquad\qquad
+
4\chi_{II}C_4y_1y_2\,\delta y_2
+
\bigl(A_2+2\chi_{II}C_4y_1^2\bigr)\delta y_3
\Bigr].
\label{eq:SH_var4}
\end{align}

For the \(u_c\)-variation, the initial data are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta^{(u)}y(0)=(1,0,0,0)^T.
}
\label{eq:SH_varu_init}
\end{equation}
For the \(w_c\)-variation,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta^{(w)}y(0)=(0,0,1,0)^T.
}
\label{eq:SH_varw_init}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact shooting Jacobian is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D\mathcal S(u_c,w_c)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta^{(u)}y_1(L_\xi) & \delta^{(w)}y_1(L_\xi)\\[1mm]
\delta^{(u)}y_3(L_\xi) & \delta^{(w)}y_3(L_\xi)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:SH_Jac}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Two-dimensional Newton shooting}

The Newton correction for the center data is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D\mathcal S(u_c^{(n)},w_c^{(n)})
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta u_c^{(n)}\\
\delta w_c^{(n)}
\end{pmatrix}
=
-
\mathcal S(u_c^{(n)},w_c^{(n)}).
}
\label{eq:SH_Newton}
\end{equation}

Then update
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_c^{(n+1)}=u_c^{(n)}+\eta_n\,\delta u_c^{(n)},
\qquad
w_c^{(n+1)}=w_c^{(n)}+\eta_n\,\delta w_c^{(n)},
}
\label{eq:SH_update}
\end{equation}
with damping \(0<\eta_n\le 1\) chosen by backtracking.

\section{8. Natural admissible region for the center data}

The even branch must remain in the basin of the chosen vacuum \(u_\infty\).
So the first admissible search window is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
0\le u_c\le u_\infty,
}
\label{eq:SH_ucwindow}
\end{equation}
for the dip branch, and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
w_c\ge 0,
}
\label{eq:SH_wcwindow}
\end{equation}
for a center minimum.

The dark-defect seed corresponds to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_c=0,
\qquad
w_c=2u_\infty m_*^2
}
\label{eq:SH_darkseed}
\end{equation}
at leading seed level.

\section{9. Acceptance at the shooting level}

The Stage-IA branch is accepted if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|\mathcal S(u_c,w_c)\|_2<\varepsilon_{\rm shoot},
}
\label{eq:SH_acc1}
\end{equation}
with a default choice
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\rm shoot}=10^{-10},
}
\label{eq:SH_eps}
\end{equation}
and, in addition, the first-integral defect satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|\mathcal I[u]\|_\infty<10^{-8}.
}
\label{eq:SH_acc2}
\end{equation}

Because the canonical \(z_0=e_1\) choice gives \(R_\perp=0\), these conditions are sufficient for Stage IA acceptance at the current working Class II level.

\section{10. Immediate next move}

The actual next move is now completely explicit:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{choose }(u_c^{(0)},w_c^{(0)})\text{ from the dark seed, integrate outward, construct }\mathcal S,
\text{ and solve }\mathcal S(u_c,w_c)=0
}
\label{eq:SH_next}
\end{equation}
first at \(\chi_{II}=0\), then by continuation to \(\chi_{II}>0\).

\section{Final Summary}

The Stage-IA scalar branch has now been reduced from a fourth-order ODE to a two-parameter shooting problem.

For the even branch, the only free center data are
\[
u_c=u(0),\qquad w_c=u''(0),
\]
since
\[
u'(0)=0,\qquad w'(0)=0
\]
are fixed by symmetry.

The exact shooting target map is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal S(u_c,w_c)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u(L_\xi;u_c,w_c)-u_\infty\\
w(L_\xi;u_c,w_c)
\end{pmatrix},
}
\]
and the branch equation is simply
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal S(u_c,w_c)=0.
}
\]

The Jacobian of this map is obtained from the variational system and is
\[
\boxed{
D\mathcal S(u_c,w_c)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\partial_{u_c}u(L_\xi) & \partial_{w_c}u(L_\xi)\\
\partial_{u_c}w(L_\xi) & \partial_{w_c}w(L_\xi)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\]

So the Stage-IA actual branch solve is now a literal two-dimensional Newton shooting problem:
\[
D\mathcal S
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta u_c\\
\delta w_c
\end{pmatrix}
=
-\mathcal S.
\]

With the canonical choice \(z_0=e_1\), the tangent residual already vanishes, so solving this shooting problem is enough to construct the Stage-IA actual branch at the current working Class II level.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Stage IA Shooting Newton: Dark-Seed Initialization, Local Start, and Continuation}

\section{Goal}

The Stage-IA branch has already been reduced to the two-parameter even shooting problem
\[
\mathcal S(u_c,w_c)=0,
\qquad
u_c:=u(0),
\qquad
w_c:=u''(0).
\]

The next real step is to convert this into a numerically stable integration-and-Newton procedure.

We now fix:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the dark-seed initial center data,
\item the exact local Taylor start away from \(\xi=0\),
\item the actual continuation rule in \(\chi_{II}\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{1. Full Stage-IA center equation}

The Stage-IA scalar system is
\begin{equation}
u''=w,
\label{eq:SN_sys1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
-YC_2\,w''
+
A_2\,w
-
M_2\,u
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u^2w
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u(u')^2
+
U_3\,u^3
-
\gamma C_6\,u^5
=
0.
\label{eq:SN_sys2}
\end{equation}

At the center of the even branch,
\[
u'(0)=0,
\qquad
w'(0)=0.
\]
Therefore the exact center acceleration is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
w''(0)
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
A_2\,w_c
-
M_2\,u_c
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u_c^2w_c
+
U_3\,u_c^3
-
\gamma C_6\,u_c^5
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:SN_w2c}
\end{equation}

This is the key local datum needed for a stable outward integration.

\section{2. Dark-defect center seed}

For the \(\chi_{II}=0\) base branch, the natural analytic seed was
\[
u^{(0)}(\xi)=u_\infty-a\,\sech^2(m_*\xi).
\]
For the dark branch we take
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a=u_\infty,
}
\label{eq:SN_dark_a}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u^{(0)}_{\rm dark}(\xi)=u_\infty\tanh^2(m_*\xi).
}
\label{eq:SN_dark_profile}
\end{equation}

Hence the corresponding center seed values are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_c^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
w_c^{(0)}=u''(0)=2u_\infty m_*^2.
}
\label{eq:SN_dark_center}
\end{equation}

This is the default initial shooting point for the \(\chi_{II}=0\) solve.

\section{3. Exact local Taylor start}

Direct integration from \(\xi=0\) is numerically awkward because of symmetry locking.
So introduce a small positive start radius \(\delta\), and begin integration at \(\xi=\delta\).

For the even branch,
\[
u'(0)=0,\qquad u'''(0)=0,\qquad w'(0)=0.
\]
Using \eqref{eq:SN_w2c}, the local Taylor expansions are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u(\delta)
=
u_c+\frac{w_c}{2}\delta^2+\frac{w''(0)}{24}\delta^4+O(\delta^6),
}
\label{eq:SN_u_delta}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u'(\delta)
=
w_c\,\delta+\frac{w''(0)}{6}\delta^3+O(\delta^5),
}
\label{eq:SN_up_delta}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
w(\delta)
=
w_c+\frac{w''(0)}{2}\delta^2+O(\delta^4),
}
\label{eq:SN_w_delta}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
w'(\delta)
=
w''(0)\,\delta+O(\delta^3).
}
\label{eq:SN_wp_delta}
\end{equation}

Thus the exact local start vector for the first-order system
\[
y_1=u,\quad y_2=u',\quad y_3=w,\quad y_4=w'
\]
is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
y(\delta;u_c,w_c)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_c+\frac{w_c}{2}\delta^2+\frac{w''(0)}{24}\delta^4\\[1mm]
w_c\delta+\frac{w''(0)}{6}\delta^3\\[1mm]
w_c+\frac{w''(0)}{2}\delta^2\\[1mm]
w''(0)\delta
\end{pmatrix}
+O(\delta^5),
}
\label{eq:SN_y_delta}
\end{equation}
with \(w''(0)\) given by \eqref{eq:SN_w2c}.

\section{4. Practical choice of the start radius}

The start radius must be small compared to the tail scale but not so small that roundoff dominates.
The natural choice is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta=\frac{10^{-3}}{m_*}.
}
\label{eq:SN_delta_choice}
\end{equation}

If the Newton map becomes noisy, one may increase to
\[
\delta=\frac{5\times10^{-3}}{m_*},
\]
but never larger than \(10^{-2}/m_*\) in the first pass.

\section{5. Shooting map with local start}

Let \(y(\xi;u_c,w_c,\chi_{II})\) be the unique solution of the Stage-IA first-order system starting from \eqref{eq:SN_y_delta} at \(\xi=\delta\).
Then the shooting map is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S(u_c,w_c;\chi_{II})
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u(L_\xi;u_c,w_c,\chi_{II})-u_\infty(\chi_{II})\\[1mm]
w(L_\xi;u_c,w_c,\chi_{II})
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:SN_map}
\end{equation}

The branch solve is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S(u_c,w_c;\chi_{II})=0.
}
\label{eq:SN_root}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Variational initial data for the shooting Jacobian}

To compute the Jacobian
\[
D_{(u_c,w_c)}\mathcal S,
\]
we integrate the variational system together with the main ODE.

Because the local start data depend on \(u_c,w_c\) through \(w''(0)\), the initial variational vectors are not simply \((1,0,0,0)\) and \((0,0,1,0)\) at \(\xi=\delta\).
They must include the derivatives of \(w''(0)\).

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Omega(u_c,w_c;\chi_{II})
:=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
A_2\,w_c
-
M_2\,u_c
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u_c^2w_c
+
U_3\,u_c^3
-
\gamma C_6\,u_c^5
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:SN_Omega}
\end{equation}
Then
\[
w''(0)=\Omega(u_c,w_c;\chi_{II}).
\]

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\partial \Omega}{\partial u_c}
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
-M_2
+
4\chi_{II}C_4u_cw_c
+
3U_3u_c^2
-
5\gamma C_6u_c^4
\Bigr],
}
\label{eq:SN_Omegau}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\partial \Omega}{\partial w_c}
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
A_2+2\chi_{II}C_4u_c^2
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:SN_Omegaw}
\end{equation}

Therefore the \(u_c\)-variation initial vector at \(\xi=\delta\) is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{u_c}y(\delta)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
1+\frac{1}{24}\Omega_{u_c}\delta^4\\[1mm]
\frac{1}{6}\Omega_{u_c}\delta^3\\[1mm]
\frac{1}{2}\Omega_{u_c}\delta^2\\[1mm]
\Omega_{u_c}\delta
\end{pmatrix}
+O(\delta^5),
}
\label{eq:SN_vu}
\end{equation}
and the \(w_c\)-variation initial vector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{w_c}y(\delta)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\frac{1}{2}\delta^2+\frac{1}{24}\Omega_{w_c}\delta^4\\[1mm]
\delta+\frac{1}{6}\Omega_{w_c}\delta^3\\[1mm]
1+\frac{1}{2}\Omega_{w_c}\delta^2\\[1mm]
\Omega_{w_c}\delta
\end{pmatrix}
+O(\delta^5).
}
\label{eq:SN_vw}
\end{equation}

This is the correct exact local initialization for the shooting Jacobian.

\section{7. Two-dimensional Newton shooting}

At fixed \(\chi_{II}\), solve
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D\mathcal S(u_c^{(n)},w_c^{(n)};\chi_{II})
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta u_c^{(n)}\\
\delta w_c^{(n)}
\end{pmatrix}
=
-
\mathcal S(u_c^{(n)},w_c^{(n)};\chi_{II}).
}
\label{eq:SN_Newton}
\end{equation}

Update by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_c^{(n+1)}=u_c^{(n)}+\eta_n\delta u_c^{(n)},
\qquad
w_c^{(n+1)}=w_c^{(n)}+\eta_n\delta w_c^{(n)},
}
\label{eq:SN_update}
\end{equation}
with backtracking damping \(0<\eta_n\le 1\).

\section{8. Continuation schedule in \texorpdfstring{$\chi_{II}$}{chiII}}

After solving the base branch at \(\chi_{II}=0\), use continuation
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi_{II}^{(k+1)}=\chi_{II}^{(k)}+\Delta\chi.
}
\label{eq:SN_chi}
\end{equation}

The robust first schedule is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta\chi
=
0.02\,\chi_{II}^{\rm target}
}
\label{eq:SN_dchi}
\end{equation}
for the first \(10\) steps, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta\chi
=
0.05\,\chi_{II}^{\rm target}
}
\label{eq:SN_dchi2}
\end{equation}
once Newton converges in \(1\) or \(2\) damped steps.

Use the converged center data \((u_c^{(k)},w_c^{(k)})\) as the predictor for the next step.

\section{9. Acceptance at the shooting level}

At each continuation step, accept the center pair if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|\mathcal S(u_c,w_c;\chi_{II})\|_2<10^{-10},
}
\label{eq:SN_acc1}
\end{equation}
and the first-integral defect satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|\mathcal I[u]\|_\infty<10^{-8}.
}
\label{eq:SN_acc2}
\end{equation}

At the final target \(\chi_{II}\), also require refinement stability:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{|u_c^{(2N)}-u_c^{(N)}|}{|u_c^{(2N)}|}<10^{-4},
\qquad
\frac{|w_c^{(2N)}-w_c^{(N)}|}{|w_c^{(2N)}|}<10^{-4}.
}
\label{eq:SN_acc3}
\end{equation}

\section{10. Immediate executable order}

So the exact immediate executable order is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(i) solve } \mathcal S(u_c,w_c;0)=0
\text{ from the dark seed }(u_c^{(0)},w_c^{(0)})=(0,2u_\infty m_*^2),
}
\label{eq:SN_exec1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(ii) continue the root in }\chi_{II}>0,
}
\label{eq:SN_exec2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(iii) reconstruct }u(\xi)\text{ and hence }\Psi_{\rm IA}(x)=u(\xi)S_{\rm BCC}(x)e_1.
}
\label{eq:SN_exec3}
\end{equation}

At this point Stage IA is fully executable as a two-parameter Newton shooting solve.

\section{Final Summary}

The Stage-IA scalar branch is now a fully explicit two-parameter Newton shooting problem.

The free center data are
\[
u_c=u(0),\qquad w_c=u''(0),
\]
with symmetry fixing
\[
u'(0)=0,\qquad w'(0)=0.
\]

The dark base seed is
\[
u_c^{(0)}=0,\qquad w_c^{(0)}=2u_\infty m_*^2.
\]

To avoid numerical issues at \(\xi=0\), start integration at
\[
\delta=\frac{10^{-3}}{m_*},
\]
using the exact local Taylor start
\[
u(\delta)=u_c+\frac{w_c}{2}\delta^2+\frac{\Omega}{24}\delta^4,\qquad
u'(\delta)=w_c\delta+\frac{\Omega}{6}\delta^3,
\]
\[
w(\delta)=w_c+\frac{\Omega}{2}\delta^2,\qquad
w'(\delta)=\Omega\delta,
\]
where
\[
\Omega=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
A_2w_c-M_2u_c+2\chi_{II}C_4u_c^2w_c+U_3u_c^3-\gamma C_6u_c^5
\Bigr].
\]

The exact shooting map is
\[
\mathcal S(u_c,w_c;\chi_{II})
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u(L_\xi;u_c,w_c,\chi_{II})-u_\infty(\chi_{II})\\
w(L_\xi;u_c,w_c,\chi_{II})
\end{pmatrix},
\]
and the branch is found by solving
\[
\mathcal S(u_c,w_c;\chi_{II})=0
\]
with two-dimensional damped Newton.

After solving at \(\chi_{II}=0\), continue in small \(\chi_{II}\)-steps to the target value.

So Stage IA is now no longer a general BVP description. It is a literal two-variable root-finding problem with an explicit seed, explicit local start, and explicit continuation rule.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Stage IA Continuation Predictor Around \texorpdfstring{$\chi_{II}=0$}{chiII=0}}

\section{Goal}

Assume the base branch \(u_0(\xi)\) at \(\chi_{II}=0\) has already been obtained from
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-YC_2\,u_0''''
+
A_2\,u_0''
-
M_2\,u_0
-
\lambda C_4\,u_0^3
-
\gamma C_6\,u_0^5
=
0.
}
\label{eq:CP_base}
\end{equation}

The next exact step is to derive the first continuation predictor for \(\chi_{II}>0\).

\section{1. Full Stage-IA equation}

The full Stage-IA scalar equation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-YC_2\,u''''
+
A_2\,u''
-
M_2\,u
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u^2u''
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,u(u')^2
+
(\chi_{II}C_\Delta-\lambda C_4)u^3
-
\gamma C_6u^5
=
0.
}
\label{eq:CP_full}
\end{equation}

We expand
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u(\xi;\chi_{II})
=
u_0(\xi)+\chi_{II}u_1(\xi)+O(\chi_{II}^2).
}
\label{eq:CP_expand}
\end{equation}

\section{2. First-order continuation equation}

Substitute \eqref{eq:CP_expand} into \eqref{eq:CP_full} and use \eqref{eq:CP_base}.
At order \(O(\chi_{II})\), one obtains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-YC_2\,u_1''''
+
A_2\,u_1''
+
V_0(\xi)\,u_1
+
S_0(\xi)
=
0,
}
\label{eq:CP_u1eq}
\end{equation}
where the linear potential is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_0(\xi)
=
-M_2
-
3\lambda C_4\,u_0(\xi)^2
-
5\gamma C_6\,u_0(\xi)^4,
}
\label{eq:CP_V0}
\end{equation}
and the explicit source is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_0(\xi)
=
2C_4\,u_0(\xi)^2u_0''(\xi)
+
2C_4\,u_0(\xi)\bigl(u_0'(\xi)\bigr)^2
+
C_\Delta\,u_0(\xi)^3.
}
\label{eq:CP_S0}
\end{equation}

Thus the first continuation predictor is governed by a linear inhomogeneous fourth-order ODE on the known background \(u_0\).

\section{3. Vacuum continuation}

Let
\[
u_\infty(\chi_{II})=u_{\infty,0}+\chi_{II}u_{\infty,1}+O(\chi_{II}^2).
\]
The full vacuum equation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-M_2u_\infty
+
(\chi_{II}C_\Delta-\lambda C_4)u_\infty^3
-
\gamma C_6u_\infty^5
=
0.
}
\label{eq:CP_vac_full}
\end{equation}

Differentiating at \(\chi_{II}=0\) gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{\infty,0}\,u_{\infty,1}
+
C_\Delta\,u_{\infty,0}^3
=
0,
}
\label{eq:CP_uinf1eq}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{\infty,0}
=
-M_2
-
3\lambda C_4u_{\infty,0}^2
-
5\gamma C_6u_{\infty,0}^4.
}
\label{eq:CP_Vinf0}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_{\infty,1}
=
-\frac{C_\Delta\,u_{\infty,0}^3}{V_{\infty,0}}.
}
\label{eq:CP_uinf1}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Boundary conditions for the predictor}

For the even branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_1'(0)=0,
\qquad
u_1'''(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:CP_centerBC}
\end{equation}

At infinity,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_1(\infty)=u_{\infty,1},
\qquad
u_1''(\infty)=0.
}
\label{eq:CP_infBC}
\end{equation}

Thus \(u_1\) is a well-posed linear BVP once \(u_0\) is known.

\section{5. Two-field form for the predictor}

Introduce
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v:=u_1,
\qquad
z:=u_1''.
}
\label{eq:CP_vz}
\end{equation}

Then the continuation predictor system becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v''=z,
}
\label{eq:CP_vsys1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-YC_2\,z''
+
A_2\,z
+
V_0(\xi)\,v
+
S_0(\xi)
=
0.
}
\label{eq:CP_vsys2}
\end{equation}

This is the clean solver form for the first predictor.

\section{6. Predictor for the center data}

Write the shooting data as functions of \(\chi_{II}\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_c(\chi_{II})=u_{c,0}+\chi_{II}\dot u_c+O(\chi_{II}^2),
\qquad
w_c(\chi_{II})=w_{c,0}+\chi_{II}\dot w_c+O(\chi_{II}^2).
}
\label{eq:CP_center_expand}
\end{equation}

The full shooting map is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S(u_c,w_c;\chi_{II})
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u(L_\xi;u_c,w_c,\chi_{II})-u_\infty(\chi_{II})\\
w(L_\xi;u_c,w_c,\chi_{II})
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:CP_shootmap}
\end{equation}

Differentiating the identity
\[
\mathcal S(u_c(\chi_{II}),w_c(\chi_{II});\chi_{II})=0
\]
at \(\chi_{II}=0\), we get the exact predictor equation
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D_{(u_c,w_c)}\mathcal S(u_{c,0},w_{c,0};0)
\begin{pmatrix}
\dot u_c\\
\dot w_c
\end{pmatrix}
+
\partial_{\chi_{II}}\mathcal S(u_{c,0},w_{c,0};0)
=
0.
}
\label{eq:CP_center_predictor}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\begin{pmatrix}
\dot u_c\\
\dot w_c
\end{pmatrix}
=
-
\Bigl[D_{(u_c,w_c)}\mathcal S(u_{c,0},w_{c,0};0)\Bigr]^{-1}
\partial_{\chi_{II}}\mathcal S(u_{c,0},w_{c,0};0).
}
\label{eq:CP_center_predictor_sol}
\end{equation}

This is the exact first-order center-data predictor for continuation.

\section{7. Predictor-corrector step}

Given the converged base solution at \(\chi_{II}=0\), define the first predictor
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_c^{\rm pred}
=
u_{c,0}+\Delta\chi\,\dot u_c,
\qquad
w_c^{\rm pred}
=
w_{c,0}+\Delta\chi\,\dot w_c.
}
\label{eq:CP_pred}
\end{equation}

Then use \((u_c^{\rm pred},w_c^{\rm pred})\) as the initial guess for the full Newton corrector at \(\chi_{II}=\Delta\chi\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S(u_c,w_c;\Delta\chi)=0.
}
\label{eq:CP_corrector}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Honest status}

At this point the Stage-IA route is fully explicit:

\begin{enumerate}
\item solve the base branch \(u_0\) at \(\chi_{II}=0\);
\item solve the linear predictor problem \eqref{eq:CP_u1eq} or equivalently \eqref{eq:CP_vsys1}--\eqref{eq:CP_vsys2};
\item extract \((\dot u_c,\dot w_c)\) from \eqref{eq:CP_center_predictor_sol};
\item run predictor-corrector continuation in \(\chi_{II}\).
\end{enumerate}

Nothing conceptual remains open at the Stage-IA scalar level.

\section{Final Summary}

The first continuation step from \(\chi_{II}=0\) is now fixed exactly.

Expanding
\[
u(\xi;\chi_{II})=u_0(\xi)+\chi_{II}u_1(\xi)+O(\chi_{II}^2),
\]
the first-order response \(u_1\) satisfies the linear inhomogeneous ODE
\[
\boxed{
-YC_2\,u_1''''
+
A_2\,u_1''
+
V_0(\xi)\,u_1
+
S_0(\xi)
=
0,
}
\]
with
\[
V_0(\xi)
=
-M_2-3\lambda C_4u_0(\xi)^2-5\gamma C_6u_0(\xi)^4,
\]
\[
S_0(\xi)
=
2C_4u_0(\xi)^2u_0''(\xi)
+
2C_4u_0(\xi)\bigl(u_0'(\xi)\bigr)^2
+
C_\Delta u_0(\xi)^3.
\]

The vacuum also continues explicitly:
\[
u_\infty(\chi_{II})=u_{\infty,0}+\chi_{II}u_{\infty,1}+O(\chi_{II}^2),
\qquad
u_{\infty,1}
=
-\frac{C_\Delta u_{\infty,0}^3}{V_{\infty,0}}.
\]

At the shooting level, the center data predictor is
\[
\boxed{
\begin{pmatrix}
\dot u_c\\
\dot w_c
\end{pmatrix}
=
-
\Bigl[D_{(u_c,w_c)}\mathcal S(u_{c,0},w_{c,0};0)\Bigr]^{-1}
\partial_{\chi_{II}}\mathcal S(u_{c,0},w_{c,0};0).
}
\]

So the Stage-IA continuation is now a standard predictor-corrector problem:
solve the base branch, solve the linear predictor equation, predict \((u_c,w_c)\), then correct by full Newton at the next \(\chi_{II}\)-value.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Stage IA Augmented Variational Integration for the Continuation Predictor}

\section{Goal}

We now derive the explicit executable formula for
\[
\partial_{\chi_{II}}\mathcal S(u_{c,0},w_{c,0};0),
\]
so that the continuation predictor
\[
\begin{pmatrix}
\dot u_c\\
\dot w_c
\end{pmatrix}
=
-
\Bigl[D_{(u_c,w_c)}\mathcal S(u_{c,0},w_{c,0};0)\Bigr]^{-1}
\partial_{\chi_{II}}\mathcal S(u_{c,0},w_{c,0};0)
\]
can be computed directly by one augmented variational integration.

\section{1. Stage-IA first-order system}

Recall the first-order system
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
y_1'=y_2,
\qquad
y_2'=y_3,
\qquad
y_3'=y_4,
}
\label{eq:AVI_y123}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
y_4'
=
f(y;\chi_{II})
:=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
A_2\,y_3
-
M_2\,y_1
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,y_1^2y_3
+
2\chi_{II}C_4\,y_1y_2^2
+
U_3\,y_1^3
-
\gamma C_6\,y_1^5
\Bigr],
}
\label{eq:AVI_f}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_3=\chi_{II}C_\Delta-\lambda C_4.
}
\label{eq:AVI_U3}
\end{equation}

The shooting map is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S(u_c,w_c;\chi_{II})
=
\begin{pmatrix}
y_1(L_\xi;u_c,w_c,\chi_{II})-u_\infty(\chi_{II})\\[1mm]
y_3(L_\xi;u_c,w_c,\chi_{II})
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:AVI_S}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Base-center initialization at \texorpdfstring{$\xi=\delta$}{xi=delta}}

At \(\xi=\delta\), the local Taylor start is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
y(\delta;u_c,w_c,\chi_{II})
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_c+\frac{w_c}{2}\delta^2+\frac{\Omega}{24}\delta^4\\[1mm]
w_c\delta+\frac{\Omega}{6}\delta^3\\[1mm]
w_c+\frac{\Omega}{2}\delta^2\\[1mm]
\Omega\,\delta
\end{pmatrix}
+O(\delta^5),
}
\label{eq:AVI_ydelta}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Omega(u_c,w_c;\chi_{II})
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
A_2\,w_c
-
M_2\,u_c
+
2\chi_{II}C_4u_c^2w_c
+
U_3u_c^3
-
\gamma C_6u_c^5
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:AVI_Omega}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Two center-data variations}

Define the two variational fields
\[
a(\xi):=\partial_{u_c}y(\xi),
\qquad
b(\xi):=\partial_{w_c}y(\xi).
\]

They satisfy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_1'=a_2,\qquad
a_2'=a_3,\qquad
a_3'=a_4,
}
\label{eq:AVI_a123}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_4'
=
f_{y_1}\,a_1+f_{y_2}\,a_2+f_{y_3}\,a_3,
}
\label{eq:AVI_a4}
\end{equation}
and similarly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_1'=b_2,\qquad
b_2'=b_3,\qquad
b_3'=b_4,
}
\label{eq:AVI_b123}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_4'
=
f_{y_1}\,b_1+f_{y_2}\,b_2+f_{y_3}\,b_3.
}
\label{eq:AVI_b4}
\end{equation}

The coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
f_{y_1}
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
-M_2
+
4\chi_{II}C_4y_1y_3
+
2\chi_{II}C_4y_2^2
+
3U_3y_1^2
-
5\gamma C_6y_1^4
\Bigr],
}
\label{eq:AVI_fy1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
f_{y_2}
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
4\chi_{II}C_4y_1y_2
\Bigr],
}
\label{eq:AVI_fy2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
f_{y_3}
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
A_2+2\chi_{II}C_4y_1^2
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:AVI_fy3}
\end{equation}

At \(\xi=\delta\), the exact local initial data are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a(\delta)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
1+\frac{1}{24}\Omega_{u_c}\delta^4\\[1mm]
\frac{1}{6}\Omega_{u_c}\delta^3\\[1mm]
\frac{1}{2}\Omega_{u_c}\delta^2\\[1mm]
\Omega_{u_c}\delta
\end{pmatrix}
+O(\delta^5),
}
\label{eq:AVI_adelta}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b(\delta)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\frac{1}{2}\delta^2+\frac{1}{24}\Omega_{w_c}\delta^4\\[1mm]
\delta+\frac{1}{6}\Omega_{w_c}\delta^3\\[1mm]
1+\frac{1}{2}\Omega_{w_c}\delta^2\\[1mm]
\Omega_{w_c}\delta
\end{pmatrix}
+O(\delta^5),
}
\label{eq:AVI_bdelta}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Omega_{u_c}
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
-M_2
+
4\chi_{II}C_4u_cw_c
+
3U_3u_c^2
-
5\gamma C_6u_c^4
\Bigr],
}
\label{eq:AVI_Omegau}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Omega_{w_c}
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
A_2+2\chi_{II}C_4u_c^2
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:AVI_Omegaw}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Explicit \texorpdfstring{$\chi_{II}$}{chiII}-sensitivity field}

Now define the genuine continuation-sensitivity field
\[
p(\xi):=\partial_{\chi_{II}}y(\xi).
\]

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
p_1'=p_2,\qquad
p_2'=p_3,\qquad
p_3'=p_4,
}
\label{eq:AVI_p123}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
p_4'
=
f_{y_1}\,p_1+f_{y_2}\,p_2+f_{y_3}\,p_3+f_{\chi},
}
\label{eq:AVI_p4}
\end{equation}
where the explicit forcing is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
f_{\chi}
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
2C_4y_1^2y_3
+
2C_4y_1y_2^2
+
C_\Delta y_1^3
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:AVI_fchi}
\end{equation}

So \(p\) is obtained by integrating one inhomogeneous linear system on top of the base branch \(y\).

\section{5. Initial data for the \texorpdfstring{$\chi_{II}$}{chiII}-sensitivity}

At fixed center data \((u_c,w_c)\), the only \(\chi_{II}\)-dependence of the local start enters through \(\Omega\).
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Omega_{\chi}
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
2C_4u_c^2w_c
+
C_\Delta u_c^3
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:AVI_Omegachi}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact local initial data for \(p\) are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
p(\delta)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\frac{1}{24}\Omega_{\chi}\delta^4\\[1mm]
\frac{1}{6}\Omega_{\chi}\delta^3\\[1mm]
\frac{1}{2}\Omega_{\chi}\delta^2\\[1mm]
\Omega_{\chi}\delta
\end{pmatrix}
+O(\delta^5).
}
\label{eq:AVI_pdelta}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Exact formulas for the shooting Jacobian and \texorpdfstring{$\partial_{\chi_{II}}\mathcal S$}{dchi S}}

Once \(y,a,b,p\) are integrated from \(\xi=\delta\) to \(\xi=L_\xi\), we obtain

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D_{(u_c,w_c)}\mathcal S
=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_1(L_\xi) & b_1(L_\xi)\\[1mm]
a_3(L_\xi) & b_3(L_\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:AVI_Jshoot}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{\chi_{II}}\mathcal S
=
\begin{pmatrix}
p_1(L_\xi)-u_{\infty,1}\\[1mm]
p_3(L_\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:AVI_dchiS}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_{\infty,1}
=
-\frac{C_\Delta u_{\infty,0}^3}{V_{\infty,0}},
\qquad
V_{\infty,0}
=
-M_2-3\lambda C_4u_{\infty,0}^2-5\gamma C_6u_{\infty,0}^4.
}
\label{eq:AVI_uinf1}
\end{equation}

This is the explicit executable formula we needed.

\section{7. Exact center-data predictor}

The continuation predictor is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\begin{pmatrix}
\dot u_c\\
\dot w_c
\end{pmatrix}
=
-
\begin{pmatrix}
a_1(L_\xi) & b_1(L_\xi)\\[1mm]
a_3(L_\xi) & b_3(L_\xi)
\end{pmatrix}^{-1}
\begin{pmatrix}
p_1(L_\xi)-u_{\infty,1}\\[1mm]
p_3(L_\xi)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:AVI_predictor}
\end{equation}

Then for a continuation step \(\Delta\chi\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_c^{\rm pred}=u_{c,0}+\Delta\chi\,\dot u_c,
\qquad
w_c^{\rm pred}=w_{c,0}+\Delta\chi\,\dot w_c.
}
\label{eq:AVI_predstep}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Minimal augmented IVP}

Thus the entire Stage-IA predictor-corrector can be implemented by integrating the following augmented IVP on \([\delta,L_\xi]\):

\[
\boxed{
\underbrace{y}_{4}
\oplus
\underbrace{a}_{4}
\oplus
\underbrace{b}_{4}
\oplus
\underbrace{p}_{4}
}
\]
that is, a \(16\)-dimensional first-order system:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(y,a,b,p)'=
\mathcal F_{\rm aug}(y,a,b,p;\chi_{II}).
}
\label{eq:AVI_aug}
\end{equation}

No further formal reduction is needed.

\section{9. Immediate next move}

The immediate executable order is now exactly:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(i) solve the base branch }y_0,
}
\label{eq:AVI_next1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(ii) integrate }(a,b,p)\text{ on top of }y_0,
}
\label{eq:AVI_next2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(iii) compute }\dot u_c,\dot w_c\text{ from }\eqref{eq:AVI_predictor},
}
\label{eq:AVI_next3}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(iv) use }(u_c^{\rm pred},w_c^{\rm pred})\text{ as the Newton corrector seed at }\chi_{II}=\Delta\chi.
}
\label{eq:AVI_next4}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The missing continuation ingredient is now fully explicit.

Let \(y=(u,u',w,w')\) solve the Stage-IA first-order system. Then the two center-data variations
\[
a=\partial_{u_c}y,
\qquad
b=\partial_{w_c}y
\]
satisfy the homogeneous variational system, while the true continuation sensitivity
\[
p=\partial_{\chi_{II}}y
\]
satisfies the inhomogeneous system
\[
p_1'=p_2,\qquad
p_2'=p_3,\qquad
p_3'=p_4,
\]
\[
p_4'
=
f_{y_1}p_1+f_{y_2}p_2+f_{y_3}p_3+f_\chi,
\]
with
\[
f_\chi
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
2C_4y_1^2y_3
+
2C_4y_1y_2^2
+
C_\Delta y_1^3
\Bigr].
\]

Its local initial data at \(\xi=\delta\) are
\[
p(\delta)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\frac{1}{24}\Omega_{\chi}\delta^4\\
\frac{1}{6}\Omega_{\chi}\delta^3\\
\frac{1}{2}\Omega_{\chi}\delta^2\\
\Omega_{\chi}\delta
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\Omega_{\chi}
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
2C_4u_c^2w_c+C_\Delta u_c^3
\Bigr].
\]

After integrating \(y,a,b,p\) to \(L_\xi\), the exact formulas are
\[
D_{(u_c,w_c)}\mathcal S
=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_1(L_\xi) & b_1(L_\xi)\\
a_3(L_\xi) & b_3(L_\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
\[
\partial_{\chi_{II}}\mathcal S
=
\begin{pmatrix}
p_1(L_\xi)-u_{\infty,1}\\
p_3(L_\xi)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Therefore the exact continuation predictor is
\[
\boxed{
\begin{pmatrix}
\dot u_c\\
\dot w_c
\end{pmatrix}
=
-
\Bigl[D_{(u_c,w_c)}\mathcal S\Bigr]^{-1}
\partial_{\chi_{II}}\mathcal S.
}
\]

So the full Stage-IA predictor-corrector is now reduced to a single augmented \(16\)-dimensional first-order integration plus a \(2\times2\) linear solve.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Stage IA Local Continuation Theorem at \texorpdfstring{$\chi_{II}=0$}{chiII=0}}

\section{Goal}

The Stage-IA branch has already been reduced to the two-parameter shooting equation
\[
\mathcal S(u_c,w_c;\chi_{II})=0.
\]
The remaining nonredundant step is to close the local continuation structure around the base solution at \(\chi_{II}=0\).

We now make the following explicit:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the fully simplified augmented IVP at \(\chi_{II}=0\),
\item the exact \(2\times 2\) invertibility condition for the shooting Jacobian,
\item the resulting local continuation theorem,
\item the special simplification for the dark-core branch.
\end{enumerate}

\section{1. Base first-order system at \texorpdfstring{$\chi_{II}=0$}{chiII=0}}

At \(\chi_{II}=0\), the Stage-IA first-order system is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
y_1'=y_2,\qquad
y_2'=y_3,\qquad
y_3'=y_4,
}
\label{eq:LCT_y123}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
y_4'
=
f_0(y)
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
A_2\,y_3
-
M_2\,y_1
-
\lambda C_4\,y_1^3
-
\gamma C_6\,y_1^5
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:LCT_f0}
\end{equation}

The local Taylor start at \(\xi=\delta\) is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
y(\delta;u_c,w_c)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_c+\frac{w_c}{2}\delta^2+\frac{\Omega_0}{24}\delta^4\\[1mm]
w_c\delta+\frac{\Omega_0}{6}\delta^3\\[1mm]
w_c+\frac{\Omega_0}{2}\delta^2\\[1mm]
\Omega_0\delta
\end{pmatrix}
+O(\delta^5),
}
\label{eq:LCT_ydelta}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Omega_0(u_c,w_c)
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
A_2w_c-M_2u_c-\lambda C_4u_c^3-\gamma C_6u_c^5
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:LCT_Omega0}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Homogeneous variational pair at the base point}

Define the two center-data variations
\[
a(\xi)=\partial_{u_c}y(\xi),
\qquad
b(\xi)=\partial_{w_c}y(\xi).
\]

At \(\chi_{II}=0\), they satisfy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_1'=a_2,\qquad
a_2'=a_3,\qquad
a_3'=a_4,
}
\label{eq:LCT_a123}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_4'
=
V_0(\xi)\,a_1+\frac{A_2}{YC_2}\,a_3,
}
\label{eq:LCT_a4}
\end{equation}
and similarly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_1'=b_2,\qquad
b_2'=b_3,\qquad
b_3'=b_4,
}
\label{eq:LCT_b123}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_4'
=
V_0(\xi)\,b_1+\frac{A_2}{YC_2}\,b_3,
}
\label{eq:LCT_b4}
\end{equation}
where the base linear potential is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_0(\xi)
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
-M_2-3\lambda C_4y_{1,0}(\xi)^2-5\gamma C_6y_{1,0}(\xi)^4
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:LCT_V0}
\end{equation}

Their local starts at \(\xi=\delta\) are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a(\delta)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
1+\frac{1}{24}\Omega_{0,u}\delta^4\\[1mm]
\frac{1}{6}\Omega_{0,u}\delta^3\\[1mm]
\frac{1}{2}\Omega_{0,u}\delta^2\\[1mm]
\Omega_{0,u}\delta
\end{pmatrix}
+O(\delta^5),
}
\label{eq:LCT_adelta}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b(\delta)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\frac{1}{2}\delta^2+\frac{1}{24}\Omega_{0,w}\delta^4\\[1mm]
\delta+\frac{1}{6}\Omega_{0,w}\delta^3\\[1mm]
1+\frac{1}{2}\Omega_{0,w}\delta^2\\[1mm]
\Omega_{0,w}\delta
\end{pmatrix}
+O(\delta^5),
}
\label{eq:LCT_bdelta}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Omega_{0,u}
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
-M_2-3\lambda C_4u_c^2-5\gamma C_6u_c^4
\Bigr],
}
\label{eq:LCT_Omegau0}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Omega_{0,w}
=
\frac{A_2}{YC_2}.
}
\label{eq:LCT_Omegaw0}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Inhomogeneous \texorpdfstring{$\chi_{II}$}{chiII}-sensitivity at the base point}

Define
\[
p(\xi)=\partial_{\chi_{II}}y(\xi)\big|_{\chi_{II}=0}.
\]
Then \(p\) satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
p_1'=p_2,\qquad
p_2'=p_3,\qquad
p_3'=p_4,
}
\label{eq:LCT_p123}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
p_4'
=
V_0(\xi)\,p_1+\frac{A_2}{YC_2}\,p_3+s_0(\xi),
}
\label{eq:LCT_p4}
\end{equation}
with explicit source
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_0(\xi)
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
2C_4\,y_{1,0}(\xi)^2y_{3,0}(\xi)
+
2C_4\,y_{1,0}(\xi)y_{2,0}(\xi)^2
+
C_\Delta\,y_{1,0}(\xi)^3
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:LCT_s0}
\end{equation}

The local initial data are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
p(\delta)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\frac{1}{24}\Omega_{\chi,0}\delta^4\\[1mm]
\frac{1}{6}\Omega_{\chi,0}\delta^3\\[1mm]
\frac{1}{2}\Omega_{\chi,0}\delta^2\\[1mm]
\Omega_{\chi,0}\delta
\end{pmatrix}
+O(\delta^5),
}
\label{eq:LCT_pdelta}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Omega_{\chi,0}
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\Bigl[
2C_4u_c^2w_c+C_\Delta u_c^3
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:LCT_Omegachi0}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Exact shooting Jacobian and parameter sensitivity}

Let \((u_{c,0},w_{c,0})\) be the converged base branch at \(\chi_{II}=0\).
Then the shooting Jacobian is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D\mathcal S_0
=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_1(L_\xi) & b_1(L_\xi)\\[1mm]
a_3(L_\xi) & b_3(L_\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:LCT_DS0}
\end{equation}
and the \(\chi_{II}\)-sensitivity is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{\chi_{II}}\mathcal S_0
=
\begin{pmatrix}
p_1(L_\xi)-u_{\infty,1}\\[1mm]
p_3(L_\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:LCT_dchiS0}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_{\infty,1}
=
-\frac{C_\Delta u_{\infty,0}^3}{V_{\infty,0}},
\qquad
V_{\infty,0}
=
-M_2-3\lambda C_4u_{\infty,0}^2-5\gamma C_6u_{\infty,0}^4.
}
\label{eq:LCT_uinf1}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Invertibility criterion and local continuation}

Define the determinant
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\rm shoot}
:=
\det D\mathcal S_0
=
a_1(L_\xi)b_3(L_\xi)-b_1(L_\xi)a_3(L_\xi).
}
\label{eq:LCT_det}
\end{equation}

If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\rm shoot}\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:LCT_nonzero}
\end{equation}
then by the implicit function theorem there exists a unique local continuation branch
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(u_c(\chi_{II}),w_c(\chi_{II}))
}
\label{eq:LCT_branch}
\end{equation}
in a neighborhood of \(\chi_{II}=0\), satisfying
\[
\mathcal S(u_c(\chi_{II}),w_c(\chi_{II});\chi_{II})=0.
\]

Moreover,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\begin{pmatrix}
\dot u_c\\
\dot w_c
\end{pmatrix}
=
-
(D\mathcal S_0)^{-1}\partial_{\chi_{II}}\mathcal S_0.
}
\label{eq:LCT_predictor}
\end{equation}

This is the exact first predictor.

\section{6. Dark-core simplification}

If the converged base branch is the dark-core branch with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_{c,0}=0,
}
\label{eq:LCT_darkcore}
\end{equation}
then the local \(\chi_{II}\)-start simplifies sharply:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Omega_{\chi,0}=0.
}
\label{eq:LCT_Omegachi_dark}
\end{equation}

So in the dark-core case,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
p(\delta)=0+O(\delta^5),
}
\label{eq:LCT_pdelta_dark}
\end{equation}
and the entire \(\chi_{II}\)-sensitivity is generated by the bulk forcing \(s_0(\xi)\) and the vacuum shift \(u_{\infty,1}\), not by the local center Taylor start.

This is numerically favorable.

\section{7. Predictor-corrector step}

For a small continuation step \(\Delta\chi\), define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_c^{\rm pred}=u_{c,0}+\Delta\chi\,\dot u_c,
\qquad
w_c^{\rm pred}=w_{c,0}+\Delta\chi\,\dot w_c.
}
\label{eq:LCT_pred}
\end{equation}

Then solve the full nonlinear shooting equation at \(\chi_{II}=\Delta\chi\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S(u_c,w_c;\Delta\chi)=0
}
\label{eq:LCT_corr}
\end{equation}
using \((u_c^{\rm pred},w_c^{\rm pred})\) as the initial Newton guess.

\section{8. Sharp status}

The Stage-IA scalar branch is now closed at the local-continuation level.

What remains is no longer formal derivation.
It is the actual numerical integration of:

\[
y_0,\quad a,\quad b,\quad p
\]
on \([\delta,L_\xi]\), the evaluation of \(\Delta_{\rm shoot}\), and the construction of the first predictor step \eqref{eq:LCT_pred}.

\section{Final Summary}

At \(\chi_{II}=0\), the Stage-IA base branch \(y_0\) satisfies the autonomous first-order system
\[
y_1'=y_2,\qquad
y_2'=y_3,\qquad
y_3'=y_4,\qquad
y_4'=\frac{1}{YC_2}(A_2y_3-M_2y_1-\lambda C_4y_1^3-\gamma C_6y_1^5).
\]

On top of this base branch, the two center-data variations \(a,b\) satisfy homogeneous linear systems, while the \(\chi_{II}\)-sensitivity \(p\) satisfies the inhomogeneous linear system
\[
p_1'=p_2,\qquad
p_2'=p_3,\qquad
p_3'=p_4,
\]
\[
p_4'
=
V_0(\xi)p_1+\frac{A_2}{YC_2}p_3+s_0(\xi),
\]
with
\[
V_0(\xi)=\frac{1}{YC_2}\bigl[-M_2-3\lambda C_4y_{1,0}^2-5\gamma C_6y_{1,0}^4\bigr],
\]
\[
s_0(\xi)
=
\frac{1}{YC_2}
\bigl[
2C_4y_{1,0}^2y_{3,0}+2C_4y_{1,0}y_{2,0}^2+C_\Delta y_{1,0}^3
\bigr].
\]

After integrating to \(L_\xi\), one gets
\[
D\mathcal S_0
=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_1(L_\xi) & b_1(L_\xi)\\
a_3(L_\xi) & b_3(L_\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\partial_{\chi_{II}}\mathcal S_0
=
\begin{pmatrix}
p_1(L_\xi)-u_{\infty,1}\\
p_3(L_\xi)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Therefore the exact first continuation predictor is
\[
\boxed{
\begin{pmatrix}
\dot u_c\\
\dot w_c
\end{pmatrix}
=
-
(D\mathcal S_0)^{-1}\partial_{\chi_{II}}\mathcal S_0.
}
\]

If
\[
\det D\mathcal S_0\neq 0,
\]
then a unique local continuation branch \((u_c(\chi_{II}),w_c(\chi_{II}))\) exists near \(\chi_{II}=0\).

So the Stage-IA problem is now reduced to one augmented integration and one \(2\times 2\) inversion.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{From the Accepted Stage-IA Branch to the Common Bloch Extractor}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The goal is not to keep refining a working PDE forever.
The goal is to obtain one accepted actual branch and read all physical quantities from that same branch.

At the current working Class II level, the canonical Stage-IA branch is already tangent-consistent.
Therefore, once the scalar Stage-IA branch is numerically accepted, the next immediate step is not another branch split.
It is the common Bloch extractor.

\section{1. Accepted Stage-IA branch}

Assume the scalar Stage-IA solve has converged and produced
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_{\rm IA}(\xi).
}
\end{equation}

Then the corresponding actual branch candidate is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi_{\rm IA}(x)
=
u_{\rm IA}(\xi)\,S_{\rm BCC}(x)\,e_1.
}
\label{eq:EX_PsiIA}
\end{equation}

At the current working Class II level with the canonical internal choice \(z_0=e_1\), this branch is already tangent-consistent, so it is the first legitimate input to the common extractor.

\section{2. Bloch linearization around the accepted branch}

Linearize the full microscopic stationary PDE around \(\Psi_{\rm IA}\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi(x,t)
=
\Psi_{\rm IA}(x)+\eta(x,t).
}
\end{equation}

The exact linearized Bloch operator is then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\rm Bloch}(k)
=
\mathcal H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\rm lin}[\Psi_{\rm IA};k],
}
\label{eq:EX_LBloch}
\end{equation}
where \(k\) is the Bloch momentum around the chosen Bragg point.

Choose the physical expansion point
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
k_*= \frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
k=k_*+p,
\qquad
|p|\ll |G_*|.
}
\label{eq:EX_kstar}
\end{equation}

\section{3. First-derivative transport operators}
