Define the exact Bloch-derivative operators
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i
:=
\partial_{k_i}L_{\rm Bloch}(k)\Big|_{k=k_*}.
}
\label{eq:EX_Ki}
\end{equation}

These are the actual branch-dependent transport operators.

Next choose the isolated low carrier projector
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_*
}
\label{eq:EX_Pstar}
\end{equation}
onto the accepted doubled low block.

Then the effective first-order symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\sum_i p_i\,P_*K_iP_*.
}
\label{eq:EX_A1}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Canonical transverse decomposition}

Introduce the longitudinal and rotated transverse coordinates
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
p_\parallel,
\qquad
q_1:=\frac{p_1-p_2}{\sqrt2},
\qquad
q_2:=\frac{p_1+p_2}{\sqrt2}.
}
\label{eq:EX_qcoords}
\end{equation}

The effective Dirac-type decomposition is then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_*K_\parallel P_*
=
\lambda_c\,\sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:EX_long_extract}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_*K_{q_1}P_*
=
\Lambda_E\,\sigma_1+\Lambda_O\,\sigma_2,
}
\label{eq:EX_q1_extract}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_*K_{q_2}P_*
=
-\Lambda_O\,\sigma_1+\Lambda_E\,\sigma_2.
}
\label{eq:EX_q2_extract}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the scalar extractor formulas are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c
=
\frac12\,\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_3\,P_*K_\parallel P_*\bigr),
}
\label{eq:EX_lambdac}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\frac12\,\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_1\,P_*K_{q_1}P_*\bigr)
=
\frac12\,\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_2\,P_*K_{q_2}P_*\bigr),
}
\label{eq:EX_LambdaE}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_O
=
\frac12\,\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_2\,P_*K_{q_1}P_*\bigr)
=
-\frac12\,\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_1\,P_*K_{q_2}P_*\bigr).
}
\label{eq:EX_LambdaO}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Reduced coefficient dictionary}

Once \((\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\) are extracted from the accepted branch, the reduced carrier coefficients are given by the exact overlap dictionary
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:EX_dict}
\end{equation}

Using the explicit defect overlaps,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}=-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:EX_overlaps}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:EX_long_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:EX_trans_final}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Actual microscopic carrier PDE on the accepted branch}

Therefore the actual reduced carrier PDE extracted from the accepted Stage-IA branch is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
\alpha\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_{q_1})+\sigma_2(-i\partial_{q_2})\bigr)
-
\beta\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_{q_2})+\sigma_2(-i\partial_{q_1})\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:EX_final_PDE}
\end{equation}

This is no longer a symbolic target.
It is the actual branch-level PDE obtained from the accepted branch through the common extractor.

\section{7. Connection to the full project goal}

Once the accepted branch \(\Psi_{\rm IA}\) is frozen, the same common extractor pipeline feeds:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
}
\label{eq:EX_out1}
\end{equation}
for the carrier PDE,

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\rm bench,\rho}^{\rm fin},\ \eta_{R,\rho},\ \Delta_{00},\ L_*,\ (c_E,c_O),\ (C_E,C_O)
}
\label{eq:EX_out2}
\end{equation}
for the carrier gates,

and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_2,\ m_*,\ g_{\rm eff},\ Z_{\rm cub}
}
\label{eq:EX_out3}
\end{equation}
for the anisotropy/hierarchy side.

So the project goal is still exactly the same:
\[
\boxed{
\text{one accepted actual branch } \to \text{ one common extractor } \to \text{ full certificate.}
}
\]

\section{8. Honest status}

At the current point, the path is correct and aligned with the final goal.

What is not yet done is the actual numerical acceptance of the Stage-IA branch and the subsequent Bloch extraction.
But the route is no longer drifting:

\[
\boxed{
\text{solve Stage IA} \to \text{freeze } \Psi_{\rm IA} \to \text{compute } L_{\rm Bloch}(k),K_i,P_*K_iP_*.
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

Yes: the goal is still to obtain an accepted actual branch and extract the actual microscopic carrier PDE from it.

The exact route is
\[
\boxed{
\Psi_{\rm actual}(x)
\to
L_{\rm Bloch}(k)
\to
K_i=\partial_{k_i}L_{\rm Bloch}|_{k_*}
\to
P_*K_iP_*
\to
(\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)
\to
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\]

For the accepted Stage-IA branch
\[
\Psi_{\rm IA}(x)=u_{\rm IA}(\xi)\,S_{\rm BCC}(x)\,e_1,
\]
the extractor is
\[
\lambda_c
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3P_*K_\parallel P_*),
\]
\[
\Lambda_E
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_1P_*K_{q_1}P*)
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_2P_*K_{q_2}P*),
\]
\[
\Lambda_O
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_2P_*K_{q_1}P*)
=
-\frac12\Tr(\sigma_1P_*K_{q_2}P*).
\]

Then
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_O.
\]

So we are going toward the correct goal.
The remaining immediate task is not another conceptual rewrite, but the accepted numerical solve of Stage IA and the common Bloch extractor built on top of it.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Bloch Common Extractor on the Accepted Stage-IA Branch}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The accepted Stage-IA branch is no longer just a nonlinear solve target.
It is now the common microscopic background from which the carrier PDE coefficients must be extracted.

So the next legitimate step is not another branch split.
It is the explicit Bloch-fiber construction and the projected derivative audit on that same accepted branch.

\section{1. Accepted background and fluctuation space}

Assume the Stage-IA solve has converged and produced the accepted branch
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)
=
u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)\,S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x)\,e_1.
}
\label{eq:BCE_PsiIA}
\end{equation}

We linearize the working refined-locked \(+\) Class II microscopic branch
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{work}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\Psi]
}
\label{eq:BCE_Lwork}
\end{equation}
around \(\Psi_{\mathrm{IA}}\), using the fluctuation pair
\[
(\delta\Psi,\delta X).
\]

\section{2. Bloch fiber Hessian}

On the accepted periodic background, the Bloch fiber quadratic operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k) & H_{\Psi X}(k)\\
H_{X\Psi}(k) & H_{XX}(k)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:BCE_HBloch}
\end{equation}

At the current working Class II level, the heavy block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{XX}(k)=M_X^2\,\mathbf 1_X
}
\label{eq:BCE_HXX}
\end{equation}
up to subleading background-induced algebraic corrections, and the mixed block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\Psi X}(k)
=
\alpha_X\,\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\,\mathcal K(k),
}
\label{eq:BCE_HPsiX}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal J(k)\) and \(\mathcal K(k)\) are the Bloch-space linearized current vertices on the accepted branch. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2} :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\section{3. Exact effective Bloch operator}

Eliminating the heavy mediator gives the exact quadratic effective Bloch operator
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
H_{\Psi X}(k)\,H_{XX}(k)^{-1}\,H_{X\Psi}(k).
}
\label{eq:BCE_Heff}
\end{equation}

At the strict working level \(H_{XX}(k)=M_X^2\mathbf 1_X\), this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\bigl(\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)\bigr)
\bigl(\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)\bigr)^\dagger.
}
\label{eq:BCE_Heff_working}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Folded Bragg convention and shell projection}

We work in the folded Bragg convention
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
k_*= \frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
k=k_*+p,
\qquad
|p|\ll |G_*|.
}
\label{eq:BCE_folded}
\end{equation}

Let \(\Pi_{S_*}\) be the projector onto the near-resonant shell pair \(S_*\).
Then the shell operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
\Pi_{S_*}\,H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*+p)\,\Pi_{S_*}.
}
\label{eq:BCE_Hshell}
\end{equation}

Let \(\Gamma\) be a contour around only the isolated low valley doublet of \(H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0)\).
Then the exact valley projector is the Riesz projector
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_*
=
\frac{1}{2\pi i}\oint_\Gamma (z-H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0))^{-1}\,dz.
}
\label{eq:BCE_Pstar}
\end{equation}

This is the correct basis-independent definition of the local doubled carrier block. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\section{5. First derivative operators and their exact split}

Define the Bloch derivatives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i
:=
\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\Big|_{k=k_*}.
}
\label{eq:BCE_Ki}
\end{equation}

At the exact operator level, the derivative splits as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i
=
K_i^{(\mathrm{bare})}
+
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
+
K_i^{(\mathrm{spec})},
}
\label{eq:BCE_Ksplit}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{bare})}
=
\partial_{k_i}H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)\Big|_{k_*},
}
\label{eq:BCE_Kbare}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
=
-
\Bigl[
(\partial_{k_i}H_{\Psi X})H_{XX}^{-1}H_{X\Psi}
+
H_{\Psi X}H_{XX}^{-1}(\partial_{k_i}H_{X\Psi})
\Bigr]_{k_*},
}
\label{eq:BCE_KII}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{spec})}
=
\Bigl[
H_{\Psi X}H_{XX}^{-1}(\partial_{k_i}H_{XX})H_{XX}^{-1}H_{X\Psi}
\Bigr]_{k_*}.
}
\label{eq:BCE_Kspec}
\end{equation}

At the strict working level \(H_{XX}=M_X^2\mathbf 1_X\), one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{spec})}=0,
}
\label{eq:BCE_Kspec_zero}
\end{equation}
so the load-bearing terms are reduced to
\[
K_i=K_i^{(\mathrm{bare})}+K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}.
\]
This is exactly the current honest decomposition of the full-PDE transport source. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5} :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\section{6. Shell-adapted projected matrices}

Choose the shell-adapted orthonormal frame
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\}.
}
\label{eq:BCE_frame}
\end{equation}

Define the projected derivative matrices
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_i:=P_*K_iP_*,
\qquad
M_\parallel:=\hat n_iM_i,
\qquad
M_1:=e_{1i}M_i,
\qquad
M_2:=e_{2i}M_i.
}
\label{eq:BCE_Mi}
\end{equation}

Then the first-order projected symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)=p_iM_i+O(|p|^2).
}
\label{eq:BCE_A1}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Pauli extraction of the microscopic coefficients}

On \(\operatorname{Ran}(P_*)\cong\mathbb C^2\), choose the Pauli basis \(\sigma_1,\sigma_2,\sigma_3\).
Then the microscopic Bloch-extracted coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c
=
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_3M_\parallel\bigr),
}
\label{eq:BCE_lambdac}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_1M_1\bigr)
=
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_2M_2\bigr),
}
\label{eq:BCE_LambdaE}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_O
=
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_2M_1\bigr)
=
-\frac12\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_1M_2\bigr).
}
\label{eq:BCE_LambdaO}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the reduced first-order symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_c\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
\Lambda_E\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\Lambda_O\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:BCE_symbol}
\end{equation}
This is the finite shell-projected coefficient-matching stage in explicit form. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7} :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

\section{8. Reduced carrier PDE coefficients}

After the Bloch extraction, the reduced carrier coefficients are obtained by the already-fixed overlap dictionary
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:BCE_dict}
\end{equation}
Using the explicit overlaps,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}=-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:BCE_overlaps}
\end{equation}
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:BCE_long}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:BCE_trans}
\end{equation}
So the actual reduced microscopic carrier PDE is fixed once \((\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\) are read from the accepted branch. :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9}

\section{9. Exact immediate computational targets}

Therefore the next explicit computational targets on the accepted Stage-IA branch are the four shell quantities
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^1(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^2(G_*),\qquad
v_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:BCE_four}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, one computes the branch-specific reciprocal-harmonic matrix elements of
\[
\mathcal J(k),\qquad
\mathcal K(k),\qquad
H_{\mathrm{rem,rem}}(k)
\]
at the intervalley harmonic \(Q=G_*\), and then assembles \(K_i\), \(M_i\), and finally \((\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\). :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10}

\section{10. Honest status}

At this point the Bloch/operator pipeline is not conceptually open.

What remains is not another theorem, but the actual branch-specific derivative-and-projection computation:
\[
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k),\quad
H_{\Psi X}(k),\quad
H_{XX}(k)
\;\to\;
K_i
\;\to\;
P_*K_iP_*
\;\to\;
(\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O).
\]

So the path is correct, and the immediate next move is concrete:
freeze the accepted Stage-IA branch and compute the Bloch derivative matrices on that branch.

\section{Final Summary}

Once the accepted Stage-IA branch
\[
\Psi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)=u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)\,S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x)\,e_1
\]
is available, the correct next step is the common Bloch extractor.

The exact effective Bloch operator is
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
H_{\Psi X}(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k),
\]
with
\[
H_{\Psi X}(k)=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k),
\qquad
H_{XX}(k)\approx M_X^2\mathbf 1_X.
\]

Its derivative at the folded Bragg point \(k_*=G_*/2\) is
\[
K_i=\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\big|_{k=k_*}
=
K_i^{(\mathrm{bare})}+K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}+K_i^{(\mathrm{spec})},
\]
and at the strict working level \(K_i^{(\mathrm{spec})}=0\).

Projecting to the isolated valley block,
\[
M_i=P_*K_iP_*,
\]
the microscopic coefficients are
\[
\lambda_c=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel),
\qquad
\Lambda_E=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_1M_1)=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_2M_2),
\qquad
\Lambda_O=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_2M_1)=-\frac12\Tr(\sigma_1M_2).
\]

Then the reduced carrier coefficients are
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_O.
\]

So the immediate forward problem is now completely concrete:
\[
\boxed{
\Psi_{\rm IA}
\to
H_{\rm eff}(k)
\to
K_i
\to
P_*K_iP_*
\to
(\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O).
}
\]

\section{Explicit Bloch-Harmonic Matrix Elements of \texorpdfstring{$H_{\Psi X}(k)$}{HPsiX(k)} on the Accepted Stage-IA Branch}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The accepted Stage-IA branch is
\[
\Psi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)=\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)e_1,
\qquad
\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)=u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)\,S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x).
\]

The next real microscopic step is to build the mixed Bloch block
\[
H_{\Psi X}(k)=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)
\]
on this branch.

At the canonical internal choice \(z_0=e_1\), the \(J\)-vertex is explicit in both the longitudinal and tangent sectors, while the \(K\)-vertex vanishes on the pure longitudinal scalar channel and survives only in the tangent channel through the profile-gradient term.

\section{1. Accepted background and internal frame}

Fix the accepted Stage-IA branch
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)=\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)e_1,
\qquad
\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)=u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)\,S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x).
}
\label{eq:HBM_bg}
\end{equation}

Use the canonical internal frame
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_1,\qquad e_2,\qquad e_3,
}
\label{eq:HBM_basis}
\end{equation}
and define the tangent basis
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_1:=e_2,
\qquad
u_2:=e_3.
}
\label{eq:HBM_tangent}
\end{equation}

Let
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T^a=\frac{\lambda^a}{2}
}
\label{eq:HBM_Ta}
\end{equation}
be the Hermitian \(SU(3)\) generators, and recall
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
n_0^a=e_1^\dagger T^a e_1.
}
\label{eq:HBM_n0}
\end{equation}

Define also the tangent couplings
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_\mu^a:=u_\mu^\dagger T^a e_1,
\qquad
\mu=1,2.
}
\label{eq:HBM_Qmu}
\end{equation}

For the canonical choice \(e_1\), one has
\[
n_0^3=\frac12,\qquad
n_0^8=\frac{1}{2\sqrt3},
\qquad
n_0^a=0\ (a\neq 3,8),
\]
while \(Q_\mu^a\) is nonzero only for the off-diagonal generators that connect \(e_1\) to \(e_2,e_3\).

\section{2. Bloch harmonic conventions}

Write the fluctuation in Bloch form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta\Psi(x)=e^{ik\cdot x}\sum_Q \psi_Q\,e^{iQ\cdot x},
\qquad
\delta X_i^a(x)=e^{ik\cdot x}\sum_Q x_{i,Q}^a\,e^{iQ\cdot x}.
}
\label{eq:HBM_Bloch}
\end{equation}

For any background field \(F(x)\), define the reciprocal-harmonic coefficient
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat F(G):=
\frac{1}{|\Omega|}
\int_\Omega e^{-iG\cdot x}F(x)\,d^3x.
}
\label{eq:HBM_hatF}
\end{equation}

Then multiplication by \(F(x)\) in real space becomes convolution in shell/Bloch space:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\langle Q|F|Q'\rangle=\widehat F(Q-Q').
}
\label{eq:HBM_conv}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Mixed block from the \(J\)-vertex}

At the working Class II level, the mixed interaction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{int}}^{(J)}
=
\alpha_X X_i^a\,J_i^a[\Psi],
\qquad
J_i^a=\partial_i(\Psi^\dagger T^a\Psi).
}
\label{eq:HBM_Jint}
\end{equation}

Linearizing around \(\Psi_{\mathrm{IA}}=\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}e_1\), the variation of \(J_i^a\) with respect to \(\delta\Psi\) gives the mixed block.

\subsection{3A. Longitudinal scalar channel}

Restrict first to the longitudinal fluctuation
\[
\delta\Psi_\parallel=\varphi\,e_1.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta J_i^a\big|_{\parallel}
=
n_0^a\,\partial_i\bigl(\overline{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}\,\varphi+\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}\overline{\varphi}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:HBM_dJpar}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the block from \(\delta X\) to the longitudinal \(\Psi\)-sector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(H_{\Psi X}^{(J,\parallel)}(k)\,x)_Q
=
-\alpha_X
\sum_{Q',i,a}
i(k_i+Q_i')\,n_0^a\,\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(Q-Q')\,x_{i,Q'}^a.
}
\label{eq:HBM_HJpar}
\end{equation}

Thus the explicit Bloch-harmonic matrix element is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\langle Q,e_1|H_{\Psi X}^{(J)}(k)|Q',i,a\rangle
=
-i\alpha_X\,(k_i+Q_i')\,n_0^a\,\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(Q-Q').
}
\label{eq:HBM_Jpar_matrix}
\end{equation}

This is the exact longitudinal mixed matrix element on the accepted Stage-IA branch.

\subsection{3B. Tangent channel}

Now take the tangent fluctuation
\[
\delta\Psi_\perp=\sum_{\mu=1}^2 \eta_\mu u_\mu.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta J_i^a\big|_{\perp}
=
\partial_i\Bigl(
\overline{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}\,\eta_\mu\,Q_\mu^a
+
\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}\,\overline{\eta_\mu}\,\overline{Q_\mu^a}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:HBM_dJperp}
\end{equation}

Hence the tangent mixed matrix elements are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\langle Q,u_\mu|H_{\Psi X}^{(J)}(k)|Q',i,a\rangle
=
-i\alpha_X\,(k_i+Q_i')\,Q_\mu^a\,\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(Q-Q').
}
\label{eq:HBM_Jperp_matrix}
\end{equation}

So the \(J\)-vertex is completely explicit on the accepted Stage-IA background.

\section{4. Mixed block from the \(K\)-vertex}

The second Class II interaction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{int}}^{(K)}
=
\beta_X X_i^a\,K_i^a,
\qquad
K_i^a=\rho_\varepsilon\,\partial_i n^a.
}
\label{eq:HBM_Kint}
\end{equation}

On the accepted Stage-IA background,
\[
n^a=n_0^a=\text{constant},
\qquad
K_i^a[\Psi_{\mathrm{IA}}]=0.
\]
So the \(K\)-block has no background value, but its linearization survives in the tangent sector.

Define the profile-gradient field
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_i(x):=
\frac{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)\,\partial_i|\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)|^2}{|\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)|^2+\varepsilon}.
}
\label{eq:HBM_Xii}
\end{equation}

Then the canonical tangent linearization gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\langle Q,u_\mu|H_{\Psi X}^{(K)}(k)|Q',i,a\rangle
=
-\beta_X\,Q_\mu^a\,\widehat{\Xi_i}(Q-Q').
}
\label{eq:HBM_Kperp_matrix}
\end{equation}

By contrast, on the pure longitudinal scalar channel,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\langle Q,e_1|H_{\Psi X}^{(K)}(k)|Q',i,a\rangle=0
}
\label{eq:HBM_Kpar_zero}
\end{equation}
at the current frozen-orientation Stage-IA level.

Therefore the exact working mixed block splits as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\Psi X}(k)
=
H_{\Psi X}^{(J,\parallel)}(k)
\oplus
\bigl(
H_{\Psi X}^{(J,\perp)}(k)+H_{\Psi X}^{(K,\perp)}(k)
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:HBM_HPsiX_split}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Branch-specific harmonic data actually needed}

Thus all branch dependence is reduced to the following three harmonic families on the accepted Stage-IA branch:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(G),
\qquad
\widehat{\partial_i\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(G),
\qquad
\widehat{\Xi_i}(G).
}
\label{eq:HBM_threefamilies}
\end{equation}

For the locked BCC branch
\[
\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)=u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x),
\]
the shell harmonics satisfy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(G)
=
\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}
\eta_Q\,\widehat{u_{\mathrm{IA}}}(G-Q),
}
\label{eq:HBM_Phihat_explicit}
\end{equation}
and similarly for \(\widehat{\partial_i\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(G)\) and \(\widehat{\Xi_i}(G)\).

So the intervalley extractor only needs those reciprocal coefficients at the physically relevant harmonics \(G=G_*,0,\pm 2G_*,\dots\), and in practice the load-bearing pieces are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(G_*),
\qquad
\widehat{\Xi_1}(G_*),
\qquad
\widehat{\Xi_2}(G_*).
}
\label{eq:HBM_loadbearing}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Effective Bloch operator and derivative audit}

Once the matrix elements above are assembled, the exact effective Bloch operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
H_{\Psi X}(k)\,H_{XX}(k)^{-1}\,H_{X\Psi}(k).
}
\label{eq:HBM_Heff}
\end{equation}

At the strict working level,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{XX}(k)\approx M_X^2\mathbf 1_X,
}
\label{eq:HBM_HXX}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\,
H_{\Psi X}(k)\,H_{X\Psi}(k).
}
\label{eq:HBM_Heff_working}
\end{equation}

Then define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i=\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\Big|_{k=k_*},
\qquad
M_i=P_*K_iP_*.
}
\label{eq:HBM_KiMi}
\end{equation}

Finally the microscopic coefficients are extracted by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel),
\qquad
\Lambda_E=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_1M_1)=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_2M_2),
\qquad
\Lambda_O=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_2M_1)=-\frac12\Tr(\sigma_1M_2).
}
\label{eq:HBM_coeffs}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Reduced carrier PDE and benchmark bridge}

The reduced dictionary remains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=I_c\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_c\Lambda_O,
}
\label{eq:HBM_dict}
\end{equation}
and the current explicit reference route is already fixed by
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c,
\]
with the matching conditions to the canonical mixed odd-active target also fixed. :contentReference[oaicite:1]{index=1}

Therefore the accepted-branch extractor is now aligned with the project goal:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi_{\mathrm{IA}}
\to
H_{\Psi X}(k)
\to
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
\to
K_i
\to
P_*K_iP_*
\to
(\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)
\to
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\label{eq:HBM_chain}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Honest status}

At this point the only thing not yet done is the literal branch-specific harmonic evaluation
\[
\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(G),\qquad \widehat{\Xi_i}(G)
\]
and the subsequent derivative/projection computation.

No new branch logic is needed.
No new audit decomposition is needed.
The remaining work is finite harmonic extraction on the accepted Stage-IA branch.

\section{Final Summary}

On the accepted Stage-IA branch
\[
\Psi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)=\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)e_1,
\qquad
\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)=u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x),
\]
the mixed Bloch block \(H_{\Psi X}(k)\) becomes explicit.

For the \(J\)-vertex,
\[
L_{\mathrm{int}}^{(J)}=\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a,
\]
the longitudinal scalar matrix element is
\[
\boxed{
\langle Q,e_1|H_{\Psi X}^{(J)}(k)|Q',i,a\rangle
=
-i\alpha_X(k_i+Q_i')\,n_0^a\,\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(Q-Q').
}
\]

The tangent matrix element is
\[
\boxed{
\langle Q,u_\mu|H_{\Psi X}^{(J)}(k)|Q',i,a\rangle
=
-i\alpha_X(k_i+Q_i')\,Q_\mu^a\,\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(Q-Q').
}
\]

For the \(K\)-vertex,
\[
L_{\mathrm{int}}^{(K)}=\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a,
\]
the longitudinal scalar channel vanishes at the frozen-orientation Stage-IA level,
\[
\boxed{
\langle Q,e_1|H_{\Psi X}^{(K)}(k)|Q',i,a\rangle=0,
}
\]
while the tangent matrix element is
\[
\boxed{
\langle Q,u_\mu|H_{\Psi X}^{(K)}(k)|Q',i,a\rangle
=
-\beta_XQ_\mu^a\,\widehat{\Xi_i}(Q-Q'),
\qquad
\Xi_i=
\frac{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}\partial_i|\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}|^2}{|\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}|^2+\varepsilon}.
}
\]

So the branch-specific data needed by the common extractor are reduced to the reciprocal harmonics
\[
\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(G),\qquad
\widehat{\Xi_i}(G).
\]

From these one constructs
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)-H_{\Psi X}(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k),
\qquad
K_i=\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\big|_{k_*},
\qquad
M_i=P_*K_iP_*,
\]
and then extracts
\[
\lambda_c,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O.
\]

So the immediate next problem is now completely concrete:
\[
\boxed{
\text{evaluate }\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(G)\text{ and }\widehat{\Xi_i}(G)\text{ on the accepted Stage-IA branch.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Reciprocal-Harmonic Extraction on the Accepted Stage-IA Branch}

\section{1. Accepted branch and longitudinal harmonic support}

Take the accepted Stage-IA branch
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)=\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)e_1,
\qquad
\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)=u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)\,S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x),
\qquad
\xi=\hat n\cdot x.
}
\label{eq:RHE_bg}
\end{equation}

Write the locked BCC shell factor as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x)=\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}\eta_Q e^{iQ\cdot x}.
}
\label{eq:RHE_SBCC}
\end{equation}

For any reciprocal vector \(K\), define the branch-profile harmonic
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U(K):=
\widehat{u_{\mathrm{IA}}}(K)
=
\frac{1}{|\Omega|}\int_\Omega e^{-iK\cdot x}u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\hat n\cdot x)\,d^3x.
}
\label{eq:RHE_UK}
\end{equation}

Because \(u_{\mathrm{IA}}\) depends only on \(\xi=\hat n\cdot x\), its Fourier support is purely longitudinal:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U(K)=0
\qquad\text{unless}\qquad
K_\perp=0.
}
\label{eq:RHE_longitudinal_support}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact reciprocal-harmonic coefficient of the accepted branch is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(G)
=
\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}
\eta_Q\,U(G-Q).
}
\label{eq:RHE_Phihat_exact}
\end{equation}

By \eqref{eq:RHE_longitudinal_support}, only those \(Q\) with
\[
(G-Q)_\perp=0
\]
contribute. Therefore the actual support is the Minkowski sum
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{supp}\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}
\subset
\mathcal S_{12}+\Lambda_\parallel,
}
\label{eq:RHE_support}
\end{equation}
where \(\Lambda_\parallel\) is the one-dimensional longitudinal reciprocal set.

For the load-bearing intervalley harmonic \(G_*\), define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_\Phi(G_*):=
\{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}\;:\;(G_*-Q)_\perp=0\}.
}
\label{eq:RHE_Iphi}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(G_*)
=
\sum_{Q\in\mathcal I_\Phi(G_*)}
\eta_Q\,U((G_*-Q)_\parallel).
}
\label{eq:RHE_Phihat_Gstar}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact harmonic formula for \texorpdfstring{$|\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}|^2$}{|PhiIA|^2}}

The exact density harmonics are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{|\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}|^2}(G)
=
\sum_H
\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(H)\,
\overline{\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(H-G)}.
}
\label{eq:RHE_density_exact}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, using \eqref{eq:RHE_Phihat_exact},
\begin{equation}
\widehat{|\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}|^2}(G)
=
\sum_{Q,Q'\in\mathcal S_{12}}
\eta_Q\overline{\eta_{Q'}}
\sum_H
U(H-Q)\,
\overline{U(H-G-Q')}.
\label{eq:RHE_density_expand}
\end{equation}

This shows that the density harmonics lie on
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{supp}\widehat{|\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}|^2}
\subset
(\mathcal S_{12}-\mathcal S_{12})+\Lambda_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:RHE_density_support}
\end{equation}

Define the shell structure factors
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_\Delta
:=
\sum_{\substack{Q,Q'\in\mathcal S_{12}\\Q-Q'=\Delta}}
\eta_Q\overline{\eta_{Q'}}.
}
\label{eq:RHE_BDelta}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x)|^2
=
\sum_{\Delta\in\Delta\mathcal S}
B_\Delta e^{i\Delta\cdot x},
\qquad
\Delta\mathcal S:=\mathcal S_{12}-\mathcal S_{12}.
}
\label{eq:RHE_S2}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exact and practical formulas for \texorpdfstring{$\widehat{\Xi_i}(G)$}{Xi-hat}}

Recall
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_i(x)
=
\frac{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)\,\partial_i|\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)|^2}{|\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)|^2+\varepsilon}.
}
\label{eq:RHE_Xi_def}
\end{equation}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R(x):=\frac{1}{|\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)|^2+\varepsilon},
\qquad
\widehat R(G):=\frac{1}{|\Omega|}\int_\Omega e^{-iG\cdot x}R(x)\,d^3x.
}
\label{eq:RHE_R_def}
\end{equation}

Since
\[
\partial_i|\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}|^2
\;\widehat{}\;(G)
=
iG_i\,\widehat{|\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}|^2}(G),
\]
the exact reciprocal-harmonic coefficient of \(\Xi_i\) is the triple convolution
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Xi_i}(G)
=
\sum_{G_1+G_2+G_3=G}
\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(G_1)\,
i(G_2)_i\,\widehat{|\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}|^2}(G_2)\,
\widehat R(G_3).
}
\label{eq:RHE_Xihat_exact}
\end{equation}

This is the exact branch-specific harmonic formula.

\section{4. Stage-IA averaged-denominator approximation}

For the first explicit extractor pass, it is convenient to use the longitudinal averaged-denominator approximation
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R(x)\approx R_0(\xi):=\frac{1}{C_2u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)^2+\varepsilon}.
}
\label{eq:RHE_R0}
\end{equation}

Then
\[
|\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}|^2=u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)^2|S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x)|^2,
\]
so
\begin{align}
\partial_i|\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}|^2
&=
n_i\,(u_{\mathrm{IA}}^2)'(\xi)\,|S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^2
+
u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)^2\,\partial_i|S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^2.
\end{align}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_i(x)
\approx
n_i\,r_1(\xi)\,|S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x)|^2S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x)
+
r_2(\xi)\,S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x)\,\partial_i|S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x)|^2,
}
\label{eq:RHE_Xi_split}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_1(\xi):=\frac{u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)\,(u_{\mathrm{IA}}^2)'(\xi)}{C_2u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)^2+\varepsilon},
\qquad
r_2(\xi):=\frac{u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)^3}{C_2u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)^2+\varepsilon}.
}
\label{eq:RHE_r12}
\end{equation}

Write the longitudinal harmonics
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_1(K):=\widehat{r_1}(K),
\qquad
R_2(K):=\widehat{r_2}(K),
}
\label{eq:RHE_R12hat}
\end{equation}
again supported only on \(K_\perp=0\).

Using \eqref{eq:RHE_S2} and
\[
\partial_i|S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^2
=
\sum_{\Delta\in\Delta\mathcal S}
i\Delta_i B_\Delta e^{i\Delta\cdot x},
\]
we obtain the practical explicit approximation
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Xi_i}(G)
\approx
\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}
\sum_{\Delta\in\Delta\mathcal S}
\eta_Q B_\Delta
\Bigl[
n_i\,R_1(G-Q-\Delta)
+
i\Delta_i\,R_2(G-Q-\Delta)
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:RHE_Xihat_practical}
\end{equation}

Because \(R_1,R_2\) are longitudinally supported, only those pairs \((Q,\Delta)\) with
\[
(G-Q-\Delta)_\perp=0
\]
actually contribute.

Define the corresponding admissible set
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_\Xi(G)
:=
\{(Q,\Delta)\in \mathcal S_{12}\times\Delta\mathcal S
\;:\;
(G-Q-\Delta)_\perp=0\}.
}
\label{eq:RHE_Ixi}
\end{equation}
Then the load-bearing harmonic is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Xi_i}(G_*)
\approx
\sum_{(Q,\Delta)\in\mathcal I_\Xi(G_*)}
\eta_Q B_\Delta
\Bigl[
n_i\,R_1((G_*-Q-\Delta)_\parallel)
+
i\Delta_i\,R_2((G_*-Q-\Delta)_\parallel)
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:RHE_Xihat_Gstar}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Mixed Bloch block in harmonic form}

On the canonical Stage-IA branch, the mixed \(J\)-vertex matrix elements are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\langle G,e_1|H_{\Psi X}^{(J)}(k)|G',i,a\rangle
=
-i\alpha_X\,(k_i+G_i')\,n_0^a\,
\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(G-G'),
}
\label{eq:RHE_HJ_long}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\langle G,u_\mu|H_{\Psi X}^{(J)}(k)|G',i,a\rangle
=
-i\alpha_X\,(k_i+G_i')\,Q_\mu^a\,
\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(G-G').
}
\label{eq:RHE_HJ_tan}
\end{equation}

The \(K\)-vertex vanishes on the pure longitudinal scalar channel at the frozen-orientation Stage-IA level,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\langle G,e_1|H_{\Psi X}^{(K)}(k)|G',i,a\rangle=0,
}
\label{eq:RHE_HK_long_zero}
\end{equation}
while on the tangent channel it is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\langle G,u_\mu|H_{\Psi X}^{(K)}(k)|G',i,a\rangle
=
-\beta_X\,Q_\mu^a\,\widehat{\Xi_i}(G-G').
}
\label{eq:RHE_HK_tan}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:RHE_Phihat_exact} and \eqref{eq:RHE_Xihat_practical} gives the fully branch-resolved mixed block
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\Psi X}(k)
=
H_{\Psi X}^{(J,\parallel)}(k)
\oplus
\bigl(
H_{\Psi X}^{(J,\perp)}(k)+H_{\Psi X}^{(K,\perp)}(k)
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:RHE_HPX_final}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Immediate load-bearing harmonics}

Therefore the immediate branch-specific harmonic data that must be extracted numerically are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(G_*),
\qquad
\widehat{\Xi_1}(G_*),
\qquad
\widehat{\Xi_2}(G_*),
}
\label{eq:RHE_loadbearing}
\end{equation}
together with the corresponding near-shell harmonics needed to differentiate \(H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\) at \(k_*=G_*/2\).

Once these are inserted, the remaining extractor chain is standard:
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)-H_{\Psi X}(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k),
\quad
K_i=\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\big|_{k_*},
\quad
M_i=P_*K_iP_*.
\]
Then
\[
\lambda_c=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel),
\qquad
\Lambda_E=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_1M_1)=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_2M_2),
\qquad
\Lambda_O=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_2M_1)=-\frac12\Tr(\sigma_1M_2).
\]

So the accepted-branch extractor has now been reduced to a finite reciprocal-harmonic evaluation problem.

\section{Final Summary}

For the accepted Stage-IA branch
\[
\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)=u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x),
\]
the exact branch harmonic is
\[
\boxed{
\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(G)
=
\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}\eta_Q\,U(G-Q),
\qquad
U(K)=\widehat{u_{\mathrm{IA}}}(K),
}
\]
with the selection rule
\[
U(K)=0 \quad \text{unless} \quad K_\perp=0.
\]

The exact \(\Xi_i\)-harmonic is the triple convolution
\[
\boxed{
\widehat{\Xi_i}(G)
=
\sum_{G_1+G_2+G_3=G}
\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(G_1)\,
i(G_2)_i\,\widehat{|\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}|^2}(G_2)\,
\widehat R(G_3),
}
\]
where
\[
R=(|\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}|^2+\varepsilon)^{-1}.
\]

For the first practical extractor pass, the averaged-denominator approximation gives
\[
\boxed{
\widehat{\Xi_i}(G)
\approx
\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}
\sum_{\Delta\in\Delta\mathcal S}
\eta_Q B_\Delta
\Bigl[
n_i\,R_1(G-Q-\Delta)
+
i\Delta_i\,R_2(G-Q-\Delta)
\Bigr],
}
\]
where
\[
R_1=\widehat{\frac{u_{\mathrm{IA}}(u_{\mathrm{IA}}^2)'}{C_2u_{\mathrm{IA}}^2+\varepsilon}},
\qquad
R_2=\widehat{\frac{u_{\mathrm{IA}}^3}{C_2u_{\mathrm{IA}}^2+\varepsilon}},
\]
again with purely longitudinal support.

Therefore the mixed Bloch block is now explicit:
\[
\langle G,e_1|H_{\Psi X}^{(J)}(k)|G',i,a\rangle
=
-i\alpha_X(k_i+G_i')\,n_0^a\,\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(G-G'),
\]
\[
\langle G,u_\mu|H_{\Psi X}^{(J)}(k)|G',i,a\rangle
=
-i\alpha_X(k_i+G_i')\,Q_\mu^a\,\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(G-G'),
\]
\[
\langle G,u_\mu|H_{\Psi X}^{(K)}(k)|G',i,a\rangle
=
-\beta_XQ_\mu^a\,\widehat{\Xi_i}(G-G'),
\]
while the longitudinal \(K\)-channel vanishes at frozen-orientation Stage IA.

So the immediate next finite task is exactly:
\[
\boxed{
\text{evaluate }
\widehat{\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}}(G_*),\ 
\widehat{\Xi_1}(G_*),\ 
\widehat{\Xi_2}(G_*)
\text{ on the accepted Stage-IA branch.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Stage-IA Branch-Specific Fourier Overlaps for the Common Extractor}

\section{Goal}

We now reduce the accepted Stage-IA branch to the finite Fourier overlaps that directly feed the common Bloch extractor.

The branch is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)=\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)e_1,
\qquad
\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)=u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)\,S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x).
}
\label{eq:SBF_bg}
\end{equation}

Define the density harmonic
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho(x):=|\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)|^2,
\qquad
\widehat\rho(Q):=\widehat{|\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}|^2}(Q).
}
\label{eq:SBF_rho}
\end{equation}

\section{1. Stage-IA \(J\)-harmonics}

On the canonical frozen-orientation Stage-IA branch, one has
\[
J_i^A(x)=n_0^A\,\partial_i\rho(x),
\]
so the exact reciprocal harmonic is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat J_i^A(Q)
=
iQ_i\,n_0^A\,\widehat\rho(Q).
}
\label{eq:SBF_Jhat}
\end{equation}

Thus the \(J\)-sector is completely determined by the density harmonics \(\widehat\rho(Q)\).

\section{2. Stage-IA tangent \(K\)-harmonics}

From the tangent-channel linearization on the accepted Stage-IA branch, the \(K\)-sector is encoded by the profile-gradient field \(\Xi_i(x)\). Write the tangent projection coefficient as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(Q)
=
\mathcal Q_\alpha^A\,\widehat{\Xi_i}(Q),
}
\label{eq:SBF_Khat}
\end{equation}
where \(\alpha=1,2\) labels the two transverse tangent channels and \(\mathcal Q_\alpha^A\) is the fixed internal shell-tangent coupling on the canonical \(e_1\)-branch.

Therefore the entire transverse Class II overlap is determined by the pair
\[
\widehat\rho(Q),\qquad \widehat{\Xi_i}(Q).
\]

\section{3. Exact Stage-IA Class II transverse overlap}

The explicit folded-Bragg Class II overlap formula is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\sum_A
\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
\widehat J_i^A(Q)\,\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(Q').
}
\label{eq:SBF_TII_start}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:SBF_Jhat} and \eqref{eq:SBF_Khat}, we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\sum_A n_0^A\mathcal Q_\alpha^A
\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
iQ_i\,\widehat\rho(Q)\,\widehat{\Xi_i}(Q').
}
\label{eq:SBF_TII_exact}
\end{equation}

Define the fixed internal contraction
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma_\alpha:=\sum_A n_0^A\mathcal Q_\alpha^A.
}
\label{eq:SBF_Gammaalpha}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\Gamma_\alpha
\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
iQ_i\,\widehat\rho(Q)\,\widehat{\Xi_i}(Q').
}
\label{eq:SBF_TII_exact2}
\end{equation}

This is the exact Stage-IA branch-specific transverse overlap formula.

\section{4. Practical explicit form using the \(\widehat{\Xi_i}\)-reduction}

From the previous Stage-IA harmonic reduction,
\[
\widehat{\Xi_i}(Q')
\approx
\sum_{(Q_1,\Delta)\in\mathcal I_\Xi(Q')}
\eta_{Q_1}B_\Delta
\Bigl[
n_i\,R_1((Q'-Q_1-\Delta)_\parallel)
+
i\Delta_i\,R_2((Q'-Q_1-\Delta)_\parallel)
\Bigr],
\]
where
\[
R_1=\widehat{\frac{u_{\mathrm{IA}}(u_{\mathrm{IA}}^2)'}{C_2u_{\mathrm{IA}}^2+\varepsilon}},
\qquad
R_2=\widehat{\frac{u_{\mathrm{IA}}^3}{C_2u_{\mathrm{IA}}^2+\varepsilon}}.
\]

Substituting into \eqref{eq:SBF_TII_exact2} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
\approx
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\Gamma_\alpha
\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
\widehat\rho(Q)
\sum_{(Q_1,\Delta)\in\mathcal I_\Xi(Q')}
\eta_{Q_1}B_\Delta
\Bigl[
i(Q\!\cdot\!\hat n)\,R_1(L)
-
(Q\!\cdot\!\Delta)\,R_2(L)
\Bigr],
}
\label{eq:SBF_TII_practical}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L:=(Q'-Q_1-\Delta)_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:SBF_Ldef}
\end{equation}

So the transverse witness is now reduced to a finite shell sum dressed by one-dimensional longitudinal profile harmonics.

\section{5. Exact Stage-IA scalar Bragg block}

The scalar shell-pair block has the form
\[
M_0=\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2.
\]
On the Stage-IA branch, the Class II contribution comes from the \(JJ\)-type elimination because the longitudinal \(K\)-channel vanishes at frozen orientation.

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
\sum_A
\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
\widehat J_i^A(Q)\,\widehat J_i^A(Q').
}
\label{eq:SBF_UII_start}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:SBF_Jhat},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*)
=
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
\left(\sum_A (n_0^A)^2\right)
\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
(Q\!\cdot\!Q')\,
\widehat\rho(Q)\,\widehat\rho(Q').
}
\label{eq:SBF_UII_exact}
\end{equation}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\nu_0:=\sum_A (n_0^A)^2.
}
\label{eq:SBF_nu0}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*)
=
\frac{\alpha_X^2\nu_0}{M_X^2}
\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
(Q\!\cdot\!Q')\,
\widehat\rho(Q)\,\widehat\rho(Q').
}
\label{eq:SBF_UII_exact2}
\end{equation}

Hence the scalar Bragg mass obstruction/survival test is also reduced to the same density harmonics \(\widehat\rho(Q)\).

\section{6. Load-bearing Stage-IA harmonic data}

Therefore the accepted Stage-IA branch feeds the common extractor through the finite data set
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat\rho(Q),\qquad
R_1(L),\qquad
R_2(L),
}
\label{eq:SBF_data}
\end{equation}
with the principal intervalley outputs
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^1_{(II)}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^2_{(II)}(G_*).
}
\label{eq:SBF_outputs}
\end{equation}

At the practical first-shell level, the load-bearing pieces are the harmonics with
\[
Q,\ Q'\ \text{near}\ 0,\ G_*,
\]
because the intervalley selection rule enforces
\[
Q+Q'=G_*.
\]

\section{7. Immediate next computation}

Thus the next literal computation on the accepted Stage-IA branch is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(i) compute }\widehat\rho(Q),
\qquad
\text{(ii) compute }R_1(L),R_2(L),
\qquad
\text{(iii) assemble }\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*),\ \widehat T^1_{(II)}(G_*),\ \widehat T^2_{(II)}(G_*).
}
\label{eq:SBF_next}
\end{equation}

Once these are known, the rest of the common extractor is standard:
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
\to
K_i
\to
P_*K_iP_*
\to
(\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)
\to
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

\section{One-Dimensional Profile Reduction of the Accepted Stage-IA Harmonics}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The accepted Stage-IA branch has the separated form
\[
\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)=u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)\,S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x),
\qquad
\xi=\hat n\cdot x.
\]
Therefore every branch-specific harmonic needed by the common extractor reduces to a finite BCC geometry sum dressed by one-dimensional Fourier coefficients of the profile \(u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)\).

This is the exact point at which the accepted-branch extractor becomes a one-dimensional profile-data problem.

\section{1. Accepted branch and one-dimensional profile transforms}

Take
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)=u(\xi)\,S(x),
\qquad
\xi=\hat n\cdot x,
\qquad
S(x)=\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}\eta_Q e^{iQ\cdot x}.
}
\label{eq:OPR_branch}
\end{equation}

For any longitudinal reciprocal number \(\ell\in\Lambda_\parallel\), define the one-dimensional profile transforms
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_1(\ell)
:=
\frac{1}{L_\parallel}\int_0^{L_\parallel}e^{-i\ell\xi}u(\xi)\,d\xi,
}
\label{eq:OPR_U1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_2(\ell)
:=
\frac{1}{L_\parallel}\int_0^{L_\parallel}e^{-i\ell\xi}u(\xi)^2\,d\xi,
}
\label{eq:OPR_U2}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_1(\xi):=\frac{u(\xi)\,(u(\xi)^2)'}{C_2u(\xi)^2+\varepsilon},
\qquad
r_2(\xi):=\frac{u(\xi)^3}{C_2u(\xi)^2+\varepsilon},
}
\label{eq:OPR_r12}
\end{equation}
with transforms
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal R_1(\ell)
:=
\frac{1}{L_\parallel}\int_0^{L_\parallel}e^{-i\ell\xi}r_1(\xi)\,d\xi,
\qquad
\mathcal R_2(\ell)
:=
\frac{1}{L_\parallel}\int_0^{L_\parallel}e^{-i\ell\xi}r_2(\xi)\,d\xi.
}
\label{eq:OPR_R12}
\end{equation}

Because \(u\), \(r_1\), and \(r_2\) depend only on \(\xi\), their full reciprocal-space coefficients have purely longitudinal support:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{u}(K)=\mathbf 1_{K_\perp=0}\,\mathcal U_1(K_\parallel),
\qquad
\widehat{u^2}(K)=\mathbf 1_{K_\perp=0}\,\mathcal U_2(K_\parallel),
}
\label{eq:OPR_support_u}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{r_1}(K)=\mathbf 1_{K_\perp=0}\,\mathcal R_1(K_\parallel),
\qquad
\widehat{r_2}(K)=\mathbf 1_{K_\perp=0}\,\mathcal R_2(K_\parallel).
}
\label{eq:OPR_support_r}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact reduction of \texorpdfstring{$\widehat{\Phi}(G)$}{Phi-hat(G)}}

The accepted branch harmonic is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Phi}(G)
=
\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}\eta_Q\,\widehat{u}(G-Q).
}
\label{eq:OPR_Phihat_start}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:OPR_support_u},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Phi}(G)
=
\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}
\eta_Q\,
\mathbf 1_{(G-Q)_\perp=0}\,
\mathcal U_1\!\bigl((G-Q)_\parallel\bigr).
}
\label{eq:OPR_Phihat_final}
\end{equation}

So the branch harmonic is already a finite BCC shell sum dressed by the one-dimensional profile transform \(\mathcal U_1\).

In particular, at the load-bearing intervalley harmonic \(G_*\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Phi}(G_*)
=
\sum_{Q\in\mathcal I_\Phi(G_*)}
\eta_Q\,\mathcal U_1\!\bigl((G_*-Q)_\parallel\bigr),
}
\label{eq:OPR_Phihat_Gstar}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_\Phi(G_*):=
\{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}:(G_*-Q)_\perp=0\}.
}
\label{eq:OPR_Iphi}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exact reduction of \texorpdfstring{$\widehat{\rho}(G)$}{rho-hat(G)}}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho(x)=|\Phi(x)|^2=u(\xi)^2\,|S(x)|^2.
}
\label{eq:OPR_rho_def}
\end{equation}

Write the BCC density shell factor as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|S(x)|^2=\sum_{\Delta\in\Delta\mathcal S}B_\Delta e^{i\Delta\cdot x},
\qquad
\Delta\mathcal S:=\mathcal S_{12}-\mathcal S_{12},
}
\label{eq:OPR_S2}
\end{equation}
with structure coefficients
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_\Delta
:=
\sum_{\substack{Q,Q'\in\mathcal S_{12}\\Q-Q'=\Delta}}
\eta_Q\overline{\eta_{Q'}}.
}
\label{eq:OPR_BDelta}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho(x)
=
\sum_{\Delta\in\Delta\mathcal S}
B_\Delta\,u(\xi)^2\,e^{i\Delta\cdot x}.
}
\label{eq:OPR_rho_expand}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\rho}(G)
=
\sum_{\Delta\in\Delta\mathcal S}
B_\Delta\,
\widehat{u^2}(G-\Delta).
}
\label{eq:OPR_rhohat_start}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:OPR_support_u},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\rho}(G)
=
\sum_{\Delta\in\Delta\mathcal S}
B_\Delta\,
\mathbf 1_{(G-\Delta)_\perp=0}\,
\mathcal U_2\!\bigl((G-\Delta)_\parallel\bigr).
}
\label{eq:OPR_rhohat_final}
\end{equation}

So \(\widehat{\rho}(G)\) is fully reduced to the one-dimensional profile transform \(\mathcal U_2\) plus pure BCC geometry.

In particular,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\rho}(G_*)
=
\sum_{\Delta\in\mathcal I_\rho(G_*)}
B_\Delta\,
\mathcal U_2\!\bigl((G_*-\Delta)_\parallel\bigr),
}
\label{eq:OPR_rhohat_Gstar}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_\rho(G_*):=
\{\Delta\in\Delta\mathcal S:(G_*-\Delta)_\perp=0\}.
}
\label{eq:OPR_Irho}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Exact reduction of \texorpdfstring{$\widehat{\Xi_i}(G)$}{Xi-hat(G)} to one-dimensional profile data}

In the averaged-denominator Stage-IA reduction, one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_i(x)
\approx
n_i\,r_1(\xi)\,|S(x)|^2S(x)
+
r_2(\xi)\,S(x)\,\partial_i|S(x)|^2.
}
\label{eq:OPR_Xi_split}
\end{equation}

First define the two pure BCC geometry tensors
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C^{(0)}_M
:=
\sum_{\substack{Q\in\mathcal S_{12},\ \Delta\in\Delta\mathcal S\\Q+\Delta=M}}
\eta_Q\,B_\Delta,
}
\label{eq:OPR_C0}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C^{(1)}_{M,i}
:=
\sum_{\substack{Q\in\mathcal S_{12},\ \Delta\in\Delta\mathcal S\\Q+\Delta=M}}
i\Delta_i\,\eta_Q\,B_\Delta.
}
\label{eq:OPR_C1}
\end{equation}

Then the shell identities are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|S(x)|^2S(x)=\sum_M C_M^{(0)}e^{iM\cdot x},
}
\label{eq:OPR_S3a}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S(x)\,\partial_i|S(x)|^2=\sum_M C_{M,i}^{(1)}e^{iM\cdot x}.
}
\label{eq:OPR_S3b}
\end{equation}

Therefore \eqref{eq:OPR_Xi_split} becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_i(x)
\approx
\sum_M
\Bigl[
n_i\,C_M^{(0)}\,r_1(\xi)
+
C_{M,i}^{(1)}\,r_2(\xi)
\Bigr]e^{iM\cdot x}.
}
\label{eq:OPR_Xi_expand}
\end{equation}

Taking the reciprocal harmonic and using \eqref{eq:OPR_support_r},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Xi_i}(G)
\approx
\sum_M
\left[
n_i\,C_M^{(0)}\,\mathbf 1_{(G-M)_\perp=0}\,\mathcal R_1\!\bigl((G-M)_\parallel\bigr)
+
C_{M,i}^{(1)}\,\mathbf 1_{(G-M)_\perp=0}\,\mathcal R_2\!\bigl((G-M)_\parallel\bigr)
\right].
}
\label{eq:OPR_Xihat_final}
\end{equation}

This is the desired one-dimensional profile reduction.

At the intervalley harmonic \(G_*\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Xi_i}(G_*)
\approx
\sum_{M\in\mathcal I_\Xi(G_*)}
\left[
n_i\,C_M^{(0)}\,\mathcal R_1\!\bigl((G_*-M)_\parallel\bigr)
+
C_{M,i}^{(1)}\,\mathcal R_2\!\bigl((G_*-M)_\parallel\bigr)
\right],
}
\label{eq:OPR_Xihat_Gstar}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_\Xi(G_*):=
\{M:(G_*-M)_\perp=0\}.
}
\label{eq:OPR_Ixi}
\end{equation}

So \(\widehat{\Xi_i}(G_*)\) is now completely reduced to the one-dimensional profile transforms \(\mathcal R_1,\mathcal R_2\) plus pure BCC geometry.

\section{5. Class II intervalley overlaps reduced to one-dimensional profile data}

The scalar intervalley overlap is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*)
=
\frac{\alpha_X^2\nu_0}{M_X^2}
\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
(Q\cdot Q')\,\widehat{\rho}(Q)\,\widehat{\rho}(Q'),
\qquad
\nu_0:=\sum_A(n_0^A)^2.
}
\label{eq:OPR_UII}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:OPR_rhohat_final}, \(\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*)\) becomes a finite BCC geometry sum dressed only by \(\mathcal U_2\).

Likewise the transverse overlaps are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T_{(II)}^\alpha(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\Gamma_\alpha
\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
iQ_i\,\widehat{\rho}(Q)\,\widehat{\Xi_i}(Q'),
}
\label{eq:OPR_TII}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma_\alpha:=\sum_A n_0^A\mathcal Q_\alpha^A.
}
\label{eq:OPR_Gamma}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:OPR_rhohat_final} and \eqref{eq:OPR_Xihat_final}, each \(\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)\) becomes a finite BCC shell sum dressed only by
\[
\mathcal U_2(\ell),\qquad \mathcal R_1(\ell),\qquad \mathcal R_2(\ell).
\]

\section{6. Final one-dimensional profile-data statement}

Therefore the entire accepted-branch common extractor is reduced to the one-dimensional profile data set
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_1(\ell),\qquad
\mathcal U_2(\ell),\qquad
\mathcal R_1(\ell),\qquad
\mathcal R_2(\ell),
\qquad
\ell\in\Lambda_\parallel,
}
\label{eq:OPR_profiledata}
\end{equation}
together with fixed pure BCC geometry tensors
\[
\eta_Q,\qquad
B_\Delta,\qquad
C_M^{(0)},\qquad
C_{M,i}^{(1)}.
\]

Then
\[
\widehat{\Phi}(G),\qquad
\widehat{\rho}(G),\qquad
\widehat{\Xi_i}(G)
\]
are explicit finite sums, and so are
\[
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^1_{(II)}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^2_{(II)}(G_*).
\]

Once these are assembled, the remaining extractor chain is standard:
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
\to
K_i
\to
P_*K_iP_*
\to
(\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)
\to
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The accepted Stage-IA branch
\[
\Phi_{\mathrm{IA}}(x)=u(\xi)\,S_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x)
\]
reduces the branch-specific harmonic data to one-dimensional profile Fourier transforms.

The exact branch harmonic is
\[
\widehat{\Phi}(G)
=
\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}
\eta_Q\,
\mathbf 1_{(G-Q)_\perp=0}\,
\mathcal U_1((G-Q)_\parallel).
\]

The density harmonic is
\[
\widehat{\rho}(G)
=
\sum_{\Delta\in\Delta\mathcal S}
B_\Delta\,
\mathbf 1_{(G-\Delta)_\perp=0}\,
\mathcal U_2((G-\Delta)_\parallel).
\]

The profile-gradient harmonic is
\[
\widehat{\Xi_i}(G)
\approx
\sum_M
\left[
n_i\,C_M^{(0)}\,\mathbf 1_{(G-M)_\perp=0}\,\mathcal R_1((G-M)_\parallel)
+
C_{M,i}^{(1)}\,\mathbf 1_{(G-M)_\perp=0}\,\mathcal R_2((G-M)_\parallel)
\right].
\]

Therefore the load-bearing Class II overlaps
\[
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^1_{(II)}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^2_{(II)}(G_*)
\]
are finite BCC geometry sums dressed only by the one-dimensional profile data
\[
\mathcal U_1,\qquad
\mathcal U_2,\qquad
\mathcal R_1,\qquad
\mathcal R_2.
\]

So the common extractor has now been reduced to a pure one-dimensional profile-data problem on the accepted Stage-IA branch.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{One-Dimensional Fourier Data of the Accepted Stage-IA Shooting Solution}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

We now reduce the accepted Stage-IA branch completely to one-dimensional Fourier data extracted from the shooting solution \(u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)\).

Because the accepted branch is even in \(\xi\), the required profile transforms split into cosine transforms for the even quantities and a sine transform for the odd derivative-current quantity.

This is the last reduction before actual numerical extraction.

\section{1. Even extension and longitudinal reciprocal lattice}

Let the accepted Stage-IA profile on \([0,L_\xi]\) be
\[
u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi).
\]
Extend it evenly to \([-L_\xi,L_\xi]\), and then periodically with period \(2L_\xi\).

The longitudinal reciprocal lattice is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_m=\frac{m\pi}{L_\xi},
\qquad
m\in\mathbb Z.
}
\label{eq:ODF_ellm}
\end{equation}

For any even profile \(f(\xi)\), the longitudinal Fourier coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat f(\ell_m)
=
\frac{1}{2L_\xi}\int_{-L_\xi}^{L_\xi}e^{-i\ell_m\xi}f(\xi)\,d\xi
=
\frac{1}{L_\xi}\int_0^{L_\xi}f(\xi)\cos(\ell_m\xi)\,d\xi.
}
\label{eq:ODF_even}
\end{equation}

For any odd profile \(g(\xi)\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat g(\ell_m)
=
\frac{1}{2L_\xi}\int_{-L_\xi}^{L_\xi}e^{-i\ell_m\xi}g(\xi)\,d\xi
=
-\frac{i}{L_\xi}\int_0^{L_\xi}g(\xi)\sin(\ell_m\xi)\,d\xi.
}
\label{eq:ODF_odd}
\end{equation}

\section{2. The four one-dimensional profile transforms}

Define the Stage-IA one-dimensional data by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_1^{(m)}
:=
\frac{1}{L_\xi}\int_0^{L_\xi}u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)\cos(\ell_m\xi)\,d\xi,
}
\label{eq:ODF_U1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_2^{(m)}
:=
\frac{1}{L_\xi}\int_0^{L_\xi}u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)^2\cos(\ell_m\xi)\,d\xi,
}
\label{eq:ODF_U2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal R_2^{(m)}
:=
\frac{1}{L_\xi}\int_0^{L_\xi}
\frac{u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)^3}{C_2u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)^2+\varepsilon}
\cos(\ell_m\xi)\,d\xi,
}
\label{eq:ODF_R2}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal R_1^{(m)}
:=
-\frac{i}{L_\xi}\int_0^{L_\xi}
\frac{u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)\,(u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)^2)'}{C_2u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)^2+\varepsilon}
\sin(\ell_m\xi)\,d\xi.
}
\label{eq:ODF_R1_raw}
\end{equation}

These are exactly the four one-dimensional profile inputs required by the accepted-branch common extractor.

\section{3. Stable reformulation of \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal R_1^{(m)}$}{R1(m)}}

The quantity \(r_1(\xi)\) contains a derivative and is numerically less stable than the others if evaluated directly.
So define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
F(u)
:=
\frac{2u}{C_2}
-
\frac{2\sqrt{\varepsilon}}{C_2^{3/2}}
\arctan\!\left(\sqrt{\frac{C_2}{\varepsilon}}\,u\right).
}
\label{eq:ODF_Fu}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{d}{d\xi}F(u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi))
=
\frac{u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)(u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)^2)'}{C_2u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)^2+\varepsilon}
=:r_1(\xi).
}
\label{eq:ODF_r1exact}
\end{equation}

Since \(u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)\) is even, \(F(u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi))\) is also even, and the boundary term vanishes on the periodic-even extension.
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal R_1^{(m)}
=
i\ell_m\,\mathcal F^{(m)},
}
\label{eq:ODF_R1_stable}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F^{(m)}
:=
\frac{1}{L_\xi}\int_0^{L_\xi}
F(u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi))\cos(\ell_m\xi)\,d\xi.
}
\label{eq:ODF_Fm}
\end{equation}

This is the preferred stable formula for \(\mathcal R_1^{(m)}\).

\section{4. Discrete formulas from the shooting solution}

Suppose the accepted shooting solution is available at quadrature nodes \(\xi_j\in[0,L_\xi]\) with weights \(\omega_j\).
Then the numerical extraction formulas are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_1^{(m)}
\approx
\frac{1}{L_\xi}\sum_j \omega_j\,u_j\,\cos(\ell_m\xi_j),
}
\label{eq:ODF_disc_U1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_2^{(m)}
\approx
\frac{1}{L_\xi}\sum_j \omega_j\,u_j^2\,\cos(\ell_m\xi_j),
}
\label{eq:ODF_disc_U2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal R_2^{(m)}
\approx
\frac{1}{L_\xi}\sum_j \omega_j\,
\frac{u_j^3}{C_2u_j^2+\varepsilon}\,
\cos(\ell_m\xi_j),
}
\label{eq:ODF_disc_R2}
\end{equation}
and in the stable form,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal R_1^{(m)}
\approx
i\ell_m\,
\frac{1}{L_\xi}\sum_j \omega_j\,F(u_j)\cos(\ell_m\xi_j).
}
\label{eq:ODF_disc_R1}
\end{equation}

For the present Stage-IA pipeline, these are the actual practical formulas to use.

\section{5. Reduction of \texorpdfstring{$\widehat{\Phi}(G_*)$}{Phi-hat(G*)} to one-dimensional data}

The accepted-branch harmonic was already reduced to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Phi}(G_*)
=
\sum_{Q\in\mathcal I_\Phi(G_*)}
\eta_Q\,
\mathcal U_1^{(m_Q)},
}
\label{eq:ODF_Phihat_Gstar}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_Q
:=
\frac{L_\xi}{\pi}(G_*-Q)_\parallel,
\qquad
Q\in\mathcal I_\Phi(G_*),
}
\label{eq:ODF_mQ}
\end{equation}
and \(\mathcal I_\Phi(G_*)\) is the admissible BCC shell subset satisfying \((G_*-Q)_\perp=0\).

So \(\widehat{\Phi}(G_*)\) depends only on the one-dimensional profile coefficients \(\mathcal U_1^{(m)}\).

\section{6. Reduction of \texorpdfstring{$\widehat{\rho}(G_*)$}{rho-hat(G*)}}

The density harmonic is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\rho}(G_*)
=
\sum_{\Delta\in\mathcal I_\rho(G_*)}
B_\Delta\,
\mathcal U_2^{(m_\Delta)},
}
\label{eq:ODF_rho_Gstar}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_\Delta
:=
\frac{L_\xi}{\pi}(G_*-\Delta)_\parallel,
\qquad
\Delta\in\mathcal I_\rho(G_*).
}
\label{eq:ODF_mDelta}
\end{equation}

Thus \(\widehat{\rho}(G_*)\) is determined entirely by \(\mathcal U_2^{(m)}\) and fixed BCC geometry.

\section{7. Reduction of \texorpdfstring{$\widehat{\Xi_i}(G_*)$}{Xi-hat(G*)}}

The profile-gradient harmonic was reduced to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Xi_i}(G_*)
\approx
\sum_{M\in\mathcal I_\Xi(G_*)}
\left[
n_i\,C_M^{(0)}\,\mathcal R_1^{(m_M)}
+
C_{M,i}^{(1)}\,\mathcal R_2^{(m_M)}
\right],
}
\label{eq:ODF_Xi_Gstar}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_M
:=
\frac{L_\xi}{\pi}(G_*-M)_\parallel,
\qquad
M\in\mathcal I_\Xi(G_*).
}
\label{eq:ODF_mM}
\end{equation}

Therefore \(\widehat{\Xi_i}(G_*)\) is determined only by the one-dimensional profile coefficients \(\mathcal R_1^{(m)}\) and \(\mathcal R_2^{(m)}\).

\section{8. Final accepted-branch overlap formulas}

The accepted Stage-IA branch feeds the Class II intervalley overlaps through
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*)
=
\frac{\alpha_X^2\nu_0}{M_X^2}
\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
(Q\cdot Q')\,\widehat{\rho}(Q)\,\widehat{\rho}(Q'),
\qquad
\nu_0:=\sum_A(n_0^A)^2,
}
\label{eq:ODF_Ufinal}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Gamma_\alpha
\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
iQ_i\,\widehat{\rho}(Q)\,\widehat{\Xi_i}(Q'),
}
\label{eq:ODF_Tfinal}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma_\alpha:=\sum_A n_0^A\mathcal Q_\alpha^A.
}
\label{eq:ODF_Gamma}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:ODF_rho_Gstar} and \eqref{eq:ODF_Xi_Gstar}, both \(\widehat U_{(II)}\) and \(\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}\) become finite BCC geometry sums depending only on
\[
\mathcal U_2^{(m)},\qquad
\mathcal R_1^{(m)},\qquad
\mathcal R_2^{(m)}.
\]

Thus the accepted-branch common extractor is now completely reduced to one-dimensional Fourier data of the Stage-IA shooting solution.

\section{9. Immediate next move}

The exact next finite task is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute }
\mathcal U_1^{(m)},\ \mathcal U_2^{(m)},\ \mathcal R_1^{(m)},\ \mathcal R_2^{(m)}
\text{ from }u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi),
\text{ for the finitely many }m\text{ selected by }G_*.
}
\label{eq:ODF_next}
\end{equation}

After that, the remainder is mechanical:
\[
\widehat{\Phi}(G_*),\ \widehat{\rho}(G_*),\ \widehat{\Xi_i}(G_*)
\;\to\;
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*),\ \widehat T^1_{(II)}(G_*),\ \widehat T^2_{(II)}(G_*)
\;\to\;
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k),\ K_i,\ P_*K_iP_*.
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The accepted Stage-IA branch extractor is now reduced completely to one-dimensional Fourier data of the shooting profile \(u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)\).

The four required profile transforms are:

\[
\mathcal U_1^{(m)}
=
\frac{1}{L_\xi}\int_0^{L_\xi}u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)\cos(\ell_m\xi)\,d\xi,
\qquad
\ell_m=\frac{m\pi}{L_\xi},
\]

\[
\mathcal U_2^{(m)}
=
\frac{1}{L_\xi}\int_0^{L_\xi}u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)^2\cos(\ell_m\xi)\,d\xi,
\]

\[
\mathcal R_2^{(m)}
=
\frac{1}{L_\xi}\int_0^{L_\xi}
\frac{u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)^3}{C_2u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)^2+\varepsilon}
\cos(\ell_m\xi)\,d\xi,
\]

and the stable odd-current transform
\[
\mathcal R_1^{(m)}
=
i\ell_m\,
\frac{1}{L_\xi}\int_0^{L_\xi}
F(u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi))\cos(\ell_m\xi)\,d\xi,
\]
with
\[
F(u)
=
\frac{2u}{C_2}
-
\frac{2\sqrt{\varepsilon}}{C_2^{3/2}}
\arctan\!\left(\sqrt{\frac{C_2}{\varepsilon}}u\right).
\]

From these, the branch harmonics become

\[
\widehat{\Phi}(G_*)
=
\sum_{Q\in\mathcal I_\Phi(G_*)}
\eta_Q\,\mathcal U_1^{(m_Q)},
\]

\[
\widehat{\rho}(G_*)
=
\sum_{\Delta\in\mathcal I_\rho(G_*)}
B_\Delta\,\mathcal U_2^{(m_\Delta)},
\]

\[
\widehat{\Xi_i}(G_*)
\approx
\sum_{M\in\mathcal I_\Xi(G_*)}
\left[
n_i\,C_M^{(0)}\,\mathcal R_1^{(m_M)}
+
C_{M,i}^{(1)}\,\mathcal R_2^{(m_M)}
\right].
\]

Therefore the accepted-branch Class II overlaps
\[
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^1_{(II)}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^2_{(II)}(G_*)
\]
are now finite BCC geometry sums depending only on the one-dimensional Fourier data of \(u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)\).

So the common extractor has been reduced all the way to a pure one-dimensional profile-data computation.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Finite Longitudinal Sample Set at the Selected BCC Harmonic \texorpdfstring{$G_*$}{G*}}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

We now stop speaking about generic harmonic sums and fix the actual finite longitudinal sample set required by the accepted Stage-IA branch at the selected BCC vector
\[
G_*=\frac{q_*}{\sqrt2}(1,1,0).
\]

The result is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Phi}(G_*)
\ \text{needs only } \mathcal U_1(0),\ \mathcal U_1(2q_*),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\rho}(G_*)
\ \text{needs only } \mathcal U_2(0),\ \mathcal U_2(q_*),\ \mathcal U_2(2q_*),\ \mathcal U_2(3q_*),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Xi_i}(G_*)
\ \text{needs only } \mathcal R_1(\ell),\ \mathcal R_2(\ell)
\text{ at } \ell\in\{0,q_*,2q_*,3q_*,4q_*\},
}
\end{equation}
with \(\mathcal R_1(0)=0\) automatically by parity.

So the accepted-branch common extractor is now reduced to a very small one-dimensional data problem.

\section{1. Selected shell geometry}

Fix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_*=\frac{q_*}{\sqrt2}(1,1,0),
\qquad
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|}=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}(1,1,0).
}
\label{eq:FMS_Gstar}
\end{equation}

The first BCC shell is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{\mathrm{BCC}}
=
\frac{q_*}{\sqrt2}
\{(\pm1,\pm1,0),(\pm1,0,\pm1),(0,\pm1,\pm1)\}.
}
\label{eq:FMS_shell}
\end{equation}

All longitudinal sample frequencies below are multiples of
\[
q_*=|G_*|.
\]

\section{2. Exact finite reduction of \texorpdfstring{$\widehat{\Phi}(G_*)$}{Phi-hat(G*)}}

The accepted branch harmonic is
\begin{equation}
\widehat{\Phi}(G_*)
=
\sum_{Q\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}}
\eta_Q\,
\mathbf 1_{(G_*-Q)_\perp=0}\,
\mathcal U_1((G_*-Q)_\parallel).
\label{eq:FMS_Phihat_start}
\end{equation}

For \(G_*=\frac{q_*}{\sqrt2}(1,1,0)\), the condition
\[
(G_*-Q)_\perp=0
\]
is equivalent to
\[
Q=\pm G_*.
\]
Indeed:

\begin{itemize}
\item if \(Q=+G_*\), then \(G_*-Q=0\);
\item if \(Q=-G_*\), then \(G_*-Q=2G_*\);
\item every other first-shell vector produces a difference with nonzero perpendicular part.
\end{itemize}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Phi}(G_*)
=
\eta_{+}\,\mathcal U_1(0)
+
\eta_{-}\,\mathcal U_1(2q_*),
}
\label{eq:FMS_Phihat_final}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\eta_{+}:=\eta_{G_*},
\qquad
\eta_{-}:=\eta_{-G_*}.
\]

So \(\widehat{\Phi}(G_*)\) depends only on the two longitudinal samples
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal U_1(0),\qquad \mathcal U_1(2q_*).
}
\]

\section{3. Exact finite reduction of \texorpdfstring{$\widehat{\rho}(G_*)$}{rho-hat(G*)}}

Write
\[
|S_{\mathrm{BCC}}|^2
=
\sum_{\Delta\in\Delta S}B_\Delta e^{i\Delta\cdot x},
\qquad
\Delta S:=S_{\mathrm{BCC}}-S_{\mathrm{BCC}}.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\widehat{\rho}(G_*)
=
\sum_{\Delta\in\Delta S}
B_\Delta\,
\mathbf 1_{(G_*-\Delta)_\perp=0}\,
\mathcal U_2((G_*-\Delta)_\parallel).
\label{eq:FMS_rhohat_start}
\end{equation}

Now \(G_*-\Delta\) is parallel to \(\hat n\) if and only if \(\Delta\) itself is parallel to \(G_*\).
Within the BCC difference set, the parallel possibilities are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta\in\{-2G_*,-G_*,0,G_*,2G_*\}.
}
\label{eq:FMS_parallel_Delta}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{align}
\widehat{\rho}(G_*)
&=
B_{G_*}\,\mathcal U_2(0)
+
B_0\,\mathcal U_2(q_*)
+
B_{-G_*}\,\mathcal U_2(2q_*)
+
B_{2G_*}\,\mathcal U_2(-q_*)
+
B_{-2G_*}\,\mathcal U_2(3q_*).
\end{align}

Since \(\mathcal U_2(\ell)\) is even,
\[
\mathcal U_2(-q_*)=\mathcal U_2(q_*).
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\rho}(G_*)
=
B_{G_*}\,\mathcal U_2(0)
+
(B_0+B_{2G_*})\,\mathcal U_2(q_*)
+
B_{-G_*}\,\mathcal U_2(2q_*)
+
B_{-2G_*}\,\mathcal U_2(3q_*).
}
\label{eq:FMS_rhohat_final}
\end{equation}

So \(\widehat{\rho}(G_*)\) needs only the four longitudinal samples
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_2(0),\qquad
\mathcal U_2(q_*),\qquad
\mathcal U_2(2q_*),\qquad
\mathcal U_2(3q_*).
}
\label{eq:FMS_U2set}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Exact finite reduction of \texorpdfstring{$\widehat{\Xi_i}(G_*)$}{Xi-hat(G*)}}

In the Stage-IA averaged-denominator reduction,
\begin{equation}
\widehat{\Xi_i}(G_*)
\approx
\sum_M
\left[
n_i\,C_M^{(0)}\,\mathbf 1_{(G_*-M)_\perp=0}\,\mathcal R_1((G_*-M)_\parallel)
+
C_{M,i}^{(1)}\,\mathbf 1_{(G_*-M)_\perp=0}\,\mathcal R_2((G_*-M)_\parallel)
\right].
\label{eq:FMS_Xihat_start}
\end{equation}

Here \(M\) runs over the shell-plus-density support
\[
M\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}+\Delta S.
\]
The condition \((G_*-M)_\perp=0\) means that \(M\) must also lie on the \(G_*\)-axis.
Inside \(S_{\mathrm{BCC}}+\Delta S\), the parallel possibilities are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M\in\{-3G_*,-2G_*,-G_*,0,G_*,2G_*,3G_*\}.
}
\label{eq:FMS_parallel_M}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Xi_i}(G_*)
\approx
\sum_{m=-3}^{3}
\left[
n_i\,C_{mG_*}^{(0)}\,\mathcal R_1((1-m)q_*)
+
C_{mG_*,i}^{(1)}\,\mathcal R_2((1-m)q_*)
\right].
}
\label{eq:FMS_Xihat_axis}
\end{equation}

Using parity:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathcal R_2(\ell)\) is even,
\item \(\mathcal R_1(\ell)=i\ell\,\mathcal F(\ell)\) and hence \(\mathcal R_1(0)=0\).
\end{itemize}

So the only independent longitudinal samples needed are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal R_1(q_*),\quad
\mathcal R_1(2q_*),\quad
\mathcal R_1(3q_*),\quad
\mathcal R_1(4q_*),
}
\label{eq:FMS_R1set}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal R_2(0),\quad
\mathcal R_2(q_*),\quad
\mathcal R_2(2q_*),\quad
\mathcal R_2(3q_*),\quad
\mathcal R_2(4q_*).
}
\label{eq:FMS_R2set}
\end{equation}

Thus \(\widehat{\Xi_i}(G_*)\) is reduced to a finite one-dimensional data set of size \(4+5\).

\section{5. Final finite one-dimensional data set}

Collecting the above results, the accepted Stage-IA branch requires only the following one-dimensional Fourier samples:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_1(0),\qquad
\mathcal U_1(2q_*),
}
\label{eq:FMS_set1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_2(0),\qquad
\mathcal U_2(q_*),\qquad
\mathcal U_2(2q_*),\qquad
\mathcal U_2(3q_*),
}
\label{eq:FMS_set2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal R_1(q_*),\qquad
\mathcal R_1(2q_*),\qquad
\mathcal R_1(3q_*),\qquad
\mathcal R_1(4q_*),
}
\label{eq:FMS_set3}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal R_2(0),\qquad
\mathcal R_2(q_*),\qquad
\mathcal R_2(2q_*),\qquad
\mathcal R_2(3q_*),\qquad
\mathcal R_2(4q_*).
}
\label{eq:FMS_set4}
\end{equation}

So the entire accepted-branch common extractor is reduced to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2+4+4+5=15
}
\end{equation}
independent one-dimensional profile samples.

\section{6. Immediate next formulas}

Once those \(15\) numbers are known, one inserts them into
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Phi}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat{\rho}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat{\Xi_i}(G_*),
}
\label{eq:FMS_insert1}
\end{equation}
then into
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^1_{(II)}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^2_{(II)}(G_*),
}
\label{eq:FMS_insert2}
\end{equation}
and finally into
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\to K_i\to P_*K_iP_* \to (\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)
\to (\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\label{eq:FMS_insert3}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

For the selected BCC harmonic
\[
G_*=\frac{q_*}{\sqrt2}(1,1,0),
\]
the accepted Stage-IA branch extractor reduces to a finite list of longitudinal Fourier samples of the one-dimensional profile \(u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)\).

The exact reductions are:

\[
\widehat{\Phi}(G_*)
=
\eta_{+}\,\mathcal U_1(0)
+
\eta_{-}\,\mathcal U_1(2q_*),
\]

\[
\widehat{\rho}(G_*)
=
B_{G_*}\,\mathcal U_2(0)
+
(B_0+B_{2G_*})\,\mathcal U_2(q_*)
+
B_{-G_*}\,\mathcal U_2(2q_*)
+
B_{-2G_*}\,\mathcal U_2(3q_*),
\]

and
\[
\widehat{\Xi_i}(G_*)
\approx
\sum_{m=-3}^{3}
\left[
n_i\,C_{mG_*}^{(0)}\,\mathcal R_1((1-m)q_*)
+
C_{mG_*,i}^{(1)}\,\mathcal R_2((1-m)q_*)
\right].
\]

Using parity, the full accepted-branch common extractor needs only the \(15\) independent one-dimensional samples
\[
\mathcal U_1(0),\ \mathcal U_1(2q_*),
\]
\[
\mathcal U_2(0),\ \mathcal U_2(q_*),\ \mathcal U_2(2q_*),\ \mathcal U_2(3q_*),
\]
\[
\mathcal R_1(q_*),\ \mathcal R_1(2q_*),\ \mathcal R_1(3q_*),\ \mathcal R_1(4q_*),
\]
\[
\mathcal R_2(0),\ \mathcal R_2(q_*),\ \mathcal R_2(2q_*),\ \mathcal R_2(3q_*),\ \mathcal R_2(4q_*).
\]

So the accepted-branch common extractor is no longer an open infinite-dimensional object.
It is a finite one-dimensional profile-data computation on \(u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Finite-Mode Closure of the Accepted-Branch Common Extractor}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The accepted Stage-IA branch has already reduced the branch-specific extractor to \(15\) one-dimensional longitudinal Fourier samples.

We now close the next step completely by writing the load-bearing Class II intervalley overlaps
\[
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^1_{(II)}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^2_{(II)}(G_*)
\]
as finite quadratic/bilinear forms in those samples.

This is the point at which the common extractor ceases to be an infinite-dimensional object and becomes a small finite-dimensional algebraic computation.

\section{1. The finite one-dimensional data vectors}

For the selected intervalley harmonic
\[
G_*=\frac{q_*}{\sqrt2}(1,1,0),
\]
define the accepted-branch longitudinal sample vectors
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbf U_1:=
\begin{pmatrix}
\mathcal U_1(0)\\
\mathcal U_1(2q_*)
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:FMC_U1vec}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbf U_2:=
\begin{pmatrix}
\mathcal U_2(0)\\
\mathcal U_2(q_*)\\
\mathcal U_2(2q_*)\\
\mathcal U_2(3q_*)
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:FMC_U2vec}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbf R_1:=
\begin{pmatrix}
\mathcal R_1(q_*)\\
\mathcal R_1(2q_*)\\
\mathcal R_1(3q_*)\\
\mathcal R_1(4q_*)
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:FMC_R1vec}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbf R_2:=
\begin{pmatrix}
\mathcal R_2(0)\\
\mathcal R_2(q_*)\\
\mathcal R_2(2q_*)\\
\mathcal R_2(3q_*)\\
\mathcal R_2(4q_*)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:FMC_R2vec}
\end{equation}

These are the only branch-dependent inputs that remain.

\section{2. Finite reduction of \texorpdfstring{$\widehat{\Phi}(G_*)$}{Phi-hat(G*)}}

From the previous reduction,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Phi}(G_*)
=
\eta_{+}\,\mathcal U_1(0)
+
\eta_{-}\,\mathcal U_1(2q_*).
}
\label{eq:FMC_PhihatG}
\end{equation}

So define the geometry row vector
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbf c_\Phi^T:=
\begin{pmatrix}
\eta_{+} & \eta_{-}
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:FMC_cPhi}
\end{equation}
and write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Phi}(G_*)=\mathbf c_\Phi^T\mathbf U_1.
}
\label{eq:FMC_Phihat_matrix}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Finite reduction of \texorpdfstring{$\widehat{\rho}(G_*)$}{rho-hat(G*)}}

Previously we obtained
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\rho}(G_*)
=
B_{G_*}\,\mathcal U_2(0)
+
(B_0+B_{2G_*})\,\mathcal U_2(q_*)
+
B_{-G_*}\,\mathcal U_2(2q_*)
+
B_{-2G_*}\,\mathcal U_2(3q_*).
}
\label{eq:FMC_rhohatG}
\end{equation}

Hence define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbf c_\rho^T:=
\begin{pmatrix}
B_{G_*} &
B_0+B_{2G_*} &
B_{-G_*} &
B_{-2G_*}
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:FMC_crho}
\end{equation}
so that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\rho}(G_*)=\mathbf c_\rho^T\mathbf U_2.
}
\label{eq:FMC_rhohat_matrix}
\end{equation}

More generally, for every reciprocal argument \(Q\) entering the finite intervalley sums, define a corresponding row vector
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbf c_\rho(Q)^T
}
\label{eq:FMC_crhoQ}
\end{equation}
such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\rho}(Q)=\mathbf c_\rho(Q)^T\mathbf U_2.
}
\label{eq:FMC_rhoQ}
\end{equation}

Because only finitely many \(Q\) appear in the selected intervalley channel, this produces only finitely many such rows.

\section{4. Finite reduction of \texorpdfstring{$\widehat{\Xi_i}(G_*)$}{Xi-hat(G*)}}

The accepted-branch reduction gave
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Xi_i}(G_*)
\approx
\sum_{m=-3}^{3}
\left[
n_i\,C_{mG_*}^{(0)}\,\mathcal R_1((1-m)q_*)
+
C_{mG_*,i}^{(1)}\,\mathcal R_2((1-m)q_*)
\right].
}
\label{eq:FMC_XiG_start}
\end{equation}

Because \(\mathcal R_1(0)=0\), the \(m=1\) term contributes only through \(\mathcal R_2(0)\).

Collect the coefficients multiplying \(\mathbf R_1\) and \(\mathbf R_2\) into row vectors
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbf c^{(1)}_{\Xi_i}:=
\begin{pmatrix}
n_i\,C_{0\cdot G_*}^{(0)} &
n_i\,C_{-G_*}^{(0)} &
n_i\,C_{-2G_*}^{(0)} &
n_i\,C_{-3G_*}^{(0)}
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:FMC_cXi1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbf c^{(2)}_{\Xi_i}:=
\begin{pmatrix}
C_{G_*,i}^{(1)} &
C_{0\cdot G_*,i}^{(1)} &
C_{-G_*,i}^{(1)} &
C_{-2G_*,i}^{(1)} &
C_{-3G_*,i}^{(1)}
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:FMC_cXi2}
\end{equation}
so that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Xi_i}(G_*)
\approx
\mathbf c^{(1)}_{\Xi_i}\mathbf R_1
+
\mathbf c^{(2)}_{\Xi_i}\mathbf R_2.
}
\label{eq:FMC_XiG_matrix}
\end{equation}

More generally, for every reciprocal argument \(Q'\) entering the transverse intervalley sum, define finite row vectors
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbf c^{(1)}_{\Xi_i}(Q')^T,\qquad
\mathbf c^{(2)}_{\Xi_i}(Q')^T
}
\label{eq:FMC_cXiQ}
\end{equation}
such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Xi_i}(Q')
\approx
\mathbf c^{(1)}_{\Xi_i}(Q')^T\mathbf R_1
+
\mathbf c^{(2)}_{\Xi_i}(Q')^T\mathbf R_2.
}
\label{eq:FMC_XiQ}
\end{equation}

Again, only finitely many such \(Q'\) occur.

\section{5. Quadratic form for \texorpdfstring{$\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*)$}{U-hat(II)(G*)}}

The scalar intervalley overlap is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*)
=
\frac{\alpha_X^2\nu_0}{M_X^2}
\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
(Q\cdot Q')\,\widehat{\rho}(Q)\,\widehat{\rho}(Q'),
\qquad
\nu_0:=\sum_A(n_0^A)^2.
}
\label{eq:FMC_Ustart}
\end{equation}

Substitute \eqref{eq:FMC_rhoQ}:
\begin{equation}
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*)
=
\frac{\alpha_X^2\nu_0}{M_X^2}
\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
(Q\cdot Q')\,
\bigl(\mathbf c_\rho(Q)^T\mathbf U_2\bigr)
\bigl(\mathbf c_\rho(Q')^T\mathbf U_2\bigr).
\end{equation}

Therefore define the symmetric \(4\times4\) geometry matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb M_U
:=
\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
(Q\cdot Q')\,
\mathbf c_\rho(Q)\,\mathbf c_\rho(Q')^T.
}
\label{eq:FMC_MU}
\end{equation}

Then the scalar intervalley overlap is exactly the quadratic form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*)
=
\frac{\alpha_X^2\nu_0}{M_X^2}\,
\mathbf U_2^T\mathbb M_U\,\mathbf U_2.
}
\label{eq:FMC_Ufinal}
\end{equation}

So \(\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*)\) depends only on the four samples in \(\mathbf U_2\).

\section{6. Bilinear form for \texorpdfstring{$\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)$}{T-hat(II)(G*)}}

The transverse intervalley overlap is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Gamma_\alpha
\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
iQ_i\,\widehat{\rho}(Q)\,\widehat{\Xi_i}(Q'),
}
\label{eq:FMC_Tstart}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma_\alpha:=\sum_A n_0^A\mathcal Q_\alpha^A.
}
\label{eq:FMC_Gamma}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:FMC_rhoQ} and \eqref{eq:FMC_XiQ}, we get
\begin{align}
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
&\approx
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Gamma_\alpha
\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
iQ_i\,
\bigl(\mathbf c_\rho(Q)^T\mathbf U_2\bigr)
\Bigl[
\mathbf c^{(1)}_{\Xi_i}(Q')^T\mathbf R_1
+
\mathbf c^{(2)}_{\Xi_i}(Q')^T\mathbf R_2
\Bigr].
\end{align}

Define the geometry coupling matrices
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb M_{T,1}^{(\alpha)}
:=
\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
iQ_i\,
\mathbf c_\rho(Q)\,
\mathbf c^{(1)}_{\Xi_i}(Q')^T,
}
\label{eq:FMC_MT1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb M_{T,2}^{(\alpha)}
:=
\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
iQ_i\,
\mathbf c_\rho(Q)\,
\mathbf c^{(2)}_{\Xi_i}(Q')^T.
}
\label{eq:FMC_MT2}
\end{equation}

Then the transverse intervalley overlap is the finite bilinear form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
\approx
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Gamma_\alpha
\Bigl[
\mathbf U_2^T\mathbb M_{T,1}^{(\alpha)}\mathbf R_1
+
\mathbf U_2^T\mathbb M_{T,2}^{(\alpha)}\mathbf R_2
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:FMC_Tfinal}
\end{equation}

Thus \(\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)\) depends only on the finite vectors \(\mathbf U_2,\mathbf R_1,\mathbf R_2\).

\section{7. Final finite-mode closure of the accepted-branch extractor}

Collecting all pieces, the accepted Stage-IA branch now enters the common extractor only through the \(15\)-component finite data vector
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbf d_{\mathrm{IA}}
:=
\mathbf U_1\oplus\mathbf U_2\oplus\mathbf R_1\oplus\mathbf R_2
\in\mathbb C^{15}.
}
\label{eq:FMC_dIA}
\end{equation}

The load-bearing overlaps are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\Phi}(G_*)=\mathbf c_\Phi^T\mathbf U_1,
}
\label{eq:FMC_finalPhi}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*)
=
\frac{\alpha_X^2\nu_0}{M_X^2}\,
\mathbf U_2^T\mathbb M_U\,\mathbf U_2,
}
\label{eq:FMC_finalU}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
\approx
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Gamma_\alpha
\Bigl[
\mathbf U_2^T\mathbb M_{T,1}^{(\alpha)}\mathbf R_1
+
\mathbf U_2^T\mathbb M_{T,2}^{(\alpha)}\mathbf R_2
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:FMC_finalT}
\end{equation}

So the infinite-dimensional branch dependence has collapsed completely to a small finite-dimensional algebraic problem.

\section{8. Immediate next move}

Once the geometry matrices
\[
\mathbb M_U,\qquad
\mathbb M_{T,1}^{(\alpha)},\qquad
\mathbb M_{T,2}^{(\alpha)}
\]
are evaluated for the selected \(G_*\), the remaining chain is mechanical:
\[
