\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X^2\nu_0 q_*^2}{M_X^2}\rho_*^2,
}
\label{eq:NWC_Uhat}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
\frac{2q_*^2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Gamma_\alpha
\rho_*
\Bigl[
27\mathcal F(q_*)
+
30\mathcal F(2q_*)
+
9\mathcal F(3q_*)
-
30\mathcal R_2(0)
-
60\mathcal R_2(q_*)
-
34\mathcal R_2(2q_*)
-
8\mathcal R_2(3q_*)
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:NWC_That}
\end{equation}

\section{12. Actual executable order}

The exact executable order is now:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(i) solve the dimensionless shooting problem \eqref{eq:NWC_shoot0} at }\chi_{II}=0,
}
\label{eq:NWC_exec1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(ii) continue in }\chi_{II}>0\text{ to the target branch,}
}
\label{eq:NWC_exec2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(iii) evaluate }\mathcal U_2(0),\mathcal U_2(q_*),\mathcal U_2(2q_*),
\mathcal F(q_*),\mathcal F(2q_*),\mathcal F(3q_*),
\mathcal R_2(0),\mathcal R_2(q_*),\mathcal R_2(2q_*),\mathcal R_2(3q_*),
}
\label{eq:NWC_exec3}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(iv) compute }\rho_*,\Xi_\parallel^*,\Xi_1^*,\Xi_2^*,
\text{ then }\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*),\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*),
}
\label{eq:NWC_exec4}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(v) pass those into }H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\to K_i\to P_*K_iP_*\to(\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O).
}
\label{eq:NWC_exec5}
\end{equation}

Nothing conceptual remains open at the selected-channel Stage-IA level.

\section{Final Summary}

The Stage-IA construction is now a direct numerical workflow.

The actual shooting problem is the dimensionless even-branch equation
\[
-\mathfrak y\,f_{ssss}
+
\mathfrak a\,f_{ss}
+
\mathfrak b\,f^2f_{ss}
+
\mathfrak b\,f(f_s)^2
+
\mathfrak u(f^3-f)
-
\mathfrak g(f^5-f)
=
0,
\]
with
\[
f_s(0)=0,\qquad
f_{sss}(0)=0,\qquad
f(s)\to 1,\qquad
f_{ss}(s)\to 0.
\]

The shooting unknowns are
\[
a=f(0),\qquad b=f_{ss}(0),
\]
and the first seed is
\[
(a,b)\approx(0,2).
\]

After convergence, reconstruct
\[
u_{\mathrm{IA}}(\xi)=u_\infty f(m_*\xi).
\]

Then compute the ten one-dimensional samples
\[
\mathcal U_2(0),\ \mathcal U_2(q_*),\ \mathcal U_2(2q_*),
\]
\[
\mathcal F(q_*),\ \mathcal F(2q_*),\ \mathcal F(3q_*),
\]
\[
\mathcal R_2(0),\ \mathcal R_2(q_*),\ \mathcal R_2(2q_*),\ \mathcal R_2(3q_*).
\]

From them,
\[
\rho_*,
\qquad
\Xi_\parallel^*,
\qquad
\Xi_1^*,
\qquad
\Xi_2^*=\sqrt2\,\Xi_1^*
\]
follow directly, and therefore
\[
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X^2\nu_0 q_*^2}{M_X^2}\rho_*^2,
\]
\[
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
\frac{2q_*^2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Gamma_\alpha
\rho_*
\Bigl[
27\mathcal F(q_*)
+
30\mathcal F(2q_*)
+
9\mathcal F(3q_*)
-
30\mathcal R_2(0)
-
60\mathcal R_2(q_*)
-
34\mathcal R_2(2q_*)
-
8\mathcal R_2(3q_*)
\Bigr].
\]

So the selected \(G_*\) extractor is now purely a numerical post-processing layer on top of the Stage-IA shooting solve.

\section{Route Correction to the Current Master and Immediate Executable Certificate Workflow}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

According to the latest uploaded master notes, the current official forward-computable route is the explicit odd extra-carrier reference route, while the canonical mixed odd-active branch remains the structural target branch.

Therefore the correct immediate task is not to keep extending the direct Stage-IA symbolic branch construction indefinitely.
The correct immediate task is to populate the already-closed carrier certificate by finite numerical extraction from the actual microscopic linearized operator.

In the current master, this is organized as:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1} \to \text{Gate 2} \to \text{Gate 3} \to \text{Gate 4}.
}

\section{1. What the current master says is the remaining problem}

\begin{equation}

\end{equation}
and then finite coefficient extraction, rather than re-solving the full nonlinear PDE from scratch.

So the immediate computational goal is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{populate the already-derived certificate by actual finite branch/operator data.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Current reference coefficient sheet}

\qquad

Under the fixed reference choice

\section{Immediate Actual PDE Population Route}

The reduced PDE coefficients are
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,\qquad
\alpha=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_E,\qquad
\beta=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_O.
\]

Under the symmetric reference choice \(\gamma_E=\gamma_O=\gamma_\perp\),
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,\qquad
\alpha=\beta=-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c.
\]

So the remaining finite microscopic tasks are:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Task A: compute } I_3,\ I_c
}
\]
from the defect zero-mode profiles \(f_\pm(\xi)\) and \(\theta(\xi)\),

\[
\boxed{
\text{Task B: compute } \lambda_c
}
\]
from the longitudinal projected low-block derivative,

\[
\boxed{
\text{Task C: compute } \widetilde\Lambda_O
\ \text{(equivalently }J_1\text{ in canonical normalization)}
}
\]
from the explicit odd extra-carrier operator insertion,

and then assemble
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel,\ \alpha,\ \beta.
}
\]

The resulting reference reduced PDE is
\[
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c\,
\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c\,
\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
\]

\section{Actual Reduced PDE on the Active Explicit Odd Extra-Carrier Route}

The reduced coefficient dictionary is
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_O,
\]
with
\[
I_3=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
I_c=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
\]

At one-mediator level,
\[
\widetilde\Lambda_E
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,C_EJ_1,
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1.
\]

Hence the general explicit lowest-order coefficient sheet is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,C_EJ_1\,I_c,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1\,I_c.
}
\]

In canonical explicit normalization
\[
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1,
\]
this becomes
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,J_1\,I_c,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,J_1\,I_c.
}
\]

Therefore the actual reduced PDE is
\[
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}J_1I_c\,
\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}J_1I_c\,
\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}J_1I_c.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
I_3,\qquad I_c,\qquad \lambda_c,\qquad J_1
}

\section{Direct Microscopic Reading of \texorpdfstring{$\lambda_c$}{lambda\_c} and \texorpdfstring{$\widetilde\Lambda_O$}{tilde Lambda\_O}}

\subsection{1. Longitudinal coefficient \texorpdfstring{$\lambda_c$}{lambda\_c}}

Write the background-dependent Hessian in block form and extract the first-order transport kernel
\[
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
H_B(\xi)-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}+\cdots.
\]

Restrict the \(OO\)-block to the tangent bundle \(Q_B\):
\[
V^\mu_{OO}(\xi):=\Pi_Q\,\mathcal V^\mu_{OO}(\xi)\,\Pi_Q.
\]

The longitudinal projector functional is
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M]
:=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu\bigr).
}
\]

Define
\[
\boxed{
a_{3;OO}(\xi)
=
\mathfrak P_\parallel[V_{OO}]
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu V^\mu_{OO}(\xi)\bigr).
}
\]

Its principal odd expansion is
\[
a_{3;OO}(\xi)
=
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}\,\theta'(\xi)
+
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\,\theta'(\xi)^3
+
O\!\bigl(\theta'(\xi)\theta(\xi)^2,\theta'(\xi)^5\bigr).
\]

In the current concrete Class II-compatible branch one has
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
so the longitudinal coefficient is Branch B and therefore
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c=2\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}.
}
\]

Equivalently, the executable limit formula is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c
=
2\lim_{\theta'\to 0}
\frac{\mathfrak P_\parallel[V_{OO}]}{\theta'(\xi)^3}.
}
\]

Hence the reduced longitudinal coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3
=
I_3\lim_{\theta'\to 0}
\frac{\mathfrak P_\parallel[V_{OO}]}{\theta'(\xi)^3}.
}
\]

\subsection{2. Odd transverse coefficient \texorpdfstring{$\widetilde\Lambda_O$}{tilde Lambda\_O}}

On the active explicit odd extra-carrier route, the decisive microscopic coupling is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_O
=
X_i^{(O)}\,\cos\theta(\xi)\,J_jD_j\psi.
}
\]

Its induced tangent transport block is
\[
\boxed{
V_{EO}^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\Bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\]

The odd projector functional is
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
:=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu\bigr).
}
\]

Therefore the odd coefficient is read directly as
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
\frac{\mathfrak P_O[V_{EO}]}{\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)}.
}
\]

At one-mediator level this becomes
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1.
}
\]

In canonical normalization \(C_O=1\),
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,J_1.
}
\]

Hence the reduced odd transverse coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
\beta=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1\,I_c,
}
\]
and in canonical normalization
\[
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,J_1\,I_c.
}
\]

\subsection{3. The actual reduced PDE with direct microscopic readout}

Thus the active-route reduced PDE is
\[
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
I_3\!\left(
\lim_{\theta'\to0}\frac{\mathfrak P_\parallel[V_{OO}]}{\theta'^3}
\right)\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
+
I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\]

If one also inserts the one-mediator odd coefficient,
\[
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
I_3\!\left(
\lim_{\theta'\to0}\frac{\mathfrak P_\parallel[V_{OO}]}{\theta'^3}
\right)\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}C_OJ_1I_c\,
\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\]

\subsection{4. What remains literally to do}

There is no new structural theorem left here.

The remaining microscopic tasks are exactly:

\[
\boxed{
\text{(A) compute }V^\mu_{OO}(\xi)\text{ from the full Hessian and evaluate }
\mathfrak P_\parallel[V_{OO}],
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{(B) compute }J_1
\ \text{(equivalently }\widetilde\Lambda_O\text{)}
\text{ from the explicit odd extra-carrier insertion.}
}
\]

Once these are inserted, the reduced coefficient point
\[
\boxed{
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
}
\]
is fully populated.

\section{Direct Source-by-Source Reading of the Remaining Actual Reduced PDE Coefficients}

\section{1. Longitudinal coefficient \texorpdfstring{$\lambda_c$}{lambda_c} from the \(OO\)-block}

Write the background-dependent Hessian block expansion
\[
\mathcal H_{OO}
=
\mathcal H_{OO}^{(0)}(\xi)
-
i\,\mathcal V^\mu_{OO}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
\mathcal W^{\mu\nu}_{OO}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
+\cdots.
\]

Restrict the first-order block to the tangent bundle:
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{OO}(\xi):=\Pi_Q\,\mathcal V^\mu_{OO}(\xi)\,\Pi_Q.
}
\]

The longitudinal projector functional is
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M]
:=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu\bigr).
}
\]

Therefore define
\[
\boxed{
a_{3;OO}(\xi)
=
\mathfrak P_\parallel[V_{OO}]
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu V^\mu_{OO}(\xi)\bigr).
}
\]

Its branch-sensitive odd expansion is
\[
a_{3;OO}(\xi)
=
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}\,\theta'(\xi)
+
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\,\theta'(\xi)^3
+
O\!\bigl(\theta'(\xi)\theta(\xi)^2,\theta'(\xi)^5\bigr).
\]

The exact identification is
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_{\parallel;OO}^{(0)}=\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)},
\qquad
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}=\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}.
}
\]

In the current concrete Class II-compatible branch one has
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
}
\]
so the practical longitudinal coefficient is forced onto Branch B:
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c=2\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}.
}
\]

Equivalently, the executable reading formula is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c
=
2\lim_{\theta'\to0}
\frac{\mathfrak P_\parallel[V_{OO}]}{\theta'(\xi)^3}.
}
\]

Hence the reduced longitudinal coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3.
}
\]

\section{2. Why the primitive longitudinal source starts at \texorpdfstring{$\theta'^3$}{theta'^3}}

The microscopic primitive longitudinal channel is generated by
\[
\mathcal T_\xi=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B].
\]
Its direct tangent restriction vanishes,
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q=0,
\]
but its square is nontrivial:
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}(\mathbf 1_2+\Sigma_3).
\]

Taking the traceless part gives
\[
S_\xi
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\Sigma_3.
\]
Because the graded overlap kills the parity-even \(\theta'^2\) piece, one additional odd factor is required, so the surviving primitive transport seed is
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{prim}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
}
\]

This is why the active longitudinal reading is cubic in \(\theta'\), not linear.

\section{3. Even/odd transverse coefficients from the \(TD+DT\) block}

Define the mixed first-order transverse carrier
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
:=
\Pi_Q\bigl(\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT}\bigr)\Pi_Q.
}
\]

The canonical projector functionals are
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
:=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu\bigr),
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
:=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu\bigr).
}
\]

So at the minimal mixed-block level,
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\mathrm{inv}}],
\qquad
\Lambda_O=\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\mathrm{inv}}].
}
\]

More generally, beyond the minimal truncation,
\[
\Lambda_E
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} e^{(1)}_{0;AB},
\qquad
\Lambda_O
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} o^{(1)}_{0;AB},
\]
but the sharp leading audit starts from \(TD+DT\).

Hence the full remaining microscopic transport point is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{OO}\to \lambda_c,
\qquad
\mathcal H_{TD},\mathcal H_{DT}\to \Lambda_E,\Lambda_O.
}
\]

\section{4. Direct odd coefficient on the active explicit odd route}

On the active explicit odd extra-carrier route,
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_O
=
X_i^{(O)}\,\cos\theta(\xi)\,J_jD_j\psi.
}
\]

Its induced tangent transport block is
\[
\boxed{
V_{EO}^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\Bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\]

Therefore the local odd density is
\[
\boxed{
b_O(\xi)=\widetilde\Lambda_O\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\]

At operator level,
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1.
}
\]
Under canonical shell normalization \(C_O=1\),
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,J_1.
}
\]

Hence the reduced odd transverse coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
\beta=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1\,I_c.
}
\]

\section{5. The actual reduced PDE after these two readings}

Once \(\lambda_c\) and \(\widetilde\Lambda_O\) are populated, the active-route reduced PDE is
\[
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+

+
I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.

If one also inserts the one-mediator odd coefficient explicitly,
\[
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)

\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)

\section{6. Immediate executable computation order}

Nothing structural remains here.
The actual microscopic tasks are exactly:

\section{Source-by-Source Hessian Audit for the Remaining Actual Reduced PDE Coefficients}

\section{1. Exact source split to audit}

The first-order tangent transport operator is obtained from the one-defect Hessian by keeping only the worldvolume first-derivative block:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)
=
\mathbb H_{1,\Psi}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,P}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,\sigma}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,X}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,J}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,K}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,EO}^\mu.
}
\label{eq:SSA_H1split}
\end{equation}

Projecting to the tangent bundle gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)=\Pi_Q\,\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\,\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:SSA_Vproj}
\end{equation}

The longitudinal and transverse projector functionals are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M]
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\mathcal M^\mu\bigr),
}
\label{eq:SSA_Ppar}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu\bigr),
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu\bigr).
}
\label{eq:SSA_PEPO}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Longitudinal source table inside the \(OO\)-block}

The orientational diagonal block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{OO}
=
-Z_{O,k}\partial^2
+
\mathcal M_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
+
Y_k\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(\xi,\partial)
+
\mathcal T_{OO}(\xi,\partial_y).
}
\label{eq:SSA_OOblock}
\end{equation}

The exact solved lowest-order verdict is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_\parallel[V_{OO}^{(\mathrm{kin})}]=0,
\qquad
\mathfrak P_\parallel[V_{OO}^{(\mathrm{pot})}]=0,
}
\label{eq:SSA_kinpot_zero}
\end{equation}
because the kinetic Laplacian and local potential pieces do not generate a first-order worldvolume transport term.

Also,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\ell_0^{(1)}=0,
}
\label{eq:SSA_BranchA_zero}
\end{equation}
so the derivative-anisotropy piece does not produce a Branch-A longitudinal coefficient in the current solved lowest-order class:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_\parallel[V_{OO}^{(\nabla\mathrm{ani})}]=0.
}
\label{eq:SSA_aniso_zero}
\end{equation}

At principal shell order, the Schur-corrected source classification is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{3;OO}^{(JJ)}\neq 0\ \text{allowed},
\qquad
a_{3;OO}^{(JK)}=0,
\qquad
a_{3;OO}^{(KK)}=0.
}
\label{eq:SSA_JJonly}
\end{equation}

Therefore the only surviving principal longitudinal source is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal T_{OO}^{(JJ)}.
}
\label{eq:SSA_TOO_JJ}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Primitive longitudinal seed and direct reading of \(\lambda_c\)}

The primitive one-defect seed is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal T_\xi=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\qquad
S_\xi=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
}
\label{eq:SSA_primitive}
\end{equation}

For the explicit defect representative,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_\xi=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:SSA_Sxi}
\end{equation}

Hence the primitive longitudinal transport kernel is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{OO,\mathrm{prim}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,S_\xi\,n^\mu
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:SSA_Vprim}
\end{equation}

Thus the longitudinal coefficient profile is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{3;OO}(\xi)
=
\mathfrak P_\parallel[V_{OO}]
=
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\,\theta'(\xi)^3+\cdots,
\qquad
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}.
}
\label{eq:SSA_a3}
\end{equation}

So the executable microscopic reading formula is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c=\lambda_{c;OO}
=
2\lim_{\theta'\to0}
\frac{\mathfrak P_\parallel[V_{OO}]}{\theta'(\xi)^3}.
}
\label{eq:SSA_lambdac}
\end{equation}

After overlap insertion,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:SSA_lambdapar}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Principal transverse source from \(TD+DT\)}

Define the mixed first-order transverse carrier
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
=
\Pi_Q\bigl(\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT}\bigr)\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:SSA_MTD}
\end{equation}

The leading transverse coefficients are then read by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\mathrm{inv}}],
\qquad
\Lambda_O
=
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\mathrm{inv}}].
}
\label{eq:SSA_Lambdas}
\end{equation}

The sharp source classification is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
JK+KJ \to (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O),
\qquad
KK \to \text{same-shell residual / correction only}.
}
\label{eq:SSA_JKprincipal}
\end{equation}

Therefore the actual leading transverse audit is not broad anymore:
it is the explicit \(TD+DT\) evaluation of the \(JK+KJ\)-driven mixed transport block.

\section{5. Odd coefficient on the active explicit odd route}

On the active explicit odd extra-carrier route, the odd insertion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_O
=
X_i^{(O)}\,\cos\theta(\xi)\,J_jD_j\psi.
}
\label{eq:SSA_IO}
\end{equation}

Its induced tangent transport block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{EO}^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\Bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:SSA_VEO}
\end{equation}

Hence the odd projector reads directly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
\frac{\mathfrak P_O[V_{EO}]}{\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)}.
}
\label{eq:SSA_tildeLambdaO}
\end{equation}

At one-mediator level, in the current reference normalization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}.
}
\label{eq:SSA_tildeLambdaO_one}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:SSA_beta}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Actual reduced PDE once the two microscopic reads are inserted}

Once \(\lambda_c\) and \(\widetilde\Lambda_O\) are populated, the active-route reduced PDE is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\Sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_E\bigl(\Sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\Sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
+
I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_O\bigl(-\Sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\Sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:SSA_PDE}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Immediate executable order}

So the literal next computation is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(A) differentiate the full one-defect Hessian block-by-block, keep only the first-order transport part,}
}
\label{eq:SSA_nextA}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(B) in the \(OO\)-block, evaluate only the }JJ\text{ source and read }\lambda_c\text{ from }\eqref{eq:SSA_lambdac},
}
\label{eq:SSA_nextB}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(C) in the \(TD+DT\)-block, evaluate the }JK+KJ\text{ mixed transport and read }(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O),
}
\label{eq:SSA_nextC}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(D) on the active odd route, equivalently read }\widetilde\Lambda_O\text{ from }\eqref{eq:SSA_tildeLambdaO}.
}
\label{eq:SSA_nextD}
\end{equation}

\section{Actual Local Tensor Form of the Pure \(JJ\) Longitudinal Source}

\section{1. Starting point: Schur-reduced \(JJ\) sector}

After integrating out the heavy mediator \(X_i^a\), the quadratic correction splits as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_X^{(2)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,\delta J\,\delta J^\dagger
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\bigl(\delta J\delta K^\dagger+\delta K\delta J^\dagger\bigr)
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,\delta K\delta K^\dagger.
}
\label{eq:LTF_Schur}
\end{equation}

At principal longitudinal shell order, only the pure \(JJ\)-sector survives in the \(OO\)-longitudinal slot:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{3;OO}^{(JJ)}\neq 0,
\qquad
a_{3;OO}^{(JK)}=0,
\qquad
a_{3;OO}^{(KK)}=0.
}
\label{eq:LTF_source_class}
\end{equation}

So the actual longitudinal microscopic source is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal T_{OO}^{(JJ)}.
}
\label{eq:LTF_TOOJJ}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Local lowest-derivative form of the pure \(JJ\) source}

At principal shell order, the background current takes the local form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_i^a[\phi_0,P_0]=m^a(P_0)\,\partial_i\phi_0.
}
\label{eq:LTF_Jlocal}
\end{equation}

The Bloch derivative insertion contributes only the spatial tensor \(\delta_{ij}\) at leading shell order. Therefore the induced axial \(JJ\)-coefficient field must have the lowest-derivative local tensor form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal A_j^{(JJ)}(x)
=
\sum_m C_{jm}^{(JJ)}\,\partial_m\phi_0(x).
}
\label{eq:LTF_Aj_start}
\end{equation}

Because no principal shell tensor survives except \(\delta_{jm}\), the coefficient tensor collapses to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_{jm}^{(JJ)}=\Xi_{JJ}\,\delta_{jm}.
}
\label{eq:LTF_Ccollapse}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact local lowest-derivative form is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal A_j^{(JJ)}(x)=\Xi_{JJ}\,\partial_j\phi_0(x).
}
\label{eq:LTF_Aj_final}
\end{equation}

This is the actual local tensor form of the pure longitudinal \(JJ\)-source.

\section{3. First-shell Fourier coefficient at the selected harmonic}

Let \(A_{G_*}\) be the first-shell Fourier amplitude of the locked background \(\phi_0\) at the selected shell vector \(G_*\). Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal A}^{(JJ)}_j(G_*)
=
i\,\Xi_{JJ}\,G_{*j}\,A_{G_*}.
}
\label{eq:LTF_Ahatj}
\end{equation}

Contracting with the shell axis \(\hat n=G_*/|G_*|\), we obtain the scalar longitudinal first-shell amplitude
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)
:=
\hat n^j\widehat{\mathcal A}^{(JJ)}_j(G_*)
=
i\,\Xi_{JJ}\,|G_*|\,A_{G_*}.
}
\label{eq:LTF_Ahat_scalar}
\end{equation}

Thus the pure \(JJ\) longitudinal noncancellation problem is reduced to the finite scalar test
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{JJ}\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:LTF_noncancel}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Collapse to the invariant \(L_*\)}

The longitudinal scalar \(\Xi_{JJ}\) has already been reduced to the invariant
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{JJ}=\mathcal N_{JJ}\,L_*,
\qquad
L_*:=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:LTF_XiJJ}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)
=
i\,\mathcal N_{JJ}\,L_*\,|G_*|\,A_{G_*}.
}
\label{eq:LTF_Ahat_Lstar}
\end{equation}

So the pure-\(JJ\) longitudinal slot is completely reduced to the finite scalar package
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal N_{JJ},\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel,\qquad
|G_*|,\qquad
A_{G_*}.
}
\label{eq:LTF_scalar_pkg}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Reading \(\lambda_c\)}

At the projected operator level, the longitudinal master slot is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{med})}
:=
\frac12\Tr\!\Bigl(
\sigma_3\,P_*(\hat n_i\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(\mathrm{med})}(k_*))P_*
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:LTF_lambda_med}
\end{equation}

On the current working branch, the pure-\(JJ\) longitudinal representative satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}
\sim
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\mathcal N_{JJ}\,
m_\parallel\,
u_\parallel\,
|G_*|\,A_{G_*}.
}
\label{eq:LTF_lambdaJJ}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}
\sim
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\Xi_{JJ}\,
|G_*|\,A_{G_*}.
}
\label{eq:LTF_lambdaJJ_Xi}
\end{equation}

This is the concrete actual-reading formula for the longitudinal coefficient on the current branch.

\section{6. Reduced actual PDE longitudinal coefficient}

Once \(\lambda_c\) is read, the reduced longitudinal PDE coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:LTF_lambdapar}
\end{equation}

Using the explicit defect overlap,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:LTF_I3}
\end{equation}
we get
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:LTF_lambdapar_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Honest remaining task}

There is no structural ambiguity left in the longitudinal source classification.

What remains is only the finite scalar extraction of
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal N_{JJ},\qquad
m_\parallel,\qquad
u_\parallel,\qquad
A_{G_*}
}
\label{eq:LTF_remaining}
\end{equation}
from the refined locked Bloch data, and then inserting them into \eqref{eq:LTF_lambdaJJ}.
